# Igros Kodesh

## Volume 5

## 1,224

B"H, 5 Tishrei, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

From time to time, I receive reports regarding the studies of the bochurim at the Yeshiva... And while in certain details I am satisfied with their conduct, even if everything were as it should be, it is well known that the Rebbe Maharash—a saying that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, repeated several times—stated: "If 'good' is 'good,' then 'better' is not 'better'." This is especially true given that in certain details, it appears their conduct and diligence in study require encouragement and strengthening.

I am writing to stir you regarding the title that the Rebbe (Rashab) gave to the Temimim: that they must be "candles to illuminate." If so, it follows simply that this must be the case for the sons of the Temimim. Each and every one of you must have engraved in his memory the great responsibility that rests upon him—that he must serve as an example to all the other students in the Yeshiva, so that they may see from him and do likewise. This applies not only to the study of Chassidus and the avodah of tefillah, but also to the study of Nigleh in general, and to matters of derech eretz between man and his fellow.

I hope that these few words will suffice to stir you and bring you to the realization that the purpose of your coming to the Yeshiva... is not only for your own benefit, but also to influence your surroundings—to serve as an example of how a yeshiva student should be, both internally and externally.

I look forward to hearing good news from you regarding the receipt of this letter, and that you have begun to put this matter into actual practice in all the aforementioned details.

With blessings for success in the study of the Torah of Nigleh and the Torah of Chassidus, with yiras shamayim.

#### ***1,224***

Most of the letters are from the secretariat's copies, and some are from photocopies of the original letters. They are not marked unless the source is different, or if they have already been printed.

## 125

125

B"H, 8 Tishrei, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the eminent Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned in Torah and wisdom, organizer and orator, distinguished in his knowledge and deeds, etc.,
Rabbi Meir, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

Many thanks for the precious gift, the two volumes of *Toras Chaim* that you sent me. I hope that you will also send the rest of your works to the library.

Enclosed is the *Kuntres* for 18 Elul, as well as a copy of a *Michtav Klali*, which I am sure will interest you.

In a separate package, I am sending you the *maamarim* from the summer of 5700 and the *Sefer HaSichos*.

With blessings for a *Chasimah v’Gmar Chasimah Tovah*, and may you increase your strength in Torah, and influence your community with *Toras Chaim*—which is the Torah permeated with the *pnimiyus* of Torah, the "Tree of Life" (*Zohar Vol. III, 124b*).

Although time does not permit due to the multitude of pressures during these days, I have nevertheless looked through your books and leafed through the topics of the day in the *drushim* concerning *teshuvah*. In the *Kuntres* that is enclosed, the matter of *teshuvah* is mentioned in the introduction, and I will therefore offer a few comments, even though one does not debate a *drush*.

Regarding the *drushim* for *Parshas Vayelech-Haazinu* where you bring the matter of "They asked Wisdom, etc.," surely it is known to you that there are several versions of this. See *Yerushalmi Makkos, Chapter 2*, and *Yalkut Shimoni, Tehillim 25* (and in *Vavei HaAmudim* of the *Shelah*, Chapter 21, he brings a version that is puzzling, as it asks Wisdom the verse from Ezekiel the Prophet, and for Prophecy it brings the verse from Proverbs, which is obviously related to Wisdom—unlike the *Yerushalmi*, which brings the verses in the opposite order, which seems more appropriate). I have written at length on this elsewhere, so I will note it here briefly:

"They asked Wisdom, etc." It answered them, "Evil pursues sinners." For according to logic and understanding, the consequence—which is the "evil"—comes about **automatically** from the cause, which is the "sin." It says "evil" generally, because the quality and quantity of the evil of the consequence depends on the quality and quantity of the cause, which is the sin.

"They asked Prophecy," the essence of which is connection to the *Shechinah*. Thus, the sinner (even inadvertently) has severed this connection (for even the inadvertent sinner requires atonement). Therefore, it answered them, "The soul that sins, it shall die," since through the sin—**whatever it may be**—its *dveikus* with the *Shechinah* has been severed. See *Moreh Nevuchim, Part II, from Chapter 34* onwards regarding the subject of prophecy.

"They asked Torah." It answered them, "He shall bring a guilt-offering (*asham*) and receive atonement." For the Torah, which is the wisdom of the *Ribono shel Olam*, is even higher than prophecy—which is why a prophet is not permitted to innovate anything, etc. Therefore, the flaw is felt in it more than in Wisdom or Prophecy. Consequently, death by itself would not atone. It is only because the Torah is a "Torah of kindness" and the *Ribono shel Olam* reaches out a hand to accept those who return, taking into account that a person only sins if a spirit of **folly** has entered them and they have acted like an animal, that the Torah provides a means for atonement. The counsel is given with the emphasis that they only committed the sin because they were like an animal at that time. And among the offerings themselves, it specifically chooses the *asham*, which may be because it encompasses all types of sins, from a doubtful inadvertent act to a willful one. There are other reasons that can be suggested for this as well.

"They asked the *Ribono shel Olam*, etc." For although the flaw is felt most acutely there, on the other hand, "Who can say to Him, 'What are You doing?' and if your transgressions are many, what do you do to Him?" Rather, one must also awaken in his soul a level that is above calculation. This is the act of *teshuvah*. The essence of *teshuvah* is that one is transformed from one extreme to the other, as the *Rambam* puts it, so that the "Knower of **hidden things**" can testify that he will not return to this folly again. In doing so, he also awakens something above, and in his own state, a transformation from one extreme to the other. Whereas he was in the "deepest pit"—as mentioned above, where the flaw is felt most acutely—through *teshuvah* he ascends to the "highest peak." For in the place where *baalei teshuvah* stand, even complete *tzaddikim* cannot stand. And this is not the place to elaborate.

Regarding what you write about "willful sins becoming like merits," see the explanation of this matter in *Tanya, end of Chapter 2*.

Regarding the portion of the sinner's Torah and *mitzvos*, see *Hilchos Talmud Torah* by our *Alter Rebbe, Chapter 4, Paragraph 3*.

I also wish to comment specifically on your conclusion that we have merited to see the *aschalta d’geulah* (the beginning of the redemption). Heaven forbid to say such things, and especially to print them—that the current situation in our Holy Land regarding matters of Judaism are signs of the *aschalta d’geulah*. It pains the heart to elaborate on this, especially since it is known to many. May it be the will of the *Ribono shel Olam* that speedily in our days we merit to emerge from the double and redoubled darkness—where they call darkness light and light darkness—and may *Moshiach Tzidkeinu* redeem us, together with all of *Klal Yisrael*, both in the Diaspora and in the Holy Land (may it be rebuilt and established), from the bitter exile, with a complete and true redemption.

## 1260

...My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, related: Once, the day after Yom Kippur, I entered the presence of my father, the holy Rebbe, and asked him: "And now, what?"

He answered me: "Now is when one must truly do teshuvah."

Now, the days from Yom Kippur until Sukkos are days of joy, and this is certainly true of the days of Sukkos themselves.

From this we have further proof that all avodah of Hashem must be done with joy, even the avodah of teshuvah itself, despite the fact that on the face of it, it leads to bitterness and the like.

On the contrary, quite the opposite: the contemplation of the reality of the concept of teshuvah —that there is nothing that can stand before teshuvah —combined with the faith and trust that one’s heart should be firm and confident in Hashem, for He desires kindness and is gracious, merciful, and abundant in forgiveness the very moment one asks for pardon and forgiveness from Him, may He be blessed, without any doubt or uncertainty in the world —this brings one to great joy.

And if, during Rosh Hashanah and the Aseres Yemei Teshuvah in general, our Sages have said that one must be not only "in trembling" but "rejoice with trembling", then during the days of joy between the Aseres Yemei Teshuvah and Sukkos, and during the time of our rejoicing on Sukkos, and during the time of our rejoicing on Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah—although, of course, they differ in the levels and modes of their joy —the common denominator among them is that they must be observed with the greatest possible joy.

May Hashem grant us the merit to fulfill the prophecy, "Israel shall rejoice in His Maker," through which there will also be, "Hashem shall rejoice in His works," speedily and in our days, literally.

**Menachem Schneerson**

In the name of Hashem, the day after Yom Kippur, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

***

1) To note the commentaries on Mishnah Kerisus 6:3; Shaarei Teshuvah to Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim 61:10, and the seforim cited there. This is not the place to elaborate.
2) **Now**—This should be explained according to what is explained in many places regarding why we say "Forgive us" after the contemplation of Pesukei D'Zimra, the blessings of Shema, and the Shema itself (Hosafos to Torah Or, Parshas Ki Sisa, and elsewhere).
3) Maharil, cited in the Acharonim at the end of Orach Chayim 624.
4) See Rambam, end of Hilchos Lulav.
5) The discussion is well-known regarding the statement that for Bnei Noach, the concept of teshuvah does not apply.
6) Midrash HaNe'elam in Zohar Chadash, beginning of Parshas Bereishis; Rambam, Hilchos Teshuvah, end of chapter 3. See also Yerushalmi, Peah 1:1.
7) Iggeres HaTeshuvah, chapter 11.
8) Explained in Likutei Torah, Parshas Nitzavim, maamar beginning *Sos Asis*.
9) See also Likutei Torah, maamar beginning *Bayom HaShemini Atzeres* (the second one).
10) See Likutei Torah, maamar beginning *Hashem Li B'Ozrai*, chapter 3 and onwards.

## 127

B.H., 12 Tishrei, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the distinguished scholar, G-d-fearing, etc., Rabbi Menachem Man, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter from the first day of Haazinu, in which you ask why the Siddur of the Alter Rebbe states that on the second night of Sukkos as well, one should first recite the blessing *Leishev BaSukkah* and then *Shehecheyanu*, whereas among us, the custom is to recite *Shehecheyanu* first and then *Leishev BaSukkah* on the second night.

**Answer**: Our customs are based on what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, related regarding how his father (the Rebbe Maharash, of blessed memory) conducted himself, and also how his father, of blessed memory, wrote in the glosses in the Siddur in which he davened (see also the *Siddur Torah Or* printed in New York, 5701, in the glosses on page 233, s.v. *Kiddush L'Shalosh Regalim*).

In general, you surely know that our Rebbes were extremely precise regarding customs, yet not everything—the way they conducted themselves—was made public. Consequently, Chassidim were unaware of these details, which led to misunderstandings. This is the merit of our generation, as my father-in-law, the Rebbe, said many times: things have been revealed that were not revealed until now, and now permission has been granted to reveal them. Similarly, we have now been granted the revelation of treasures of stories of our Rebbes, of blessed memory, which had not been revealed until now; many of them are already printed in the *Sichos* that have been published, and many more are ready for print.

It gave me pleasure to read in your letter that you are aware of your Chassidic lineage, and even more so that you feel how to cherish it and conduct yourself accordingly in practice. I wish you *arichus yamim v'shanim tovos*—simply healthy, long years, and also in the sense of the inner meaning of this: that they should be filled with good things, and "there is no 'good' other than Torah and Mitzvos," etc.

Surely you are keeping the *shiurim* that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, established: to study every day a *parsha* of *Chumash* with Rashi (from the *sedra* of the week), to recite the daily *Tehillim* (as the *Tehillim* is divided according to the days of the month), and also a *shiur* in *Tanya*—as it is laid out in the *Moreh Shiur*—for these are vessels to draw down blessing and success in all matters.

With blessings.

Regarding what is written in the Siddur that the second night should be like the first night—this was inserted by the compiler, not the Alter Rebbe. On the contrary, in the *Shulchan Aruch* of the Alter Rebbe (Chapter 643, Section 1), the Alter Rebbe **specified** the words **"on the first night"**—and from this, the Rebbe (Maharash), of blessed memory, derived that on the second night the law is **not** the same. And as he wrote in the aforementioned gloss.

## 1,228

1,228

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, 13 Tishrei, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

Enclosed is the Kuntres for 13 Tishrei—the upcoming Sukkos holiday—intended to provide merit to the many. This is especially relevant during the days of *Zman Simchaseinu* (the time of our rejoicing), where the word *simchaseinu* (our rejoicing) is in the plural form.

It is also known that in times of joy, a person’s desire and effort is to be in the company of others, as it is written: "You shall rejoice, you and your household"—and the members of your household.

This is especially true regarding the company of Torah study, the unique quality of which is to draw hearts together until they become lovers of one another. This is particularly so when studying the inner dimension of Torah, which is the "Tree of Life," where there is neither difficulty nor dispute.

When the many are united as one, nothing they plan will be withheld from them. This is especially true if this unity is expressed through study and *farbrengens* of *ahavas Yisrael*. At that point, the request is fulfilled: "Bless us, our Father, all of us as one, in the light of Your countenance." This also causes joy from Above to below—*Zman Simchaseinu* in the plural: the joy of the Ribono shel Olam—"Hashem will rejoice in His works"—and the joy of Yisrael—"Yisrael will rejoice in their Maker."

With blessings for a happy holiday,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***1,228***

General details. Printed in *Likutei Sichos*, Vol. 8, p. 392.

**Joy... to be in the company of others:** See *Yevamos* 62b: "He dwells without joy." And *Moed Katan* 7b: "The company of the world is preferable to me."

**Become lovers:** *Kiddushin* 30b.

**Where there is neither:** *Zohar*, Vol. 3, 124b. And *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 26.

**Will be withheld:** See *Bereishis Rabbah*, ch. 38:6: "I cannot prevail over them." And at length in *Likutei Torah*, *Shir HaShirim*, end of *Parshas Noach*.

**All of us as one:** See *Tanya*, ch. 32. *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, Mitzvah of *Ahavas Yisrael*. *Kuntres Heichelotzu*.

**Our rejoicing... the Ribono shel Olam... Yisrael:** *Likutei Torah*, *Shemini Atzeres*, discourse entitled *Hashem Li BeOzri*, ch. 3. *Sicha* of the first night of Sukkos, 5704, from the Rebbe Rayatz, and in his own handwriting.

## 1229

B"H, Erev Chag HaSukkos, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and occupied with communal needs, etc.,

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter in which you write regarding the establishment of a committee for Taharas HaMishpacha in the Brighton Beach neighborhood for the construction of a kosher mikveh, and you request that I provide words of encouragement to the members of your camp, may they live.

I fulfill your request with pleasure, and I am enclosing my "Call to Action." Surely, with the proper efforts, Hashem will assist them in bringing their good intention from potential into actuality as soon as possible.

With blessings for a happy holiday.

#### ***1229***

**R' Moshe Meir:** Yeshar.

## 1,230

B"H, Erev Chag HaSukkos, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel in Brighton Beach,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

It was with joy that I received the news that a "Vaad Taharas HaMishpacha" has been formed in Brighton Beach, the goal of which is to build a kosher mikveh there.

The observance of Taharas HaMishpacha is essential not only for the spiritual, but also for the physical existence of the individual and the community at large.

The existence of a kosher mikveh in every Jewish neighborhood, which would provide the opportunity for every Jewish woman to observe Taharas HaMishpacha without undue difficulty, is therefore an absolute necessity, and no obstacles should hinder the construction of such a mikveh.

It goes without saying that it is of the utmost importance that the mikveh be built as soon as possible; for whoever saves one Jewish soul is considered as if they have saved an entire world, and the responsibility is too great to delay it even for a short time.

I therefore turn with my request to all who can assist in this, and in particular to the Jewish residents of Brighton Beach, to participate with the greatest warmth in providing the necessary means to build the mikveh.

I also wish to express my firm hope that the Rabbonim, synagogue presidents, and activists of the area will surely not rest until the mikveh is opened, with the help of Hashem Yisbarach, in the near future.

May the merit of this great mitzvah stand by everyone, man and woman, who takes part in this, to be blessed by Hashem Yisbarach in all that they need, with children, life, and ample sustenance.

## 131

B"H, 28 Tishrei, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc.,
Rabbi Refael Nachman, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

In response to the questions in your letter:

... Regarding having intention (*kavanah*) during *Birchas Kohanim* for someone who has already passed away — this does not seem correct to me. This is unlike reciting *Tehillim* or the verses at the conclusion of the *Shemoneh Esrei*, which depends on the nature of one's *hiskashrus*, the feeling of the heart, and so on.

4) The verses for the name of the *Mashpia* are: "The light of the eyes gladdens the heart, and a good report fattens the bone" (*Mishlei 15:30*), and "How goodly are your tents, O Yaakov, your dwelling places, O Yisrael" (*Bamidbar 24:5*).

5) I would be grateful if you would inform me of the *kavanos* for *Birchas Kohanim* that my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, wrote to you (as you mention in your letter).

6) Thank you, thank you for having me in mind during *Birchas Kohanim*, and for fulfilling the words of our Sages, of blessed memory: "One who gives a gift to his friend must inform him." May it be Hashem’s will that the promise of the Holy One, Blessed be He, "And I will bless them," be fulfilled in you in a good, revealed, and manifest way, with the addition that exceeds the essence.

With blessings for proper health for you and your wife, may they live, and much *nachas* from all your children, may they live.

#### ***131***

**That he wrote to him:** *Igros Kodesh* of the Rebbe Rayatz, Vol. 8, Letter 2,299.

## 1,132

1,132

B"H, 28 Tishrei, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your question: If doctors state that it is dangerous for a woman to become pregnant, is it permitted for her to use a *moch* (contraceptive) or similar methods?

This has already been discussed at length by the *Rishonim* and *Acharonim*. Our *Nesi'im* permit it; see *Responsa Tzemach Tzedek*, *Even HaEzer*, end of section 70. There is also a written response regarding this from the son of the *Admur*, the *Maharil*, and I have heard from others that the *Rebbe Rayatz* instructed this in practice (contrary to the opinion of some of the rabbis of Hungary).

I await good news regarding the improvement of your health, that of your wife—may she live and be well—and all your children, may they live.

I conclude with a blessing for true health for each of you.

#### ***1,132***

**To use a *moch*:** See also above, Vol. 4, Letter 1,122, and the references in the notes there. Below, 1,411.

## 1,233

B”H, 28 Tishrei, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R’ Yisrael Yehuda, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification regarding the *upsherenish* of your son, Shalom DovBer, may he live and be well—and due to the matters of the month of Tishrei, time did not permit an earlier response—

I hereby express my blessing that his parents raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, in a state of abundance.

The following is the language of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding the haircut at three years of age:

“...And regarding the cutting of the hair—*upsherenish*—it is a great thing in the custom of Israel, and its essence lies in the education regarding the leaving of the *peios* of the head. From the day of the cutting and the placing of the *peios* of the head, it is customary to be meticulous in accustoming the child to the wearing of *tzitzis*, the morning blessings, *birchas hamazon*, and *krias shema* before retiring to bed. May Hashem be their helper that they raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, with a livelihood in abundance and with peace of mind, both materially and spiritually.”

With blessings for proper health for you and your household, may they live and be well.

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***1,233***

**R’ Yisrael Yehuda, may he live and be well:** Levin.

## 1233

B"H, 30 Tishrei, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

To my great sorrow, I have heard that the misunderstanding between your son, may he be well, and his wife, may she live, has not yet been resolved. My distress is even greater upon hearing that they are still not living together, and that there are even those who speak of a divorce between them.

I find it my duty to write to you, as you surely have influence over your son, so that you may know that this matter concerns your son’s entire life. Consequently, it is also a **life-or-death issue** for you, as his parents. You must involve yourselves in this matter and ensure that there is *shalom bayis* between them, and that they establish a normal life together on their own—not with her parents and not with his parents. In that way, it will be easier for them to solidify their *shalom bayis*, as it should be in a Jewish home.

I have heard the various reasons given for why they are hindered from restoring *shalom bayis*, and I have also heard the reasons your son told me when he was with me. After considering all these reasons, I find it my duty to emphasize that we are dealing here with the life-issue of two young people; one must not allow any extraneous matters to interfere with this.

One must also remember what our holy Torah teaches us: that Hashem said that one may even—in specific cases—erase His holy Name in order to establish *shalom bayis* between a husband and wife. From this alone, one can understand how great is the danger for all those who hinder *shalom bayis*, and how immensely great is the reward for those who help restore *shalom bayis* between a husband and wife.

I believe that for parents, to whom the happiness of a child is surely dear, I need not write more on this matter. I hope that you will do everything possible to bring your son and his wife back together and rebuild their *shalom bayis*. May Hashem help that you should have health and *Yiddishe nachas* from them, and from your other children, may they live.

With blessing.

## 1,234

B"H, 1st of Marcheshvan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of the Yeshivos in Lod and Tel Aviv, may they live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your inquiry conveyed through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, etc., R' Sh. Gurary, may he live, regarding the relationship between the two yeshivos in Lod and Tel Aviv:

My words have already been stated: both must continue to exist, and under no circumstances should the yeshiva in Tel Aviv be closed.

However, on the other hand, the curriculum in both yeshivos must be organized in a way that they are compatible, ensuring a continuation from one to the other without any interruption. And since, apparently, the best resources—both in terms of mashpi'im and students—are in Lod, it should be arranged so that students from the yeshiva in Tel Aviv can transfer and continue their studies at the yeshiva in Lod directly.

With blessings for success in your holy work,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1,035

B"H, 3rd of Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from last Wednesday, and as is your custom in "holy" fashion, you conclude your letter with a request for a blessing for success. It seems that as soon as you crossed the border into Canada, you once again fell into *marah shechorah* (melancholy) in your thoughts. I have already told you several times that you and your wife, *shichyeh*, must put an end to this *marah shechorah*. If there is no other way, it is explained in *Torah Ohr* that *marah shechorah* can be utilized for *hasmadah* (diligence) in Torah study. There is a benefit in this, as it preserves one’s health by avoiding *marah shechorah* over material matters, and it also provides spiritual sustenance through the benefit gained from studying Torah.

I await good news regarding the health of your wife, *tichyeh*, and also that it should be as you wrote—and may it be through *kabbalas ol* (accepting the yoke of Heaven), that you both take upon yourselves to serve Hashem with joy.

With blessings.

## 1,230

B"H, 7 Marcheshvan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and refined, who engages in communal needs with faithfulness, etc., Rabbi N. [Teleshevsky]

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter of 26 Tishrei, in which you describe the positive influence of the visit of the *bochurei chemed*, the *talmidei hatmimim*, to your *shul* this past *Simchas Torah*, and the impression they left upon all the congregants.

I must add that the *yashar koach* due to these *bochurim* is far greater than one might imagine. For them, this visit involved a significant degree of *kabbalas ol*, as they had to leave the *farbrengen* here among the *Chassidei Chabad* and *Anash* to go for several hours to the *batei knesios* and *batei medrash*. Furthermore, they had to do all of this with joy and lightness of heart.

May it be the will of Hashem that the joy of *Zman Simchaseinu* in general, and *Simchas Torah* in particular, be drawn down throughout the entire year. May it be a year of joy, and we rely on the familiar saying, "joy breaks through barriers," that all the barriers, limitations, concealments, and hiddenness in the lives of the sons and daughters of Yisrael be removed, and may it be a good and sweet year, with revealed and manifest goodness in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings.

Enclosed is a booklet on *Chabad* communal activity, which I am sure will interest you.

#### ***1,230***

**Rabbi N.:** Apparently, Teleshevsky. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 4, 883; below, 1,505.

## 137

It has already been brought in other places that there are those who say that regarding whether new insights and additions are possible after death and histalkus, the Rambam and the Raavad disagree. However, it is stated simply in Chassidic discourse in many places in explanation of the verse "You who dwell in the gardens," and in the explanation of the concept of the *mesivta d'rakia* (heavenly academy), that the souls in Gan Eden study Torah.

Nevertheless, there is room for both opinions—and with this, we can also understand how this does not contradict the principle that "it is not in heaven." For the **essence** of Torah —the clarification of a halacha that was not known at all, or whose reasoning was not well understood due to difficulties, etc.—is possible only through a soul clothed in a material body, a "skin of leather". Yet, Torah also exists in heaven, and specifically for those souls who studied it while they were alive on earth—which is the factor that enables them to study the spirituality of the halacha afterward in Gan Eden. Even among the angels it exists, for they too listen (**and are changed** by the listening) to your voice, but not in the same manner as Torah.

***

Regarding the author of the maamar in particular, I am copying here an excerpt from a reshimah of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which reads as follows:

20 Cheshvan.
Today is the birthday of the glory of my father, the holy Rebbe, of blessed memory, who was born on Monday, Chayei Sarah, on the twentieth of the month of Cheshvan, in the year 5621, at the ninth hour of the morning.

In my dream, I saw the glory of my father, the holy Rebbe, in his Shabbos garments and with a very radiant countenance.

And he said: "In this twenty-four-hour period, eighty-four years have been completed since my soul descended into the lower world. I will have good guests, and according to the order, each of our holy Rebbes and ancestors will say a discourse on the chapter of Tehillim 84." End of quote regarding our subject.

— The reshimah is from the year 5705, eighty-four years from the birthday of the author of the maamar, at which point the connection to chapter 84 of Tehillim concludes, as is known regarding the customs of reciting Tehillim, which is a tradition from the Baal Shem Tov. —

Thus, even after the histalkus, there is study and hearing of Torah from the Nesi'im, and a "study" that is dependent on the addition of time below.

**Menachem Schneerson**
7 Cheshvan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 1,339

B"H, 15 Marcheshvan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc.,
R' Moshe HaKohen Sheyevitz, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter from Sunday, Parshas Lech Lecha, along with the enclosed contribution to Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch and Kehot, and the receipts are enclosed herewith.

It is my firm hope that you will bring me good news regarding your health and the health of your wife, may she live and be well, as well as regarding your good work in your communal activities. It is known from our Sages, of blessed memory, that "there is no 'good' other than Torah." This means that an activity is called a "good activity" if it brings about—or at the very least contributes to—the raising of the banner of Torah, both within oneself and in one's surroundings.

And just as the Torah is "longer than the earth and broader than the sea," so too, activities to raise the banner of Torah have no limit. As our Sages, of blessed memory, said, "Whoever adds, they add to him"—meaning that whoever adds to the aforementioned activities is granted additional strength and vigor, as well as the desire and will to continue and increase these activities, both in quality and in quantity.

In a general sense, this is true not only regarding Torah, but also regarding all matters of holiness, for it is a principle in the *sitra d'kedusha* that "we elevate in matters of holiness, and we do not lower." It is known that there are various opinions that the principle of "we elevate in matters of holiness" is a Torah-level obligation.

Based on the above, the story I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, is also understood: When his father was four or five years old, he entered on his birthday (20 Marcheshvan) to receive a blessing from the Tzemach Tzedek, and the *parsha* of the week was *Vayeira*. When he entered, he began to cry. When the Tzemach Tzedek asked him the reason for his tears, he replied that the *parsha* of the week recounts that Hashem appeared to Avraham Avinu, and therefore he, too, yearns for Hashem to appear to him, and that is why he is crying.

The Tzemach Tzedek answered him: "When a Jew is a complete *tzaddik* at ninety-nine years old, and knows that he must circumcise himself, he merits that the Ribono shel Olam should reveal Himself to him."

With wishes for proper health for you and your wife, may she live and be well.

***

**R' Moshe... Sheyevitz:** Additional letters to him appear in Vol. 4, 880, and in the notes referenced there. See below, 1,427; 1,443; 1,487.

**Opinions... Torah-level obligation:** See below, letter 1,527.

**The story:** See at length in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 5, p. 86.

## 1,140

1,140

B"H, 15 Marcheshvan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter from Monday of Parshas Lech Lecha, in which you describe the situation of the elderly, G-d-fearing, and esteemed R... may he live, and ask my opinion regarding the two options available to him: either to live near the shul, or in the house where his two daughters live, but where there is no shul in the vicinity.

At his age, it is important that he be among people, especially since he has been accustomed to this his entire life. Therefore, the first option seems to me the correct one—that is, that they find him a suitable apartment near the shul, and they should endeavor that the other conditions regarding his care, etc., will also be in a manner suitable for him.

Please convey to R... may he live, my heartfelt wishes for long life and good years—good in the literal sense, meaning with peace of mind and physical well-being; and good as interpreted by our Sages, for "there is no 'good' other than Torah and mitzvos," meaning that his days and years should be filled with Torah and mitzvos. And based on what the Rambam, of blessed memory, explained in Hilchos De'os regarding the concept of "In all your ways know Him," which is also cited in Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim, section 231, it is understood that every single moment of a person's life can be filled with Torah and mitzvos, which are the true good.

With blessings,

## 1141

1141

B"H, 15 MarCheshvan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Association of Young Women of Anash in Montreal, may Hashem protect them,

Blessings and peace!

It was with pleasure that I received the letter written by the secretary of your group, Mrs. Chaya Kramer, may she live, in which she writes that elections for officers have taken place and a presidium has been elected, and she requests a blessing for success in your work.

I wish you all, with the officers at the head, that you should continue your work with success, to spread the light of Torah and mitzvos in general, and of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidim in particular—not only within your own homes, but also in your surroundings, so that each of you may serve as a bright lantern (a torch that illuminates the darkness of golus in a certain area around it).

The saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, is well known. He once answered someone who complained that he was all alone in an environment that was not spiritual, and certainly not Chassidic. The Rebbe, my father-in-law, replied to this: When one places a lantern in the street at night, people gather around it.

From this we learn two things: a) That a Yid in general, and a Chassid in particular—man or woman—must not be satisfied with keeping a lantern in their own home, but must take it out into the street as well. b) Not only does this draw people to you, such that you must make an effort to bring them closer, but there will also be specific circles of people who will, of their own accord, gather around the lantern.

May the Ribono shel Olam help that through the additional light that each of you adds in the street, the Ribono shel Olam will add light many times over, so that it should be bright for everyone, both in gashmius and in ruchnius.

With blessings for success in your communal work, and also in your personal matters,

I await good news that you have already begun the work in practice and are already seeing good fruit from your labor.

**The saying:** See also above, Vol. 2, Letter 330. Below, 1152. 1160. 1174.

## 1242

1242

B"H, 20 Marcheshvan, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc.,
Moreinu HaRav Shmuel Menachem Mendel, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

... In response to your notification that on the upcoming 6th of Teves, three years will have passed since the birth of your son—may it be His will that you raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, in comfort and abundance.

Transcribed here is an excerpt from a letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the custom of the three-year haircut, and these are his words:

"... And regarding the cutting of the hair—the *upsherinish*—it is a significant matter in the customs of Yisrael, and its essence lies in the chinuch of leaving the *peios* of the head. From the day of the haircut and the leaving of the *peios* of the head, it is customary to be diligent in accustoming the child to wearing *tzitzis katan*, reciting *birchos hashachar*, *birchas hamazon*, and *krias shema* before retiring. May Hashem be their help that you raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, with livelihood in abundance and peace of mind, both materially and spiritually."

Regarding your question whether to perform the haircut on the birthday or to postpone it until Lag B'Omer: If there is no **established and accepted** custom among *anash* to postpone it until Lag B'Omer, it **does not** seem appropriate to me to delay the haircut and the *chinuch* (as mentioned above in the letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe) for such a long time. This is especially true since there is also a *regel* (festival) in between, and some say (see *Sefer Mahari"d*, Vol. 1, 159b) that this haircut is related to *reishis hagez* (the first of the shearing), which is one of the priestly gifts. At most, you could perform a haircut on Lag B'Omer as well—meaning that would be when the conclusion of the haircut takes place.

With blessings for *mazal tov* and *Chassidishe nachas* from your aforementioned son, may he live, and from all your offspring, may they live.

#### ***1242***

Printed in *Likutei Sichos*, Vol. 7, p. 350, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

**Moreinu HaRav Shmuel Menachem Mendel, may he live:** Schneerson.

1443

The Ribono shel Olam does not remain a debtor, and all those who act and assist in the field of proper chinuch, and especially the participants and helpers of Bais Rivkah, will surely be blessed by Hashem with all that they require, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for much success in their holy work and for an abundance of good, both materially and spiritually.

## 144

B"H, 20 Marcheshvan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received his *pidyon nefesh* regarding the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing and upright, who engages in communal needs with faith, etc., R' Shmuel Dovid Reitzik, may he live.

I would suggest to him that he maintain the three *shiurim* that are appropriate for every person: the recitation of the daily *Tehillim* (according to the monthly division) after *Shacharis* each day; the study of the *Chumash* portion with *Rashi* (from the weekly *parsha*) each day—on Sunday from the beginning of the *sedra* until *Sheni*, on Monday from *Sheni* until *Shlishi*, and so on; and the study of the daily *Tanya* *shiur*, according to the division of *Tanya* for the days of the year. He should also exert himself in the study of *Pnimiyus HaTorah*, which brings one to *ahavah* and *yirah*—which are one's spiritual son and daughter—and this is a *segulah* for children, as the Alter Rebbe wrote (in the letter printed in *Meah Shearim*).

His wife, may she live, should set aside *tzedakah* for the charity of Rabbi Meir Baal HaNes (Rambeh"n) before lighting candles every *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov*.

With blessings.

## 1245

1245

B"H, 21 Marcheshvan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter from Wednesday, Parshas Lech Lecha, in which you write that you have an opportunity to receive a subsidy that was allocated at the convention of [organization name] for [Yeshiva name] and other yeshivos.

You surely know that the Lubavitcher yeshivos have existed for over 50 years, and have always distinguished themselves by being non-partisan and independent of any outside influences or interference, and are characterized by strict yiras-shomayim in every detail.

Through this, the Lubavitcher yeshivos have earned a reputation everywhere—a name that does not merely recall a city, but is a symbol of an entire shita. The main foundations of the shita of the Lubavitcher yeshivos are: to stand firmly on the program that the founder of the yeshiva established, not to yield to the various winds that blow in the street, and not to allow the stamp of any party whatsoever to be placed upon us.

Notwithstanding the fact that this stance has very often made the financial situation of the yeshiva more difficult, for the 54 years since the yeshivos were founded, the greatest effort has always been made not to deviate from the program, even when it involved colossal and permanent subsidies from this or that party.

From this overview of the history and conduct of the Lubavitcher yeshivos, it is also clear what, in my opinion, your stance should be on this question: there can be no question at all about accepting a subsidy from a party, even if the subsidy were colossally large. For this is the opposite of the will of the founders of the yeshivos, whose names and thoughts are dear to us, and which we must uphold with all our strength.

When one also takes into account that, after all calculations, the Baal-Habayis over the income and expenses of an institution is the Ribono shel Olam, a Yid, a believer, cannot entertain the thought that by following the instruction of the yeshiva founders—my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and his father, may their souls be in Eden—the Ribono shel Olam would therefore provide less income for the yeshiva. On the contrary, when one holds firmly to their ways, the Ribono shel Olam will widen the channels and sources to maintain and expand the yeshivos.

With regards to all the staff, and with a blessing for success in their holy work, and all the best in your personal matters as well.

## 1146

1146

B”H, 22 Marcheshvan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of Yeshivas Lod, may they live,

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter, as well as the report from the Yeshiva dated 18 Tishrei, along with the students’ files and their photographs. One can tell at a glance that they are the seed blessed by Hashem. It is a pity that several files are missing photographs; I am sure you will complete this next time.

Photographs are missing from files numbered: 6, 29, 30, 31, 32, 35, 40, 44, 47, 91, 93, 100, 104, 109. From number 109 onwards, the files themselves are also missing.

2) Regarding your question about sending a shaliach, and your writing that it seems from my letter that I am not comfortable with his traveling to certain countries: I do not know upon what this assumption of yours is based. My opinion is only that the institutions must coordinate with one another so that there are no contradictions, confusion, or damage caused by unorganized travel. Surely it is possible to arrange the travel schedules of the various institutions in such a way that the shaliach of your institution will also be able to visit all the countries.

3) Regarding your question about sending a private individual and whether he is capable of being a shaliach: It is difficult for me to express an opinion without knowing him personally. Surely you can clarify on the spot the extent to which he is suited for this mission, and it certainly also depends on which country he is to travel to.

4) In response to your question regarding hiring a special *ram* for the study of *nigleh*: This is very correct, for many reasons, both internally and externally. One must strive greatly not only to elevate the manner of studying Chassidus, but also to elevate the manner of studying *nigleh* so that it should be with *chayus*, with liveliness and warmth. Surely a *ram* who is specifically suited for this will be able to accomplish a great deal in this regard.

5) It is difficult for me from here to express an opinion regarding a private individual, but I am confident that on the spot you will be able to clarify, after observing the influence of this or that *ram* on the students, to what extent he arouses *chayus* in their studies, etc.

6) Regarding your question about the study curriculum: In general, the classes should strive to be close to the curriculum that has existed in Tomchei Temimim since its inception, naturally with the changes necessitated by the conditions of your location at this time (except for the Yemenite children, who require excellent supervision until they become accustomed to the new arrangements, as well as a special approach regarding the study of Chassidus, which is, of course, essential for them as well). I have already raised the matter previously regarding the study of the *maamarim* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

7) Continuing from the above, I will emphasize once again the necessity, in my opinion, of training all the students—at least those who have an affinity for it—in repeating *maamarim* of *Chassidus* in public, and even before *baalei batim* from circles outside of *anash*. I will also emphasize once again the necessity of developing educators and guides from among the Yemenite children themselves.

8) I hope you will fulfill your promise in your letter to also send the files of the Yemenite children, as well as those regarding the staff in the administration. Thank you in advance.

9) I would be interested to know if, for the current school term, you have expanded your enrollment of students, and of what type they are.

Please convey my regards to the esteemed and G-d-fearing individual, who is involved in communal needs, etc., R’ Sh. Gurary, may he live. Surely you have received him, and surely there was also a Chassidishe *farbrengen*, as I spoke with him before he traveled from here.

I hope that the *farbrengen* brought about a strengthening of existing activities, their expansion, and an awakening toward new activities.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and regards to each and every one.

Enclosed is a *kuntres* for 19 Kislev that we have just published.

I believe you have already been informed that the *esrog* you sent was received in due time. Thank you, thank you.

## 1151

By the Grace of G-d
23rd of Marcheshvan, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in his holy work,
Rabbi Michael, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings,

I received your letters in due time, and surely by now you have received all the kuntresim and letters enclosed with them.

... In connection with the upcoming month of Kislev, it is worthwhile to make the necessary preparations to utilize the days of the holidays and the farbrengens of 19 Kislev, 10 Kislev, and the days of Chanukah in an appropriate manner and with proper publicity.

4) It is possible that by these days the translation of the 19 Kislev booklet into Hebrew will be completed here. At that time, a copy will be sent to you so that you may print it locally and distribute it to the necessary places. But, of course, this is not enough, as there must be preparation even in the distant locations by finding suitable people to speak about the significance of the holiday. This should be arranged with Rabbi R. S. [Lipsker], may he live, of Meknes, so that he may inform each of his acquaintances and those he influences regarding the above, with general instructions on what to speak about. Most importantly, focus on practical actions that can be expected of them, both in enrolling students for "Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak" and for strengthening [their commitment].

5) A set of *Sdei Chemed* has been sent to Rabbi Tolidano, may he live, as a gift in appreciation of his participation in our institutions. When he receives it, he will surely be aware of this, and my hope is that this will also serve as assistance in providing him with additional encouragement in our work.

6) Regarding what you wrote about printing in their newspaper and finding someone here to translate it into French: it is very difficult to find such a person here. It would be appropriate to find an expert for this locally, even if it requires some expense beyond the usual; it is worth doing. You can send the translation here before it is printed, and naturally, the translation can be reviewed here as well. It is understood that if you find a translator who has a connection to the newspaper, the translator himself will be interested in having the article printed in the paper. I am specifically urging this now, as it is worthwhile to have at least one article in the newspapers regarding the upcoming 19 Kislev.

7) You surely remember the matter of the seforim, particularly those of the *Chevra Dovevei Siftei Yesheinim*, as well as the very many seforim printed in the city of Djerba (in Kabbalah and other areas of Torah). "One only urges the diligent."

... You have surely also organized the new *Seder Chitas*. It is necessary to gradually publicize this order in those places where you have influence, while, of course, mentioning the name of the founder of this takanah, my father-in-law, the Rebbe. The new *Seder Chitas* for Teves is an appropriate day for this, as it falls between 19 Kislev and Chanukah. 19 Kislev is the Rosh Hashanah for the light of Chassidus, which is the inner dimension of Torah, and the miracle of Chanukah was also with oil, which represents the "secrets of the secrets of the Torah," found in a flask sealed with the seal of the Kohen Gadol, the holy one of Israel—the Rebbe of that generation.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and blessings and success in your personal matters as well.

Enclosed is the kuntres for 20 Cheshvan, which has just been published.

## A'rnav

B"H, 23 Mar-Cheshvan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., Rabbi Nissan Nemanov, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...Enclosed is the Kuntres for 20 Mar-Cheshvan which has just been published, and surely you will merit the public through it in an appropriate manner.

If time permits, I will write more regarding this, but I wish to alert you even now regarding the necessity of preparations for the days of farbrengens in the coming month of Kislev, which are the days of 10 Kislev, 19 Kislev, Chanukah, and the Shabbosim in between.

It would be appropriate to fulfill during this time the concept of "may your springs spread **outward**," which is the theme of these days. That is to say, in addition to the farbrengens that will take place in the homes of anash and especially in the Yeshiva, and in addition to the farbrengen that will be held by all of anash together, it is worthwhile to endeavor to hold farbrengens in the shuls associated with this. Naturally, at every such farbrengen, there should also be representatives from anash and the temimim who can breathe a spirit of life, the life of life, and the life of the life of life (as explained in the letter—printed at the end of the Kuntres for 19 Kislev, which was sent at the time to the late Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, Rabbi Avrohom Eliyahu Plotkin). It is also appropriate to endeavor to publicize the matter in the press and in other suitable ways, so that even those who are completely on the outside will know about the matter of "setting up the lantern." This is subject to the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that when one sets up a lantern in the street, people gather around it. The lesson in this is **twofold**: 1) That one must not be satisfied with the light inside the house, for the purpose of the lantern is to set it up in the street; 2) That besides those whom one must endeavor to bring closer, there are also many, many people whom the very existence of light attracts. I thank you in advance for your notification regarding all of the above.

With blessings for success in your holy work and in the proper path.

1253

B"H, 23 Mar-Cheshvan, 5712

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Vayeira, in which you inform me that you are being pressured to go to the consulate to receive your visa, and that the departure would also be immediate, and you ask for my guidance on how to proceed:

I have already expressed my opinion in the past that they should have looked into relocating to Morocco, which is in close proximity to France. Regarding your specific situation: since you have already submitted the paperwork and received the documents from all the institutions, and they are pressing you to go to the consulate, if you are unable to delay the matter further, go and receive it. May the Ribono shel Olam guide you to your true destination—which is the desire of Hashem—and may things be arranged for you in a manner that is suitable for you, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings,

## 154

154

B"H, 23 Mar-Cheshvan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 12 Cheshvan, in which you write regarding...

...who is currently in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and is having difficulty regarding a shidduch. You suggest that if he were to trim his beard, it would be easier for him to find a shidduch, especially since you see many frum Jews doing so.

It is unnecessary to elaborate at length on the fact that all Jews without exception—men and women, believers, the children of believers—believe and know that the Ribono shel Olam conducts the great world, as well as the small world of every individual person, through Hashgacha Pratis. In order that people should know how to conduct themselves, the Ribono shel Olam gave them the Torah Hakdosha, which indicates the path of what one is permitted to do and what one is forbidden to do throughout the entirety of a person’s life. Among all these mitzvos, there is also the mitzvah of wearing a beard. (There are even some who hold that one is permitted to shave the beard, but even they know that wearing a beard is a mitzvah. However, there are those who hold that one is forbidden to shave the beard, such as the Tzemach Tzedek, a grandson of the Alter Rebbe, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, who rules as halacha that one is forbidden according to Torah to shave the beard.) In any event, it is clear that wearing a beard and not shaving it is a mitzvah, and that this indicates that it is a matter of yiras shamayim.

Consequently, it is understandable that since everything depends on the Ribono shel Olam—and especially in matters of shidduchim, where it is more apparent than in other matters that the Ribono shel Olam is the sole Master—and He, blessed be He, has commanded that wearing a beard and not shaving it is a mitzvah, everyone understands clearly and correctly that a beard cannot be an impediment to a shidduch that is truly his zivug. And if it seems that the beard is hindering the shidduch, this is proof that it is a blessing for him that such a shidduch should not come to fruition. Hashem Yisbarach will provide his true zivug at the proper time, and they will lead a happy Jewish life in the path of Torah and mitzvos.

It would be pleasant for me to hear from you regarding your family: how long have you been in the country, and what are they occupied with?

With blessings.

## 1,255

B"H, 23 Marcheshvan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter of 13 Cheshvan, along with the enclosure from you and the others, and you have surely already received the receipts for this.

You write in your letter that Mrs. ... is sending a donation in memory of her mother. Since it appears to me that she is a friend of yours, perhaps you should draw her attention to the fact that although giving tzedakah is a great mitzvah, this alone is not enough. Just as it is not enough for only one limb of a person to be healthy—rather, all limbs must be healthy—so too, regarding the soul of a Yid, it is not enough that it is healthy in one mitzvah, no matter how great that mitzvah may be. Rather, one must ensure that the entire soul is healthy, which means one must fulfill all the mitzvos, through which one makes the entire soul healthy.

I hope that you will find the appropriate words and language so that if she has been lacking in certain mitzvos until now, from today onward she will also fulfill all the mitzvos that a Jewish daughter is required to perform. May Hashem Yisbarach grant you success so that your words to her will be effective.

When I am at the tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I will mention all of you, each according to what they need. May Hashem help you to report good news, especially regarding your son’s shidduch.

With blessings.

## 1,256

B"H, 23 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have received your detailed letter of the 9th of Cheshvan regarding your travels until your arrival in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), as well as the situation of your family life, and you ask for my opinion regarding your wife (may she live and be well).

My opinion is that you should not think of separating, Heaven forbid, from your wife (may she live and be well). Be strong in your bitachon in Hashem Yisbarach, that He, blessed be He, will send her a refuah and she will return home in good health, and you will be able to raise your children (may they live) together for Torah, chuppah, and maasim tovim.

It is appropriate that your wife (may she live and be well) has been admitted to the hospital, where she will receive the necessary care.

Regarding what you write about your father-in-law and mother-in-law (may they live), it is always difficult to hear grievances from a distance. My opinion is that you should appoint three of our elder Rabbonim from anash, or you and your father-in-law should agree upon one of the Rabbonim, and they—or he—should hear your grievances. They will surely find a way forward. Please ask the Rabbonim to write to me with their opinion on the matter after hearing the arguments from both sides.

I am pleased to hear of your daily schedule of learning, and I would also like to suggest that you memorize sections of Torah, such as the first chapters of Tanya, a maamar Chassidus from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and several chapters of Mishnayos. This way, when you are walking to and from work or the like—and especially when foreign thoughts begin to intrude—you will immediately have words of Torah with which to push away those foreign thoughts, as the saying goes: a little light pushes away much darkness.

With blessings for a speedy refuah for your wife (may she live and be well), and that together with her you may raise all your children (may they live) for Torah, chuppah, and maasim tovim.

## 1,257

1,257

B”H, 23 Mar-Cheshvan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 12th of Mar-Cheshvan, in which you inform me that you have accepted upon yourself and are fulfilling the instructions regarding the *shiurim* and the giving of *tzedakah*, but regarding *shalom bayis*, while externally it has improved, internally it is still not as it should be.

I have already written to you in my previous letter regarding this, that there will certainly be *he'lemim* and *hesterim* specifically regarding the matter of *shalom bayis*. It is precisely in this area that extra effort is necessary, for the abundance of *he'lemim* and *hesterim* proves that this is, in fact, one of your primary *birurim*. This is understood from the writings of the Arizal and is explained in *Chassidus*—see *Kuntres HaAvodah*, end of chapter 6. Aside from unique individuals, the souls of our current generations have already been in this world, and they now come in *gilgul*. The primary purpose of their arrival is to rectify what they lacked in the fulfillment of the 613 *mitzvos* in previous *gilgulim*. Nevertheless, they are, of course, also obligated in the fulfillment of all 613 *mitzvos*, even those they did not lack in their previous *gilgul*. The difference is that regarding those *mitzvos* which they did not lack previously, the *yetzer hara* does not oppose them as strongly—only to the extent necessary to maintain the matter of *bechirah chofshis*, since these matters were already clarified in previous times. This is not the case regarding the matters they lacked in previous times—meaning, where their portion in this world and their portion in the *nefesh* pertaining to these matters were not clarified. In those areas, the opposition of the *yetzer hara* is with full force. There is no need to elaborate on a matter that is explained, etc.

Regarding the practical application—which is the main thing—I will once again awaken and urge you regarding the effort for *shalom bayis* with even greater intensity, even if it requires concessions (since these concessions are not in matters of *Torah* and *mitzvos*). As I have written to you before, our Sages have said that a woman’s tears are easily shed, the gates of tears are never locked, and a man’s blessing comes through his wife.

## 156

B.H., Erev Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all our brethren, the Children of Israel, lovers of Torah and mitzvos,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

We see eye to eye the spiritual and Elokus success that has rested, thank G-d, upon the Tomchei Temimim-Lubavitch yeshivos since their founding fifty years ago by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and the Rebbe, of blessed memory—and continuing until this day.

The Tomchei Temimim-Lubavitch yeshivos have succeeded, with the help of Hashem, in producing thousands of students—may they increase—who are outstanding in Torah and yirah. A large portion of them have served and continue to serve with distinction as Rabbonim, Roshei Yeshivos, Shochtim, and in similar holy positions within important communities in Israel. The vast majority of the students and alumni of the yeshivos, thank G-d, stand in the front lines of avodah and good works in the field of disseminating Torah and yiras shamayim, and strengthening matters of Yiddishkeit in all the places where they reside.

However, despite this spiritual success, the material situation of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim-Lubavitch at this time is extremely difficult and severe. The debts have risen above our heads and are shaking the very existence of this massive, holy institution.

On Sunday, Parshas Va'era, the twenty-second of the month of Teves, 5712, G-d willing, the annual celebration of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim-Lubavitch will take place. This event must serve as an important source of income to remove the burden of past debts and to enable the continued existence of these holy yeshivos in the future.

Therefore, I am turning to all lovers and supporters of Torah and mitzvos with a call and a request—a twofold and threefold request—to assist and participate in the efforts to prepare for this annual celebration, to attend the celebration in large numbers, and to contribute with a generous eye and an open hand for the benefit of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim-Lubavitch. By doing so, you will provide it with the possibility to continue its holy work of raising a generation of upright people who are blessed, engaged in Torah and mitzvos, with pure yiras shamayim and refinement of character according to the teachings of Chassidus.

And it is my prayer that we shall all merit, very soon, the fulfillment of the blessing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in his final letter to the participants of the Tomchei Temimim-Lubavitch yeshivos celebration, which is:

"May Hashem strengthen the health of you all and grant you all a good livelihood in abundance, and may we all, together with our families, merit the raising of the horn of Torah and the horn of Israel, and a near redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, who will lead us upright to our Holy Land, speedily in our days, Amen."

With blessings for goodness, both material and spiritual,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1161

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Rabbis and leaders of Israel,
To the heads of the yeshivos and the heads of the study halls,
May they live.

Peace and blessing!

The nineteenth of Kislev is approaching—a Tuesday (corresponding to the parsha *Es achai anochi mevakesh*, Zohar I, 184a), a day upon which "it was good" was doubled. It is the day of the *yom hilula rabba* of Admur the Maggid of Mezritch—the great disciple and successor of Admur the Baal Shem Tov, whose waters we drink and by whose light we walk.

It is the day of the redemption of Admur HaZaken and the victory of the Torah of Chassidus—the Torah of the Baal Shem Tov—with which the children of **Israel** emerged with a high hand.

The question of the Baal Shem Tov to Moshiach is well known: "When will you come, Master?" and the response of Moshiach Tzidkeinu: "When your teachings become publicized, **revealed in the world, and your wellsprings spread outward.**"

For this is the preface and preparation for the coming of Moshiach.

In light of the holy obligation incumbent upon all of Israel, and especially upon the Rabbis and leaders of Israel and the heads of the houses of study in general, and upon the leaders of the Chassidic community in particular, as well as their great privilege to spread the wellsprings of Chassidus as bequeathed to us by our teacher the Baal Shem Tov, and after him our teacher the Maggid and his disciples, the leaders of the Chassidic community:

I hereby propose that on this bright day, the upcoming 19th of Kislev, and on the Shabbosos preceding and following it, you organize gatherings and *farbrengens* for all those over whom you have influence. In these *farbrengens*, you should specifically inspire them toward the *avodah* of spreading the wellsprings—the wellsprings of the Torah of the Baal Shem Tov, his disciples, and his disciples' disciples—outward. Furthermore, inspire them generally toward setting fixed times for Torah study, the observance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*, brotherly love, and the refinement of character traits according to the teachings of Chassidus.

May the merit of our *Nesi'im*, the leaders of Israel, protect us all, that we may succeed in fulfilling our mission in this world.

And may our eyes behold the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days, *b'agala di'dan*, amen.

With blessings for success and good news,

**Menachem Schneerson**
