## 1762

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Anash, and to all lovers of Torah and Mitzvos, wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

The day of good tidings, the 19th of Kislev, is drawing near. This is the day on which the righteousness of the Alter Rebbe (author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch) was revealed to the world—and with it, the righteousness of the teachings of Chassidus: the teachings of Chabad Chassidus and the teachings of Chassidus in general.

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, wrote in his letter dated the 10th of Kislev, 5710—two months before his passing—that "the study of the teachings of Chassidus is not a matter that pertains only to any particular group; rather, the obligation to study it is incumbent upon all of Klal Yisrael, and upon those who study Torah in particular." And it is an obligation upon Anash to be **engaged** in the dissemination of the study of Chassidus. Engagement means constant, unceasing effort, such that in all of one's affairs—even the peripheral ones—one intends to achieve this goal, "just as in business, where one is occupied with it all day long—not only at the time when one is physically and essentially engaged in the business, because the matter concerns him deeply. He is 'clothed' in it at every hour and at every time."

In another place, it is explained at length how the condition that "your springs be dispersed **outward**"—the springs of the Baal Shem Tov—is the prerequisite, preparation, and vessel for the coming of Moshiach.

This condition, which each and every one of us must strive with all our might to fulfill, contains three details:

1) **"Be dispersed" (Yafutzu):** To teach the study of Chassidus in a manner of *hafatzah*—spreading it over a wide area, so that the study reaches all parts of the place where one teaches this Torah.

2) **"Your springs" (Ma'ayanosecha):** The teachings of Chassidus that one disseminates must retain the characteristics of a spring. There are two primary characteristics of a spring: a) Its waters are living and flow without interruption from the source of the spring. b) One does not pay as much attention to the quantity, for the spring flows from its source drop by drop. So too with the Tanya: in the dissemination of this Torah, quantity is not the primary factor; rather, it is essential that the study be "living"—with the vitality of the soul and internal enthusiasm—and that it flows from its source, from the inner soul of the one disseminating the Torah, who is connected in the depths of his heart to the Nesi'im of the teachings of Chassidus.

3) **"Outward" (Chutzah):** We must not be satisfied with studying only in the beis medrash or the shul, but also while walking on the road, while sitting in the shop, and the like. Similarly, regarding the nature of those who study: one should not be limited to certain groups or specific types of people. The obligation to study the teachings of Chassidus is incumbent even upon the simplest of the simple, and even the greatest of the great cannot reach its ultimate depth.

And even for those who are found outside of all the camps, even in a place that scripture testifies is **"outward"**—even there, one must disseminate the springs.

May the merit of the effort to disseminate the springs outward serve as a vessel to receive the blessings of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, who blessed each and every one of us on the 19th of Kislev, shortly before his passing, saying directly: "May you be blessed by Hashem with a good year in the study and dissemination of Chassidus; you, your households, your sons and your daughters, may they live in the ways of Chassidus; may you, your households, and all who are joined to you be blessed with everything you require, both materially and spiritually."

With blessings for success in this avodah and for an abundance of material and spiritual good.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 1,263

It is recounted that while the Alter Rebbe was imprisoned in the Peter-Pavlovsky fortress, the Maggid and the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory, came to him from the *olam ha-emes*. The Rebbe asked them why this was happening to him and what was being demanded of him. They replied that a *kategor* (prosecutor) had been strengthened against him Above because he was teaching *Chassidus* so extensively and openly. The Rebbe asked them: "If I am released from here, shall I cease teaching *Chassidus*?" They replied: "Since you have begun, you shall not cease; on the contrary, when you leave, you will teach even more." And so it was, for after his release, the Alter Rebbe increased the frequency of his *maamarim*, and the *maamarim* were **longer** and more explanatory, etc.

As is known, before the imprisonment in Petersburg, the "revelation of the light"—the *Chassidus*—was "burning the world," because it was in the category of *makif*. "There was not one person who heard *Chassidus* from him and remained in his previous state." But after Petersburg, it was "in a sequence and gradation within a vessel, with a multitude of words of understanding." It was "the great descent to clothe *Chassidus* in intellect".

When the *kategor* was nullified Above and they agreed upon the new path, the imprisonment Below was naturally nullified as well; he was set free, and the new *hanhagah* began—and this is on the day of 19 Kislev.

And since "on the day that great supernal lights were revealed and shone forth in brilliance, every year on that day, this is repeated, returning and shining, going and shining".

Every year on 19 Kislev, it returns and is awakened and shines, both Above and Below—the victory of the Alter Rebbe’s path and his *shittah*. And with this, it is explained what is written in many places that this day is the *Rosh Hashanah* for *Chassidus*, and it is a *segulah* to be strengthened and encouraged in this.

And in the words of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for this day:

**"Good Yom Tov. May you be inscribed and sealed for a good year in the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus."**

**Menachem Schneerson**

3 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 1,264

1,264

B”H, 3 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

Enclosed is the Kuntres for the festival of our redemption and the salvation of our souls, the day of 19 Kislev, may it come upon us for good, so that you may use it to benefit the many in the most appropriate manner.

The custom is generally that the primary farbrengen of 19 Kislev takes place on the night of 20 Kislev, because the redemption from imprisonment occurred during the time of Mincha, and for three hours thereafter, he was in the residence of the opponent, enduring spiritual suffering, etc.

Nevertheless, in many places, farbrengens are also held on the night of 19 Kislev. May the blessing of the Chassidim rest upon them.

In general, there are two approaches to a farbrengen: a) To organize them in many locations throughout the city, so that those who would not come to another location might also participate. b) To gather all participants in one place, where—in the multitude of people is the King’s glory—the farbrengen will be held with the elders and the greatest of the group, etc.

—Quantity versus quality. The debate regarding which of these is preferable is well known.

An example of this:

See Shabbos 127a: "To minimize walking," "to minimize carrying." Megillah 3a, Tosfos s.v. *mevatlin* at the end. Avos, Chapter 3, Mishnah 15: "Everything is according to the majority of the deed." See also the Commentary on the Mishnah there. And in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 21. And elsewhere. Although, of course, it is not entirely identical to our case. But this is not the place to elaborate.

My suggestion, therefore, is that on the first night, the night of 19 Kislev, they should farbreng in various locations (and announce there about the farbrengen for the following day). And on the following day, the night of 20 Kislev, they should gather in one place for a farbrengen.

It is understood that the main thing is to be inspired with good resolutions, to establish fixed times for the study of the revealed Torah and Chassidus in public, and to strengthen the ways of the Chassidim in the love of fellow Jews.

With the blessing of the festival—awaiting good tidings regarding the above,

**M. Schneerson**

***

1,264

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 18, p. 230, and completed based on a photocopy of the letter, which was sent to various individuals.

**The Kuntres:** Indicated in the note to the previous letter.

**Quantity versus quality:** This is also the concept of "How great are Your works, how profound are Your thoughts" (Torah Or, Maamar *Va'era*—the second one—59b). "Many lights, many vessels" (Matzah Zu, 5667) and elsewhere. **Which of these is preferable:** See Lekach Tov by Mahar"i Engel, Rule 15.

**Good resolutions... fellow Jews:** A letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, at the beginning of the 19 Kislev booklet.

## 1,151

B"H, 3 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter in due time, in which you ask for advice regarding the dreams that are troubling your wife, may she live and be well.

First and foremost, you must have the mezuzos in your home checked. Furthermore, ask your wife, may she live and be well, whether she has inadvertently offended any Jewish man or woman during those days. If there has been any such offense, she should request a general forgiveness in the presence of three Jewish people—that is, she should say: "If I have offended the honor of any Jewish man or woman, whether inadvertently or intentionally, I regret it with a whole heart and ask for forgiveness."

I believe I have already told you that before lighting candles on Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov, she should give tzedakah to the charity of Rabbi Meir Baal HaNess (Rambeh"n), according to her ability—so as not to be a burden upon herself. I am confident that after all of the above, she will find relief, and gradually, all these dreams will depart from her.

It would be appropriate that before sleeping, and before reciting Krias Shema Al HaMitah, she should read a few lines from the memoirs of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, whether in Yiddish or in English—whichever is easier for her.

With blessings for a livelihood in tranquility.

## 1,050

1,050

B"H, 3 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from the 27th of Mar-Cheshvan, in which you describe the state of your wife’s health—may she live and be well—who, according to the doctor, is currently experiencing various issues, and from time to time, bouts of gallbladder trouble, etc., and is now confined to bed with various pains.

In my opinion, it would be worthwhile to find a general practitioner—meaning, even if he is not particularly renowned, he should have knowledge in all areas. You should relate to him the opinions of all the doctors your wife has consulted until now, and ask him to oversee the entire matter and provide her with a general regimen for her conduct, diet, and drink. Since our Sages of blessed memory have said that healing comes through a specific remedy and a specific person, etc., without limitation as to his stature or status, it is very possible that it is precisely a doctor of this nature who will hit the mark for her, and through him, healing will come to your wife—may she live and be well.

With blessings that you should share good news regarding the improvement of your wife’s health—may she live and be well.

## 1,257

B"H, 3 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your *pidyon nefesh* requesting an awakening of Divine mercy for your proper health. When I am at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will read it, that your heart’s desires may be fulfilled for the good in whatever you require.

It is well known that in order to receive blessings from Above, a person must create the appropriate *keilim* below, and the *kli* for receiving every such blessing is Torah.

Therefore, I suggest that you take upon yourself, *bli neder*, to observe the three *shiurim* that are standard for all *anash*, as instituted by my father-in-law, the Rebbe: reciting the daily *shiur* of *Tehillim* every morning after *davening* (according to the division of *Tehillim* for the days of the month); studying the daily portion of *Chumash* from the weekly *parsha* (on Sunday, from the beginning of the *parsha* until *Sheni*; on Monday, from *Sheni* until *Shlishi*, etc.); and the daily *shiur* in *Tanya*, as divided for the days of the year. These will surely be good *keilim* for the drawing down and receiving of the blessing.

I was pleased to read in your letter that you are one of *anash*, and also from a lineage of *anash*, and furthermore, that you were born on 13 Tishrei, which is the *yom hilula* of the Rebbe Maharash. This is certainly a *simana milta*. I am sending you, in a separate envelope, the *Sefer Toldos Maharash*. It would be worthwhile for you to study his *sichos kodesh* with the appropriate depth, as printed in the second part of that volume; this will surely bring light and *chayus* into your Torah study, your performance of *mitzvos*, and your daily life.

With blessings.

## 1,268

B"H, 3 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

You should invest this in your aforementioned business. The saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the words of our Sages, "Whoever takes a *prutah* from Iyov is blessed," is well known; this applies as well to the aforementioned *kupah*, that even a *prutah* brings blessing and success, and in material matters literally.

5) I will be interested to hear what is happening with your brother (may he live), whom you surely see from time to time, and I hope you are endeavoring to bring him closer and closer to Torah and *mitzvos*.

With blessing.

## 1160

B.H., 5 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interval, I have finally received your letter, dated 26 Cheshvan, in which you describe the situation in the city in general, as well as your own personal situation. I hope that by the time you receive this letter, your circle of acquaintances has already expanded, and consequently, you will be able to draw their hearts closer to their Father in Heaven and illuminate them with the light of mitzvah and the light of Torah—specifically, the light of Torah that is the teachings of Chassidus.

The saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is already well-known: when one places a lantern in the street, people gather around it. We learn two things from this: a) That it is not enough to rely on the light found inside the house; one must also place a lantern in the street. b) The measure of good is greater; not only do the people one actively engages with gather around the lantern, but the very existence of the lantern—even when placed in the street in the dead of night and darkness—attracts the people who are in the street. We see tangibly that the greater the darkness, the greater the attractive power of the lantern’s light.

Regarding what you wrote—that due to preparations for your wedding, in a good and auspicious hour, you were forced to discontinue part of your fixed study sessions in Torah—this does not seem right to me at all. On the contrary: if in ordinary days one must strengthen oneself and hold fast (*anhaltan*) to Torah, as it is the conduit and vessel for drawing down and receiving blessing and success, then all the more so is this necessary as a preparation for a wedding. Even if it is true that you are burdened with many concerns regarding the wedding preparations, you should arrange to shorten the duration of your study sessions, but not cancel any fixed study entirely. For we do not know which area of Torah one is in greater need of at any given moment and place, etc.

With this, we can resolve the statement of our Sages in *Eruvin* 54a: "If one suffers from a headache, let him occupy himself with Torah... if one suffers from a sore throat, let him occupy himself with Torah... it shall be a healing." The difficulty is simple: we see that one may suffer from a headache and occupy himself with Torah, yet he is not healed immediately. There are several explanations for this, one of which is that the Torah is a complete structure, as it is written, "This is the Torah of **man**." Consequently, it contains matters that pertain to the head, matters that pertain to the throat, and so on. When one suffers from a headache, he should occupy himself with Torah; if Hashem grants him the merit to encounter the specific part of Torah that pertains to the head, he will be healed. However, not everyone possesses the clear and refined vision to find the specific place in Torah that corresponds to a particular limb.

The same applies to our present case: we do not know which part of Torah is most relevant to your current situation. Since, through *hashgacha pratis*, you have fixed times for study in several areas of Torah, you must hold on to all of them. If it is impossible to maintain them all as before, then you should only shorten the duration of the sessions, but not cancel any of these study sessions entirely.

When I am at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I will mention all those you wrote about in your letter, for whatever they may need.

With blessings for success in your work in the field of education and in your personal affairs, and may your wedding take place in a good and auspicious hour. May you build a home in Israel on the foundations of Torah and mitzvos as explained in the teachings of Chassidus. I will certainly send a letter of blessing for your wedding day, *bli neder*.

Enclosed is a booklet and *kuntres* for 19 Kislev and the general letter; you will surely merit to share them with the many.

With blessings.

## 1051

B"H, 5 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs, etc.,

Greetings and blessings!

You have surely already received the kuntresim and booklets for 19 Kislev and the general circular pertaining to them. As per your suggestion, I am enclosing my letters to the esteemed Rabbi Y. Sabag, as well as to the bochur Shlomo Shushan, may he live.

Regarding your question as to what to name the girls' school: you should name it "Beis Sarah." As for the curriculum, you surely have the curriculum from the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, which includes a special department for a girls' curriculum.

Regarding what you wrote—that the matter of the library has not yet been arranged—this is not correct. You surely have the ability to arrange it in one of the yeshiva halls, at the very least in a proper manner. Aside from the publicity that this brings, we do not know the extent of the influence; it is possible that because a certain person is able to study a Chassidus sefer on a certain day, this will lead to special and great results in several areas. Especially since we know the words of our Sages on the verse, "Lest you weigh the path of life" (Mishlei 5:6)—do not sit and weigh [whether to do a mitzvah or not], etc. The same applies to Torah and those who study Torah, and further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

With blessings, and awaiting good news.

P.S. It is surely unnecessary to remind you once again regarding the seforim.

## 1571

B"H, 5 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the distinguished Rabbi and Chossid, whose fear of Hashem is his treasure, who engages in communal needs with faith,
Rabbi Yitzchak Sabag, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

For some time now, I have been receiving frequent reports from my representative, the distinguished Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, who engages in communal needs with faith, a Rosh Yeshiva and teacher, Rabbi Michael Lipskar, may he live, regarding your dedicated service, which is given over to lofty influence in the holy institutions of Yeshivas Oholei Yosef Yitzchak. You infuse the institution with a spirit of purity and holiness, and you also assist the aforementioned Rabbi Michael in the material affairs of the Yeshiva. It is already well-known that the saying of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe (author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch), is that the physicality of a Yid is itself spirituality. This is also evident in the Rambam, Hilchos Deios, chapter 4, that a healthy body is one of the ways of Hashem. The great value of this influence cannot be sufficiently described, and I am confident that for a person such as yourself, it is unnecessary to elaborate on this. I have come only—relying on the words of our Sages in Sifra, beginning of Parshas Tzav, "One only encourages the encouraged"—to encourage you. This is needed only to add strength and courage to your holy work, to expand and glorify this holy institution, and through you and through us, the Almighty will be praised.

On this occasion, I am enclosing the booklet for 19 Kislev, in which is told the story of the festival, the festival of festivals, 19 Kislev—the liberation and victory of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, who sacrificed his holy soul for the sake of the Torah of Chassidus, to teach the people of Bnei Yisrael the path that ascends to the House of G-d, through love of Hashem, love of Torah, and love of Yisrael. And when we walk in his ways, then "a person who sanctifies himself a little below, they sanctify him much from above," in both physicality and spirituality alike.

I look forward to good, and there is no "good" other than Torah, mitzvos, and the light of Torah, which is the Torah of Chassidus, and I bless you with success in all your affairs.

## 1,074

B"H, 5 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the avreich, Mr. Shlomo Shushan, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to be informed by the brilliant Torah scholar and chossid, the G-d-fearing man who engages in communal needs with faith, our teacher Rabbi Michael Lipskar, may he live, regarding the awakening you inspired while in your city among the Jewish youth, to prevent them from desecrating the holy day. And also that you are continuing your work to prevent them from desecrating the holy Shabbos, Heaven forbid.

The magnitude of this matter is beyond measure. Just as we see tangibly that from one grain sown in the earth, many more grains grow—provided that the sowing is done at the appropriate time, in the appropriate place, and in the appropriate manner—then how much more so is this true in spiritual matters. Even a single action, when performed for the sake of Heaven, produces fruits and the fruits of fruits that are beyond measure, extending to the "end of all the world."

It is known how this is explained in the writings of Chassidus: "to the end of all the world" means that these fruits bring an end and a termination to the "world" (*olam*)—from the root *he'elem* (concealment)—meaning, to that which causes the world to conceal and hide the matters of holiness.

May it be the will of Hashem that you continue your aforementioned activities according to the guidance of the brilliant Torah scholar and chossid, Rabbi Lipskar, may he live. It goes without saying that this should not distract you from your diligence in Torah study, both in the revealed and the hidden aspects. May Hashem grant you success in your studies, in fear of Heaven, and in drawing the hearts of our fellow Jews closer to their Father in Heaven.

With blessings.

## 1513

1513

B.H., 5 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from the end of Tishrei in due time, and I was pleased to read that you are participating in public Torah classes at your shul, specifically the study of Mishnayos and a chapter of Tanya.

Surely you have heard the saying of the Rebbe Maharash, which the Rebbe Rayatz often repeated: "If 'good' is good, then 'better' is not 'better'" [i.e., one should not settle for "good" when "better" is possible]. Therefore, I would like to suggest that you take upon yourself a regular shiur in the study of Gemara. You are surely aware of the statement of the Rebbe Maharash that every person must study Torah Shebichsav with Rashi every day, which includes the contributions of the Midrashim of our Sages and the word of Hashem, Torah Shebaal Peh. As is written in the Laws of Talmud Torah and in Iggeres HaKodesh, at the very least, everyone should complete a masechta of Gemara each year. Surely you have the booklet that was printed for 24 Teves 5711 in your community; please look at the end of that booklet.

It is also appropriate that each week you study some maamarim from the Chassidic sedra—that is, during the winter months from Torah Or, and during the summer months from Likutei Torah, from the maamarim of the weekly parsha. It is well known in many places from our Sages that Torah is the vessel for the drawing down and reception of all blessings, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings.

We learn two things from this: a) that it is impossible to be satisfied with the light that exists inside the house; one must also set up a lantern in the street. b) The measure of goodness is even greater: not only do the people one actively engages with gather around the lantern, but the very existence of the lantern—even when it is in the street in the dead of night and darkness—attracts the people who are in the street. ## 1. Letter

B"H, 5 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure and joy that I received your letter from Monday, Parshas Chayei Sarah. I had already been wondering why I had not received any news from you for such a long time, though I was somewhat reassured by the letter I received from your son, *sh’y*, in which there was a greeting from you.

I am pleased that you have found an apartment, and I hope that you and your wife, *tichyeh*, will feel well there, and that you will be able to utilize this time to properly strengthen your health—*brius haguf* in the literal sense—which, among Jews, also leads to *brius haneshamah*. This is as the Maggid of Mezeritch wrote to his son, R’ Avraham HaMalach, who held fasting and self-affliction in high regard and was generally detached from the physical world. His father, the Maggid, would often argue with him and seek to convince him to serve the Ribono shel Olam in a different way. The father wrote to his son that "a small hole in the body makes a large hole in the soul."

We see this with our own eyes as well: those who wish to serve the Ribono shel Olam without being hindered by the body—such as through weakness and the like—are able to perform their *avodah* with greater perfection.

Furthermore, it is explained in many *seforim* that the body is not the person’s own property, but the Ribono shel Olam’s. Consequently, a person must ensure to guard and maintain the body in a good state (naturally, not at the expense of *hezek haneshamah*). Therefore, according to Jewish law, one who harms himself—who damages his own body—even if he is not punished by a human *beis din* for doing so, is nonetheless liable in *dinei shamayim*. In the words of the Alter Rebbe: "A person has no authority over his body at all to strike it, nor to shame it, nor to cause it any pain, etc., unless it is done by way of *teshuvah*, for this pain is good for him to save his soul from destruction."

I hope that before long you will acquire a circle of acquaintances there, upon whom you will also be able to exert an influence, so that in Florida they may become healthy not only in body but also in *neshamah*.

I am taking this opportunity to enclose the first pamphlet published for 19 Kislev, as well as the *kuntres* for 19 Kislev, where, at the end, several letters from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h nbg"m ziy"a*, are printed.

I wish you, together with your wife, *sh’ti*, to utilize your time in Florida in the best possible way in all details, with enjoyment in both *gashmius* and *ruchnius*.

With blessings.

#### ***1. Letter***

**Maggid wrote:** See *HaTamim*, issue 7, p. 664 [664].

**Alter Rebbe’s words:** *Hilchos Nizkei Guf V’Nefesh*, sec. 4.

## 1505

B.H., 5 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn

...I am not satisfied. As your letter indicates, that *bitachon* in Hashem Yisbarach—which one must expect from a Jewish daughter in general, and a Chassidishe woman in particular—is not present in you to the proper degree. Consequently, this affects your health and also your home.

Every Jew—man and woman—must always remember that Hashem Yisbarach, who leads the great world, undoubtedly leads the small world of each one of us as well. Just as He has a say in the great world, He certainly has a say in the small world. One must rely on Him, knowing for certain that He leads everything toward the good. One should not disrupt this through a lack of firm *bitachon* in Him, *Baruch Hu*, or through matters that are not *al pi Torah*, one of which is *shalom bayis*.

Until the coming of Moshiach, there is no person without a shortcoming. Therefore, it is certain that just as one person has a shortcoming, the other has a shortcoming as well. Just as one does not wish to expose and emphasize one’s own shortcomings, one should not emphasize or magnify the shortcomings of another. This is how it should be among all Jews in general, and especially when it concerns your husband and the father of your child.

I have not come to lecture you, but to draw your attention to the fact that your situation is not as dire as you imagine, and it is not an exceptional case as you think. Each of you must overlook certain things and find better ways to ensure that there is *shalom bayis* between you. When *shalom bayis* prevails, it is the *keli* into which Hashem Yisbarach pours blessing and success, along with good health, *parnassah*, and *nachas* from children.

My opinion is that you should ask your doctor to give you instructions regarding your eating, drinking, and household management, and do as he says. Hashem Yisbarach will surely help you so that everything will be in its time, in a good way, and with success.

With blessing.

## 1027

1027

B"H, 5 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and wise, who conducts himself with piety, etc.,
Moreinu HaRav Elazar Aryeh, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

It is with pleasure that I have learned that, with the help of Hashem, a *melaveh malkah* is being organized for you this coming Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Vayeitzei. It is my hope that all those participating will assist you to the best of their ability, so that you may be able to settle in a suitable manner, enabling you to utilize your strengths in leading a congregation in Yisrael, bringing their hearts closer to their Father in Heaven, with peace of mind and peace of body.

I hereby express my blessing in advance to all those who will participate in this, and I am enclosing my contribution to the aforementioned, together with my blessing that in the near future you may come to your rest and your inheritance in a manner that is good for you, both materially and spiritually.

As the conclusion of Parshas Vayeitzei states: "And Yaakov went on his way, and the angels of Hashem met him... and Yaakov said when he saw them, 'This is the camp of Hashem,' and he called the name of that place Machanayim." Rashi explains that these were two camps—the camp of those outside of Eretz Yisrael and the camp of Eretz Yisrael. The moral lesson to be drawn from this is that even at the very beginning of Yaakov’s journey, "the angels of Hashem met him." As our Sages of blessed memory said: "Open for Me an opening the size of a needle's eye, and I will open for you an opening the size of a great hall." And they "met him"—**two** camps.

The life of a Yid, in general, is divided into two types: the life of Eretz Yisrael—meaning the time dedicated to Torah, tefillah, and the performance of mitzvos—and the life of *chutz la'aretz*—involvement in worldly matters. Even in the latter, one must fulfill the directive to "know Him in all your ways," as explained by the Rambam at the beginning of *Hilchos Deios* and in the *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim*, siman 231. In both of these areas, we require *siyatta d'shmaya*, which is granted to us by our Father in Heaven with a generous eye. This *siyatta d'shmaya* is what gives us the strength and fortitude to fulfill our *shlichus* in this world, which is to illuminate the world and bring it closer to that day of which it is said: "On that day, Hashem will be One and His Name will be One."

With blessings.

1278

## 105

B"H, 7 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...When I am at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will read the Pidyon Nefesh on your behalf. I hope that he—my father-in-law—will arouse great mercy so that your health will begin to improve and continue to get better and better.

Surely you know that to receive a blessing from Hashem, one must have vessels. Therefore, I would like to suggest that you be especially careful to put on Tefillin every day (except for Shabbos and Yom Tov). The Tefillin shel Yad, which is placed against the heart, brings health to the heart, and the Tefillin shel Rosh, which is placed against the brain—which directs the entire body through the nerves—brings health to the entire body. Furthermore, you should recite a few chapters of Tehillim every day, and give a certain amount to Tzedakah every day, without a vow, until the upcoming Pesach. It goes without saying that it is good to give Tzedakah afterwards as well, but at the very least, you should be careful to do this until Pesach. I hope to hear good news from you that your health is improving and that the doctors are satisfied with your state of health.

With blessings for a speedy recovery.

## 1880

7 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Anash in the country of Australia, and foremost among them, the committee involved in the organization of the Yeshivos in Shepparton and Melbourne, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

I received with pleasure your letter dated the 2nd of Cheshvan, which reached me with some delay. In it, you inform me of the decision made at the meeting held in Melbourne regarding the relocation of the Yeshiva from Shepparton to Melbourne. In the meantime, I have also received the news that on the upcoming 10th of Kislev, you will be celebrating the Chanukas Habayis, may it be in a good and auspicious hour.

For the Chanukas Habayis celebration of the Yeshiva on the Yom Geulah of the Mitteler Rebbe, I send my blessing that the merit of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—in whose name the Yeshiva is established—will continue to influence blessing and success in its work to raise a generation of upright individuals. A generation faithful to Torah and mitzvos, and permeated with the spirit of Chassidus, the "light of the Torah." May they fulfill the intention and purpose of the founder of the Yeshiva: to be candles that illuminate their entire surroundings. May Hashem bless all the founders, assistants, and supporters of the Yeshiva, those who have participated in the past and those who will participate in the future, that their participation may bring to them and to all that is theirs blessing and success, to illuminate their homes with goodness, both materially and spiritually.

In order to avoid errors, and primarily so that it may be understood by those participating in the celebration, I have instructed that the content of my blessing be cabled in English. It is a sign of good fortune that the Chanukas Habayis falls on the 10th of Kislev, the day the Mitteler Rebbe was released from his imprisonment; surely the Nesi'im of all generations will cast their shade upon you, and in their merit, all who participate in and assist this sublime endeavor will be blessed with all good, materially and spiritually.

Regarding the theme of the day: I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that two avreichim in Liadi—during the time of the Alter Rebbe—were walking and discussing Chassidus. Upon their return, the Mitteler Rebbe—who was the commander of the avreichim who were sitting [and learning], while R. Aharon of Strashelye was the commander of the older Chassidim—asked them, "What were you discussing?" They answered him: "What the Baal Shem Tov said, that even a falling leaf that rolls along the ground does so through Hashgacha Pratis, with judgment and precision regarding the time and place where it must roll." A few days later, the Mitteler Rebbe told them that he had recounted this before the Alter Rebbe, who replied: "It is not only that Hashgacha Pratis applies to the leaf that is rolling, but also to the modes and causes of its rolling—whether it is by a person, or by the blowing of the wind, and the like."

Let this be your consolation: as you look at yourselves, having been sent to a distant country, etc., etc.—according to what is explained above, this is Hashgacha Pratis in all its modes and details. And since it comes from the Holy One, blessed be He, who is the Essence of Good, and it is the nature of the Good to do good—as is explained in Chassidus and the books of Kabbalah regarding the matter of creation—it is certain and beyond doubt that, in the end, you will see that this is also for the benefit of all who participate and are involved in this, with good that is visible and revealed, both materially and spiritually.

With blessing.

## 1881

By the Grace of Hashem, 8 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from before Rosh Hashanah, which, due to the many preoccupations of the eve of the month of Tishrei and the month of Tishrei itself, etc., my response has been delayed until now.

1) Regarding your note that concerning the *taamim* (cantillation notes) in the Torah, if it is proper to read the verses according to the literal meaning of the text or according to the *taamim*, you had no doubt about this, and the doubt is only regarding one specific case. And it is precisely in this instance that the doubt exists, because according to the rules of the *taamim* in the text, the *taamim* in these verses should have been different from how they are in practice, because one rule is overridden by another rule.

**Response:** The rules of the *taamim*, as I wrote to you in my previous letter, are, for the most part, only the handiwork of man, who compiled them by searching through the *taamim* in the scriptures. In order to resolve the contradictions that exist from place to place, they derived these rules. Consequently, if another person takes an interest in this and can find a rule that resolves all the difficulties in a different way, then it is possible that the previous rule would be nullified, and they would hold by the rule that this person invented (naturally, this applies only to most of the rules of the *taamim*, for some of them are founded upon the "mountains of holiness," and as is known, there are some rules of grammar and musical notation that are rooted in the wisdom of Kabbalah). This is unlike the *Torah Shebe'al Peh*, which was **entrusted** to the discretion of the Torah sages.

The conclusion from the above is that even in the specific case you raised, in my opinion, it is clear that one must read it according to the *taamim*.

2) More than all of the above, even if the aforementioned rules were received as a *Halachah L'Moshe MiSinai*, since the detail that a certain rule is overridden by a second rule is also a *Halachah L'Moshe MiSinai*—that in the place of this specific case, the *taamim* must be according to the second rule—it follows that one must also chant the text in that manner. As I suggested in my previous letter, based on the *Zohar*, the *taamim* were given to chant the scriptures with them, and they are like the *nefesh* and *neshamah* to the body.

3) A supporting point to the above: In other places, it is **explicit** that one should chant differently than the written text (e.g., *pashta*, *zarka*, *tevir*, which are always at the end of a word; *tarcha*, which is always at the beginning of a word; see also *Shemini*, 10:2). This implies that there are no others.

4) Your question as to why one rule is stronger than another, such that it overrides it and not the other way around: as mentioned above, the rules were established based on the reality observed in the scriptures. This compelled the grammarians and masters of the *taamim* to formulate a rule that in a case where two rules contradict one another, we **see** in the text which one is superior and overrides the other. The reason for the overriding, in simple terms, could be that it depends on the beauty of the melody and the pleasantness of the voice.

5) Regarding what you wrote as to why I did not mention the *sugya* in *Nedarim* that discusses the *taamim*: the answer to this is in the letter where I referred to the books cited in *Piku'ei Sadeh*, in which the *sugya* of *Nedarim* is also explained as necessary.

6) I was alarmed to read in the margin of your letter that it has been over a year since you ceased your involvement in educational affairs, except for occasional matters and in a way that would not burden you, as you wrote, **"only on rare occasions."** I am astonished: how, in this day and age, and in the place where you are, where many Jewish children are in danger of spiritual apostasy, *chas v'shalom*, how is it possible to stand on the sidelines and not involve yourself in this with all strength and vigor? Imagine for yourself: if one is standing on the bank of a river studying a deep *sugya* in a place where his heart desires, and he sees someone drowning in the river, he would surely stop his study and engage in saving lives, and he would also be confident in the help of the *Ribono shel Olam* that he is doing what is good and upright in His eyes—(and it has not escaped me what our Sages said regarding Mordechai on the verse, "and acceptable to the majority of his brethren, but not to all his brethren," etc.)—and especially since we are promised by our *Rebbe HaZaken*, who was a *gaon* not only in *Chassidus* but also in the *Nigleh*, and he promised in his book—at the beginning of *Torah Or*—that through engaging in *tzedakah*, one's mind and heart become a thousand times purer. And it is understood that the *sefer Torah Or* is not a book of flowery rhetoric, and its meaning is literal: that then one succeeds in study a thousand times more. Therefore, it is simple that this is not a loss in study, but on the contrary, one gains through this work of saving lives, such that his study in a short time will be with *siyata d'shmaya*, and he will succeed in *Torah study* a thousand times more. I think it is unnecessary to elaborate on this, for the matters in all of the above are well-known, and surely you will rectify this after reflecting on it once more. May the *Ribono shel Olam* guide you on the path of truth, which is also the path of our Torah—the Torah of truth and the Torah of life.

... In connection with the arrival of the "Festival of Festivals," 19 Kislev, I am enclosing the booklet and the *kuntres* for 19 Kislev, along with a copy of the general letter pertaining to this.

With blessings.

## 1,283

Brooklyn.

I received your letter with the *pidyon nefesh* dated the beginning of the month of Kislev, in which you ask for forgiveness for not having written until now.

Regarding this, I do not see any place here for a request for forgiveness for not writing. Furthermore, since you have already been stirred to write, you fail to mention the main point with which you should have begun: the matter of your *kvi'us itim* for Torah—both in *nigleh* and in *Chassidus*—and your influence upon your surroundings. This is in accordance with the demands of our *Nasi* upon each and every one of us to be "candles to illuminate." Since you are in a place upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year, all these matters must surely be carried out with even greater intensity and strength. I am certain that in your next letter you will also report on all of the above, as well as on your activities regarding *hafotzas hama'ayanos chutzah* during this month of redemption, the month of Kislev.

With blessings for an abundance of *nachas*—*Yiddishen Chassidishen nachas*—from all your children *shiy*, and *Chassidishen nachas* from you and your wife *shichyu*.

## 1,484

B”H, 10 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

To [Name]... may she live,

Blessings and peace!

I received your letter of a few lines—without an indication of when it was written—and as you requested, I will mention you when I am at the tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

I was surprised to read in your letter, “if, Heaven forbid, an unpleasant event should occur, etc.” It is unnecessary to elaborate on the importance of the quality of bitachon, how essential it is in general, and especially according to our religion and Torah, and all the more so now, when we, the remnant of the survivors, are living proofs of open miracles in our very existence. Furthermore, this thought itself—what will be if, Heaven forbid, a bitter event occurs—is in itself a bitter event.

In these days of ours, when there is a vast field for great avodah in every single area, and we see tangibly how the work is great and the time is short, it is a pity to waste the spiritual strength and energy that are being used and lost in connection with the aforementioned thoughts, at a time when they are so needed for the work of foundation and building. Especially for all those in whom the strengths of many generations of distinguished individuals have been invested as an inheritance, it is a grave sin to spend even a moment not using these strengths for the aforementioned purpose. And if this is true for those who are older, then all the more so regarding those who have just established a home in Yisrael—they have no right to calculate what will be, etc., at a time when the Master of the House is pressing, and even though you are not obligated to complete the work, you are not free to desist from it.

I trust you are taking part in the appropriate manner in the work of kosher chinuch in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt, where the situation is most critical, dangerous, and vital.

Give my regards to your husband, may he live, even though I do not know him, with a blessing to fulfill in practice the motto of the Baal Shem Tov: “Serve Hashem with joy,” and in accordance with the teachings of our religion that every moment of life is an avodah to Hashem.

## 1885

1885

B”H, 10 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-scholar, and communal activist,
Rabbi Moshe, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

From time to time, I receive news about you from those who come here from your region, and I was pleased to hear that you are taking part in communal affairs and are striving to support the foundations of Torah and Yiddishkeit in your area.

I am writing to you now regarding a pressing matter: the education of the younger generation. According to the reports I receive regarding what is happening in Philadelphia, the youth are drifting further away day by day. If more than the usual measures are not taken, then, G-d forbid, there is reason to fear—as I am told—that the entire younger generation, with the exception of a few select individuals, will, G-d forbid, become estranged from Torah and mitzvos.

Based on the words of our Sages (Sifra, beginning of Parshas Tzav), “One only urges those who are already diligent,” I am hereby awakening and encouraging you, with every possible expression of encouragement and strengthening, to delve into the matter of education in the city of Philadelphia with the appropriate attention. Do everything possible and everything within your power to improve the situation and thereby save the souls of the sons and daughters of Yisrael from descending into the pit, G-d forbid. It is a well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that an effort in *taamulah* (outreach/propaganda) never returns empty.

I am certain that for a person of your stature, further elaboration on this is unnecessary. I will be grateful if you inform us of good news, that you have begun the work in practice, and may it be the will of Hashem that the desire of Hashem will succeed in your hands.

I am writing regarding this matter to Rabbi Popack as well, and I have also spoken in person with Rabbi and Chossid, Rabbi Shneur Zalman Schneiderman. There is salvation in a multitude of counselors, especially since the youth of Philadelphia—whose fate hangs in the balance—are with them.

Enclosed is a booklet and a *kuntres* for 19 Kislev that has just been published, and I am sure you will use them to benefit the many.

With blessing.

## 1,286

Brooklyn

According to the information reaching me regarding the state of chinuch in the city of Philadelphia, it is declining from day to day. I wish to draw your attention to this issue, and I am confident that you will seek, and surely find, the appropriate means to improve the situation as much as possible. It goes without saying that "better one hour sooner," for if "you abandon it for a day, it will abandon you for two." If this is said regarding the study of Torah, then how much more so regarding matters of Yiddishkeit and yiras shamayim, especially concerning the boys and girls of our people, the younger generation, which is the future of our entire nation.

Thank you in advance if you will inform me of your perspective on the above, as well as the measures you intend to take in this matter.

With blessings and respect.

## 1887

1887

B"H, 12 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-scholar, and communal activist,
Rabbi Yitzchak, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

The esteemed Chossid, the G-d-fearing, Torah-scholar, and communal activist, a man of good deeds for the strengthening of the *Torah Temimah*, etc., Rabbi Yosef HaLevi Weinberg, may he live, has departed these days for your country on a mission from the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch.

During his visit here, your honor was able to see and know of the activities of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim in the field of disseminating Torah and pure *yiras shamayim* in your city.

Therefore, I am turning to you, in accordance with the words of our Sages (Sifra, beginning of Parshas Tzav), "One only urges those who are already diligent," with a request to exert every possible effort to assist Rabbi Yosef HaLevi Weinberg, may he live, so that he may succeed in his aforementioned important mission. I am certain that for someone like you, there is no need to explain the magnitude of the matter of supporting the *Torah Temimah* with *yiras shamayim* at all times, and especially in this time of *ikvesa d'Meshicha*, when "the wisdom of the scribes" (though it exists, yet) "has become putrid"—like something lacking vitality—because "those who fear sin are despised" (as our Sages state in Shabbos 31a: "a measure of wormwood... and it becomes worm-eaten"). The reason for this disdain is that "the truth"—as the verse says, "And Hashem commanded us to perform all these statutes—and *Talmud Torah* is included among them—to fear Hashem our G-d"—is missing.

I am interested to hear about the continuation of what we discussed while you were here, and that you have settled in well.

With blessings for success in your general and personal matters.

P.S. Enclosed is the booklet published for the upcoming Yud-Tes Kislev.

## 1288

B"H, 12 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, who engages in communal needs with faith, a man of fine character, etc., R' Yirmiyah, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

My previous letter, along with the Kuntres and the booklet for the upcoming 19 Kislev, have surely arrived by now.

Relying on our Sages' teaching (Sifra, beginning of Parshas Tzav) that "one only urges those who are already diligent," I am adding to this letter—not out of necessity, but to encourage further effort. It is this:

We see with our own eyes the spiritual and Divine success that has rested, thank G-d, upon the Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch Yeshivos since their founding, these "hen" (55) years ago—(hen, a singular unit, "Behold, the fear of Hashem, that is wisdom," see Shabbos 31b)—by the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, and my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, until this day.

Today, the financial situation of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim is difficult. The debts have mounted, and they are shaking the very existence of this immense institution.

The esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, who engages in communal needs, etc., R' Yosef, may he live, HaLevi Weinberg, has traveled to your region to conduct the fundraising campaign on behalf of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim.

I am writing to you with a twofold request: to exert every effort to ensure that the visit of R' Yosef, may he live, is met with outstanding success, and that it brings the necessary and hoped-for assistance to enable the Merkaz to continue its work of raising a generation of upright descendants who engage in Torah and mitzvos with pure fear of Heaven and with the refinement of character according to the teachings of Chassidus.

Great is the merit of this, to draw down for you, your family—may they live—and for all who assist through you, an abundance of life and manifold blessing in all your general and personal affairs.

With blessings.

## 1889

B"H, 12 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Rabbi, the Gaon, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished scholar, a man of many accomplishments, etc., Moreinu HaRav Levi Yitzchak, may he live, Chief Rabbi,

Greetings and blessings!

I am writing to you regarding a current matter:

We see with our own eyes the spiritual and Divine success that, thank G-d, has rested upon the Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch Yeshivos since their founding fifty-eight years ago, until this day.

With the help of Hashem, these Yeshivos have succeeded in producing thousands of students—may they increase—who are outstanding in Torah and yirah. A large portion of them have served and continue to serve with distinction in holy positions within important communities in Eretz Yisrael, and the majority of the students and alumni of the Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch Yeshivos stand in the front lines of avodah and good works in the field of disseminating Torah and yiras shamayim, and strengthening the matters of Yiddishkeit in their places of residence—often to the point of mesiras nefesh.

However, despite this spiritual success, the material situation of the Tomchei Temimim Yeshivos center at this time is difficult and grave; the debts have mounted and are threatening the very existence of this massive institution.

In connection with this, the shaliach, the distinguished and G-d-fearing scholar, a man of fine character, etc., Moreinu HaRav Yosef, may he live, HaLevi Weinberg, has departed in these days for Africa, on a mission for the Tomchei Temimim Yeshivos center.

I am hereby requesting that your honor, may he live, assist him in every possible way, so that he may succeed in his mission to bring the hoped-for help and support to this massive institution.

The magnitude of the mitzvah of supporting the study of pure Torah certainly requires no explanation for one such as you. May it be the will of Hashem that in our near future we will see the raising of the banner of Torah and the banner of the elder Israel, until our righteous Moshiach comes, and "the earth will be filled with the knowledge of Hashem," etc., speedily and in our days.

With blessings and appreciation.

P.S. Regarding the subject of the parsha and the matter of mesiras nefesh:

It is known that there are two opinions regarding the source of the law that a thirteen-year-old is obligated in mitzvos: 1) The opinion of Rashi (Nazir 29b) s.v. *v'Rabbi Yosi*, that we find that Scripture calls a thirteen-year-old an "ish" (man), as it is written, "The two sons of Yaakov, Shimon and Levi, took each man (ish) his sword," and this is also found in the Machzor Vitry on Avos at the end of the chapter. The intention here is that the title "ish" denotes maturity, as it is written, "Who made you a man (ish)?" (see Rashi and Rabbeinu Bachya there; this is unlike what is written in Shemos Rabbah there), and "You shall become a man (ish)," and so on. 2) The opinion of the Rosh (in his Responsa, beginning of Klal 16) that this is included in the category of *shiurin* (measurements) which are a Halacha L'Moshe MiSinai.

One could suggest a practical difference between these two opinions regarding the laws of a Ben Noach: according to the first opinion, a Ben Noach also becomes obligated in his mitzvos at thirteen, whereas according to the second opinion, he does not (see Rambam, Hilchos Melachim, ch. 9, law 10; ch. 10, law 2; Responsa Chasam Sofer, Yoreh Deah, sec. 317).

That is to say, according to the second opinion, it is a decree of Torah, but according to the first opinion, it is the natural state—in the majority of cases—that a thirteen-year-old becomes mature in intellect and understanding.

One can hint at a moral lesson here: that the proof for the obligation in mitzvos is derived from the verse "they took... each man (ish)"—a proof whose foundation is that, according to logic and intellect, it should be so.

Yet, the verse writes its own refutation alongside it, so that one should not say that a lifestyle based on logic and intellect is sufficient for the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos. Therefore, they point it out to him:

See and contemplate what the sons of Yaakov did: "Each man took his sword"—immediately upon their obligation in mitzvos, they began with the avodah of mesiras nefesh specifically.

1290

With blessings.

## 1191

B.H., 13 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the administrations of Chabad institutions in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt,
To whom this may concern,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your inquiry regarding my opinion on the structure and management of the institutions:

I have already expressed my opinion and written about this at some length in my letter to Agudas Chabad dated 24 Sivan, 5711. I will reiterate it here with further clarification, or at the very least, in brief.

Generally, there are two distinct categories: a. Internal matters, and b. External matters.

a. Regarding internal matters: In my opinion, it is proper and correct that each institution should have its own autonomy and maintain a direct connection with here [the Rebbe’s office]. It is understood that this does not preclude the existence of a form of control or oversight by an individual or institution over another, provided that this oversight function also maintains a direct connection with here.

b. This is not the case regarding external matters. In many areas, it is necessary—and in many others, at the very least, it is beneficial—that there be one representative for all the institutions. This role belongs to Agudas Chabad; that is, Agudas Chabad should represent all the institutions in the Holy Land that bear the Chabad stamp to the outside world in any matter that requires it.

I emphasize "that bear the Chabad stamp," because there are matters in which Anash must act in the Holy Land as neutral parties, rather than as representatives of Chabad, and in such cases, the intervention of Agudas Chabad might be counterproductive.

c. It follows from the above that since Agudas Chabad must represent the various institutions to the outside world, it is necessary that the administration of Agudas Chabad include a representative from each and every institution. Based on what you have written regarding the members of the Agudas Chabad administration, there is indeed a representative from each institution on the board.

d. Agudas Chabad does not intervene by issuing commands in the internal affairs of each institution (unlike offering advice, which the institution's administration is free to accept or reject).

e. Regarding the members of the institutions' administrations, for the time being, I **propose** that they be: ...

f. **Oversight and Control.** It goes without saying that the control and oversight must be permeated with *ahavas chassidim* and brotherly love. As the individuals for oversight, for the time being, I **propose**: ...

g. The role of the oversight is to offer advice, to examine, and to maintain a direct connection with here and report on what is happening in the institution, but it does not have the authority to overturn a decision of the administration.

h. It goes without saying that the responsibility rests with the administration of each and every institution, and it must take all necessary steps for the maintenance and development of the institution.

- Seemingly, this is a simple matter, yet I am compelled to write it explicitly, as there are some institutions that are deteriorating, and it appears the administration is sitting idly by, responding with the quote from the Mishnah: "What is this trouble to us?" The magnitude of the negligence in such a response is clear and requires no proof. *V'd"l* (and to the wise, a word is sufficient).

I request that each of the aforementioned institutions, after reading and discussing all that is stated herein, confirm receipt of this letter and inform me of their comments and of all actions taken regarding the above.

With blessings for success in your holy work,

**M. Schneerson**

***

**From 24 Sivan:** See above, Vol. 4, 1064.

## 1,192

B"H, Chag HaGeulah, 19 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

With many thanks, I hereby acknowledge receipt of the books that you kindly sent to my library, which are: [list of books].

In such matters, the more one adds, the more praiseworthy it is. May the Master of Peace bestow peace, goodness, and blessing upon your honor, shlita, in both material and spiritual matters.

In honor of the Chag HaGeulah of our Rabbeinu HaZaken, the Rebbe, Rabbeinu Schneur Zalman, may his merit protect us, the founder of the Chabad Chassidic path, I sent my blessing to your honor via telegram: "A joyous day for the Chag HaGeulah of our Rabbeinu, the Baal HaTanya, and the victory of the Torah of Chassidus; may his merit protect us all, together with all of Klal Yisrael. May you succeed in your holy avodah."

It is well known that Rabbeinu HaZaken, the master of the celebration, stated that the Torah of Chassidus is not the inheritance of individuals or a specific party, but rather an inheritance for all of the Jewish people. This is as in the well-known letter of the Baal Shem Tov, who ascended in his soul on Rosh Hashanah and entered the chamber of Mashiach, asking him, "When will the Master come?" to which he replied, "When your wellsprings spread outward."

Thus, every matter and action that assists in the spreading of the wellsprings of the Torah of Chassidus—the "light within the Torah"—is a preparation for and hastens the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days and in the near future, amen, may it be His will.

May there be peace for your honor and your Torah; may your strength in Torah study increase, and may you succeed in all the works of your hands for good and for blessing, in both material and spiritual matters.

## 1,193

1,193

B"H, 19 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter, and I am pleased to hear that your pains have almost passed; I hope that you will feel even better.

Regarding what you write—that your daughter, may she live, is embittered by the fact that her children are not conducting themselves in a Jewish manner:

Tell her that bitterness alone does not help. Rather, she must influence them, and only through kind ways, gentle words, and requests. She must not grow weary of speaking about this—once, twice, three times—until, in the end, she makes an impact; first a little, and later, more and more.

You also write that your daughter’s son, may he live, is about to get married. You **must** and **need** to speak with his kallah, so that she will conduct herself as a Jewish daughter should, specifically regarding taharas hamishpachah, kashrus, and keeping Shabbos. Help her understand that her own happiness, as well as the happiness of her chassan and the children they will have, depends upon her conduct. When one believes in Hashem Yisbarach, one eventually sees with physical eyes as well that this has brought goodness, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for good health and Yiddishe nachas from children and grandchildren.

## 1,294

B"H, 19 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and honest merchant, R' Yaakov HaKohen, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I have received your letter of 17 Kislev, along with the enclosed *pidyon nefesh* for...

Regarding *shalom bayis*: When I visit the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention her for the aforementioned.

You do not provide any details about her. I hope that she conducts a Jewish home, and I only wish to suggest that she have the *mezuzos* in her home checked as soon as possible. Furthermore, each time before lighting candles on *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov*, she should give *tzedakah* to the *kupah* of Rabbi Meir Baal HaNes. I hope that in time—and especially once they both resolve that sometimes one must yield, for through giving a little one can gain everything—she will soon be able to report good news that the *shalom bayis* is improving.

I was pleased to read in your letter that you are ensuring that the study of *Mishnayos* is maintained at the Anshei Shalom shul. However, regarding what you wrote—that your family is unhappy about this because it causes the *seudah* to be late—my opinion is that you should find someone else to take on the responsibility of teaching the *olam*. There is another reason for this: one should not discourage a shul from paying for public study (if they previously paid for it), especially in America, where paying for it gives it greater importance.

You have surely received the *kuntres* for 19 Kislev and the *michtav klali* associated with it. I hope you held a *farbrengen*—as my father-in-law, the Rebbe, writes—a *Chassidishe farbrengen*. May Hashem help us all that 19 Kislev, which is the *Rosh Hashanah* for *Chassidus*, should see the blessing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, fulfilled in us: "May you be inscribed and sealed for a good year in the study of *Chassidus* and the ways of *Chassidus*."

With blessing.

## 1,295

1,295

B”H, 19 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification that your wife, may she live and be well, has given birth to a son, mazal tov, I hereby express my blessing: May you raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, with peace of mind and peace of body.

Regarding your question concerning the naming of your newborn son, may he live and be well, you have heard several times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that he does not involve himself in this matter. Whatever name the parents agree upon, may it be for long days. I sent you a telegram today which reads: “Mazal tov, he and his wife should choose the name, and may Hashem bless him with long and good days and years.”

With blessings of mazal tov on the day of our redemption and the liberation of our souls.
