## 1,297

B"H, 20 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of Yeshivas Lod in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

When the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, a man of intellect and good deeds, a man of many virtues who engages in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Eliyahu, may he live, known as Dr. Young, visited me, he informed me that the Joint Distribution Committee’s program includes support for vocational schools that are operated by **Yeshivos** in the Holy Land and constitute a part of them.

He added that he spoke with you regarding this matter—namely, that Yeshivas Lod should open a department for the study of crafts and trades—and you replied that you would ask for my opinion on the matter.

In response to this question:

It is impossible to change the order of the Tomchei Temimim Yeshivos, wherever they may be, from the manner and program outlined by their founders and leaders, the Rebbe (Rashab) and my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Since this is the case, it is impossible to include classes for the study of crafts and trades within the Yeshiva itself.

However, on the other hand, since there are several avreichim and bochurim whom, for various reasons, it is impossible to integrate and keep in the Yeshiva for the **entire** day, but who would study Nigleh and Chassidus for several hours a day—on the condition that they also be taught a craft or trade—this is highly appropriate. One should strive for the above, ensuring they remain under the **constant** supervision and influence of the Yeshiva. This is possible by establishing a special institution for the study of Nigleh and Chassidus, as well as crafts and trades, which would stand under the sponsorship, supervision, and administration of the Yeshiva. Surely, such an institution would bring great benefit to many bochurim and avreichim.

According to my conversation with Rabbi Young, may he live, he will exert all his efforts to ensure that the question of the expenses involved will be resolved by the Joint.

Since Rabbi Young, may he live, has significant influence within the Joint, it is to be hoped that the Joint will fulfill this request in its entirety.

I await your detailed letter regarding the above (which craft, the program, the budget, etc.), and the sooner this is done, the better.

- Seemingly, it is good that the institution should be in the village, but under your administration.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1298

1298

B”H, 21 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Y. [Yosef], may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your telegram—and surely you will write more details regarding the farbrengen of Chag HaGeulah—see the booklet for Yud-Tes Kislev, page 4, footnote 3—

I sent a telegram today to the Chief Rabbi, and this is its text:

"For the Bar Mitzvah of his son, may it be His will that he raise him for Torah—'Yaakov dwelling in the tents of Shem and Eiver'; for the chuppah—Yitzchak, who was bound on Mount Moriah, the Beis HaMikdash; and for good deeds—Avraham, who performs acts of kindness; the three branches of the vine of Yisrael. With blessings of Mazal Tov." [Followed by] the signature.

And by way of a note and reference:

**For Torah—Yaakov dwelling in the tents of Shem and Eiver:** This refers to the study of Torah, as explained in *Ohr HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek, Parshas Toldos, on the maamar beginning "Dwelling in tents": Shem—the Written Torah, the names of Hashem; Eiver—the Oral Torah, according to the verse "And he passed (*avar*) before them," the drawing down and revelation of the Torah, which is accomplished through the Oral Torah.

**For the chuppah—Yitzchak, etc., in the Beis HaMikdash:** Based on our Sages in *Midrash Shir HaShirim Zuta* at the end (see also *Zohar* Vol. III, 4b; in the Mishnah at the end of *Taanis*): "On the day of his wedding"—when the Shechinah descended to the Beis HaMikdash, which is the chuppah of Hashem and Yisrael together. And therefore, the matter of Yitzchak’s marriage is explained in such detail specifically, unlike that of Avraham and Yaakov.

**For good deeds—Avraham, who performs acts of kindness:** As it is said, "For I have known him, to the end that he may command his children and his household after him... to do charity," which is the essence of the practical mitzvos and transcends them all, etc. (*Tanya*, Chapter 37).

**The three branches of the vine of Yisrael:** Based on our Sages in *Chullin* 92a.

It is worth noting the letter I wrote to the Chief Rabbi in connection with the trip of the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, occupied with communal needs, a man of character, etc., Rabbi Yosef, may he live, Weinberg, the shaliach (12 Kislev), where the subject of a Bar Mitzvah is also discussed.

***

**Rabbi Y.:** Eliyahu. Another letter to him—above, 1288.

**To the Chief Rabbi:** Moreinu HaRav Levi Yitzchak Rabinowitz, mentioned above—letter 1289 to him.

**For Torah—Yaakov:** See also below, letter 1310.

## 199

B"H, 22 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your request to become a Chossid: The path has already been paved by our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, may the merit of their holy souls protect us—how to become a Chossid. This is achieved through the study of Chassidus and by conducting oneself in the ways of Chassidim. Most importantly, it is achieved by "rubbing shoulders" with other Chassidim, for "serving [the wise] is greater than studying [from them]." When one does all of the above to the best of their ability, all the concealments and obstructions are removed, and one is granted Siyata Dishmaya to become a true Chossid, connected to the Tree of Life.

With blessings for success in all that you do regarding the above.

## 1,100

B"H, 22 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Tzvi Hirsch
May he live.

Greetings and blessings!

On the occasion of his wedding, in a good and auspicious hour, with his bride, may she live, I hereby express my blessing—a blessing of Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov—that it should be in a good and auspicious hour, and that they may build a home in Israel upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, as they are explained in the teachings of Chassidus.

In response to your request for guidance for the bride, may she live, regarding some spiritual preparation for her wedding: I have not heard a definitive tradition regarding this, but I know that it is customary to recite several chapters of Tehillim, though it is not clear to me which chapters. Therefore, when I am asked about this, I instruct the bride to recite the entire book of Tehillim on the day of the wedding. It is understood that this is in addition to knowing the halachos that apply to her, which is, after all, the main thing, as the Zohar states, "Action is supreme."

At the farbrengen of the "Holiday of Holidays," 19 Kislev, you were mentioned for good, for blessing, and for Mazal Tov.

Regarding specific guidance for you: You are surely aware that one wears a kittel under the chuppah, though it is worn beneath the outer garment so that it does not create a bulge (and on the Yom Kippur of the year of the wedding, one does not wear the kittel, since he has already worn it on the Yom Kippur of that year, which is his wedding day).

Likewise, one makes an effort that at the time of the kiddushin, there should be no gold or silver valuables or coins in one's pockets. Furthermore, there should be no knots upon one's person; that is, one unties the necktie and shoelaces, and the like. It is understood that this is in addition to the customs accepted throughout all the dispersions of Israel regarding other matters, such as reciting the Mincha prayer with the addition of "Al Chet," etc. May it be His will that it should be in a good and auspicious hour in all details.

With the blessing of Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov.

**M. Schneerson**

## 101

B.H., 22 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter of 13 Kislev, in which you confirm receipt of my letter and mention that, thank G-d, you are feeling healthy and are more or less satisfied with your current situation.

In your letter, you write that there are 26 other Jewish bochurim with you who are currently unaffiliated (in terms of Torah and mitzvos). You are surely doing as much as you can to bring them closer to Torah and mitzvos so that they will actually perform them in practice. You must not be discouraged by the excuses they give you; on the contrary, this only shows how great the pity is for them. When one speaks with them, one eventually has an effect on them—at first a little, and later, more and more. Especially regarding the laying of tefillin, you should explain to them that besides this being one of the mitzvos of Hashem Yisbarach, it is also a segulah for long life. Just as in the military, one learns how to conduct oneself to avoid harm, G-d forbid, and one who does not learn this brings damage upon himself and also acts against the government, so too, every Jewish soldier has his means of protection. One of them is the laying of tefillin. When it is not possible to lay tefillin in the morning during the time of davening, they can at least do so throughout the entire day, until sunset. I hope that you will find the appropriate words to influence your Jewish comrades.

The calculations of Hashem Yisbarach cannot be known, and it is possible that this is one of the reasons why one is kept in a certain place. When he fulfills this, it is possible that he will then return home, with the consent of the government.

On the occasion of the Yom Tov of Chanukah, enclosed is the publication from Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch which was released in connection with Chanukah. I expect that you will be able to explain to your comrades, with additional explanations regarding Chanukah, that the lesson for us all is that we must all, without exception, study Torah and perform mitzvos, without taking into account any obstacles.

With blessings.

## 122

122

B.H., 22 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Toldos, in which you ask about the path for beginning the study of Chassidus, and also whether there is a structured work in Da"Ch regarding the Seder Hishtalshelus.

1) Regarding your request for a suggested order for beginning your studies, it is difficult to answer this without knowing your background and the path of study to which you have an affinity, your current knowledge of Chassidus, etc. However, a general answer that is suitable for the vast majority is that, in addition to studying Tanya, you should study *Derech Mitzvosecha* (also called *Sefer HaMitzvos*) by the Tzemach Tzedek. As with study in other parts of Torah, for the first time through, do not delay to understand every single word; rather, focus on the general concepts. Once you have studied it in a manner of "just reading through" once or twice, and you have acquired a knowledge—even if superficial, yet comprehensive—of many topics, you will then be able to be precise regarding the details and the specific wording.

2) Regarding your question as to whether there is a book in Da"Ch that explains the Seder Hishtalshelus, such a book is *Shaar HaYichud* by the Mitteler Rebbe, and at its beginning, he also explains the method of *hisbonenus*.

3) The verse is well known: "Hashem made man upright, but they sought many calculations." For many generations, people studied Torah without entering into "many calculations" as to how to arrange their study so that it would be most successful and conform to the rules of educational science, etc. Recently, however, people have come along who delve into various systems and strategies, and the results of these methods are the opposite of what one would seemingly expect from them. For in the earlier generations, the desire to study Torah was great, without excessive over-thinking, and the knowledge of Torah grew in both quantity and quality. This is not the case with study following all the aforementioned rules, where the number of students has diminished, their desire has lessened, etc. All these things apply as well to the study of the teachings of Chassidus. The most correct path is not to seek "many calculations," but to study and review, and not to look at the clock or calculate how many topics one has grasped during this hour. When one turns and returns and turns again in the study of the teachings of Chassidus, then, *derech mashal*, his mind and heart will be refined and become vessels prepared to receive the light of the teachings of Chassidus, and most importantly—the "Light" within it.

4) It is known in the *Yad* of the Rambam, at the end of *Hilchos Mikvaos*, that there is a hint regarding the matter of *tevilah*: it alludes to a *tevilah* in upright opinions. We learn from this that just as a *tevilah* is valid only if the water rises above one's head, so too, when are one's opinions purified? When they "rise above his head"—meaning, above the power of his intellect and knowledge. That is to say, he nullifies his own intellect and knowledge in the waters of upright opinions. May the Ribono shel Olam grant you success and assist you toward complete *yiras shamayim*, and may you increase your strength in the mitzvah of *tzedakah*. For then, as promised by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe (at the beginning of *Torah Ohr*), one's mind and heart become refined "a thousand times over." See *Likutei Torah* for the three *parshiyos* on this *maamar*, where it explains that "a thousand times over" is literal, a thousand times, and not merely a figure of speech or hyperbole. Then, in a short time—but with a great deal of focus—you will succeed in your studies and fulfill the mitzvah of *talmud Torah* as it ought to be.

I trust you participated in the *farbrengen* of the "Festival of Festivals," 19 Kislev. I am interested to hear of the good resolutions made during that *eis ratzon*, in *ahavas Yisrael*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Hashem*.

Regarding the hours of study in *nigleh* and Da"Ch, see *Kuntres Eitz Chaim*, chapters 22-25.

With blessings.

## 1033

B”H, 24 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R’ Pinchas, may he live,
Secretary of the Nusach Ari Anshei Lubavitch Shul

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter on behalf of the mispalelim of the Nusach Ari Anshei Lubavitch Shul, along with the enclosed check for the benefit of the orphans in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily. Enclosed is my letter to the shul, which you will surely deliver to the mispalelim, may they live, in the appropriate manner.

Regarding your question, on behalf of the mispalelim, may they live: some mispalelim say that one should wear a tallis when davening at the amud for Kabbalas Shabbos and also for Mincha on Shabbos afternoon, while other mispalelim say that in a Nusach Ari shul, one should not wear a tallis when davening at the amud for the aforementioned tefillos. You ask for my opinion on this matter.

**Answer:**

The custom of Lubavitch—as I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and as it was also printed in the *Hayom Yom* for 19 Kislev 5703—is: **"The shaliach tzibur does not wrap himself in a tallis for Mincha or Maariv, neither on Shabbos and Yom Tov nor on Rosh Hashanah."**

On the other hand, it is not worthwhile to cause a machlokes over this. If it can be implemented smoothly without machlokes, it is appropriate that your shul should also conduct itself as all Anshei Lubavitch do: that one only wears a tallis for davening in the morning and on Yom Kippur for the entire twenty-four-hour period. If there is a concern of a machlokes, then *gadol hashalom* (great is peace), and for the sake of peace, one must concede on certain matters. However, in any event, concede only regarding davening Mincha on Shabbos, but not regarding Kabbalas Shabbos, as there are some who hold that there is a **sakana badavar** (a danger involved) *.

May Hashem Yisbarach help to preserve the minhagei Yisrael, for *minhag Yisrael Torah hi* (the custom of Israel is Torah), and this also brings success in material matters.

With blessings.

***

 *Sefarim mentioned in Shaarei Teshuvah, Orach Chaim, Siman 18. See also Pri Megadim there; Shu"t Shem Shimon, Mahadura Kamma, Siman 1-2.

## 1054

B"H, 24 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed congregants of the Nusach Ari Shul
The Anash of Lubavitch, and at their head, the respected Gabbaim,
In the city of Dorchester, may it be built and established, may they live.

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your support for the orphaned children in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established.

I was very pleased, both by the assistance itself, and even more so by your interest in the situation of Jewish children in Eretz Yisrael. Assistance from a frum Jewish community for the children in Eretz Yisrael is a double success: the assistance itself is a salvation in gashmius, and the fact that it is sent from a frum Jewish community is a salvation in ruchnius. For then, the help is given to the children in Eretz Yisrael in a spirit that is in harmony with the desire of Torah and mitzvos, which strengthens the bond of the Jewish children with their Father in Heaven.

My father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, often said that Hashem Yisbarach does not remain a debtor, and He repays measure for measure, but with a much greater abundance, as only Hashem Yisbarach can. When one helps orphaned children in our Holy Land, Hashem Yisbarach helps all the donors and those involved in collecting the donations with full nachas—Yiddishe nachas—from their families, children, and grandchildren, and also from themselves.

And regarding the upcoming days of Chanukah, when Hashem Yisbarach showed the great miracle that a little bit of olive oil, which should have only sufficed for one night, burned for eight full days until new kosher oil could be prepared—so too today, in the merit of the Torah and mitzvos that all Jews are fulfilling, may Hashem Yisbarach help that the darkness of the golus should immediately begin to brighten, soon, with one little light, two little lights, and so on, until the great light arrives speedily in our days, through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings for good in both gashmius and ruchnius.

## 1005

B"H, 25 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished R. Boruch Shetz, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding your question, where one of the members of your shul pointed out to you that since everyone in shul puts on tefillin during Chol Hamoed, you should also put on tefillin—you ask for my opinion on this matter:

**Answer:**

This question is brought in many responsa, as it touches upon the issue of *lo tisgodedu* (do not cut yourselves), which Chazal interpret as "do not form separate groups." Therefore, the halachic ruling is: If someone who is accustomed to **putting on tefillin** during Chol Hamoed finds himself in a shul—during davening—where everyone is **not** wearing tefillin, he must not put on tefillin. Conversely, one who is accustomed **not to put on** tefillin—as is the custom of the Arizal, the Baal Shem Tov, and his students—during Chol Hamoed, even if he finds himself davening in a shul where everyone is wearing tefillin, he must maintain his custom not to put on tefillin. In this case, there is no concern of *lo tisgodedu*, because someone who sees him not wearing tefillin may assume it is for entirely different reasons, such as, for example, that he has already worn tefillin, or that he is not yet prepared to put on tefillin, for which one requires a *guf naki* (a clean body), and so forth.

The aforementioned halachic ruling is brought in the seforim *Eshel Avraham*, siman 31; *Responsa Menuchas Moshe*, siman 64; *Responsa Levush Mordechai*, second edition, siman 123; and in the sefer *Me'asef Lechol Hamachanos* in the *Kitzur Shulchan Aruch* with the commentary *Shaarei Metzuyanim Behalacha* (New York printing, 5711), end of siman 10, etc.

With blessings to hear good news, and regards to all the congregants of your shul.

P.S. Enclosed is the booklet for 19 Kislev, which you will likely find useful for the congregants, may they live.

## 156

B"H, 26 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding your second question concerning the Bar Mitzvah of your son... who will be called to the Torah in Parshas Beshalach of this year.

In general, I am surprised by your question, and that you are not seeking reasons to be at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Since your son’s Bar Mitzvah falls in the days close to the Hilula on Yud Shevat, it is, on the face of it, an indication that you should seize this opportunity to be at the Tziyun, and to refresh what you merited to experience for some time during those bright days when you were in the Yeshiva and in the environment of Anash. If not on this occasion, then when? And if, for whatever reason, it is impossible—or at least it seems to you that it is impossible—then may it be the will of Hashem that the Bar Mitzvah take place where you are now, at a good and auspicious time, and may you and your wife, long may you live, and your household, long may they live, all rejoice together in a true simcha, which is a simcha of mitzvah.

With blessings.

## 1007

B"H, 26 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you ask regarding a kindergarten in your city where the teachers are not Jewish, though the director is a shomer Torah u'mitzvos, and he—the director—promises that the teachers do not instruct the children regarding their faith, etc., and consequently you are considering sending your daughter—may she live—there:

First and foremost, it must be clarified whether it is indeed true that there is no concern regarding the teaching of faith or prayer in the kindergarten, as well as regarding matters of kashrus of food and the like. Even after that, if it is possible to arrange for your daughter in another way—that is, in a manner where she will not be constantly in a group and under the supervision of non-Jews in a place where they are the masters and the educators—it would be preferable. For to a certain extent, in kindergarten, the teachers penetrate the child's soul more than they do in schools. If there is absolutely no room for the aforementioned concern, then may it be the will of Hashem that there be success, and may you have from her, and from your other children—may they live—Yiddishe nachas.

I had thought that you would be present at the farbrengen of Yud-Tes Kislev. Seemingly, the time has already come for you to bring along several members of your community. It appears that you did not come, and I also do not know if you held a farbrengen for Yud-Tes Kislev in your camp. It is a pity for every day of farbrengen that passes without being utilized to bring the hearts of Yidden closer to their Father in Heaven and to improve them through ahavas Hashem, ahavas haTorah, and ahavas Yisrael. For the kochos have been given to us, and if we do not use them, then, chas v'shalom, it is a waste of the kochos of our holy Nesi'im, our Rebbeim—may their merits protect us.

With blessings for proper health for you and all your household—may they live—and awaiting good tidings.

## 1098

B”H, 26 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have duly received your two letters dated Tuesday and Wednesday of Parshas Vayeitzei. Surely, in the meantime, you have seen my general letter to the administration of the mosdos in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. It is my hope that you will inform me **as soon as possible**, in an unofficial capacity, of what has been done since the receipt of the aforementioned letter, and in continuation of that letter, please also share your suggestions regarding this matter.

Enclosed is a copy of the general letter pertaining to the Yud-Tes Kislev kuntres. The kuntreisim and booklets for Yud-Tes Kislev have been sent separately in the name of Agudas Chassidei Chabad and Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, with several copies to be distributed in the appropriate manner.

During these days of Chanukah, when the miracle occurred through the "light and the luminary" of Torah—as explained in Chassidus, that they sought to make them "forget Your Torah," which is the Torah of Hashem, for they did not mind the study of Torah as an intellectual pursuit, and regarding this they stood the test with mesiras nefesh beyond the limits of intellect—the victory was therefore also miraculous. In addition to the victory of the war, there was also the matter of the lamp: that there was no oil, yet it was sufficient to kindle, etc. This means that although according to the revealed dimension of Torah it would have been permissible for them to kindle even with oil that was not pure, as explained in the Acharonim, nevertheless, as a sign of affection, a miracle occurred to kindle for eight days, and the entire kindling was with pure oil.

From this we can derive several lessons. One of them is that this serves as an instruction: when there is a war from within and from without, as was the case in the time of the Chashmonaim, who fought against the Greeks and against the Hellenizers, it is impossible to prevail without the "luminary of the Torah," the "Tree of Life," where there is no foothold and no tumah, unlike the "Tree of Knowledge of Good and Evil."

It may be suggested that this is also the explanation for why specifically in the mitzvah of the Chanukah lamp we have the concept of *mehadrin* and *mehadrin min hamehadrin*. For during a time of war and cunning schemes, it is impossible to engage in intellectual *shakla vetarya* and be satisfied with avodah that is within the limits of intellect. All matters must be done with *hiddur*, and even that is not enough; one must be *mehadrin min hamehadrin*. It is possible to say that this corresponds to the revealed Torah, the secrets of the Torah, and the "secrets of the secrets"—water, wine, and oil that floats on top of wine. See *Imrei Binah* regarding the dispute as to whether oil floating on wine constitutes a *chibur* (Shaar Krias Shema, p. 54 and onwards; see also *Likutei Torah*, Shir HaShirim 3:3).

With blessings for Chanukah and regards to all those who seek my welfare.

#### ***1098***

**As explained in the Acharonim:** See also below, Igros 1096-97.

## 1119

B"H, 26 Kislev, 5712

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter in due time, in which you write that you are feeling better. I hope that from then until today, your health has improved even further, and I look forward to hearing good news regarding this.

Yosef, may he live, HaLevi Weinberg, the shaliach, and I assume that you participated in the Yud-Tes Kislev farbrengen. My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, writes in one of his letters that every hitva'adus of Chassidim must bring about good resolutions, both in Torah and in mitzvos, and especially in ahavas re'im—but the main thing is that this should also be realized in actual practice.

I was pleased to read in your letter that those good years when you were in Lubavitch are etched in your memory. Just as every memory brings a drawing and a pull of the neshamah, it is certain that this pull of the neshamah from those good memories will not remain without a positive effect. It will surely bring about a strengthening in the ways of Chassidus and the study of the teachings of Chassidus. At that point, this is what the Admur HaZaken writes: that anyone who holds onto his door-latch, he will take him out from the straits to the expanse, from the physical to the spiritual, and from Gehenom. And the Rebbe (Rashab) explained this—"from Gehenom"—as the physical, material matters of this world. Especially for those who have merited to be with a Rebbe for a longer time, it is certain that, in the end, this will have the desired effect and will place him in a corner of light, for his own good, both physically and spiritually.

I look forward to hearing good news from you, and I will conclude with a blessing for proper health, in both body and soul.

## A'shi

B"H, 26 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you inform me that your son...sheyichyeh has reached the age of five and you have brought him into the cheder, may it be the will of Hashem that he grow to Torah, chuppah, and maasim tovim, together with his wife tichyeh, in a state of abundance, peace of mind, and physical well-being.

It was explained at the farbrengen of Shabbos Mevarchim of the previous month that one can find precision in the customary phrasing used among Yisrael: "to Torah, to chuppah, and to maasim tovim." This corresponds to the three Avos:

"To Torah" corresponds to Yaakov, who "dwelled in the tents of Shem and Eiver," which refers to the Torah Shebichtav and the Torah Shebe'al Peh, as explained in Ohr HaTorah by the Tzemach Tzedek in the maamar beginning "Yoshev Ohalim."

"To chuppah" corresponds to Yitzchak, who was bound (ne'ekad) at the site of the Beis HaMikdash. As our Sages of blessed memory state (Midrash Shir HaShirim; see also Zohar Chadash 3:2; and the end of Maseches Taanis in the Mishnayos), when the Shechinah descended to the Beis HaMikdash, that was "the day of His wedding"—the chuppah of the Ribono shel Olam with Yisrael. This is explained in Chassidus in many places regarding the statement of our Sages, "The conversation of the servants of the Patriarchs is more beautiful than the Torah of the children," explaining why the Torah recounts the marriage of Yitzchak and Rivkah at such length; it is a general concept that applies to all of Yisrael.

"Maasim tovim" corresponds to Avraham, whose essence is acts of kindness (gemilus chasadim), and specifically the matter of tzedakah. It is explained in Torah Ohr, at the beginning of Parshas Va'era, that the aspects of the three Avos must be present within every single Yid (unlike the Tribes).

You also inform me in the aforementioned letter that you are traveling on a shlichus of Torah U'Tefillah to other countries. May it be the will of Hashem that you be successful in both gashmius and ruchnius. As is the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, to the shluchim traveling from our holy institutions: "They should gather gashmius and sow—lizro'a—ruchnius."

With blessings.

## 1111

B.H., 26 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn

To the Ladies Auxiliary
of Brownsville and East New York,

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to hear that you are making preparations for the annual banquet of your Ladies Auxiliary. I hope that you have made the proper preparations, and may Hashem Yisbarach help that it should be successful in all details, both in gashmius and in ruchnius.

My father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, would always demand that every gathering should lead to good deeds, both in gashmius and in ruchnius. We clearly see that when Yidden who are imbued with a Chassidishe spirit gather together, it results in good actions in the three areas that are, in truth, one thing: Ahavas Hashem Yisbarach, Ahavas HaTorah, and Ahavas Yisrael.

I ask you to convey my greetings to all the participants in the banquet, and I send my blessing that your work for the Auxiliary should continue to grow. Since Hashem Yisbarach rewards measure for measure, may Hashem Yisbarach grant His blessings to each one of you, so that you may all continue to rise in all the matters that you and your families require, with children, life, and ample sustenance.

With blessings for success in your general and personal matters.

## 1112

B"H, 26 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from 1 Cheshvan, in which you describe your standing, your situation, and your conduct, and request my opinion on the matter:

What I do not find favorable is the fact that you always study alone, and likewise that you daven alone. Regarding your explanation that there is no one with whom to study together or to daven with composure—consider for yourself: you and your father-in-law (may he live and be well) have been living in [name of city] for some time. Is it truly impossible that during all these months and years, you could not have drawn at least a few people toward the conduct of the ways of Chassidus and the study of Chassidus?! Especially since, as is known from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, there is a presumption that outreach (*taamulah*) does not return empty-handed. Even one who can justly say of himself, "I am asleep," the verse testifies regarding him that "my heart is awake." This is especially true regarding the teachings and customs of Chassidus, which are the "Light." Consequently, its nature is to draw the "sparks" toward itself, provided that one brings the Light into close proximity to the sparks. Thus, the matter depends only on a person who already knows—or at least has a connection to—the Light, whose role it is to bring the spark closer, wherever it may be found.

It is known from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, that he spoke at length describing the situation of one of the Chassidim of the Rebbe Maharash who was sent to a remote corner. When he complained about this to the Rebbe, explaining how it was impossible to accomplish anything for others in that place, the Rebbe Maharash replied that for his physical livelihood, Hashem could have provided him with a living in a place where G-d-fearing Jews reside, and so on. This means that the fact that he was sent to a town where he found himself isolated was specifically so that he could influence his surroundings until, little by little, things would become as they ought to be.

All these things apply as well to you and your father-in-law (may he live and be well), who are in a city where there are quite a few G-d-fearing Jews, among them many people from the lineage of *anash*. Our Sages have already ruled, "Throw a stick into the air, and it will return to its root"—it only requires the act of throwing. If you begin this *avodah*, then, as per the promise of our Rebbes, you will succeed.

With regards and blessings.

## 1113

B"H, 26 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn

To the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., R' Menachem Man, may he live.

Shalom u'Bracha!

I was very pleased to receive your letter, in which you write that you celebrated the Yom Tov of 19 Kislev with a Siyum on Mishnayos, sang the Alter Rebbe’s nigun, and reviewed Chassidus.

It would be very appropriate to arrange such farbrengens more often.

Especially on Shabbos Mevarchim and on yomei d'pagra (special days), for when Chassidishe Yidden gather together, they surely speak about a Torah thought—a Chassidishe Torah thought—as well as stories of tzaddikim, the foundations of the world. For the statements of our Sages and the stories of tzaddikim refresh the nefesh elokis and give it the strength to continue the avodah that has been placed upon it: to illuminate one's body, nefesh habehamis, and one's portion in the world that is connected to that Yid.

And just as the mitzvah of Chanukah is to kindle lights when it grows dark, and from night to night to add more light to the candles, this serves as a lesson for the general darkness of the golus: that every Yid has been given the strength to illuminate the darkness of the golus and, from time to time, to add more light, as our Sages say, "We increase in holiness."

I ask you to convey my greetings to all those who participated in the 19 Kislev farbrengen. And as a participant in the next farbrengen, I am symbolically enclosing $5, which should be used for things that contribute to the farbrengen, such as mashke, refreshments, etc.

With blessings for proper health, and regards to all the participants, may they live.

## 1114

B.H., 26 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn

Blessings and Peace!

...I would like to write and reiterate regarding what you yourself wrote, that the most important matter is that of a shidduch; you write that, in your opinion, you do not see any suitable proposals.

My hope, however, is that when you adopt the correct approach toward the proposals that come your way, Hashem Yisbarach will certainly provide you with a shidduch that is suitable for you, both materially and spiritually.

One must always be aware that in this world, there is no such thing as perfection—*tachlis hashlimus*—and this is true regarding people as well; there is no person who possesses every virtue. Consequently, one should not wait to find the person one has imagined in one’s mind. And since it is true that no person has all the virtues, it is certain that you, too, have shortcomings. However, one looks at oneself with a favorable eye; therefore, one must take this into account as well—that in certain matters, one must to a certain degree bend and overlook things, hoping that in time, some of these—whether imagined or real—shortcomings will smooth out and improve. Then, in one’s approach to a shidduch, the selection—*bechirah*—is much easier, and the entire approach to the question of a shidduch is more joyful.

I also want to draw your attention to the fact that one cannot calculate and estimate exactly what two people will look like after their wedding, because a wedding is an experience that brings about certain significant changes in the two people who marry, and these changes are impossible to foresee. This means that regarding a shidduch, one has only a limited degree of choice—*bechirah*—and one must rely on Hashem Yisbarach, that He, blessed be He, will lead you to happiness and goodness. Indeed, one sees clearly that people do this, and subsequently lead a life—a happy life—until 120 years.

And so it is in your case as well: one cannot calculate in advance, with 100 percent certainty, how any proposal presented to you will look in the future after the wedding. One must rely on Hashem Yisbarach, and He, blessed be He, who is able to lead such a vast world, will certainly also be able to lead the "small world" of each individual, in such a way that it will be good, both materially and spiritually.

I hope that you will read this letter once and twice, and contemplate what I am writing to you. The main point of my letter is that from today onward, your approach to a shidduch proposal should not be with the preconceived notion that the shidduch is not suitable for you—and that therefore one need not inquire further. Rather, the exact opposite: your approach to a shidduch should be that Hashem Yisbarach will surely provide you with a shidduch that is good for you, and therefore it is possible that this proposal is indeed it. Consequently, one must inquire and find out what the matter is about. I wish you that this should be very soon, a *zivug hamit'am* (a suitable match) for you, in both physicality and spirituality, and that you should build a *bayis b'Yisrael* (a home in Israel) upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos.

With blessings.

P.S.
You may write to me in whichever language is easier and more comfortable for you: Russian, Yiddish, or French.

## 115

B"H, 26 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification regarding the health of your wife, *tichyeh*, may it be Hashem’s will that the pregnancy proceed properly and the birth take place at its proper time, easily, and may she certainly follow the instructions of the doctors.

My suggestion—which should be done without publicizing the matter—is that every day, during the Krias Shema she-al HaMitah before the *Hamapil* blessing, you should recite the chapter of Tehillim, *Lamnatzeiach Yaancha*, and upon concluding it, repeat the verse *Yaancha* once more, while intending in your thoughts that it should be as if you had directed all the necessary *kavanos* that are required for this. All of the above should be done, *bli neder*, until after the birth, in a good and auspicious hour. Likewise, you should have the *mezuzos* in your home checked, and your wife, *tichyeh*, should give *tzedakah* to the *kupah* of *Rambae"n*—Rabbi Meir Baal HaNes—every Erev Shabbos Kodesh, before lighting the Shabbos candles—*bli neder*.

With blessings.

## 1116

B.H., 28 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc., R' Dovid Nosson
May he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I received with pleasure your gift of beeswax candles for Chanukah. Relying on what I told you previously—that it is known (Zohar Vol. III, 128b) that "a mitzvah should cost a Yid money"—I am enclosing a check. Please use it in good health for whatever you wish, in a good way.

**Regarding the topic of the day:**

Seemingly, regarding the miracle of Chanukah, since the miracle occurred through the victory in war, why was an additional miracle required with the cruse of oil? Furthermore, from any perspective, if one cruse of pure oil remained, the miracle could have simply been that it would suffice to light until more pure oil could be prepared. Why was a "miracle within a miracle" necessary—both the finding of the cruse and the fact that the small amount of oil lasted for eight days?

It can be explained based on what is elucidated in the Acharonim: that according to the strict letter of the law, it was permissible to light even with impure oil, whether because it is a communal offering, or because the vessels of the Beis Hamikdash do not become tamei, etc. However, since Bnei Yisrael had reached a level in their avodah at that time that was above logic and intellect—each with mesiras nefesh—Hashem showed them His affection from Above. Even though according to the law it was permissible to light with impure oil, through a miracle—which is above logic and intellect—they found a cruse of pure oil, etc.

Just as in the avodah of mesiras nefesh there are two modes, as explained in Chassidus regarding the difference between the mesiras nefesh of Rabbi Akiva—who said, "When will it come to my hand that I may fulfill it?"—where, although the essence of the avodah is above logic and intellect, he still derives taanug from it; and the even higher level of the mesiras nefesh of Avraham Avinu, who fulfilled his task and "called out there in the name of Hashem, G-d of the world" (the verse says "he caused others to call out"). If mesiras nefesh was required to fulfill this, there was no obstacle; meaning, his avodah of mesiras nefesh did not come from the preciousness and sweetness of the act of mesiras nefesh, but as something self-evident and natural, because it is impossible to fulfill his purpose in the world otherwise.

In Chanukah, it was also in this manner: Yisrael stood for their lives so as "not to forget Your Torah and the statutes of Your will." If it were impossible without mesiras nefesh, there was no obstacle from that side, but it was not because of the "preciousness" of the mode of mesiras nefesh. Therefore, in this miracle of the oil, they were shown a miracle within a miracle. The finding of the cruse of oil was itself a miracle, and there was an additional miracle: although it only sufficed for one night, they lit from it for eight days—provided that the oil was pure. It is known that Bnei Yisrael are compared to oil because they do not mix with other liquids, just as oil does not mix with other liquids (Midrash Rabbah, beginning of Parshas Tetzaveh). It can be said that this is also the reason why specifically in the mitzvah of Chanukah candles there is the concept of fulfilling the mitzvah in its simple sense, *mehadrin*, and *mehadrin min hamehadrin*, which correspond to the three levels in Torah: the revealed part of Torah, the secrets of Torah, and the "secrets of the secrets."

May the Ribono shel Olam grant us that in our time, the "footsteps of the Tarmudai" (which spells *moredes*—rebellious) will cease, and we will be "increasing and ascending in holiness" until, when the sun sets in the darkness of the night, the night will shine like the day.

With blessings.

## 1117

B"H, 28 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc.,
Rabbi Efraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and Blessing!

Thank you for your letter of 21 Kislev... I was pleased to hear of your beginning to study Chassidus in the Siddur, and may it be Hashem’s will that it be successful, including in terms of time. This is in accordance with the instruction of the mitzvah of Chanukah, which contains the fulfillment of the mitzvah in its simple form, the *mehadrin* (beautified) level, and the *mehadrin min hamehadrin* (most beautified) level. [One could say this is analogous to the miracle itself; according to many of the *Acharonim*, it would have been possible to light with impure oil, since it is a communal offering, etc. (The Rebbe and Gaon of Ostrovtza elaborated on this in his pilpul, as is his custom, in his book now in print). Nevertheless, a miracle (a *hiddur*) occurred, and a cruse of oil was found. And within that very miracle, another miracle occurred (*mehadrin min hamehadrin*), that it contained only enough for one day, yet it burned for eight days—like the harp of the future, which has eight strings]. And all the people followed this custom—as if from the *Mem* (the source)!

I await good news regarding your positive activities in proper education: *Chinuch* (education) is the concept of Chanukah, and *Kasher* (proper) refers to the "one cruse sealed with the seal of the Kohen Gadol," etc.

P.S.

I also received your letter from the fourth night, and thank you for the list of memories of the bright days, from what you recall of your ancestors, of blessed memory.

When I was at the Ohel of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, this past Thursday, I mentioned you for the things you require. I am informing you of this, relying on our Sages’ teaching that one who gives [a gift] to his friend must inform him.

I believe I mentioned to you when you told me what the Ramban says regarding seeing the face of a Tzaddik, that I had seen something similar in a certain book. I have now found it in the book *Vayosef Avraham* by Rabbi Lifshitz (Munkacs, 5691), section 34. He cites there that this is discussed in *Divrei Torah*, Part 1, letter 27, by the Rebbe of Munkacs.

Enclosed is a list of points that I said to the students, may they live, on the fifth night of Chanukah.

Regarding what you wrote, that you recall that the *shamash* candle was taken **immediately after** the blessing, this requires study in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim*, 673:3.

## A'shich

B"H, 28 Kislev, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Avraham Chaim, may he live:

Shalom u’Bracha!

I received your letters in due time, and in response to them:

Regarding what you wrote in your letter of 7 Cheshvan, concerning whether one should recite the *Haftorah* of *Hashamayim Kis’i* when Rosh Chodesh Elul falls on Shabbos and the following day, and whether one should also recite the two verses of the *Haftorah* for *Machar Chodesh*, and your inclination in the letter not to recite them and to push off the *Haftorah* of *Machar Chodesh* entirely—this reasoning is written in the sefer *Ketzos HaShulchan*, section 3.

1) Since we have merited the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—as printed in the *Siddur Torah Or* of the year 5701—that when *Parshas HaChodesh* falls on Rosh Chodesh or Erev Rosh Chodesh, one should recite after the *Haftorah* of *Parshas HaChodesh* also the first and last verses of the *Haftorah* of *Rosh Chodesh* or *Machar Chodesh*, it is clear from this that the recitation of these verses is not dependent on the existence of an opinion to recite the entire *Haftorah*. For in *Parshas HaChodesh*, according to all opinions, one should not recite the *Haftorah* of *Machar Chodesh*, yet we do recite the first and last verses of that *Haftorah*. Consequently, the same applies to Rosh Chodesh Elul when it falls on Shabbos and Sunday, that one must also recite the verses of *Machar Chodesh*. Regarding the upcoming Shabbos—Shabbos Chanukah, Rosh Chodesh Teves, which falls on Shabbos and the following Sunday—based on the above, in my opinion, after the *Haftorah* of Chanukah, one should recite the first and last verses of the *Haftorah* of *Rosh Chodesh* and also of *Machar Chodesh*.

One may recite the verse *Hashamayim Kis’i* first, as it is more significant than the *Haftorah* of *Machar Chodesh* and also precedes it in time (even though the second day of Rosh Chodesh is the primary one).

2) Regarding the matter of *Hataras Nedarim*, where you feel that one should also recite the *Yehi Ratzon Milfanecha* and write that this is the custom:

The customs printed in the *Kuntres* are based on the explicit instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. I also heard this from him personally, that he would not recite the aforementioned *Yehi Ratzon*. This is also the explicit instruction of his father (the Rebbe Rashab), as printed in the *Siddur Tehilas Hashem* of **5718** in Rostov, where nothing is printed there except *Shim’u Na Rabosai*, *Kol Yihyu Mutarim*, *Hareini Moser Moda’ah*, *Kulam Yihyu Mutarim*.

3) Regarding the *Makri* (prompter) for the *Tekios*, where you wish to explain that he only points with his finger, implying this is only when the Rebbe himself was the *Tokei'a*:

Surely you are aware that in previous years—for many years of the Rebbe Rashab—the Rebbe was not the *Tokei'a*, but rather the *Makri*. The same was true in the final years of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. They would only prompt with a finger, not with speech.

4) Regarding what I asked concerning the order of reciting *Selichos* on *Tzom Gedaliah*, my intention was to know which *Pizmonim* are recited and how many times *Kel Melech* is recited, etc. For it is clear that we do not recite them as printed in the *Selichos* books. The proof is the order of *Selichos* printed according to the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the aforementioned *Siddur Torah Or*, that one does not recite the *Yud-Gimmel Middos* more than three times (except on *Motzaei Menucha* and Erev Rosh Hashanah). Seemingly, according to our custom that we do not recite *Selichos* during the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah* except on *Tzom Gedaliah*—which is in the category of a *Ta’anis Tzibbur*—one should recite *Kel Melech* three times as in every *Ta’anis Tzibbur*, as printed in the *Liaut* Siddur. In that case, it requires clarification as to which *Pizmonim* to omit. Perhaps there is a tradition for this from the elders of *Anash* in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and I would be grateful if you could inform me regarding this...

5) In addition to the *Shiur* of *Achilas Pras* brought in the notes at the end of the *Reshimot* on *Megillas Eichah* (p. 61, notes 2-3), I have now found in the sefer *Vaya’as Avraham* (by the Rebbe of Ciechanów), p. 56, that according to his calculation it is: 5 and 1/3, 2 and 2/3, or 2 minutes.

6) I happened upon what you wrote in *HaModia* regarding *Hilchos HaChag*. Although one does not challenge a *Drush*, I must note regarding your wonderment that *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim* 625 contains no *Halacha*: 1) The *Sifrei Torah* are also like this. 2) In 625, it can be said that the *Halacha* is the general *Mitzvah* of dwelling in the *Sukkah*, but it is written in the language of the verse. With this, the beginning of 639 is resolved peacefully: "**How** is the *Mitzvah* of dwelling in the *Sukkah* performed?" Or, it can be said that the words **"Lema’an Yeidu"** should also be in the *Shulchan Aruch*—and this is also a *Halacha*, that (at least *L’chatchila*) there must be the knowledge that one is dwelling in the *Sukkah*, etc., as the *Bach*, *Magen Avraham*, *Pri Megadim*, *Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken*, etc., have elaborated. (For according to your explanation in *HaModia*, the *Shulchan Aruch* is missing the **essential** point, which is that there must be knowledge). Rather, a printer who had not studied sufficiently came along, and due to a lack of knowledge, wanted to reduce his labor by shortening the language of the verse, and omitted the words *Lema’an Yeidu Doroseichem*.

A strong proof for the above, that the words **"Lema’an Yeidu"** should be in the *Shulchan Aruch*, is that they are found in the *Tur* and *Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken*, even though they too did not quote the entire verse.

Wishing you and your Torah well—with blessing.

## A'shit

B"H, Chanukah, Fifth Candle, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our brethren, the Children of Israel, lovers of Torah and mitzvos,
In our Holy Land, may it be built and established, and in every place,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

It is well-known among the Children of Israel, the sanctuary of Torah, which is Yeshiva "Toras Emes," located in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be built and established.

Forty years ago, it was founded by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (the Rashab), of blessed memory, and from that time on it stood under his presidency, and subsequently under the presidency of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, who labored greatly to assist the Yeshiva and develop it.

Lately, in connection with the immigration to the Holy Land, may it be built and established, despite its most severe financial situation, this Yeshiva has expanded its borders and has labored and exerted itself in absorbing students from the immigrant youth, who are thereby able to realize in their lives their aspiration and desire to be in the tent of Torah, saturated with yiras shamayim, to cleave to Hashem our G-d through **d**ivrei **e**lokim **c**hayim (words of the living G-d).

It is understood that all of this has caused a significant increase in expenses, and the Yeshiva is now in a serious and difficult material situation.

And with this, I turn to all lovers of Torah and mitzvos in every place:

**Support with a generous eye and a giving hand Yeshiva "Toras Emes - Jerusalem." Give it the possibility to continue its holy work and to expand it — fitting for the demands of the hour.**

And in the merit of this great mitzvah, may the Holy One, blessed be He, bestow blessing and success upon you, upon your homes and your offspring, in all good things, from soul to flesh.

And may your eyes and our eyes behold the raising of the horn of Torah with yiras shamayim and the horn of Israel, for Yisrael, the Torah, and the Holy One, blessed be He, are all one.

With blessings for goodness and success in material and spiritual matters,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***A'shit***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 473.

## 1,211

B"H, 1 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who is involved in communal needs, etc., R' Aryeh Leib Kramer, I received your letter along with the *pidyon nefesh* for your cousin...

I am interested to know whether your cousin observes *taharas hamishpachah*. If not, Heaven forbid, she should take it upon herself to observe *taharas hamishpachah* with full stringency from this day forward. Also, tell her to give *tzedakah* every day in the morning (except for *Shabbos Kodesh*) to the *tzedakah* of Rabbi Meir Baal HaNes, and also ensure that the *mezuzos* in her home are *kosher*. I hope that she can be strong in her *bitachon* in Hashem Yisbarach, that everything will be in order and in its proper time, and she will be able to report good news regarding this.

Certainly, she has a doctor who visits her from time to time, and she should follow his instructions regarding refraining from carrying heavy objects, and so on.

I am not writing to her directly, because I want you, from your side, to write to her and explain the necessity of following what I have written, especially regarding *taharas hamishpachah*. I look forward to hearing good news from you regarding this, and please convey my blessing to your cousin, Mrs. ... *tichyeh*, as mentioned above.

With blessings.

## 1,324

B"H, 1 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Simon [Jacobson]
Shlita,

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your report regarding the farbrengen of the "Chag HaChagim," 19 Kislev—though it is a pity it was only in general terms—and regarding the good resolutions made by those who participated. Surely, in accordance with our Sages' teaching that "it is not the study that is the essential thing, but the deed," they will bring these into actual practice in the year ahead, for us and for all of Israel for good.

Nevertheless, it is very appropriate from time to time to remind and arouse those who participated regarding the fulfillment of these resolutions. In accordance with our Sages' teaching that "great is the drink that brings [people] close," it is well to utilize upcoming farbrengens to urge the fulfillment of these resolutions. May Hashem grant each and every one of us the merit to bring into action that which has been given to us in potential. As it is written, "A person who sanctifies himself a little below is sanctified much from above," and "he who comes to purify himself is assisted." It is known how this is explained in Chassidus (Likutei Torah, Devarim 88b): the precision of the word "to purify" (*l'taher*) rather than "to be purified" (*l'hittaher*) implies that one must also purify others.

With blessings for success in all the above, awaiting good tidings, and signing with regards to all Anash and with regards to the sender,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.

Regarding your question concerning your visits to various countries, where you enter into discussions with those who, for the time being, do not observe Torah and mitzvos as they should, and there are those who complain about this:

**Response:**

The approach of Lubavitch has always been **not** to distance any Jew, even those of the aforementioned type. On the contrary, one should bring them closer to our Father in Heaven through words of pleasantness and matters of *kiruv*. Of course, there must be caution in this, as per the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in one of his holy sichos: "One must not lower oneself to the other, but rather lift the other up to oneself." However, it is understood that even in this, one must extend a hand—to the one in need of help—and sometimes even a long hand. Yet, almost always, with the aforementioned caution, one succeeds in this avodah and "brings forth the precious from the vile." We have no other approach but this, and we are assured that it will be successful.

## 1,526

Yisroel Abba Pliskin - Melbourne

I received your letter with pleasure, in which you inform me of the current state of the yeshivah and your study schedule with the bochurim. Regarding your question as to how much time per day should be set aside for the study of Chassidus, there are two points to consider: a) The study of Chassidus is essential; b) One must not overburden beginners with this, so that they do not withdraw from the yeshivah entirely. However, the goal must be to approach this as much as possible, but **only** if it is feasible to have the study of Chassidus both in the morning and in the evening, and especially on Shabbos and Thursday night.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter—that you surely have received detailed information about the *chanukas habayis*—this has fulfilled the saying of our Sages, "A pot belonging to partners..." [is neither hot nor cold], as each one relies on the other. You also write in the same vein. It would be appropriate that when you divide all the areas of work in the yeshivah, the responsibility for reporting the details here should also be placed on the shoulders of one of them. In this way, it will be certain that reports of what is happening will reach here.

With the blessing of *hatzlocha* in your *avodah* and regards to those who seek our welfare.

## 1,328

I have received your letter...

It is self-understood that if it is at all possible, it is appropriate, right, and good that you exert influence within the circles of the yeshiva. This is a matter that benefits both sides—both for you and for the yeshiva. The time has already come for true *ahavas achim* (brotherly love) to prevail in our camp. As is well known, the current *galus* is due to the sin of *sinas chinam*—that is, hatred without any foundation, and even contrary to reason. Consequently, the rectification for this—a rectification that is essential, especially now in the *ikvesa d’meshicha*—is *ahavas chinam*, which is love that, even if it has no basis in human reason, and is even contrary to reason, is nonetheless practiced. To elaborate on this is superfluous, especially since these matters and their immense value have been explained in *Tanya*, Chapter 32; in the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the *Tzemach Tzedek*, in the *mitzvah* of *ahavas Yisroel*; in the *maamar* "Hechaletzu" in *Likutei Torah*; in the *maamarim* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, printed at the end of *Kuntres Hechaletzu*. May Hashem bless His people with peace, which is the vessel that holds blessing—the blessing of the *Ribono shel Olam*, which is without limit. All of the above is even more imperative for you, since Hashem has granted you the merit of being involved in matters whose inner essence is to bind all *Chassidim* together in true unity. And it is known that when one wishes to influence another even slightly, one must possess a great deal oneself.

With blessings for success and for good tidings in all of the above.

Written as an addendum to letter 1,325 above.

## 1,329

1,329

I received your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Vayigash with pleasure, and for several reasons, the response has been delayed until now.

When I am at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention you and your family, may they live, specifically regarding the matters of shidduchim and zivugim. However, you are surely aware of the verse, "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do," which implies that one must also put in effort. It is also well-known what the holy Rabbi Zusia of Anipoli, of blessed memory, said: that one can learn lessons in the avodah of Hashem from every person, even from those who do not conduct themselves as they should. He learned several things from the conduct of a thief, among them that when he tries the first time and does not succeed, he nevertheless tries a second and third time until, eventually, he succeeds. How much more so is this true regarding the measure of goodness, etc. Especially in the matter of zivugim, regarding which our Sages said that it is as difficult [to arrange as the splitting of the Red Sea], one must try time and again, but in the end, it is certain that one will find a suitable zivug, and there is no reason to be discouraged by the fact that effort is required in this matter.

I was pleased to read in your letter that you find the kuntresim to be enjoyable for those you meet with, and I am enclosing the booklet for 19 Kislev that was published not long ago. May it be the will of Hashem that you be privileged to share good news regarding all of the above, very soon.

With blessing.

## 1031

1031

B"H, 3 Teves, 5712

Rabbi, the Gaon, etc., etc., Moreinu Harav M. Rosen
Shlita

Greetings and Blessings!

In the name of the Rebbe Shlita, I hereby acknowledge with great thanks the receipt of your sefer, *Nezer HaKodesh* on Maseches Tamid. Surely you will also send the rest of your compositions to the library of the Rebbe Shlita, and thank you in advance.

Enclosed is a list of notes from the Rebbe Shlita regarding several matters in your aforementioned sefer.

By the instruction of the Rebbe Shlita, we are sending you *Sefer HaMaamarim 5700*, in which you will surely find much of interest.

With respect and blessing.

**Notes**

**At the beginning (5a):** You raise a difficulty regarding why the Tanna adds "in three places" — why is the count necessary?

In my humble opinion, it is simple: because this is the **essence** of the law, that there must be guarding, and in three places, as we derive from the verse. Afterward, he adds that in the Beis HaMikdash, this was in Beis Avtinas, etc. (Seemingly, this is also self-evident; if they stationed guards in three other places, they would also fulfill the requirement of guarding, for does the verse say specifically "Beis Avtinas," etc.?)

Furthermore, if the language of the Mishnah were: "In Beis Avtinas, etc., there must be guards," as your question implies, there would still remain doubts: a) In how many places within Beis HaMoked, etc., were the Kohanim stationed as guards? b) If it is impossible to station them in one of the places enumerated in the Mishnah, what is the law? c) What is the law regarding the First and Third Beis HaMikdash (and likewise the Mishkan)? All of this is resolved by what is written: **in three places** the Kohanim guard in the Beis HaMikdash (and we find that the Mishkan is also called a Mikdash).

**15b. Regarding the Mitzvah of Teshuvah:** You raise a difficulty as to why the Rambam omitted "that which the Torah said, 'And you shall return' — to say that it is a mitzvah to return in Teshuvah."

In my humble opinion, the Rambam himself avoids this in *Hilchos Teshuvah* (Chapter 7, Halacha 5), where he explains that the verse is a narrative and a promise to Yisrael that **at the end of the exile** they will do Teshuvah. (It can be said that he has his reasons, for that is the literal style of the verse — a narrative of that which will occur in the end of days.)

And what you wrote at the end of the matter (16a), that the Torah did not command a mitzvah regarding that which is in the heart, and the practical difference regarding the fulfillment of *tashbitu* (removing) of Chametz if one fulfills the mitzvah through a thought in the heart — this is puzzling, for there are many mitzvos regarding matters of the heart: to unify Him, to love Him, to fear Him, etc. See also Rambam, *Hilchos Maaseh HaKorbanos* (Chapter 14, Halacha 12), which proves that an animal is sanctified through his thought (and not only that the person has an obligation to sanctify the animal with his speech and bring it as a donation). This is contrary to Rashi and Tosafos, etc., at the beginning of Chapter 2 of *Meilah*, who wrote "from the moment it is sanctified by speech."

See also *Shaar HaMelech*, *Hilchos Terumos*, Chapter 4, Halacha 16, and this is not the place to elaborate.

But the question that must be asked regarding this matter is: Since all the prophets **commanded** Teshuvah, and it is a condition for the offering of a Chatas, etc., for the atonement of Yom Kippur, etc. — how is it possible that it is not established as a mitzvah?

And were I not afraid, as I have not found this explicitly in a sefer thus far, in my humble opinion, it can be said simply that the command for this came in the Torah — in *Devarim* (10:16): "And you shall circumcise the **foreskin** of your heart, and your neck you shall not harden **any more**." This means a **command** to circumcise the foreskin of the heart and to remove the hardness of the neck **that already exists**. The verse does not define whether they have already caused the sin in practice (the matter of Teshuvah) or not.

Consequently, both aspects are included in this command.

It is also understood why the Rambam did not count it in the *Sefer HaMitzvos* — because Teshuvah is a command that includes the entire Torah, and such mitzvos are not included in the count, as he wrote in *Sefer HaMitzvos*, Shoresh 4, where he also cites the command "And you shall circumcise," etc.

See the *Biur* of the Ridvaz Perla to the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of Rav Saadia Gaon, Parsha 42, regarding his difficulty with several Sugyos concerning the Rambam's view that Viduy is the essence of Teshuvah.

See also *Zohar* Vol. 3, 122a. *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* (by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, author of the Shulchan Aruch and Tanya), Chapter 1. *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, Mitzvah of Viduy and Teshuvah.

**At the end, 34b:** Regarding the formula of *Lechai Olamim*.

You did not explain this as much as is necessary, and consequently, the words are not precise and leave room for error.

For there are three details in this matter: a) *Lechai* — with one *yud* or two. b) If you say with one — is it vocalized with a *patach* or a *tzeirei*? c) *HaOlamim* — with a *hei* or without a *hei*. This has practical implications for the *Birkas Baruch She'amar*, *Yishtabach*, *B'Nishmas*, and the *Piyut* of *Adon Olam* (or *Adereis V'HaEmunah*).

There are several opinions on this: a) In *Chok Nasan* at the end of Maseches Tamid, he seemingly standardized his approach — to say *Chai HaOlamim* as mentioned above — also in the *Piyut* of *Adereis V'HaEmunah*. b) In *Siddur Rav Amram Gaon*, it is printed in *Baruch She'amar* and *Yishtabach* — *Chai* with one *yud*, and in *B'Nishmas* — with two *yuds*. And in all of them with a *patach*. c) In *Siddur Yaavetz*, he rules to say in *Baruch She'amar*, *Yishtabach*, and *B'Nishmas* — *Chai HaOlamim* with one *yud* and a *patach*, and in the *Piyut* of *Adereis V'HaEmunah* — *Lechai Olamim* and with a *patach*. d) In the *Siddur* of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe (author of the Shulchan Aruch and Tanya) regarding the above — *Chai HaOlamim* with one *yud* and a *tzeirei*. But in the *Piyut* of *Adereis V'HaEmunah* — *Lechai Olamim*, and so it is written in *Sefer Ohr Chadash*.

The *Magen Avraham* in *Orach Chaim* 281 does not reveal his opinion except regarding *B'Nishmas* (that it should be with a *tzeirei*), and his reasoning regarding *Baruch She'amar*, *Yishtabach*, and the *Piyut* of *Adereis V'HaEmunah* requires study. This doubt exists also in the opinion of the Gra. See also *Abudraham*, *Birkei Yosef*, and *Shaarei Teshuvah* to *Orach Chaim* 281. *Iyun Tefillah* in the *Otzar HaTefillos* series on *Birkas Baruch She'amar*. *Hagahos* of the Rishon LeTzion in the Mishnayos at the end of Tamid. And others.

#### 1031

**Mitzvah of Teshuvah:** See *Likkutei Biurim* in *Sefer HaTanya* (Karff), Vol. 2, p. 41, a Sicha of the Rebbe Shlita on this. *Chiddushim U'Biurim B'Shas*, Vol. 1, p. 136 and onwards.

**Sanctified through his thought:** See above, Vol. 1, p. 239, note 8. *Likkutei Levi Yitzchak, Igros*, p. 304-305.

## 1332

1332

B”H, 3 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., R’ Shmuel
May he live

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 14 Kislev, in which you ask regarding the source for the matter of naming sons and daughters—whether this belongs to the father or the mother. You wish to find support from what is written in Scripture, where sometimes the naming of a son was done by the father, such as, “And Avraham called the name of his son...” (Bereishis 21:3), and sometimes by the mother, as is the case with the tribes, regarding whom it is said, “And she called his name...”

**Response:**

1) In my opinion, one cannot derive a conclusion from the above. For example, the names of all the tribes (except Binyamin) were given by their mothers. It is not logical at all to say that the naming of **all** sons belongs to the mother and the father has no part in it, especially since we find in Scripture several instances of the naming of a newborn by the father, and other times by both [whether with one name (the name Yishmael) or with different names (Binyamin)], and sometimes even by others (Zerach, Peretz, Oved). See Shmuel II 12:24-25.

Perhaps the reason the names of the tribes were given by Rachel and Leah can be explained based on what our Sages said (Bereishis Rabbah, end of ch. 72): The matriarchs were prophetesses, and the patriarchs were secondary to them in prophecy, as it is written, “Whatever Sarah tells you, listen to her voice” (Shemos Rabbah, ch. 1; see also Likutei Torah for Shir Hashirim, s.v. *Kol Dodi*, ch. 4). As for the names Yitzchak and Esav, it could be said that they were also given by Sarah (Bereishis 21:6) and Rivkah (Rashi there 25:26, based on the Midrash Rabbah there and Tanchuma, Shemos 4).

2) Regarding the essence of the matter: Naming a child is, in general, a great thing and carries great responsibility. As is explained in many places in Chassidus, the name is the channel through which vitality and influence are drawn down to the thing being named (see at length in the Shelah, Introduction, final house; Tanya, Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah, end of ch. 1; Likutei Torah, Behar, s.v. *Es Shabbososei*, ch. 2; and elsewhere). Therefore, it is stated in the writings of the Arizal: When a person is born and his father and mother name him... the Holy One, blessed be He, places in their mouths that name which is necessary for that soul (Sefer HaGilgulim, Introduction 23; Emek HaMelech, Shaar 1, end of ch. 4; Ohr HaChaim, Devarim 29:17).

3) To whom does the naming belong? I have not heard an explicit instruction on this, but see the commentaries of the **Rishonim** (Hadar Zekeinim, Daas Zekeinim, and others) to Bereishis (38:5), on the verse, “And it was in Cheziv when she gave birth to him.” They state that the custom was that the first name belongs to the father, the second name belongs to the mother, and the third name to the father. This is the interpretation of the verse: **“And she called** his name...” [because it was Yehudah who was in Cheziv when she gave birth to him]. Therefore, in my opinion, in a place where there is no established custom, the naming should follow the aforementioned order. Even though the Ramban rejects this interpretation, that is only to say that this verse is not intended to explain a custom, but regarding the matter itself, there is no proof that he disagrees with the Rishonim. See also Ikarei HaDat (Yoreh Deah), 21:7, which cites a custom to name the first son born to a man after his father.

I am enclosing the Kuntres and the booklet for 19 Kislev, along with my general letter pertaining to them; Torah is best studied at its proper time.

With blessings.

## 1,333

B”H, 4 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Histadrut Tzeirei Agudas Yisrael
26 Achad HaAm St., Tel Aviv

Greetings and Blessings!

In due course, your invitation and request regarding the thirteenth anniversary of the founding of your movement in Eretz HaKodesh were received by the Rebbe shlita, and a telegram was sent from the Rebbe shlita, which reads as follows:

May Hashem grant you success.”

[The Rebbe’s] signature

I trust you will confirm receipt of the telegram.

With respect and blessing,

Secretary

## 1,137

B"H, 8 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...After requesting forgiveness, as this might be considered an intrusion on my part without having first received your permission, I rely upon what I have heard many times from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding the matter of ahavas Yisrael—to what extent every single Jew must be concerned with everything that happens to every other Jew, even if he has never seen him face-to-face. Therefore, I permit myself to touch upon this matter as well, which is:

Some time ago, when your brother visited me, in the course of our conversation I also asked about your family situation. He told me that for the time being, you are alone with your daughter. I was very surprised as to why you are not making an effort to search for a suitable shidduch. Surely you are aware of what our Sages have said regarding this, based on the verse, "In the morning sow your seed, and in the evening, etc." Especially since you are still far from the "evening," and with the help of Hashem, you can build a home in Yisrael, "a generation of the upright shall be blessed." It is obvious that, as our Sages say, "it is the way of a man to seek," and it is written, "Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do," which implies that there must be some hishtadlus on the part of the person as well. If this matter was necessary in all years, then how much more so in these years, after the terrible losses our Jewish people have suffered. Furthermore, given the scarcity of observant, G-d-fearing Jews, it is all the more certain and obvious that anyone who can be expected to establish an observant home—filled with the "candle of mitzvah and the Torah of light" and the inner light of Torah—is obligated to make every possible effort in this regard, for all of Yisrael are responsible for one another, and this is not merely a private matter of your own.

Once again, I ask forgiveness for writing to you regarding this, even though I do not know you, and I am confident that you will not take offense at this at all. The main thing is that you should contemplate this matter and make an effort to search for a suitable shidduch, and may Hashem grant you success.

With blessings for a good year in all the above.

## A'Shlach

B"H, 9 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...In response to your inquiry regarding the book *Zohar Torah*: I have seen it once, and as I recall, it is a translation of the Zohar into Hebrew, not a commentary on the Zohar. Therefore, I am puzzled: why would one study from a translation if one is able to study from the original Zohar? It is impossible for a **translation** to encompass all the interpretations, and consequently, it also lacks the same level of holiness present in the original language spoken by Rashbi and his *Chavraya*.

Regarding your question about your desire to wear *tefillin* of *Shimusha Rabba* and *Ra'avad*: it is perhaps advisable to begin wearing them after the age of forty. See the *sicha* of 14 Shevat, 5710, page 7.

Concerning your question regarding the writing of the *parshiyos* for these *tefillin* and the manner of wearing them: this is known to the *sofrim*. See also *Mishmeres Shalom*, section 4, and the additions at the end, where he cites the books that discuss this matter. Surely you have also seen in *Hayom Yom* regarding the study of the *shiurim* pertaining to each of these pairs of *tefillin*, as well as the manner of wearing them.

With blessings for *mazal tov*,

**M. Schneerson**

With blessing.
