## 1442

B.H., 12 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, etc., Rabbi Sholom Charitonov, shliach.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the 19th of Elul, the 8th and 22nd of Mar-Cheshvan, and the 4th of Kislev. I trust that the kuntresim (the entire series) as well as the kuntres of the 20th of Mar-Cheshvan and the letters enclosed with them were received in due time.

Regarding your letters:

1) I, too, desire to correspond more frequently, but what can I do? I have been made, as it were, no longer the master of my own time, due to the multitude of preoccupations, etc., etc. The delay in my response to letters and questions is, in the vast majority of cases, solely for this reason, and should not be attributed to other matters.

2) Please be so kind as to publicize once again among the administration and the students the general note from my letter of the 26th of Menachem Av, 5751: "I do not know — it is impossible to estimate," for what is stated there is, in my opinion, even more valid now than it was then. This publication will serve as a response to many questions.

3) Many thanks for the report on the students' activities in saving the souls of Jewish children and in disseminating the wellsprings of Chassidus. Regarding [the student]... shliach, and those like him: it is for the administration, and especially the spiritual leadership, to ensure that those students who are already involved in such tasks—and not necessarily those who have a knack for consistency in the avodah of tefillah, etc.—are the ones tasked with fundraising, registration, and the like. (It is understood that the process of removing them from their current duties must be done slowly and diplomatically, and a word to the wise is sufficient.) It is surprising that instructions are needed for such a matter, as it is simple. Incidentally, I wrote to the aforementioned regarding a change in his conduct concerning fasting and self-affliction at the end of the summer, and I do not know if he received my letter or if he heeded my advice.

4) Regarding [the student]... and his repeating of Chassidus by heart: since he is only fourteen years old, and furthermore his father objects, it should suffice for the time being that he repeats it only on days when there is no regular study schedule and on Yomim Tovim.

5) What does Hashem require of this generation of Tomchei Temimim? Who among us stands in the counsel of Hashem to know this clearly and answer this question? But what seems to be the case, at least on the surface, is that everything necessary and required has been prepared for us, and they have already fought our battles. We have nothing left to do but to **bring** the wellsprings outward. It has already been prepared for us, laid out on the plate with the utensils for eating, and almost all the opposition to the dissemination of the wellsprings has been removed...

Regarding the times for studying Chassidus, and the type and manner of study: in my opinion, it should be, as much as possible, as it was in Tomchei Temimim in the past. In addition to this, there is the matter of study for the sake of fluency, about which I wrote on the 7th of Chanukah, 5711, which in my opinion is a major fundamental.

## 1444

B"H, 12 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

To my dear friend, the illustrious Rav and Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc.
Rabbi Yeshaya, may he live, HaLevi

Greetings and blessings!

Enclosed is a response to the *pidyon nefesh* that was received through you, may you live. Due to several reasons, the response was delayed until now, and I ask for your forgiveness.

Regarding what you noted concerning that which is written in *Chassidus* in various places—among them *Likutei Torah* (Devarim 36d; Shir HaShirim 24a—in the name of the Baal Shem Tov; Devarim 71d, without attribution)—the interpretation regarding the *bas kol* (heavenly voice) that proclaims, "The *mazal* hears it" (see *Kesser Shem Tov*, Part I, 11a; at the beginning of Part II; Part II, 30, bottom of the page), it requires study, as it is already found in the *Shelah* (243b) in the name of *Sefer Chareidim*.

However, the explanation itself provides its own refutation, for the Baal Shem Tov explains it more deeply, which is not the case in the aforementioned sources. In the *drushim* in *Likutei Torah*, the addition of the Baal Shem Tov is the primary point, or at the very least, it is significant.

See *Tanya*, *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*, beginning of Chapter 11; and the explanation of the **Baal Shem Tov**, etc.; and in *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Acharei*; and it is likewise in *Midrash Tehillim*, etc. See also on this matter in the *Kuntres* of 18 Elul 5703, *Sicha* 3.

With blessings.

## A'shmah

B"H, 12 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

When I visit the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention you for *mazel tov* and for the building of a home in Yisrael—a building that will endure forever.

You surely know that the most effective way to influence another is by setting a personal example in one's own conduct in life. When one wishes to influence another by a *tefach*, one must increase one's own efforts by two *tefachim*. I consider it unnecessary to urge you, for if this is true regarding any fellow Jew, it is certainly true when it concerns one’s own son or daughter. In such cases, parents spare no effort or exertion, provided that it adds strength and courage to the structure being built by their child, ensuring it is established on firm and solid foundations. I am confident that you, on your part, will do as mentioned above. It is known from our Sages that when a person sanctifies himself (which has two meanings: making oneself holy, and separating oneself from matters one held onto until now), they sanctify him greatly from Above.

I will conclude as I began, with a blessing of *mazel tov*, and may you and your wife see *Yiddishe nachas* and *Chassidishe nachas* from your daughter and her husband, and from your second daughter as well.

With blessings for *mazel tov* and appropriate blessings.

P.S. I consider it unnecessary to ask you regarding assistance for the shlichus of the esteemed Rav and Chossid, Rabbi Yosef haLevi Weinberg, for surely, even without this, you are exerting yourself in this matter to the best of your ability.

## 1541

16 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to hear greetings from your shul and the mispalelim in general, and of your participation in the various activities that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, established and led. These activities continue to be conducted with the help of Hashem, and like every living thing, they keep growing and expanding. Therefore, I am certain that your participation will also grow from time to time.

A shul, a beis medrash, is, as the name indicates, a place that gathers together and unites many Yidden, may they increase. It goes without saying that there are various categories of people among them, but the essence of the shul unites them.

There is also a union of people for another reason, such as a business partnership. However, there is a fundamental difference between that union and the one mentioned above.

When people unite for business, it is not a true union, because one partner goes along with the other so that he may derive his own benefit from it. In other words, he seeks in the other that which he himself can use; he does not seek the other person, but rather himself. Therefore, it happens that when one of them calculates that he cannot derive the proper personal profit from the other, the union falls apart.

Fundamentally different is a union based on the foundation of Torah and mitzvos in general, and a shul in particular. Here, Yidden do not unite for personal, material profit, but to carry out a matter of Torah and mitzvos, tefillah, and tzedakah. They are united by the general idea of doing the will of the Ribono shel Olam, which in general is expressed through ahavas Hashem, ahavas haTorah, and ahavas Yisrael. Such a union can also endure for all time, just as Torah and mitzvos are eternal.

I send you my blessing that your shul should be a true beis medrash, where all the members and mispalelim are united with the thought of "and they shall all form a single band to do Your will with a whole heart." This also opens the way to receive the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam for everyone, in whatever they need, with children, life, and ample sustenance.

With blessings.

## 1,447

B"H, 15 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The Administration of Chabad Institutions in the Holy Land, may it be built and established,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to questions regarding my opinion on the division of roles and authority between the administration of the Chabad institutions in the Holy Land, Agudas Chabad, and the auditors, which were discussed in my previous letters... for the sake of clarity, I am stating once again my opinion regarding the aforementioned division of roles:

1. As I wrote in my previous letters to Agudas Chabad, it is good and proper that each institution should have its own autonomy and maintain a direct connection with here, and that Agudas Chabad should not interfere in the internal affairs of the institutions.

2. Agudas Chabad shall represent the institutions externally in matters where it is necessary for the Chabad institutions to act as a single bloc. Therefore, the administration of Agudas Chabad must include a representative from each of the institutions; indeed, there is currently a representative from each institution on the board.

3. The role of the auditors is, as the word implies, *bikores* (auditing/reviewing)—that is, to review the work of the institutions' administration, to maintain a direct connection with here, and to report on what is happening in the institution. Therefore, the institution's administration must describe their work to them, show them the accounting books, etc., but the auditor does not have the authority to issue orders, change the administration's decisions, or make decisions for the institution.

4. It is self-understood that both Agudas Chabad and the auditors are permitted to submit proposals to the institution's administration—and furthermore, they are obligated to do so if they find matters that are inconsistent with the institution's purpose or matters that are generally detrimental—but all of this is only in the form of a proposal.

5. As a result of all the above, the responsibility for the development of each and every institution rests upon the administration of that institution, and it is they who must take all necessary steps for the institution's existence and development. Likewise, the responsibility rests upon the auditors to know all the details of the institution's work, to suggest necessary improvements according to their opinion (solely as a proposal, as mentioned above), and to inform here if there are any matters or details that are harmful or inconsistent with the institution.

I hope that after all the above, there is no room for doubts or interpretations that are not in accordance with my opinion. As with my letter of 19 Kislev, I request that all institutions confirm receipt of this letter. And peace be upon Israel.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1747

15 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the twelfth annual celebration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in the United States, may they live:

Shalom u’vracha!

With pleasure, I greet and offer a blessing from the depths of my heart to all the participants in the celebration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in the United States. By your very presence here, you express your desire and will to merit the great privilege of providing and continuing your support for the Merkaz Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim.

All American Jews who look with open eyes and warm interest at the Jewish situation in this country recognize the indescribably great achievement that my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, accomplished in America through his work in general, and through his yeshivos in particular.

The powerful and profound impact that the Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim exert on American Jewish life, and the model of mesiras nefesh for Yiddishkeit that the students of these yeshivos demonstrate, is a universally recognized fact.

The Merkaz Yeshivas is currently experiencing a difficult financial crisis which not only hinders the highly necessary expansion of the yeshivos, but also, G-d forbid, places the already existing institutions in danger.

The greatness of the mitzvah of tzedakah is well known. Often, however, people make calculations to limit their giving of tzedakah for various reasons.

It must be recognized that the Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim are among the most important factors upon which depends the existence not only of the study of Torah with yiras shamayim—which in itself is a fundamental pillar of the existence of the Jewish people—but also of the individual and communal Jewish life, which must be influenced by the spirit of Yiddishkeit and Torah. When faced with problems of such vital importance, the reasons for limitations and calculations regarding the support that must unconditionally be given fall away.

I hope and wish to be certain that you all, friends of the Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, will make the greatest effort and provide maximum support in order to cover the deficits of the Merkaz Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim and enable them to continue their work.

Hashem does not remain a debtor, and He will surely help all those who fulfill their duty in everything they need.

I conclude my appeal with the words of the Rebbe, my revered father-in-law, of blessed memory, from his final letter to the participants of the annual dinner of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in the year 5710, and these are his words:

"May Hashem strengthen the health of you all and grant you all good parnassah in abundance, and may we all and our families, may they live, merit the raising of the horn of Torah and the horn of the Jewish people, and may we merit the imminent Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, who shall lead us upright to our Holy Land, speedily in our days."

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1048

B.H., 17 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc.,
Rabbi [Schneur Zalman] may he live,

Peace and blessing!

...According to the information I received from the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, occupied with communal needs, Rabbi Binyamin may he live, Gorodetzky, you have already received the permit for travel to Morocco. I am distressed that the matter is being delayed so much, at a time when every single day there is the potential to accomplish great and hidden things there. It is well known that "days were fashioned, and for Him one of them" (*Tehillim* 139:16) — written with a *vav* and not an *alef*. The meaning of this is that there must be *avodah* every single day, and every day that passes without being utilized as it should be is an irretrievable loss. For every moment of the days that follow must be filled with its own content, and there is no room left for the content of the previous days. This is regarding the personal reckoning. Regarding others, the sons and daughters of Yisroel in Morocco who could receive positive influence in spirituality during these days are not at all to blame, and they should not have to suffer in the slightest from any "politics" regarding the personal matters of one who could have influenced them, or through whom they could have been influenced with what they need. I am not coming to preach, but rather to speak of what is practical, and as is known, the Zohar states that *asiyah* (action) is supreme.

4) Regarding what you wrote concerning the isolation (*elendkeit*) in Morocco, there is a large settlement of Jews there — may they increase — and the Ribono shel Olam Himself is present there as well. My hope is that in the not-too-distant future, more families from anash will come to live there. It is possible, and quite likely, that there will be work found there for your wife, may she live, as well. Obviously, not for the entire day, but once you are already on-site, I hope you will find a way for her to also assist in the *avodah*, just as you wrote to me that even while you were in Marseille, she assisted you in your work.

I hope to hear good news from you regarding your health and the health of your wife, may she live, in physical matters, and also good news regarding all of the above.

With blessing.

## 1549

B"H, 17 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote in your letter concerning yourself, that you are learning with some youths and you request a blessing: May it be the will of Hashem that you succeed with them in every detail, and that they grow to be Chassidim, G-d-fearing, and scholars. However, in general, I am surprised by you; as I have written to you previously, I am astonished that you have left your place—and I hope that this is only temporary—in the vineyard of Chabad, at a time when there is work to be done in our own domain, Chabad, and especially for those who have the capacity to act in the field of chinuch.

It is difficult to point a finger from such a distance as to the specific manner in which you should return and participate in the work of Chabad, and especially in your profession of chinuch. But surely, on the spot, if you only contemplate it and exert the *tzurah* (form/intellect) over the *chomer* (matter), you will easily find a way to continue your activities in this field. And as per the promise of our Nesi'im, our Rebbeim, it will surely be with success, and you will be able to bring me good news.

With blessings.

## A'shn

B"H, 17 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

And according to what is written in Toras Kohanim at the beginning of Parshas Bechukosai, cited by Rashi on the Torah there, when the number of those working increases twofold, the work and the effect of the mitzvos grow even more than twofold, for those who are few in number are not like those who are many. I look forward to hearing good news regarding this.

With blessings.

## 1551

B"H, 17 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the distinguished Rabbi, the pious Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi [Mordechai] HaKohen, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter of 6 Teves, as well as the one preceding it, in which you inform me that you have settled in the city [of Milan], and have already succeeded in communal activity regarding a public shiur, and have also made a beginning—though, for the time being, a small one—regarding the matter of the mikveh. I was very distressed that this matter is being delayed. As is known, the matter of taharas hamishpachah is not merely a private matter or mitzvah; rather, it touches upon the essence and life of the children who will be born, and it also influences the essence and general character of the husband and wife, as is explained in many books, both in the revealed and the hidden aspects of Torah. It is also known what even the Acharonim*—and even those of the world—have ruled, that it is permitted to sell a shul in order to arrange for a mikveh. See also the Tosafos Yom Tov at the end of Maseches Yoma on the Mishnah: "Happy are you, Yisrael, before Whom you purify yourselves... The Mikveh of Yisrael is Hashem; just as a mikveh purifies the impure, so too does the Holy One, blessed be He, purify Yisrael." Explanations of this are surely superfluous; I have only come to urge you regarding this matter, as per the command of our Sages in Sifra, beginning of Parshas Tzav, and also so that you may have a pretext and an opening to urge your baalei batim once again to do everything necessary in this matter as soon as possible.

2) Likewise, I am sure you are occupying yourself with the appropriate vigor regarding the matter of chinuch, where, according to information I have from some time ago, there is a vast field in your city, and very little opposition in proportion. If effort in propaganda does not return empty, then how much more so regarding concrete actions undertaken with great vigor. And I trust that the pious Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, Rabbi Yaakov, may he live, a shochet and bodek, will assist you as much as possible...

4) Thank you for the telegram regarding your farbrengen on the past holiday of 19 Kislev. Enclosed is a copy of a general letter in connection with the "Holiday of Holidays," which is the day of 19 Kislev; please be so kind as to inform those who gathered of its content.

With blessings for success in your holy work and regards,

**M. Schneerson**

* Ein Yitzchak, Orach Chaim 63.

## 1,052

B.H., 17 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

I have received your *pidyon nefesh* for your mother, *tichyeh*.

One must be strong in *bitachon* in Hashem Yisbarach that He will help so that her health improves. One must ensure that she is under the care of doctors; if she is in a hospital, this is certainly the case. From time to time, one should inquire as to how she is doing, as this inquiry itself influences the hospital staff, who, seeing that there is interest in her, will improve their treatment of her.

And above all, as a son, you must be careful with the three *shiurim* that *kavod kedushas moreinu v’rabbeinu Admur ztzuklaleh-h nebga-m zya* established: *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*. Also, recite five chapters of *Tehillim* every day in order, specifically for the health of your mother, *tichyeh*. May Hashem Yisbarach help that you should be able to report soon that your mother’s health has improved and is continuing to get better and better.

With blessings for Torah study with *yiras shamayim*.

## 1,353

I am certain that you are utilizing your positive influence upon your relatives. Hashem does not remain a debtor; when Hashem sees that one does a favor for a fellow Jew—whether a relative or a stranger, whether a favor in material matters or a favor in spiritual matters—He adds His blessing to the one who performs the favor many times over.

## 1,353

B"H, 18 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter containing a *pidyon nefesh* on behalf of your daughter and son-in-law, that they may be blessed with children. When I visit the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will read it there.

You write at the end of your letter, "And I will, G-d willing, distribute much money for Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch when we are blessed." This statement does not sit well with me, for why should one enter into conditions with the *Ribono shel Olam*? It is known from our Sages that one who gives a *sela* to *tzedakah* so that [their child may live], etc., is considered a *tzaddik gamur*. Nevertheless, we do not find in their words a condition that they will give only after the request is fulfilled. Surely, you yourself understand that when there is a question of who is more reliable, the *Ribono shel Olam* is certainly the most trustworthy, and He is also all-powerful.

I am interested to know about your *kvius itim*—your fixed times for study—in *Toras HaNigleh* and *Toras HaChassidus*, and I am certain that you are also careful to recite *Tehillim* every day.

With blessings,

## 1,354

B"H, 18 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, who occupies himself with the needs of the community in faith, etc., etc., Moreinu Harav Shlomo Yosef, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...For the time being, the volumes of the encyclopedia that you sent have not reached me. In the meantime, I trust that the *piskei dinim* and the volumes of *Sdei Chemed* that were sent from here have reached you...

Regarding what you write concerning the matter of caution, etc., and the times of my *avodah* here: for the most part, this is not within my control. What can I do? It is impossible to trim any more time, for even as it is, everyone complains about the delay in my responses to them, about why *maamarim* and *sichos* are not being printed and published, why there is no money in the treasury, why I do not have assistants, etc., etc. Naturally, the complaints are directed at me. May it be the will of Hashem that everything be for the good, and that the strength and time be utilized for matters of value...

With a blessing for proper health and for success in your *avodah*.

And on another note: In the Rambam, *Hilchos Deios*, Chapter 4, it seems to me that a word was omitted in the printings, and it should read: "It is one of the ways of the **avodah** of Hashem." The same applies to the end of Chapter 3 there as well.

P.S. Enclosed is a copy of a general letter for 19 Kislev; I hope it will be of interest to you.

Some time ago, I asked the Chief Rabbi whether any rectification had been made so that one could travel on Jewish-owned ships, given that they also travel on Shabbos. I have not yet received a response. Perhaps you are aware if any rectification has been made regarding this, as I am sometimes approached with questions about it.

## 1551

B"H, 18 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Chaim Hillel, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter with the *pidyon nefesh*, regarding the birth of your daughter, may she live, for *mazal tov*, and her being named in Israel Esther Hadassa, may she live: I hereby express my blessing of *mazal tov*. May you and your wife, may she live, raise her to Torah, to the *chuppah*, and to good deeds, with peace of mind and physical well-being.

It is known from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (the Rashab), of blessed memory, that our custom is to say "to **Torah**, to the *chuppah*, and to good deeds" even upon the birth of a daughter, based on the words of our Sages (Berachos 17a): "How do women merit? By sending their children to learn... by waiting for their husbands... and by guarding their children..."

I was pleased to read in your letter that you are encouraging parents who, for various reasons, were unable to circumcise their sons, regarding the necessity of this matter, and that you have also succeeded in this. Regarding what you wrote—that you have certain questions concerning the *bris*, since there will not be a *minyan*, etc.—you should turn to the *rabbonim* of *anash* in your area and explain the details of the situation to them, as they are familiar with the local circumstances, and they will instruct you on what you must do. See *Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah* 265:6.

Regarding your question concerning the study with the students: since they only study for a short time, what is better—to *daven* with them or to study *Chumash* and the like? Generally, these students are almost all before *bar mitzvah*. Therefore, one must strive to study with them matters of practical application—that is, the *halachos* they require—and also to ground them in the study of *Chumash* and the like. The method of studying *halachos* also includes the *b'po'al mamash* (the practical application) aspect; therefore, one must also *daven* with them every day in a way that they become accustomed to *Krias Shema*, *Shemoneh Esrei*, *Birkos HaShachar*, *Birkos Hanehenin*, and the like.

Enclosed is a general letter in connection with the "Festival of Festivals," the 19th of Kislev. I am certain you will publicize it in an appropriate manner.

With blessings for success in your work and in your personal matters.

## 150

B"H, 18 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Following our telephone conversation, I felt that you have not yet fully internalized the importance of health in general, and specifically regarding eating food before davening. I am therefore transcribing here a teaching from the Baal Shem Tov HaKadosh, printed in Kesser Shem Tov. You are surely aware of what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, said at the final farbrengens: that a Chossid must study the Kesser Shem Tov and the Ohr Torah of the Maggid of Mezritch.

In Kesser Shem Tov, Part 1, page 17 (of the edition I have), it states: "When one’s body is ill, his soul is also weakened, and he cannot daven properly, even if he is free of transgressions. Therefore, a person must guard the health of his body very carefully."

With blessings for proper health, and that you may be able to share good news. And surely you also remember what we discussed regarding approaching the Sephardic community in your city for assistance with our work in Morocco.

## 1558

B"H, 19 Teves, 5712

It is to be hoped that in the near future there will finally be results from the work of the Coordinating Committee. If, even by that time, it is not possible to have educational institutions under our authority established within the "non-affiliated" stream, this will cause a loss that I do not know if it will be possible to rectify later.

Please circulate my aforementioned general letter among the administrations of the Chabad institutions, and inform me of your opinion regarding it, unofficially.

With a blessing for proper health for you and your wife, may they live,

**M. Schneerson**

## 159

23 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Agudas Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

...I learned by chance (though it is a known principle of the Baal Shem Tov that everything is by Divine Providence) that the Department of Culture and Education in Eretz Yisrael has received hundreds of thousands of books from the spoils of the Nazis, may their names be blotted out. These books have already arrived in Eretz Yisrael, and they are now searching for the owners. Furthermore, the Ministry of Religious Affairs intends to distribute a portion of these books—especially those pertaining to religion—among the yeshivos and institutions in Eretz Yisrael. It seems this information is accurate, as they provide several specific details.

Therefore, I suggest that you prepare a request and demand as soon as possible, covering two points: 
a) Perhaps it is possible to ascertain whether there are any books there from the library of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. 
b) To demand that they allocate a specific and significant portion of these books for our yeshivos in Eretz Yisrael, such as Yeshivas Lod and Toras Emes. It may also be possible to include the yeshivos in Kfar Chabad and Tel Aviv if they are also distributing to such institutions. 

It is understood that if any books from the library of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, are found, they must be received and sent here. Regarding the books for the yeshivos, beyond the importance of the matter in itself, it is essential that in all such matters, all institutions and ministries should know that they are obligated to allocate a specific portion to the Chabad institutions in Eretz Yisrael.

5) I urge you—regarding the future, do not rely on my learning of such matters by chance (even if it is through Divine Providence). Rather, one of the members of the Agudas Chabad committee should take an interest in such matters and the like (and certainly, you must take care that it does not become a case of "a pot belonging to partners" [where no one takes responsibility]). Please inform me here as soon as possible.

6) I was visited by the G-d-fearing man, Rabbi Aryeh Leib Gelman. According to what he said, he will return to Eretz Yisrael in three or four weeks. It is appropriate to prepare for that time a specific plan of what should be demanded of him in his capacity as chairman of the Coordination Committee in Eretz Yisrael. This is in continuation of the memorandum that was submitted to him some time ago regarding the requirements of our institutions in Eretz Yisrael (which made a good impression on him; he even informed me here of this, noting that Chabad were the only ones who presented him with detailed information regarding their work). 

I demanded of him, regarding the practical implementation, that as soon as the funds are received, he should not delay, and that they should give Chabad the necessary means to begin actual operations. Of course, he could not give me a clear answer, as ultimately the Mizrachi must also receive assistance in this. However, if you demand it once, twice, and three times—and in his heart, he also desires this—it is possible to rely on his assistance. Then, one can hope for an earlier receipt of funds and also for a larger sum. Of course, the practical outcome will depend on the timing of the funds being sent from here (when there are details on this, I will inform you), but in any case, all preparations for this, including putting pressure on Mr. Gelman, should be done as early as possible.

7) I have learned that the yeshivos and Talmud Torahs in Eretz Yisrael can receive assistance through three channels: the Committee of Yeshivos, the Ministry of Religious Affairs, and the Ministry of Welfare. Please inform me of the details regarding this—concerning each of the institutions, whether they receive from the aforementioned [offices] and how much from each, and also if it is possible to do more from here regarding this...

I await a response to all of the above, as well as to my previous letters, and the sooner the better. Thank you in advance.

With blessings for success in your holy work,

**M. Schneerson**

160

## 1361

23 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter of the 18th of Teves, as well as the one preceding it, and the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed. I read it at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukl"l, nbg"m, zy"a*, and I pray that the *Ribono shel Olam* will awaken compassion upon you for true health.

Regarding what you wrote—that you may have caused displeasure in your previous letter by stating that you were not satisfied with the phrasing of the response—Heaven forbid, there is no displeasure here at all. However, there is a certain sense of *nefilas ruach* (lowered spirits) in this, because my intention in my response was the opposite of how you interpreted it. As is explained regarding the phrase "great is the power of the promises of the *tzaddikim*," it was clear to me that the promises of the *tzaddikim* must, in the end, be fulfilled. Consequently, there was nothing left for you to do but to decide for yourself—*op paskenen ba zich*—with absolute certainty, as the expression of Rabbi R.Y.M. of Poltava goes: "This is how the matter is." But since you interpreted my phrasing to the contrary, I am also perplexed, for I do not know what else to answer you. As is known from the saying of the Rebbe Maharash, "Letters are the *yechidah* in the soul," and the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, "Sometimes one answers what answers itself," and the saying of the *Chassidim*, that the response received by a certain person depends to a certain extent on how the recipient interprets it—especially if the recipient is a person of stature who stands by his own opinion, similar to what is stated in the *Mishnah* (beginning of *Horayos*), "This is the rule: one who relies on himself..." In any case, as for your request for forgiveness in your letter, there is no place for that at all. It goes without saying that there is no room here for any matter of "dismissal," Heaven forbid. If the concept of dismissal is ruled out at all times, then certainly in these days—the *ikvesa d'meshicha* (heels of Moshiach), where we are treading one step after another—the closeness and unity are paramount. As the Tzemach Tzedek said: "When *Chassidim* are united, they will go to meet Moshiach."

I was pleased to hear from the esteemed *Chossid*, *yerei shamayim*, and *baal avodah*, Rabbi Ben Zion Shemtov, *shye*, about your teaching in public. He also complained to me that he noticed a certain *nefilas ruach* in you. I implore you to contemplate the magnitude of the mission entrusted to us by our *Nasi*, *ztzukl"l, nbg"m, zy"a*. Who can compare or be likened to us, given that such a mission rests upon our shoulders? It is similar to what Rashbi says, "I am merely a sign," and as explained in *Chassidus*: since he had no existence of his own, he could say, "I have seen the sons of the *aliyah* (ascension), and they are few..." And even though who is the one who can take this upon himself? Yet, because every *Chossid* possesses the power of the Rebbe, it is—at the very least—in a state of concealment, as it should be. In the *Chossid*, this is a concealment that exists in reality, and furthermore, it is close to revelation. Therefore, there should be no lack of *breitkeit* (breadth/expansiveness). One only needs to ask the *Ribono shel Olam* to utilize this—*oistznitzn dos*—as one should and for what one should, especially regarding the study of Torah. As is known, the difference between Torah and *tefillah* is that *tefillah*—especially *tefillah* on weekdays—is from below to above and from a place of constriction (*meitzar*), while Torah—especially the study of *Chassidus*, the "Tree of Life"—is from above to below, and with *breitkeit*.

With blessings for true health and to hear good tidings, *tche"i*, in general, and regarding your health in particular.

Enclosed is the general letter in connection with the "Festival of Festivals," the 19th of Kislev.

## 1662

27 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings!

I have received your letter of 24 Teves, in which you describe your situation, the fact that you have seen the doctor’s report and how it has affected you, and how you are imagining the future. Because of this, you are reciting Tehillim and praying to Hashem, and you ask for my opinion.

**Answer:**

The fact that you are reciting Tehillim and praying to the Ribono shel Olam is certainly good, for He, blessed be He, is the Master of the entire world and of every person with all their details. However, regarding what you write—that you have been dwelling on the doctor’s report and imagining the future—I do not agree with you, for that does not belong to you at all, and it is not for that purpose that you were created.

Rabbi Dov Yehuda Shochet, may he live, writes to me that you are a Jew who is a *baal Torah* and *mitzvos*. Consequently, it is certain that you believe that Hashem Yisbarach is the *Adon Olam*—the Master of the world. We see even in human management that when one is a good manager, everything is organized so that one thing does not interfere with another, and every part of the management serves the purpose for which it was created. If this is true for a human being, who is limited in all his affairs and can, at times, even make a mistake, then *kal v’chomer* it is certainly true regarding the management of the Ribono shel Olam: that every thing, wherever it is found, must fulfill its goal and perfection—its completion—in **its** *shlichus*. When one grabs hold of a different matter, there are two deficiencies in this: a) Since it is not suited to its own matter, it only causes damage; b) It draws one away—diverts one—from fulfilling the *shlichus* for which it was truly designated.

All that has been said above is also applicable to your situation. Due to many reasons, which are certainly by *hashgacha pratis*, your profession is not medicine. Since you were raised as a Jew who is a *shomer Torah u’mitzvos*, we know two things: a) Medical matters are not your *shlichus* from Hashem in this world; b) Guarding *Torah u’mitzvos*—which also includes the *mitzvah* of "Love your fellow as yourself," "You shall surely rebuke," etc., and also as it is written in the *sefer Tanna D’bei Eliyahu*, "If you see a naked person, clothe him"—meaning that when you see a Jew who is "naked" of *Torah u’mitzvos*, one must endeavor to clothe him with *Torah u’mitzvos*—this is your goal and the *shlichus* for which you were created.

From this, it is understandable that when you offer conjectures and opinions in the science of medicine, firstly, it diverts you from carrying out **your** *shlichus* for which you are designated. Secondly, in matters of your health, you could, *chas v’shalom*, only cause damage, but in no way can you fix it. The damage in this can be, *chas v’shalom*, that because of agitation, you imagine things that will **not be**. Consequently, this weakens your *mazal* and weakens your *bitachon* in Hashem Yisbarach through your dwelling on and delving into what the doctor says, what that professor might think, and so on.

Since you ask for my opinion, I tell you that you must conduct yourself as the *Torah Hakedosha* demands. The Torah says that it—the Torah—has given permission to **heal**; that is to say, the Torah has given permission for people to turn to doctors, and has given permission and capability to the doctors, only to heal and fix the person. Therefore, the world is conducted such that one goes to a doctor and then does what they instruct to do. You have nothing more to do in this matter, and you must leave it to the doctor. What you must do is be certain in Hashem Yisbarach that you will have long days and years. According to the verse, "The fear of Hashem leads to life," the stronger your *bitachon* in Hashem Yisbarach is, the fewer doubts you have, and the more you devote yourself to carrying out your *shlichus* in the world—as mentioned earlier—to guard *Torah u’mitzvos* and also to influence others in this direction, the more long days and years you will have, literally, without any forced interpretations. Forget entirely about the report and what you have read in medical books, for that is not your *shlichus* and it does not belong to you at all. Since it does not belong to you, it cannot make you better, and generally, it makes things worse, *chas v’shalom*.

You should see to it to recite a *yom Tehillim* every day (as the Tehillim is divided into the days of the month) after *davening* in the morning, and study *Chumash* with *Rashi* every day, and also take part in the *shiurim* that are studied in public, at least one of which should be the study of *Chassidus*. And, it goes without saying, set for yourself the goal (*matara*) as it is written in the verse, and as the Baal Shem Tov Hakedosh demanded of *Chassidim*: "Serve Hashem with joy." "Serve" means in *davening* and learning, and also in eating and drinking, and all other things that a person does, and even in sleeping, as the *Rambam* writes in *Hilchos Deios*. When you do this, you will begin to feel better and better, and you will become healthier and healthier, and you will be able to report good news to me regarding this.

It would also be appropriate that every day before *davening* in the morning and before *Mincha*, you should give a few pennies to *tzedakah* (naturally, excluding Shabbos and Yom Tov).

I hope and am certain that you will accept my suggestion and instructions as stated, and will let me know about all this as soon as possible.

With blessings for good health and a speedy recovery, and may you be able, with peace of mind and peace of body, to fulfill your *shlichus* in this world for long, good days and years, and to be a *Chossid*.

P.S. You are surely participating in the *Chassidishe farbrengens* which are being organized [...] in your city.

## 1364

1364

B"H, 23 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, active in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Yosef, may he live, Halevi

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 18 Teves, 5712, and I trust that in the meantime you have also received my letter along with the enclosures.

1) I was happy to read in your letter that the fundraising campaign is proceeding successfully. May Hashem grant that in the days to come, this success continues in a fitting manner, and also in increased quantity in the literal sense. I am sure you will continue to keep me informed in this regard.

2) I was pleased to read in your letter that you intend to travel in the coming days to Rhodesia and visit the large towns there. Surely, even there, you will conduct yourself according to the wishes of my father-in-law, the Rebbe: not only to gather material things, but also to sow spirituality. I am certain you will succeed in finding those of the lineage of Anash there, and to awaken and stir them regarding their ancestral roots. It would be excellent if you were to research and inquire about other nearby countries and visit them as well.

3) I was pleased to read in your letter about your arrangement to study with Rabbi... may he live, and today I also received his letter. I am sure you will find ways to ensure that the impression and desire for this study remain with him, even after you have departed from there.

4) It is very good that you are encouraging the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, active in communal needs, Rabbi Yirmiyah, may he live, Alay, regarding the great necessity of organizing farbrengens and shiurim from time to time. You should also look into the possibility of publishing articles on Chassidus and Chassidim in the local press in the language of the country. Surely you will find material already prepared from what has been published until now in English, such as *Sefer HaZichronos* and transcriptions of the sichos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in English, as well as in *HaKriah VeHaKedushah*, and the like.

5) Regarding the youth, I am sending you by mail, in a separate envelope, what was transcribed here from the sichos with the students here. Perhaps you will be able to utilize this in a fitting manner.

6) Regarding your notification concerning Mrs... may she live, that they have decided to perform surgery on her one eye without waiting a long time: May it be the will of Hashem that the surgery goes well and that she returns to full health soon. I do not know the custom there, but if there is a *ner tamid* in the shul, she should participate in it (though not initiate it from scratch). If there is no such arrangement, she should take upon herself, for a certain period, the expense of the candles in the shul. Surely she lights candles on Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov, and it is good that she set aside money for the charity of *Rambae"n* (Rabbi Meir Baal HaNes) before lighting the candles.

7) Enclosed is a letter to... may he live, and thank you for the trouble of delivering it to him.

8) Enclosed is a transcript of the sicha before the students, may they live, on the fifth night of Chanukah, as well as a transcript of the sicha before the *baalei batim* and activists of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim during their visit with me.

9) I happened to see—and as is known, the Baal Shem Tov’s principle is that everything is by Divine Providence—about the elderly Rabbi, R' Chaim Yosef Isser Halevi LeBeis Gad, may he live, of Johannesburg, who published the sefer *R' Ephraim* on the Torah. It would be appropriate, if it is suitable, to encourage him. Likewise, if there are other authors in the places you are visiting, they should send everything they have published to my library. You should also suggest that they send them in exchange for Chassidic texts, etc., published by Kehot. I also request—if it is not too much of a burden—that if you encounter rare books or those that are not easily found, and it is possible to exchange them for the aforementioned books published by Kehot, you should do so. This will be a double benefit: they will receive the books of Chassidus, etc., and it is inevitable that at some point they will study them, and the aforementioned books will be here, which surely contain inner content as well.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and regards to all of Anash, and especially to the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, active in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Yirmiyah, may he live.

## 1565

B"H, 23 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Avraham Chanoch, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter of 18 Teves with pleasure, as well as those that preceded it. I also see in the issues of *HaModia* your articles regarding the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and the celebration of 19 Kislev. Thank you, thank you for your efforts in this matter, which is part of the preparation for spreading the wellsprings outward—that is, when they are disseminated, they will be received well. Surely there are those who have been stirred by this to develop a desire to seek out the wellsprings, and I trust you will continue in this path further. Since I am not certain that all issues of *HaModia* containing your articles reach here, it would be appropriate for you to send a clipping of your article each time.

Regarding your question as to whether such articles should be printed in non-Chareidi newspapers: it is difficult to provide a general answer for all newspapers. On the face of it, if such articles were printed without the byline of a Chareidi individual, there would be no concern of spiritual harm, provided the content is appropriate. Naturally, this is only a general observation, and each instance must be evaluated based on the specific newspaper and the article itself. But in general, in the manner described above—where the secular newspaper cannot claim that so-and-so, a Chareidi individual, is among its editors or contributors—there is no concern in this.

I would like to propose the following: Since we are planning to publish *Beis Rebbe* (in Hebrew) once again, and since Hashem has graced you with a scribe’s pen, perhaps you could take it upon yourself to transcribe into clear Hebrew all the stories regarding the Alter Rebbe, as well as those regarding the Mitteler Rebbe and the Tzemach Tzedek, which are brought in the sichos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Each should be in a separate manuscript. Please also inform me how much time this would take you (to prepare the first booklet) and what your compensation would be for this work. It is understood that if this is printed, it will be noted that it was transcribed by so-and-so. It is also necessary to include references at the end of the booklet or in the footnotes, indicating the source of the story in the sichos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe...

Awaiting good news regarding the above.

Enclosed is a copy of a general letter in connection with the "Festival of Festivals," 19 Kislev. Please publish it, as it is difficult to send it to everyone individually from here.

## 1,366

B"H, 23 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

Toward the end of last summer, I wrote to you regarding your conduct, specifically concerning the matter of fasting. To date, I have not received a response from you on this subject. Furthermore, I am unaware of the nature of your learning and your engagement in the avodah of tefillah.

I am writing now to prompt you and to request that you inform me about this as soon as possible. I am certain that you are increasing your strength and vigor in maintaining the schedule of your study of Nigleh and Chassidus, as well as in the avodah of tefillah. It is understood that there is no contradiction between this and maintaining physical health, for a person has the capacity for both, as the Rambam writes in the fourth chapter of Hilchos Deios: that keeping the body healthy is among the ways of Hashem, and it is the intention of the heart that matters. In general, every Chossid—and especially a student in the higher classes of the Yeshiva—serves as an example to others, particularly to the students in the lower classes. Since the responsibility is very great, you have been granted very great strengths, such that you also have the capacity to be one who is "moistened in order to moisten others" [i.e., to influence others], and the matter depends solely on you.

To bring this out from concealment (for this is a concealment that exists in reality, and is close to revelation) and to bring it into actual practice through the "candle of a mitzvah and the Torah of light," and the "light of the Torah"—this is the Torah of Chassidus.

I await good news regarding all of the above.

## 1367

B"H, 23 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs, etc.,

Greetings and blessings!

... 2) I was pleased to read about the raising of the spirit of the study of Nigleh, and about the benefit he sees from the visit and the examination in Nigleh by the esteemed Rabbi, who engages in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Eliezer Kresik, may he live. The Yeshiva and the institutions must strive for the good of the institution, which, in the natural order of things, will also be good for the students of the institutions. In accordance with this, they must strive all the more for the growth of the institution. Consequently, it is necessary that they be able to show and say, "See the great ones that I have raised," and not be satisfied with the announcement that the older students have traveled to another country, etc., as I have already written in previous letters regarding this matter.

4) Regarding your suggestion that students from here travel to study in the institutions in Eretz Yisroel, may it be rebuilt speedily, for the time being, this is connected with great difficulties, especially since the students here are accustomed to such comforts, etc., and not all the parents are satisfied in any case with their education in Lubavitch. I await good tidings regarding all of the above.

## 1368

23 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you through the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, who is engaged in communal needs, etc., R. Yosef Weinberg, and also to learn from him of your heartfelt participation and assistance to him in his shlichus.

It is certain that Hashem will repay you many times over, in all the matters that you and your family require. However, it troubles me to read in his letter that you are not in good spirits and are feeling down. This surprises me greatly, for when one gives tzedakah and supports the Almighty’s kosher institutions and the like, one becomes a partner with the Ribono shel Olam. What greater joy can there be than connecting oneself with the Ribono shel Olam? And with what can one have stronger bitachon that "everything the Merciful One does is for the good" than when one is connected to the Ribono shel Olam? As the Alter Rebbe writes in Tanya, a person who gives tzedakah elevates the remaining money and assets that he has left. Furthermore, as the Alter Rebbe explains at length in Iggeres HaKodesh, through the mitzvah of tzedakah, the Ribono shel Olam bestows goodness in gashmius matters—in health and the other physical needs that a person requires.

My father-in-law, the Rebbe, once said that the sign of a healthy person is that he does not "feel" his limbs. When one begins to feel one’s head or heart, it is a sign that something is not in order (which is, in truth, alluded to in the verse—Melachim II 4:19: "He said to his father, 'My head, my head!'"). From this, one can also learn about the deficiency of the trait of gaavah (pride): when a person feels his own virtues—even when they are truly present—the very fact that he feels them is proof that he is not "in order." When one does not feel one’s spiritual virtues, that is, for the most part, the sign of a healthy person in ruchnius. This is also true regarding physical health: one should not be preoccupied with one’s state of health. It goes without saying that one must take precautions and follow the instructions of doctors, but one should not dwell on it. Rather, one should be confident that Hashem, who directs the great world, will certainly also direct his "small world"—the person himself—for the good. He, blessed be He, will certainly provide everything needed for health. What is required of the person is "you who cleave to Hashem your G-d"—which refers to the matters of Torah and mitzvos. When one keeps this in mind, one has health, is free of worries, and experiences great success, not only in ruchnius matters but also in gashmius matters, such as business, and so on.

I hope to hear good news from you, and that you have placed the worry of your health upon the Ribono shel Olam, while you take upon yourself the "worry" (the provision) of the matters of Torah and mitzvos for yourself and your surroundings.

I bless you with true health and goodness, both gashmius and ruchnius, and I await good news.

## 1,369

B"H, 26 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

... It is surely unnecessary to point out to one such as yourself that in order to receive blessings from Above, one must have broad vessels below. For anyone connected to Torah, their broad vessels are the Torah itself, which is "longer than the earth and broader than the sea" (Iyov 11:9). However, according to our Sages (Shabbos 31a), there must be a "mixture of a kav of chometin" (a measure of spice/diligence) through which one’s Torah study is sustained. As explained in Yoma 72b, one must make an effort so that it becomes a "potion of life" for him. In our times, this is achieved through the study of Chassidus—the inner dimension of Torah—and by being careful regarding tefillah, the recitation of Tehillim, and so on. As our Sages state in Eiruvin 65a, "a halachic discussion requires prayer" and a **clear mind**. Further elaboration on this is surely unnecessary.

With blessings that you should share good news soon.

## 170

B"H, 26 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Great peace to the great man, pillar of Torah, luminary of light, one of the elite, from his head and above a great golden crown, the distinguished Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., etc., our teacher and master, Rabbi Yisrael Abuchatzeira, shlita, formerly Chief Rabbi of the holy community of Erfoud and its surroundings, and now in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established.

Peace and blessing!

On the occasion of his arrival in our Holy Land—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days, amen, may it be His will—may his coming be blessed by Hashem.

"The steps of a man are established by Hashem," and since the Holy One, blessed be He, has merited him to ascend to our Holy Land, may it be built and established, surely Divine Providence has placed upon him a special mission on this holy soil: to be a **living** spirit among our Sephardic brethren, and to influence them to strengthen Torah and mitzvos in general. In particular, [to ensure] that they guard their children and little ones so that they do not become a mockery and do not fall into the net of unrestrained education, Heaven forfend. Rather, they should watch over them with an open eye, so that all of them—their sons and daughters without **exception**—will be educated on the knees of Torah and mitzvos, with yiras shamayim and the tradition of our holy ancestors, in educational institutions conducted in purity and holiness.

And in the merit of his work in fulfilling this mission with mesiras nefesh, may the Holy One, blessed be He, lengthen his days and years in goodness and pleasantness, and may he continue to flourish in old age, fat and fresh. May he succeed in his monumental work to magnify and glorify Torah, and in his personal matters, from soul to flesh, in abundance.

With blessing.

## 1771

1771

B"H, 26 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have received the checks for "Machne Israel" that you left before your return trip, fulfilling and maintaining your good custom.

Beyond the act of tzedakah involved in participating in the broad and all-encompassing work of "Machne Israel"—where the more one increases, the more praiseworthy it is—and beyond the merit of not diminishing the amount of tzedakah one was accustomed to giving previously, the greatness of which needs no emphasis,

I especially appreciate your current good deed, knowing the nisayon you surely faced in doing so—according to how **you** perceive your situation at this moment.

The more difficult the nisayon, the stronger must be the middah of *itkafya* (subduing oneself to overcome challenges). Beyond the great mitzvah associated with this, the act of *itkafya* works to refine and ennoble the "self." The middah of *itkafya* is very precious to the Ribono shel Olam and opens extraordinary channels to draw down *bracha* and *hatzlacha* in both *gashmius* and *ruchnius*.

With blessings that you will soon report that you are doing good business.

## 1,373

B”H, 27 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn

To the students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Paris,

Peace and blessing!

In response to the question posed by many of the students, may they live:

It is a well-known saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that regarding blessing, the term "rain of blessing" (*gishmei bracha*) is used. Just as rain is only beneficial if it falls upon a field that has been plowed and sown, so too is the matter of blessing: there must be, on the part of the recipient of the blessing, a "plowing and sowing." Yet, even a small amount of sowing—relatively speaking—draws down a great and extraordinary blessing and success.

Regarding *bnei Torah* and yeshiva students, the "plowing" is the observance of the yeshiva’s study schedule with precision, even if this sometimes necessitates a reduction in sleep or eating and drinking, and most importantly, acting against the inclination toward laziness, lack of appropriate consistency, and lack of diligence. The "sowing" is study with appropriate diligence and consistency. When this preparation exists, it draws down blessing, success, and intellectual grasp, understanding, and comprehension.

When I am at the holy gravesite of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention you for success in Torah study and in *yiras shamayim*, and surely you, for your part, will do as mentioned above.

I trust that you are reciting *Tehillim* every day, at least according to the monthly division, and that you are also studying at least a few verses from the *parsha* of the week every day.

With a blessing for success in Torah study and *yiras shamayim*.

## 1,474

B”H, 27 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding the matter of the thoughts that are confusing you, etc.: You should divert your attention from this entirely. You should have words of Torah ready by heart, and surely you also know chapters of Tanya and maamarim of Chassidus by heart.

The saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in the name of several of our Nesi’im, is well known: when people complained to them about the matter of foreign thoughts, they would reply, "Into an empty space, one crawls." Consequently, when the mind is filled with the letters of Torah and tefillah, and one knows them by heart, then even during the time that one is not reviewing them aloud, they are engraved in one’s mind—as is explained in Likutei Torah, in the maamar beginning *Ve’hadarta Pnei Zaken*. Thus, when it is not a *postke* (an empty space), one crawls in less, and if they do so occasionally, it is easy to drive them away.

With blessings for success in Torah study and in yiras shamayim.

## 1170

B.H., 27 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 14 Teves, in which you write about the chazaras da"ch and the farbrengen you held during these days. Many thanks for the news of these good tidings, for if at all times people are hungry and thirsty to receive good tidings—and there is no good other than Torah and mitzvos—then how much more so in our times, and especially in places that are distant in terms of spirit (for distance in location is of no consequence in such matters, even though at times it serves as a cause for distance in spirituality).

It is understood that this does not mean that all matters are being accomplished in their fullness, for to my regret, this is not the case at all. I have already told you many times that one of your primary tasks is as my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, said: "A good melamed is not defined by the fact that he teaches the student these subjects, but that he teaches him so that he can learn on his own. And not only to succeed with a student who is diligent and consistent, but he is a 'master-teacher' who succeeds with a student who is lazy and does not have good talents." All these things apply to your situation as well: your primary task is to make frum Yidden and Chassidim. Ultimately, this must spread throughout the entire community. One should not be satisfied with merely repeating da"ch and accustoming the listeners to hear it and then donate to the institutions; rather, one must awaken in them the desire that they themselves should demand these things and the like. The main thing is to strive to make [the location] a Chassidishe environment. For this, it is necessary that other avreichim of anash settle there. That is why I have asked you many times to strive and take an interest in how you might find a place for parnassah there for avreichim of anash whom you know, and whose character, nature, and requirements you are familiar with. To my regret, nothing has been done in this regard.

Furthermore, I suspect that you also view your being [there] and your residence there as a matter of being sent to a "distant land," and you wait every single day for the "hoped-for appointment" so that you may fulfill your obligation of galus and be able to be, in a good and auspicious hour, in Brooklyn or Williamsburg. It is understood that such thoughts throughout the course of one's avodah cannot help but interfere and cause a deficiency in fulfilling the task of shlichus as it should be. This is in addition to the fact that, in general, this is not the inner approach, as the Rebbe (Rashab) said, quoted in Toras Shalom, page 41: "They are with kabbalas ol, etc. One thinks of something else; one would already want to leave there, etc. Even though one is doing it, one would already want to be finished with it, etc., in truth, etc. But where one is, one must be there. And after that, I will be in another place, etc. But as long as I am doing this, I must be here, etc. For this is an instruction regarding the truthfulness of the matter." See there at length. How much more so in our case, where your work now is primary work, just as our Sages praised the act of "bringing forth the precious from the vile." Based on the aforementioned premise—that where one is, one must be there—you would be striving to bring avreichim of anash there so that you would not be alone. But now, your desire is the opposite: for if you are alone, then eventually they will have mercy on you and release you from the servitude of galus...

With blessings for success in your general and private matters.

#### 1170

**In Toras Shalom:** In the new edition, p. 39.

## 1576

B"H, 27 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in the needs of the community, etc.,
Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter of 22 Teves with pleasure, and as you requested, I mentioned you at the farbrengen of 24 Teves, the day of the yahrtzeit of our great Rebbe.

It has also been noted, as you requested, that you are participating in the Shas distribution.

In response to your question regarding which tractates I have taken upon myself in this distribution, they are Maseches Sukkah and Sanhedrin, bli neder.

And so as not to waste paper, etc., I am transcribing a chapter from what was said during the farbrengen, based on the story that the Maggid arranged that at the beginning of the Alter Rebbe’s arrival in Mezritch, his son, the "Malach," would teach our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe Chassidus, and the Alter Rebbe would teach the "Malach" the revealed Torah. When they began their study—"From when..."—and the Alter Rebbe began to explain the Mishnah, the Malach said that he interprets "from when" (*me'aimasai*) as stemming from the word *eimah* (awe) and fear. And by connecting the beginning of the Shas with its end (for in the Shas distribution here, we also distribute the orders of Mishnayos, and even though the conclusion was with Maseches Niddah, they are connected to one another).

For the conclusion of the Mishnah is: "The Holy One, Blessed be He, found no vessel that holds blessing for Israel other than peace"—peace and the unity of all the children of Israel, as is also explained in Tanya, Chapter 32: "Bless us, our Father, all of us as one."

True unity of people in general, and even of the children of Israel in particular, is impossible when there is some ulterior motive or benefit involved, for then one is not uniting with **the other**, but rather seeking benefit **for oneself**. True unity is only possible as explained in Tanya, Chapter 32, because "all of them are equal and one Father for all of them," etc., by virtue of the root of their souls in Hashem, who is **One**. And as is explained in Chassidic discourse, the root of the souls is higher even than Torah and mitzvos, as our Sages of blessed memory said in Bereishis Rabbah at the beginning: "The thought of Israel preceded everything," even the Torah, as it is written, "Speak to the children of Israel." This is the beginning of the Shas with the Shema, and the conclusion with the vessel that holds blessing, which is peace—for peace comes through saying the Shema: "Hashem is One." But in order for that declaration to be true, it must come through "from when"—the acceptance of the yoke of Heaven—and not from intellect and reason, even the intellect and reason of holiness.

For one such as yourself, this brevity will suffice.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

**M. Schneerson**

## 1,157

1,157

B”H, 27 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It has been a long time since I have heard from you, and I am interested to know, firstly, how you are feeling in terms of health, and also your wife, may they live. I am also interested in the matters we discussed when you were here with me—regarding the house, the neighbors, and so on—as well as the spiritual side, concerning influencing the children in the spirit we spoke about.

I wish to reiterate my words, as I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and as one can see with one’s own physical eyes: there is no doubt that when one speaks once, a second time, and more, in the end, one achieves results, at the very least partially. Especially when speaking with children, and doing so in a peaceful manner, for “the words of the wise are heard in tranquility.”

Enclosed is a transcript of what I said to the students when they came to see me this past Chanukah, which is relevant to all Jews. For the entire work of a Jew is, as it is written, “And you shall be to Me a kingdom of priests and a holy nation,” meaning that every Jew must consider himself a *kohen*, whose purpose is to draw down *kedushah*—holiness—within himself, and especially within his family. And being a *chossid*, you also have the promise of the Alter Rebbe, who said that in the merit of his *mesiras nefesh*, when one acts in the matter of *Torah* and *mitzvos*, one will certainly be successful.

With blessings for all the best for you and your household, may they live, and to hear good news regarding all the above.

## 1,378

B"H, 27 Teves, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter of 9 Teves, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein, regarding your son, may he live, who has a tendency toward stealing, Heaven forbid. You must consult a specialist in this field, as this is akin to a weakness, and there are now medical means to address this. It is understood that you should not neglect to recite a *kapitel* of *Tehillim* every day (in addition to the regular order), and also to give a *pruta* or three to *tzedakah* before *davening* *Shacharis* and *Mincha* specifically in the merit of your son. Also, check the *tzitzis* of your son’s *tallis katan*, ensure that he does not go with an uncovered head, and check the *mezuzos* in your home. If it is the custom among the students to wear a *yarmulke* under the hat, you should accustom him to this without it being conspicuous, and it should come about through the suggestion of his peers. I hope that you will be able to share good news regarding this.

With blessings,
