## 1,080

B"H, 1 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

2) It is a pity that I did not find in your letter any details regarding your influence on others as well, to gladden their hearts. This is like the well-known story of the holy Rabbi, the great Gaon, etc., etc., our teacher Rabbi Levi Yitzchak of Berditchev, of blessed memory, whom they once found dancing with great joy in the early morning light. When asked, "What is this joy for?" he replied that when he contemplated the morning blessing, "Who has not made me a gentile," and realized what he had been spared and how good his portion, his lot, and his inheritance are—that he is a Jew—there is no joy greater than that. For us, there is the added dimension of what was revealed to us through the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, that we should "serve Hashem with joy." This is in addition to what is explained in the Rambam’s *Hilchos Deios*, that it is possible to serve Hashem "in all your ways"—meaning even through eating, drinking, etc.—for now, an additional level has been added: that all of this can be done with true joy.

3) I trust you are maintaining the *shiurim* that we discussed when you were here.

4) Enclosed is a copy of the general letter in connection with the "Festival of Festivals," the day of 19 Kislev. Surely you are aware that the upcoming 10 Shevat is the second *yahrzeit* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. It is appropriate that, to the extent possible, you conduct yourself in accordance with what was explained in my letter from last year, a copy of which is enclosed here.

I hope that you are not diverting your attention from improving your situation, as the verse states, "It is not good for man to be alone." May Hashem grant you success in this and in all the aforementioned matters.

With blessings.

## 181

181

B.H., 1 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Agudas Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established,

Greetings and blessings!

My previous letters were surely received in due time, and I await a detailed response to them. I am writing now regarding the following:

1) In connection with the upcoming second Yahrtzeit — 10 Shevat — you will surely endeavor to hold a farbrengen for the public in an appropriate manner. Furthermore, in response to the questions of many, my opinion is that the procedure should be as detailed in last year’s letter.

2) It would be most appropriate that on the day of the Yahrtzeit, or close to it, at least one branch or institution of the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchak Lubavitch be opened. I have written regarding this to the director of the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchak, the esteemed Chossid, who toils for the needs of the community, etc., R’ Chaim Zusia Vilimovsky, may he live.

3) It seems that the division of responsibilities between the yeshivos, the Talmud Torah, and the aforementioned Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchak institutions is clear. Nevertheless, I am writing here to clarify my opinion and proposal:

The Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Lod should be the highest institution in Eretz Yisrael. This also applies to those students and pupils who are being educated in the spirit of Lubavitch at the yeshiva in Tel Aviv. The Tel Aviv yeshiva is primarily for those students who, for various reasons, do not wish to leave their parents' home. In any case, it must have lower grade levels than those in Lod. Only if absolutely necessary should there be classes in both Lod and Tel Aviv, but in any event, the highest classes—for which there is a lack of mashpi'im, etc.—should only be found at the Lod yeshiva. It is self-understood that one of the functions of the yeshiva in Tel Aviv is to attract the children living in Tel Aviv and to serve as a local example of what a Tomchei Temimim education is, since everyone who comes to Eretz Yisrael spends some time in Tel Aviv, and it is not possible for everyone to visit the Lod yeshiva.

4) The yeshiva and Talmud Torah in the village (Kfar Chabad) are primarily for the children of the village and its surroundings. It is self-understood that after completing their studies at this yeshiva, they should continue their education at the Lod yeshiva, which is the highest institution, as mentioned above.

5) The Toras Emes Yeshiva in Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established, apparently has a unique character, following the custom of the yeshivos in Eretz Yisrael—meaning that students study in two yeshivos, etc., and that married men and heads of families also study there. In any case, it would be appropriate to arrange that for at least a few months of the year, the older students from Toras Emes come to the Lod yeshiva, so that they may absorb the spirit of Tomchei Temimim in its purity, as much as is currently possible.

6) In those settlements and circles that do not yet agree to an education in the spirit of Tomchei Temimim (for example, the schools currently being organized by the activists, or the institutions that had to be founded among the Yemenite settlements because they would not agree to come to Lod or the village to study), these institutions should join the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchak. As mentioned above, it is understood that they will not have classes as high as those in Lod, and anyone who wishes to continue his studies in the teachings of Chassidus Chabad, etc., must endeavor to transfer to study in Lod.

7) The conclusion from all the above is that there must be concern from Agudas Chabad in general, and from Anash and the Chassidim in particular, for the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchak. It is to be hoped that from among the students of the aforementioned Reshet, a significant percentage will come to study at the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Lod, in accordance with the saying of our Sages: "A thousand enter for Mikra, a hundred emerge for Mishnah," etc.

8) Just as every institution has its own autonomous administration and an external auditor, so too, the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchak Lubavitch should have the director, the esteemed Chossid R’ Chaim Zusia Vilimovsky, may he live (who will surely add a few of the younger men to assist him), and the auditors should be the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid R’ Eliezer Kresik, may he live, and the Rabbi R’ Avraham Paris, may he live.

9) Since the Reshet is in great need of funds, it is worthwhile and necessary to organize a campaign in an appropriate manner in Eretz Yisrael. Please, I implore you, make every possible effort in this regard. Surely a way will be found so that this does not conflict with the other institutions; on the contrary, etc.

10) Since the age and the students in the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchak are such that it is possible to request support from the government, every effort must be made for the existing institutions in the Reshet to join, as soon as possible, the stream into which other Chabad institutions are entered. This will lighten the burden of expenses and enable the founding of institutions in new locations.

11) If the above proposals are accepted by you, please be so kind as to inform me of this as soon as possible. The main thing is that for the upcoming Yahrtzeit of 10 Shevat, or close to it, you should act as stated in section 2.

With blessings for success, awaiting your prompt response.

## 1882

1882

B”H, 1 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned individual, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
R’ Chaim Zusia, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from 12 Cheshvan and your two letters from 22 Teves...

2) I was pleased to read the enclosures in your letter of 22 Cheshvan regarding what appeared in the newspaper concerning the Simchas Beis Hashoeiva farbrengen, as well as the farbrengen of N’shei Chabad and the connection to them. Surely, in the future as well, you will exert effort in such matters. In addition to the work itself, one should strive to publicize it—specifically in an appropriate manner, meaning without cheap publicity. As is known from the responsa of the Rashba, it is a mitzvah to publicize those who perform a mitzvah, since through this it is possible to draw others in, similar to the concept that "the jealousy of scribes increases wisdom."

3) Regarding the assistance you request for the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok, as I have written previously, there is no fund or resources here to commit to a fixed amount of aid. However, my hope is that from time to time I will be able to send you Scrip parcels and the like. Although it is difficult to know in advance the frequency or size of the shipments, in any event, this will not suffice for the budget they require. It is imperative that you seek appropriate ways to find the resources in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. I have sent a letter to Aguch to assist you (in a way that will not create conflict between one institution and another).

4) I am not at all pleased that [name] left his work at the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok, and I have already written to him directly regarding this. If the reason is solely due to a lack of resources, one must seek solutions **for that**, not abandon the work. If the reason is internal friction among the employees of the Reshet, then it is absolutely obvious that this must be nullified and rooted out. Especially in Eretz Yisrael, where the matter of *machlokes* (strife), etc., must be guarded against to the greatest extent—and who is to say this, especially among Chassidei Chabad? As is known from our holy Rebbes, our leaders, may the merit of their holy souls protect us, how much they sacrificed themselves to root in the hearts of the Chassidim, those who are connected and belong, and even among ordinary Bnei Yisrael, the concept of *ahavas Yisrael*. To elaborate on this would be superfluous.

5) In connection with the upcoming *yom hilula* of 10 Shevat, one should strive, if at all possible, to open at least one more department of Oholei Yosef Yitzchok on that day or close to it.

6) Regarding the division of roles between the institutions so that they do not interfere with one another, my perspective is understood from the letter to Aguch, enclosed here, which I requested be delivered to them as soon as possible.

## 1,383

B"H, 1 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you inform me that you have been studying at the yeshiva in Sefaria for two years and two months, and that a doctor is advising you to have your tonsils removed and is recommending that it be done now, and you also request a blessing for your father, [Name]—

Regarding the surgery: You should consult one more specialist in this field. If he also agrees that the surgery should be performed, and that it should be done now, then may it be His will that the surgery proceed properly and at a good and auspicious time. Once you know the date of the surgery for certain, please inform me here.

You should convey to your father that he should keep up the three daily study sessions that are incumbent upon every person as established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe—namely, Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya.

I am certain that in your next letter you will inform me in detail about your studies and your good conduct in yiras shamayim.

With blessings for success in Torah study with yiras shamayim.

## 1884

1884

B”H, 1 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I read with pleasure your letter from Vayigash, as well as the one preceding it, in which you inform me of the order and manner of the farbrengen for the “Chag HaChagim,” 19 Kislev, and of your efforts in your camp. I was pleased to read that the Rav of your camp also participated and spoke about the significance of the Yom Tov. Regarding your mention that someone stood up at the end and caused a disturbance, one should not be affected by this; surely, at future farbrengens, the unpleasant impression left by the aforementioned individual will be rectified, and ultimately, even he will turn into someone who assists in the work. If, in your opinion, it is worthwhile for me to write to him, please inform me of his background regarding his knowledge of Torah and in which language (Hebrew, Yiddish, or English), and, G-d willing, I will do so.

2) Thank you for enclosing in your letter the photograph of the bochurim who are learning with you. It is a pity that you did not note their names and their mothers’ names on the note or on the back of the photo; surely you will rectify this in the future.

3) Regarding your question about the difficulty you have in explaining to them the matter of the mitzvos—whether they are observed out of *kabbalas ol* or because they have a rational basis—the general point is this: The mitzvos were given by Hashem to human beings. Consequently, it is understood that the wisdom within them is infinite. On the other hand, it is also understood that there is some grasp and hold within human intellect, and this is the subject of the *taamei hamitzvos* brought in the seforim. However, since they originate from the wisdom and will of the *Ribono shel Olam*, it is simple to understand that no matter how much a person delves into the *taamei hamitzvos* and the benefits within them, it is never complete, for it is impossible for a finite being to grasp and encompass that which is infinite—only "the end of its edge and a mere fraction of it."

Furthermore, since the mitzvos were given by the Creator, may He be blessed, for the benefit of the human being He created, it is certain that He, may He be blessed, is capable of intending what is for the benefit of the creature He created. Just as it is impossible for a person to say they will not eat until they understand with their intellect the benefit of eating and drinking, and just as it is absurd for a sick person to say they will not accept any medicine until they understand with their intellect if it will help them—for on the contrary, taking the ingredients, medicines, eating, and drinking strengthens the brain and the power of the intellect, so that in time they will be able to understand the benefit of the food, drink, and medicines.

So too is the matter regarding the mitzvos: It is certain that they can be understood—at least "the end of their edge"—even with human intellect. But this is not a condition, Heaven forbid, for the performance of mitzvos and the study of Torah. On the contrary, the *Torah u’mitzvos* are the very things that lead to a state where, in time, one’s intellect will be qualified to understand and grasp the aforementioned. One could elaborate on this, but the explanation must be tailored to the level at which the students are currently holding. I rely on your understanding to be able to adapt these matters to their capacity for comprehension and grasp.

Enclosed are some points from what I have here in English, which you can use to explain the aforementioned point. May Hashem grant you success in your *avodah* in holiness, as well as success in your personal matters, and may He grant proper health to your wife and daughter, may they live.

With blessings for success in your general *avodah* and in your personal matters.

P.S. Regarding your complaint that you do not see tangible results from your efforts, and even when you do see a result, it is not long-lasting: It is a pity to waste time on complaining, for that will certainly yield no benefit; on the contrary, it causes much damage due to the weakening of the spirit and, ultimately, the weakening of health as well. Especially since there is no place for complaining. See *Tanya*, end of Chapter 13, regarding the level of *tzaddikim*, etc., that even though it passes and goes, etc., nevertheless, etc., and since it is "in the power of their *neshamah elokis*" to return and awaken, etc., that which connects, etc., until the "end" of all levels. And there in *Tanya*, Chapter 25: "And this union above is eternal, forever and ever." Elaborating on this is superfluous. It is a well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zya":* "One should abandon the sighs and the calculations, and strengthen oneself in *avodah*." Ultimately, Hashem will surely grant you success in this, and you will see good fruit from your labor, and "according to the effort is the reward."

## 1095

1 Rosh Chodesh Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings!

Through the esteemed Chossid, who is involved in communal affairs, Rabbi Nissan Pinson, I received the news at the time regarding the doctors’ opinion concerning your health. Today, I received his good news, which I was very pleased to hear, that the surgery went well. May Hashem Yisborach help that your condition should improve from time to time until you are able to report that your health is completely restored.

However, in order to be able to receive the blessings of Hashem Yisborach, one must have proper vessels to contain them. For a Jew, these vessels are Torah and mitzvos. I hope that you, too, will take it upon yourself, without a vow, to hold more firmly to Torah and mitzvos. The more strongly and frequently you do so, the more and the faster Hashem will send His blessings to you. In particular, I would like to suggest that you be careful to put on tefillin every day, and after davening, recite a few chapters of Tehillim. Before putting on the tefillin, you should give a few coins to tzedakah.

You should also see to it that you influence your brother to also put on tefillin (except on Shabbos and Yom Tov). You should explain to him that, as a doctor, he knows how much the health of the body depends on the health of the neshamah, which acts through the nervous system to keep it strong and courageous. Furthermore, as a doctor, he certainly knows that there are many medicines and methods used to heal people, even without knowing exactly how or why they heal. Nevertheless, they are used because it is observed that they bring benefit and help. It is the same regarding Torah and mitzvos: the main thing is not to understand, but to do it, with the certainty that this is the way it is. As we see in the history of the Jewish people, despite all the persecutions and troubles that the nations have devised and inflicted upon Jews, the Jewish people have remained and continue to live. It is the same for the individual Jew: the commitment to Torah and mitzvos must be the main thing. One should not set conditions for the Almighty—who is the greatest doctor—that one must first understand how the remedies will work before taking them. Rather, one trusts the doctor and professor. This is how a Jew’s approach to Torah and mitzvos should be, and this brings health to a Jew’s neshamah and also to his body.

With blessings that you should share good news that you are feeling an improvement in your health.

## 1580

B”H, 1 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

On this occasion, as I am writing to your father, may he live and be well, I wish to reach out to you as well. Especially since the Baal Shem Tov’s approach is well known—that every opportunity comes about through Hashgacha Pratis.

You will surely see in my letter to your father, may he live and be well, regarding the significance of the festival of 19 Kislev, and naturally, the details are elaborated upon in the enclosed booklet and the letter to your father. I hope that from time to time, you too will take an interest in the fundamental principles of Toras HaChassidus, and you will certainly find ways to learn about it in greater detail.

The nature of the Jewish religion is well known—a fundamental characteristic that distinguishes it from other "religions"—which is that the approach of this religion toward man is to guide him regarding concrete actions in daily life, while the explanation of the principles of the religion comes only afterward. We see this clearly, as the Torah, the Shas, and so on, are filled with practical instructions for daily life, and the study of this Torah is a fixed obligation for every single person since the Giving of the Torah. At the same time, the religious perspective regarding the attributes of the Creator, the Seder Hishtalshelus of the Sefiros, matters of Gan Eden, Techiyas HaMeisim, and so forth, were only explained in general terms, and were revealed to a greater extent only in the later generations.

It is the same regarding the study of Chassidus itself; its essence is the translation into action, particularly in the three pillars: Ahavas Hashem, Ahavas HaTorah, and Ahavas Yisrael—through which the fulfillment of Torah and Mitzvos in the daily life of every Jewish man and woman must be permeated.

With blessings for a suitable match soon, and for proper success in both material and spiritual matters alike.

## 1,387

B"H, 1 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter informing me that your wife, may she live and be well, visited a doctor and followed his instructions, and also traveled to the hot springs of Tiberias, and you are asking for my opinion on whether to wait for some time or to go to "Hadassah" again.

In my opinion, after her return from the hot springs of Tiberias, it is advisable that she see a doctor again. If he tells her that the tubes are open, then you should wait a few months. Surely, the Ribono shel Olam will fulfill the desires of your hearts for the good, to be blessed with healthy children soon.

It is well known that the Alter Rebbe wrote that a *segulah* for the birth of sons and daughters is involvement in the study of Chassidus, which leads to the love and fear of Hashem. Regarding what you write—that you have a set *shiur* every Thursday night—this is not sufficient. In addition to the obvious necessity of studying Chassidus on Shabbos, it is certainly appropriate to set an additional *shiur* two or three times during the week as well. If possible, it should be arranged so that no more than three days pass without studying the teachings of Chassidus. This is, of course, in addition to the study of Tanya, as divided in the *Moreh Shiur* for the days of the year.

Regarding what you wrote about suffering from constipation, etc., you should consult a doctor about this as soon as possible. As is well known, the books of Chassidus speak strongly against this condition, and it is worthwhile to make every effort to resolve it as soon as possible. See also Rambam, *Hilchos De'os*, Chapter 4, Halacha 13.

With blessings that you should report good news soon.

P.S. Enclosed is the general letter in connection with the "Festival of Festivals," the day of 19 Kislev.

## 1878

B"H, 1 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and diligent worker in communal affairs, etc.,
Rabbi Yehuda Aryeh, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter with pleasure, in which you inform me of the state of health of the esteemed Chassid, etc., Rabbi [Name], may he live and be well. It appears from your letter that his health has improved somewhat, and I hope that in your next letter you will inform me that his eyesight is growing stronger, and that in time he will be able to write himself as well. May the Ribono shel Olam, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, send him a complete recovery soon.

It is known from our Sages that "Who is wise? He who sees what is born" (Pirkei Avos 2:9). The explanation in Chassidus is that one sees the birth of creation from *ayin* (nothingness) to *yesh* (being)—that he **sees** this at every time and every moment. As is explained in *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah* by the Alter Rebbe, creation is not a one-time act from the six days of Bereishis; rather, the word of Hashem brings the entire creation into being from *ayin* to *yesh* at every moment. So too, in every Jew, physical health is dependent on spiritual health. When one feels a weakness in a physical limb, he goes to a doctor, because one must conduct oneself according to the way of nature, and the Torah has given permission (which also means power) to the doctor to heal. But one must also be concerned about weakness in the spiritual limb—in this case, the matter of "seeing what is born" from *ayin* to *yesh* at every moment. I am not writing this for the sake of a *derashah*, but to encourage [Name], may he live and be well, to strengthen himself in the study of Chassidus, and as a start, to study the aforementioned *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*. I thank you for your trouble in conveying all of this to [Name], may he live and be well. Just as you took it upon yourself to be a *shaliach* to write to me regarding his condition, I am sure you will also take upon yourself my mission as stated in this letter, and will assist him in bringing this into good practice.

Enclosed is a copy of the general letter in connection with the "Festival of Festivals," the 19th of Kislev, and a transcript of things I said to the students when they came to me on the fifth night of Chanukah, as well as the booklet regarding the 19th of Kislev. I hope all of this will be of interest to you.

With blessings that the Ribono shel Olam should grant you the merit to bring good news regarding the improvement of the patient's condition, and also to bring news of your own activities in your city to bring the hearts of our fellow Jews closer to their Father in Heaven.

P.S. In the year 5688, while I was in Berlin, I once visited his father, of blessed memory, on a Friday night. I remember that his father was teaching Rambam to his family at the time, and among those present was one of the students of the Kelm Yeshiva, though I do not recall his name.

***

**1878**

**Strengthen himself in the study of Chassidus:** See also above, Letter 1860.

## 1,859

B"H, 2 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

Through the esteemed Chossid, who is involved in communal needs, Rabbi Schneur Zalman Taubel, I learned that you have set the date of your wedding, *b'mazal tov*, for 21 Shevat. May Hashem Yisborach help that it be in a good and auspicious hour, and together with your wife, may you build a home within the Jewish people upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos. These foundations of Torah and mitzvos have been upheld and tested by thousands of Jewish families, and they have endured and withstood all the storms and difficulties of time—and remained whole.

And so it is also in the life of every Jew who is getting married: when he makes a firm resolution to build his home and family life upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, Hashem Yisborach blesses him with a warm, luminous home—a home from which light and warmth shine and radiate into the surroundings, and in particular, to brighten and warm the immediate family members, the Jews who live in the vicinity, and in general, all Jews over whom one has and can have an influence.

May Hashem Yisborach help you and instill in you the good thought and firm resolution to build your home and family life upon the aforementioned foundations, in the path of Torah and mitzvos, for this is the path of true happiness and success in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings of *mazal tov*.

## 1,191

B"H, 2 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

It is surely known to you that your brother, [Name], may he live, visited me. Following our conversation, I am enclosing a copy of the letter I wrote to him. It is certainly good and appropriate that your brother, may he live, should not know that I have sent you a copy of this letter. I must say that I am greatly astonished by you, for based on the impression your brother made upon me, he is receptive to influence, and there is a need to draw him even closer to matters of Torah and Yiddishkeit. Yet, when he speaks with me—for example, regarding the fact that he is a member of a Conservative temple—it is not at all evident that you are involved, nor does he seem to know anything about it, which is not as it should be.

Is it your opinion that the only reason Hashem brought him to [Location] is so that he might enjoy the prosperity of the United States and no longer be subject—G-d forbid, and may it not come to pass—to the tribulations he endured in our country in the past, and subsequently the comfort he had in France? It is clear that since he is in the same city as you, and Hashem has privileged you to know of the light of Torah in general and the teachings of Chassidus in particular, you are obligated. In the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of his father, the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory: "Just as a Jew must put on tefillin every day, so too must he concern himself every day with the education of his household." In your case, this refers to your brother and his household; it is your duty and your holy privilege to draw his heart and the hearts of his household toward matters of Torah and mitzvos as much as possible. Without a doubt, if you work at this day by day, using the appropriate words and with calmness, you will succeed.

It is possible that the "clever one" [the yetzer hara] will approach you with the argument that since you are compelled to receive material support from him, your words will not be heeded. But this is not the case at all; it is entirely a ruse of the yetzer. This is the lot of all Torah scholars and all those who provide spiritual influence—that very often, they are forced to receive material support precisely from those whom they influence. On the contrary, this is one of the kindnesses of Hashem. See *Ra'aya Mehemna*, cited in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 26: "Those sages who are like Shabbos and Yom Tov have nothing except what is prepared for them on a weekday..." See also the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, page 112b, regarding what our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, wrote concerning the conduct of the holy Rabbi Mendel of Bar, who would not speak words of Torah except in a place where they gave him a donation. Study it well.

With blessings for success in the above, and I thank you in advance if you will inform me of good news regarding this.

## 1992

2 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc., Rabbi Yoel
May he live

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter with pleasure on the day of the Hillula of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, and I was happy to read that you are satisfied and, thank G-d, all is well.

You are surely familiar with the maamar from our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe (copied in *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus*, Chapter 3), which states:

"‘*Maskil l’Eisan HaEzrachi*’ — *Eisan* is the essence of the soul, which is attached to the Essence, a ‘part of G-d above.’ For the soul that You have placed within me is pure; You created it, You formed it, You breathed it into me — corresponding to the four worlds. In the Midrash, five levels are counted: *nefesh, ruach, neshamah, chayah, yechidah*, and in the Zohar they are summarized into four levels: *nefesh, ruach, neshamah*, and *neshamah l’neshamah*, corresponding to the four letters of the Name *Havayah*. *Eisan* is the strength of the soul that comes into revelation through the power of *mesiras nefesh*. *Eisan* is a term meaning ‘old,’ not renewed. It is the Name *Ayin-Beis*, which is not renewed, whereas *Sag* and *Mah* are *Tohu* and *Tikkun*, both of which are renewed. The Name *Ayin-Beis* is above *Tohu* and *Tikkun* and is not renewed. It is known that the Name *Ayin-Beis* is in *Chochma* — specifically, the inwardness of *Chochma*. As the saying goes, ‘The inwardness of *Abba* is the inwardness of *Atik*.’ *Atik* is a term meaning ‘old,’ which is the drawing down of the Essence. This is the meaning of ‘the soul that You have placed within me is pure’ — this is the root of the soul as it is in *Atzilus*. *Atzilus* is the separation of a light from the *Ohr Ein Sof* of the *Matzil*, blessed be He, which is not in the category of renewal, but rather in the category of the revelation of the hidden. This is *Maskil* — the source that originates and reveals the intellect. This *Maskil* is only for *Eisan*, for *Eisan* possesses a *Maskil*, and through the power of the *Maskil*, the *Ezrachi* illuminates all the powers and senses."

Based on what is brought in many places in *Chassidus* regarding the verse, "The fear of Hashem is for life," that as the measure of *yirah* grows, so too is life and health added to the physical body of a Jewish person — this applies specifically to the *Eisan* in the soul, the strength of the soul. When this comes into revelation — and as is known, the matter of *mesiras nefesh* (where *nefesh* means will), is that one surrenders his will to *mitzvos* — vitality and health are added in the literal sense as well. May Hashem lengthen your days and years in goodness and pleasantness, and may He illuminate your portion in the world with the candle of *mitzvah*, the light of Torah, and the light within the Torah — which is the teachings of *Chassidus*.

Regarding what you wrote, that in your environment there is no one to talk to: it is known how the Tzemach Tzedek answered the esteemed Chossid and Tzaddik, Rabbi Hillel of Paritch: "The souls hear." Especially now, when our leaders, our Rebbes, have revealed to us the deepest concepts in the teachings of *Chassidus*, and also in our **mother tongue**, in a way that they can be understood — and especially the *uvchen* (the conclusion) and the *b'po'al* (the practical application) — this emerges for every Jewish person, even the simplest of the simple, and the matter requires nothing more than the appropriate attention.

I sign off as I began, with a blessing for length of days and years in the literal sense and in its inner meaning — filled with the true good, which is Torah and *mitzvos*, permeated and illuminated by the inwardness of the Torah.

P.S. Regarding what you wrote in your letter about what is found in *Chassidus* explaining the Sages' statement that the Holy One, blessed be He, desired to have a dwelling place in the lower worlds — that we do not know *why* He desired it — and you were troubled by this, for surely this provides Him with great *nachas ruach*. Just as we see in ourselves, a wise man finds *nachas* when he is able to reveal his wisdom, and "more than the calf wants to suck, the cow wants to nurse," etc.

It is understood that one cannot compare this matter to Above at all. As explained in many places, the *nachas ruach* of a wise man is when he reveals the matter to another, but this concept does not apply Above, since there is no "other." Furthermore, the matter of it being specifically in the worlds of *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah* is only according to the Supernal Will. For the reason why the *nachas ruach* is specifically in a dwelling place in the lower worlds is not understood, as explained in the *biur* in the *maamar* "Yom Tov Shel Rosh Hashanah" 5626, at the beginning.

The essential and general point in all of this is that it is impossible to understand "why" He desired it prior to the entire *Seder Hishtalshelus*, because at that time there was not yet the existence of intellect, reason, or knowledge, as all of these are created things. Before the worlds were emanated, there was only He and His Name alone. It is in that state that the Will was aroused to have a dwelling place in the lower worlds. If so, it is not possible to find a reason or intellect for this, since the concept of intellect did not yet exist. *Davar zeh l'meivin* (a word to the wise).

## 1,393

B"H, 2 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote in your letter concerning the matters of *marah shechorah* [melancholy]—that you do not know if it is appropriate to study with the class, etc.—surely it is clear even to you that this is nothing but an incitement of the *yetzer* to weaken your efforts to draw the hearts of the yeshiva students closer. It is a pity to spend time debating these claims. You should be firm in your resolve, for you have merited to be a *mashpia* in a yeshiva founded by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, and consequently, you are *mekushar* to him. This connection also serves as a conduit to channel to you the strength and ability to fulfill the task of guiding your classes in such a way that, ultimately, they will be *Chassidim*. After all the calculations, this is your *shlichus* and your role in this world. And when one fulfills the task placed upon him by the Creator, blessed be He, then, in the words of the Alter Rebbe: "For that which you are needed, Hashem gives you everything you need."

Enclosed are the *hanhagos* for the upcoming *yom hilula*, 10 Shevat. I trust you will publicize them in an appropriate manner.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and may you do it with *simcha*, which is an advantage both for you and for the work itself.

## 1394

B"H, 2 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter of 13 Teves, as well as the one preceding it. On the day of your thirty-first birthday, I hereby express my blessing for long life and good years, with all the interpretations that implies. In accordance with the chapter of Tehillim that you must now recite, may you hold fast to your path in the way of the Baal Shem Tov, and as the conclusion of the chapter states: **"Rejoice** in Hashem and be glad, you righteous ones, and sing for joy, all you upright of heart." As it is written in the chapter preceding this: "For this let every pious one pray to You at a time of finding," and although these are lofty levels, nevertheless, a portion and a semblance of all levels exist within every one who is connected and a Chossid, since he is engaged in strengthening his hiskashrus through the study of the teachings of Chassidus of the Nasi, and especially by maintaining the three daily shiurim that are equal for every soul: Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya. However, it is the duty of the Chossid not to be satisfied with working on himself alone; he must also influence his surroundings—to bring them close, to awaken them, and to illuminate them with the candle of mitzvah and the light of Torah, permeated with the "light of Torah," which is the teachings of Chassidus.

With blessings for success in influencing your surroundings, and may this serve as broad vessels for the drawing down and receiving of the blessings of the Ribono shel Olam, in revealed goodness.

## 1,395

B”H, 2 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Regarding your question asking for my opinion on the state of your health: I have already conveyed through the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and scholarly individual, who is involved in communal needs, etc., Moreinu Harav Chaim Mordechai Aizik Hodakov, may he live, that in general you are a healthy man. You simply need to listen to the doctor—that is, to fulfill his instructions. One should not raise a difficulty as to why you must follow the doctor’s orders if you are healthy, for in general, every such question stems from the *sitra achra*. Furthermore, the insistence on understanding every matter specifically through one’s own intellect and logical analysis is a new path in the customs of Chassidim. From the beginning, the order was that one would listen (obey), and afterward, one would strive to understand as much as possible. And if they did not understand, they still slept peacefully (this is, of course, provided that it was not a deficiency in understanding Torah in general, and the teachings of Chassidus in particular, which would cause distress and worry while awake, and sometimes even in one’s sleep).

I have already told you several times that you are the *shaliach* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, to make [the city] a *Chassidishe shtot*. For the time being (meaning, for ten years or more!), there has been only preparation, in that to a certain extent, the obstacles were removed so that there would be, at the very least, a *yeshiva*—a *Chassidishe* one—and you established a *yeshiva ketana* as preparation for a *yeshiva* as it ought to be. Now is the opportune time to move from the introduction and preparation to having a *yeshiva gedola* and to becoming a *Chassidishe shtot*, as is the desire of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. This matter depends solely on the **will** of the *avreichim*... and to a greater extent than the other *avreichim*, it depends on you, since from the day the *yeshiva* was founded there, you have been its leader in many, many details, with the agreement of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. Further elaboration on this is unnecessary, as I have spoken with you about this many times.

My only desire in this is to say once again that it is enough to play games. At the very least, now, let everyone strive together—with you among the first—so that there will be a healthy *Chassidishe yeshiva*, and you will be a healthy *Yid* and also a healthy *Chassid*.

May Hashem grant you success in your general and personal affairs, so that with joy and without excessive calculations, you may arrange matters in a good way. Regarding your personal affairs, may you and your wife, may they live, raise your children, may they live, to Torah, to the *chuppah*, and to good deeds, in true health and with genuine abundance.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

P.S. Enclosed are the *hanhagos* for the upcoming *yom hahilula*, 10 Shevat. I am certain you will publicize them in the appropriate manner.

Perhaps it would be worthwhile to include an article in your publication in connection with the *yom hahilula*.

## 1596

B"H, 2 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In continuation of our conversation when you visited me, I would like to emphasize what we discussed: that every person must consider and contemplate the fact that they were created by the Ribono shel Olam. It is certain that there is a purpose to this, and that purpose is as stated in the Mishnah in Maseches Kiddushin: "I was not created except to serve my Maker." This means that a person was created to fulfill the will of Hashem in this world. And what is the will of Hashem Yisbarach? It has already been stated clearly and explicitly in the Torah Shebichtav and Torah Shebaal Peh, which contain precise instructions on how one must conduct oneself in daily life—and not only for Rabbis, shochtim, and melamdim, but also for merchants, employees, doctors, lawyers, and so on.

The beginning of a Jew’s day is when he rises from sleep and says, "**Modeh** ani lefanecha **melech** chai v'kayam shehechezarta bi nishmati **b'chemlah rabbah** emunatecha." This means that he acknowledges that Hashem Yisbarach is the Master of the world and governs the world with **chemlah rabbah** (great compassion). This implies that what Hashem Yisbarach demands of a person—and of a Jew in particular—He, Baruch Hu, only demands what one **is able** to do. More precisely, what is demanded of a Jew is **certainly** within his ability to fulfill at the appropriate time.

Especially in your case, since Hashem Yisbarach has helped you and you have established yourself in your city, and you also have influence over your surroundings, you must—as a shaliach of Hashem Yisbarach—take an interest, day in and day out, in illuminating your surroundings with the light of Torah and mitzvos. And—

One cannot be satisfied with the status quo of yesterday and say that one has already fulfilled one's obligation. For proof that something is alive is that it **grows**. As my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, gave a parable regarding the spiritual life of a Jew: it is like someone climbing a steep mountain; he cannot stop in the middle, because wherever he stops, he will slide back down. And one should not be afraid of how one can constantly climb—go upward—without stopping. As mentioned earlier, since Hashem Yisbarach demands it, it is certain that He, Baruch Hu, provides the strength and the capabilities for it. An example of this can also be seen in the human body: while the various limbs of a person must rest from time to time, the brain and the heart work constantly without pause, and that is proof that the human body is alive.

I hope that you will reflect on what we discussed and on what I am writing to you here. May Hashem Yisbarach strengthen you to carry out your spiritual Jewish mission from Hashem Yisbarach in your city of Norwalk, to influence your surroundings and all those over whom you have influence, to bring them even closer to Yiddishkeit and Torah and mitzvos. And if you act in this way, it will certainly be with success.

You told me about your son and daughter, may they live and be well, and not knowing if they read Yiddish fluently, I am enclosing a copy of a letter I wrote to a group of students who visited me, and I hope that this will also interest your children, may they live and be well.

I wish that you will bring me good tidings regarding all of the above, and hopefully we will see each other before your departure, and possibly even sooner than we discussed when you were with me.

With blessings.

## 1,397

B"H, 2 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in the city of Montreal, may it be built and established,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter via the esteemed Chossid, active in communal affairs, one of the elder rabbonim of Anash, R' Shmuel, may he live.

In response to your questions and the various proposals he presented in your name and his own, I hereby suggest the following:

1) It is highly appropriate to arrange the studies in such a way that those who wish—and especially those who have come from overseas—will be able to avoid secular studies. Certainly, there are also those among the students themselves who desire this, and it is incumbent upon the administration to make every effort to ensure they do not study the aforementioned subjects.

2) One must find a way to engage the students even on Shabbos and Yomim Tovim. If this is not possible in the yeshiva building due to the distance or similar reasons, you must find ways to hold farbrengens or gatherings in a central location in each neighborhood. The main thing is to avoid a situation where there is a disconnect between the weekday and the holy days—that is, that the students have a connection to Tomchei Temimim during the week, but this connection weakens on Shabbos and Yomim Tovim.

3) I hereby approve your proposal that the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and scholarly, R' Menachem Zev, may he live, serve as the spiritual mashpia of the yeshiva. He will surely be able to arrange matters in such a way that it will not interfere with his work of strengthening the standing and drawing the hearts of the baalei batim he influences toward their Father in Heaven.

4) I was pleased to read in your letter that you will be accepting the students from [Yeshivas] Netivos Olam into your yeshiva. May it be with success. The main point is that this should open a new path in the conduct of the yeshiva, where the matter of yiras shamayim is highlighted more prominently.

5) "The jealousy of scribes increases wisdom" (see the note on this in Kuntres Hecholotzu, p. 16). Given the current situation in your city, where additional schools and yeshivos have been established, you surely understand the hint from Above regarding yourselves: that you now require extra effort and a **significant** increase beyond the baseline to establish the yeshiva at the necessary height, in accordance with the will of its founder, my father-in-law, the Rebbe. It is certain that since He demands this of you—with all strength and vigor—you surely possess the inner powers for this, and there is the possibility to develop the yeshiva in this direction within your camp. May it be the will of Hashem that you also do not lack the **will** to bring all of the above into actual practice. This will be good for the yeshiva, not only in spirituality but also in material matters.

I am certain you will confirm receipt of this letter immediately upon its arrival, and I look forward to your response as to whether my aforementioned suggestions were accepted. Most importantly, [I look forward to hearing] about their implementation in practice and in the proper conduct appropriate for the various classes of the yeshiva.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

***

**R' Shmuel:** Levitin.

## 1,398

B"H, 3 Shevat, 5712

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter of 15 Teves in due time. When I was at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I mentioned your son, may he live, and yourself, as you requested in your letter.

Based on what is explained there, it is understood that involvement in this is also a channel and vessel for drawing down and receiving the blessings of Hashem, especially for the proper health that will enable you to set times for the study of the revealed Torah and the Torah of Chassidus with peace of mind and peace of body.

With blessings for proper health—awaiting good news.

May Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted, bestow upon you and upon all who participate in this holy work an abundance of blessing and success, both in your communal work and in your private affairs, in a manner that is good, visible, and revealed, from soul to body.

With regards and blessings to the entire group.

#### ***1399***

Printed in Sefer Zikaron (Gorodetzky), p. 220.

## 1

B"H, 3 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and exalted, a G-d-fearing man, an activist of many accomplishments, the generous R' Moshe Levanda, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive a report from my personal representative and director of our European relief bureau, the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, who occupies himself with the needs of the community in good faith, etc., Rabbi Binyamin Gorodetzky, regarding his visit to Madrid.

I was particularly pleased to hear of your important work for the benefit of the community: that you and your wife, may she live, have dedicated a shul for the benefit of the congregation, etc., and that you have now undertaken to bring about a great improvement in your community by establishing a kosher kitchen, having dedicated a suitable building in the center of the city for this purpose.

It is unnecessary to elaborate on the great merit and mitzvah of being among those who "bring merit to the many," especially in such important matters as those mentioned in the *Mi Sheberach* prayer—those who dedicate shuls for prayer, etc., and provide bread for guests, etc.—for which the reward is specified: "The Holy One, blessed be He, will pay their reward, etc., and will send blessing and success in all the work of their hands."

However, I wish to express my hope and emphasize that, like every living thing, your good work will continue to grow, and that you will increase your efforts in all matters for the benefit of the community, to strengthen Torah and Yiddishkeit both among the local residents and among the student youth.

The Almighty does not remain a debtor, and He will surely bestow upon you an abundance of blessings and grant you success, both in your work for the benefit of the community and in your own personal affairs, in both material and spiritual matters.

It will give me great pleasure to hear further good news regarding your work.

With blessing.

## 1,303

1,303

B”H, 3 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning the damage they sustained due to the flood, etc.: You have surely seen the letter of the Alter Rebbe regarding what he wrote to R’ M. of Dribin (printed in *Beis Rebbe*, Part 1, p. 150. See also *Meah Shearim*, p. 36; and similarly from the Mitteler Rebbe—ibid., p. 28. And the Tzemach Tzedek in *Sefer HaMitzvos*, p. 228). [The concept is] that after a loss, the *middas hadin* (attribute of judgment) awakens the *middas harachamim* (attribute of mercy), which is greater than the *middas hachesed* (attribute of kindness) that existed initially. As is known, this is the level of Yaakov, an inheritance without boundaries, reaching from one end to the other, and this is the concept of wealth. May it be the will [of Hashem] that you see this very soon with physical eyes, below ten *tefachim*.

With blessings for success in all your affairs.

## 1504

B"H, 3 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your notification that you have reached the age of sixteen, you have surely learned in Chassidus the explanation of the concept, "And Avraham was old, advanced in days" (*Bereishis* 24:1)—that the essence of time and days is that they be filled with the substance of Torah and *mitzvos*. When you write in your letter that you have reached sixteen years and ask for a blessing, without informing me of your studies or your standing and situation in *yiras shamayim*, the essence is missing from the book. For in the fact that sixteen years have been filled for you with length of days and years, you yourself are taking no part; and regarding the purpose of your creation, as the Sages ruled (*Kiddushin* 82b), "I was not created but to serve my Maker," you mention nothing at all.

May it be the will of Hashem that you grow to be a *yirei shamayim*, a *Chossid*, and a *lamdan*, and that you study Torah with *hasmadah* and *shekidah* in both the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus. May your parents, *shichyu*, derive from you and from all their children, *shichyu*, *nachas*—*Yiddishen nachas*, *Chassidishen nachas*.

I trust you are strengthening yourself to keep the three daily *shiurim* that are incumbent upon every soul, which were instituted by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nivgam, zia*—namely, the *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*, as is well known.

With blessings for Torah study with *yiras shamayim*.

## 1005

B"H, 4 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

Yesterday, Rabbi Hodakov, *sh’yichyeh*, relayed to me the content of your telephone conversation, and shortly thereafter, your special delivery letter arrived, along with the newspaper clippings.

Regarding your concern that another merchant might restrict your orders and diminish your *parnassah*, *chalilah*, and your request for my opinion: in accordance with your request, when I am at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, navgam, zi"a*, I will mention you once again.

In any event, like all Yidden, who are *ma'aminim bnei ma'aminim*, you must be certain that a person’s sustenance is determined from Rosh Hashanah until Yom Kippur. The income that the *Ribono shel Olam* has designated for you—which I am certain is *b'harchavah*—no one, *ch"v*, will be able to diminish, and certainly not take away.

One must only be strong in *bitachon* in the *Ribono shel Olam*, and this must be done *b'simchah*. As it is written in the *Zohar*, *Parshas Tetzaveh* (183b), our world, the lower world, receives all *hashpa'os* from above. If here below there is joy and light, then from above, things proceed in a similarly bright and joyful manner. And it is written, "Serve Hashem with joy"; consequently, when a Yid is joyful, that joy below draws down upon him joy from above.

Especially in your case, as you have the *zechus* of *mezakeh es harabim* by enabling the printing of a *sefer* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, navgam, zi"a*, this will surely ensure that you have *parnassah b'harchavah*. And, what is even more important, that you utilize it with *hatzlachah* for healthy matters and for *inyanim* of Torah and *mitzvos* *b'yad rechavah*.

I hope to hear good news from you.

In connection with the *yom hahilula* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I am enclosing my suggestions regarding the *minhagim* for this day.

## 1507

Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 1508

B"H, 7 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Peretz, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter in good time, in which you inform me that you will soon be completing the Six Orders of the Mishnah. May it be the will of Hashem that just as He has helped you to complete the Six Orders of the Mishnah now, so too may He help you to begin them once again, and to complete them, to learn and to teach, to observe, to perform, and to fulfill. It is well known that the letters of the word *Mishnah* are the same as the letters of **"neshamah"** (soul), and through this, the light of "a mitzvah is a candle and the Torah is light" and the *maor* (luminary) of the Torah—which is the teachings of Chassidus—will be increased within it. This will assist you in your personal matters.

To your brother, the esteemed Rav and Chossid, who is occupied with communal needs, R' Gershon, may he live, I have written a direct response to his letter to me.

With blessings for success in the study of Torah, the fulfillment of mitzvos, and your personal matters.

P.S. Transcribed here is an excerpt from what was said during the farbrengen on the day of the Hillula of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, which was the 24th of Teves just passed.

The story is well known that the Maggid arranged, at the beginning of the Alter Rebbe’s arrival in Mezritch, that his son, the "Malach," would study the teachings of Chassidus with the Alter Rebbe, and the Alter Rebbe would study the revealed Torah with the "Malach." When they began their study of "From when..." [the first Mishnah in Berachos], and the Alter Rebbe began to explain the Mishnah, the Malach said that he explains "from when" (*imasei*) as being derived from the word *eimah* (awe) and fear. And in connecting the beginning of the Shas with its end (for in the division of the Shas here, the orders of the Mishnah are also divided, and even though the completion was in Masechta Niddah, they are connected to one another):

The conclusion of the Mishnah is: "The Holy One, Blessed be He, found no vessel that holds blessing for Israel other than peace." Peace and the unity of all the children of Israel, as is also explained in Tanya, Chapter 32: "Bless us, our Father, [as] we are all as one." True unity of people in general, and even of the children of Israel in particular, is impossible when there is some personal bias or benefit involved, for then one is not uniting with **the other**, but rather seeking **one's own** benefit. True unity is only possible as explained in Tanya, Chapter 32, because all are equal and "one Father for all of us," etc., by virtue of the root of their souls **in the One Hashem.** As is explained in Chassidic discourse, the root of the souls is even higher than Torah and mitzvos. As our Sages of blessed memory said in Bereishis Rabbah at the beginning, that the thought of Israel preceded everything, even the Torah, as it is written, "Speak to the children of Israel." This is the beginning of the Shas with the *Krias Shema*, and the conclusion with the vessel that holds blessing, which is peace. Peace comes about through saying the *Krias Shema*, "**Hashem is One.**" But in order for the unity to be true, it must be "from when"—an acceptance of the yoke of Heaven, and not from the perspective of intellect and reason, even the intellect and reason of holiness. This is also explained in Chassidic discourse in several places.

## 1,009

B"H, 7 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Through one of your acquaintances, it was conveyed to me that your state of health is not so good. I am writing to awaken you—though surely this is not new to you—to the fact that every single one of us is under the individual providence of the Creator, may He be blessed. Consequently, if it seems to you that someone has the power to harm you, this is merely an illusion, for such a thing is impossible. Therefore, you must be strong in your bitachon, knowing that just as Hashem leads the entire world, He likewise leads you and your body, for man is called a "small world" (*Tanchuma*, beginning of *Parshas Pekudei*; *Tikkunei Zohar*, *Tikkun* 69, p. 117b). If at times you feel a weakening in this bitachon, it is not worth dwelling on it; divert your attention from this weakness, for it is surely nothing but an illusion. Before long, you too will see that just as all Bnei Yisrael are believers, the children of believers, you also are strong in your bitachon.

You should certainly follow the doctor’s instructions, for the Torah has given permission (which also means strength) to the physician to heal. May Hashem grant that you soon bring me good news of an improvement in your health and that it is steadily getting better.

It would be appropriate to recite a few chapters of Tehillim each day. It is well known that King David requested that the recitation of Tehillim be considered as equivalent to engaging in the study of *Negaim* and *Ohalos*, and thus it encompasses both the aspect of tefillah (see *Berachos* 4b) and the aspect of Torah.

With blessings for a speedy recovery and proper health, awaiting good news.

## 1,311

B"H, 7 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 2 Shevat, in which you write that your wife’s physician suggests she undergo surgery to: a) repair the sutures from the previous surgery that have come apart, and b) lift and reposition the uterus:

In my opinion, this is the correct course of action, provided that another specialist in this field agrees to it.

Regarding the third proposal, where the physician also suggests c) tying and sealing the fallopian tubes during the aforementioned surgery:

This does not seem right to me. You should consult with an observant Rav regarding the halachic ruling on this matter. Even if it were to be permissible according to Halacha, it seems from your brief words that such a procedure would deprive your wife of the possibility of conceiving again. Why would you do that?

As for what you wrote—that the doctors attribute your wife’s weakness to the frequency of her pregnancies and births until now—it is possible: a) that they are mistaken in this, and the matter depends only on proper eating and drinking and conducting one’s life in a way that will restore her strength. b) Even if it were to be determined that it is a danger, G-d forbid, for her to conceive in her current state of health, see the Responsa of the Tzemach Tzedek, Even HaEzer, Siman 89, which permits the use of a *moch* in such a situation. Regarding the specific methods for this, you should consult with an observant Rav.

Enclosed is a copy of the general letter regarding the *farbrengen* of the "Festival of Festivals," 19 Kislev, as well as the customs for the *hilula* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May Hashem merit us to the fulfillment of the prophecy, "Awake and sing, you who dwell in the dust," with him among them, speedily in our days, truly.

With blessings.

## 1,513

B"H, 15 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 8 Shevat in due time, and the names were mentioned at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Surely, he will arouse Divine mercy for all those mentioned in your letter for whatever they may need.

I hope that by the time you receive my letter, your health has already improved; please inform me of this, as well as the status of your family members, may they live.

I am somewhat surprised that you were not here either on 19 Kislev or on the day of the Hilula to visit the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. Even if it is true that you have a reason and justification for this, that only pertains to the matter of reward and punishment—so as not to be punished, Heaven forbid, for not being present here. However, it is known that regarding the concept of *ones* (compulsion), while the Merciful One exempts one from liability, we do not say that it is considered as if one actually performed the act. Surely, further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

You should certainly use your influence on your son, may he live, to support him and encourage him in the path of Torah and mitzvos, and from time to time remind him of his promise to me to return to the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva. There is reason to hope that, in the end, he will agree to this.

With blessings.

## 1414

1414

B”H, 15 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, who engages in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Greetings and blessings!

It is with pleasure that I hereby acknowledge receipt of your two letters, dated 7 Shevat and 5 Shevat (Beshalach). It is a pity that you were unable to be present at the farbrengen of the second Yahrtzeit of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory; surely, everything depends on mazal, even a Sefer Torah.

I would point out the two statements of our Sages regarding whether a Sefer Torah is superior or a Torah scholar is superior (Kiddushin 33b, see Ran there; Makkot 22b, see Chiddushei Agadot there), and the statement of our Sages at the beginning of Bereishis Rabbah that the thought of Yisrael preceded everything (even the Torah), as it is stated in the Torah, "Speak to the Bnei Yisrael," etc.

I was pleased to read in your second letter that, finally, you have succeeded in nullifying and rectifying the matter of kosher meat. May it be the will of Hashem that very soon you will also succeed in rectifying the matter of chinuch. As is well known, the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, is that in the United States, for what one puts into a pot, one demands supervision and inspects it, yet for what one puts into the head, it is ownerless—anyone who wishes may take for himself the title of teacher, G-d-fearing person, educator, pedagogue, etc. (It is worth noting how great is the conversation of a Torah scholar, for even in the Shas, the head is called a "pot." Seemingly, this can also be connected to the concept of "Your Torah is within my **innards**," as written in Tanya, Chapter 5).

Of course, as you requested, I mentioned you and your wife, may they live, at the tziyun of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, on the day of the Yahrtzeit. May it be the will of Hashem that all prayers and requests be fulfilled through the merit of the tzaddik, the foundation of the world. And he shall continue to be a **supreme** tzaddik, and he is the one who provides grain for all the **land**.

With blessings.

## 1515

1515

B"H, 15 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., R' Mordechai HaKohen
Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter, in which you describe your situation and relate that you have been approached with a request: since your community is organizing a "Brotherhood Week," it has been suggested that you, as the rabbi of the congregation, should participate by delivering a speech or the like, together with—lehavdil—a priest, etc. Furthermore, this gathering is being held in a building belonging to their house of worship, even if not in the sanctuary itself, but within the building. You ask for my opinion on this matter.

It is clear that this is forbidden, both according to the letter of the law and, even more so, because of *maris ayin* (the appearance of impropriety). For the observer will not analyze the nuances at all; it is enough for him to see, *chas v’shalom*, a Chareidi rabbi and a priest associating in friendship, etc., etc.

Regarding your question as to how to explain this to your board members, there are several ways to explain it. I will provide one of them, which may be appropriate for your status and situation:

One of the things these countries pride themselves on is the concept of freedom and liberty, where everyone can live according to their own opinion and faith. It is therefore understood that one must not do anything that would lead to coercion or misunderstanding, especially in matters of religion—which is one of the areas where coercion in one form or another is most common.

According to what is written, the people of Israel are the "fewest of all the peoples"—meaning few in quantity and few in physical power. Despite this, throughout the entire time of the golus, they have not compromised even by a *kutz shel yud* (the tip of a letter) in matters concerning their faith, even to the point of *mesiras nefesh*. For in matters of faith, it is difficult to distinguish between a "minor" matter and a "major" one, as even a minor matter can, *chas v’shalom*, lead to *kefirah*. This is because it is a matter of faith. An analogy for this: a very large hole in the leg of an animal—even if the leg is removed—does not render the animal *treif*, yet a hole the size of a needle prick in the membrane of the brain renders the entire animal *treif*. The same applies to a person, both physically and regarding his soul. It is therefore understood that in all matters of faith, one must be extremely careful and not give any room for misunderstanding to the masses, even to women and children. The latter, upon seeing a Chareidi rabbi speaking after a priest of the Christian religion—lehavdil—will learn from this that there is a commonality between the religions, or that one religion has precedence over the other, etc. This is especially true if the location of this event is in the building of their religion, which holds the physical power in their country. And if this were to cause a misunderstanding in even one observer, even a child, it is worth canceling the entire event for that reason alone. As it is brought in *Midrash Rabbah, Devarim* (Chapter 7:8), at the time of the giving of the Torah, the *Ribono shel Olam* said that if even one person out of the six hundred thousand had been missing—and our Sages did not specify who that one individual was, and it makes no difference whether it was the most prominent or the most spiritually insignificant—the *Ribono shel Olam* would not have given the Torah to all of Israel, not even to Moshe Rabbeinu.

One should not view this as an affront to the honor of the priest, etc., etc., for as I wrote at the beginning of my letter, this is precisely what they pride themselves on: that in these countries, everyone has the right to conduct themselves according to their own faith and opinion.

As you requested, I am sending this letter quickly; therefore, I will respond to the other matters, *im yirtzeh Hashem*, next time.

With blessings for leading your congregation in the fear of Heaven.

## 1516

1516

B.H., 15 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the congregants of the Anshei Lubavitch Synagogue
in Boston,
and at their head, the President and the gentlemen, may they live.

Peace and blessing!

With satisfaction, I received your greetings through the esteemed Chossid, the G-d-fearing man, who engages in communal needs with faith, etc., Rabbi Eli Simpson, may he live. I accepted the blessing and in return, I ask that he convey my blessing to all the congregants and members of the shul, together with their families, may they live, with all that they require in children, life, and ample sustenance.

As one of the oldest shuls in the country, and specifically in Boston, which bears the name Lubavitch, it is superfluous to emphasize the great merit of possessing this name—the name of the town of Lubavitch, from which the study of Chassidus and the conduct of Chassidic ways spread with greater strength and intensity since the time of my grandfather, the Tzemach Tzedek, and onwards. The name Lubavitch itself evokes an entire philosophy of life.

As my father-in-law, the Rebbe, related, the name Lubavitch (a small town in Lithuania), which in the Russian language means "love," was given in its time because one of the founders of the town, one of the *tzaddikim nistarim*, distinguished himself by his love for people in general and for all creatures that Hashem Yisbarach created.

The fact that Chassidei Chabad are connected with the name Lubavitch is not a coincidence. As my father-in-law, the Rebbe, said in the name of the Baal Shem Tov, every word in the world is by *hashgacha pratis*. This is also the case here, which demonstrates the deep connection of Chassidus with the three loves: *ahavas Hashem*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Yisrael*, which are inseparable and which must accompany the daily life of every Jew.

These three aforementioned loves find expression, to a certain extent, in a shul. In a shul, one davens and recites *V'ahavta es Hashem Elokecha*—*ahavas Hashem*; one reads from the Torah and makes the blessing, "Who chose us from all the nations and gave us His Torah"—*ahavas haTorah*; and in a shul, matters of *tzedakah* are also conducted, which is an expression of *ahavas Yisrael*.

It troubled me to hear from the esteemed Chossid, the G-d-fearing man, who engages in communal needs with faith, etc., Rabbi Eli Simpson, may he live, that many are moving out of the neighborhood where the shul is located, and that it is difficult to have a *minyan* every day. Perhaps it would be advisable for the members of the shul to consult with one another about establishing a branch of the shul in the new neighborhood where Jews are moving. Gradually, they will be able to transfer all the activities of the shul, and especially the *derachei u'minhagei hachassidim*, to the new neighborhood, so that there, too, the name Lubavitch will serve as a guide for other congregants as to how Chassidic Jews should conduct themselves.

I conclude with my blessing to all the congregants, in both material and spiritual matters.

#### ***1516***

**Related:** *Sefer HaZichronos*, Part 1, Chapter 1.

## 1717

B"H, 15 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Many thanks for the good news you conveyed to me, that the surgery performed on Mrs. ... *tichyeh* was successful. May Hashem grant that you always be a "good man who brings good news," as our Sages of blessed memory say in *Kiddushin* 40a: "Good to Heaven and good to people." In the context of a person's *avodah* to his Creator, this means: "Good to Heaven" refers to the *neshamah elokis*, and "good to people" refers to his body and his *nefesh habahamish*. This is a teaching of the Baal Shem Tov, as he explains the verse, "When you see the donkey of one who hates you crouching..." which is transcribed in *Hayom Yom*, page 23.

I am interested to hear about your studies. Surely you also have a set time for the area of Torah that our Sages of blessed memory call *kav chumtin* (*Shabbos* 31a), for upon this depends the endurance and benefit of all the "wheat-gatherers" (as Torah is called "wheat").

With blessings for success in Torah study with true *yiras shamayim*.

## 1,818

1,818

B"H, 15 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, engaged in the needs of the community, etc.,
R' Saadia, may he live, Shliach

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the 7th, 8th, and 12th of Shevat, along with the *pidyon nefesh* and the lists enclosed therein. You will surely receive the receipts directly from the office.

It is a great pity that the matter of your papers and permits is being delayed so significantly, but my hope is strong that, in the end, *didan notzach* (ours shall be the victory) and you will participate with all your strengths and talents in "spreading the wellsprings outward." And although one cannot refer to G-d-fearing and observant Jews as "outward," nevertheless, regarding the knowledge of the inner dimension of Torah—and especially the teachings of Chassidus, which are not known there—this too is called "outward." This is similar to what is explained in *Tanya*, *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 29, regarding the *mitzvos*: that even though the *mitzvos* are the inner dimension of the supreme will of Hashem, etc., there are many levels of "inner within inner," etc.

The office will surely also inform you that they have received the *pidyon nefesh*, for due to the current order of things, the processing of the matter is delayed.

With blessings.
