## 1221

1221

B"H, 15 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with joy that I received your letter from Tuesday of Parshas Shemos, in which you describe your upbringing and life up until recently. I write with joy because I have heard of you many times before, though not directly from you yourself, and I hope that from today onward you will maintain a written connection, which will bring about an increase in Torah and mitzvos.

You do not mention in your letter the fixed times you have for studying Nigleh and also Toras HaChassidus. There are currently several young men in your city with whom you can speak about these matters and also establish a fixed time to study Nigleh and Chassidus with them. I hope that you will not delay this and will arrange it as soon as possible, if you have not already done so until now.

Regarding your complaint that you did not have the opportunity to study in your youth, there are two points to consider: a) There were many among the Gedolei Yisrael who, due to various circumstances, began their studies only in their later years, and yet they achieved great success. b) From this, it is also understood that this is no excuse to exempt yourself or to make the matter of studying Torah—and the various disciplines of Torah, especially regarding Toras HaChassidus—easier for yourself now.

And in continuation of the fact that Hashem has granted you the merit and given you the opportunity to educate Jewish children—who are the children of Hashem, blessed be He—and to bring their hearts closer to their Father in Heaven, it is certain that you will have Siyata Dishmaya to succeed in your own studies and also in the education of your children, together with your wife, may they live. I hope to hear good news from you.

With blessings.

## 1222

1222

B"H, 15 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you also write regarding the condition of your wife, tichyeh: You should consult with a specialist physician in this field, who will provide your wife, tichyeh, with instructions on how she should conduct herself during the days of her pregnancy. For his part, he should: a) check the mezuzos in your home to ensure they are kosher; b) see to it that your wife, tichyeh, gives tzedakah to the Kupas Rabbi Meir Baal HaNess before lighting candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov; c) when she becomes pregnant, do not publicize the matter until she enters the fifth month of her pregnancy; d) when she becomes pregnant, during Krias Shema Al Hamitah, before the blessing of Hamapil, recite the chapter of Tehillim "Lamnatzeiach Yaancha," and upon finishing the chapter, repeat the verse "Yaancha" once more; at the time of its recitation, or prior to it, he should contemplate that it be the will of Hashem as if he had directed all his kavanah toward this; e) when your wife becomes pregnant, in a good and auspicious hour, inform us here, so that it may be conveyed to the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, zatzuklalleh, nishmaso b'eden gan eden, zechuso yagein aleinu.

It is unnecessary to elaborate on the necessity of proper conduct in all matters pertaining to Taharas Hamishpachah, as explained in the Poskim. May Hashem grant you the merit to share good tidings.

With blessings.

## 1523

B"H, 15 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from the eve of the second yahrtzeit of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and I begin by asking your forgiveness. It seems that my intention in sending the check was not interpreted in accordance with what I had in mind. While I certainly appreciate the "magnitude" of the sum, on the other hand, I must also take into account the possibilities of our fund. The essence of this is based on a story my father-in-law, the Rebbe, told in the name of the Tzemach Tzedek, and which he subsequently established as a foundational principle for himself: When one of those connected to him was in a difficult situation, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, would send him a very small sum. He explained this by noting that the Tzemach Tzedek said his fund was like the statement of our Sages (Bava Basra 10b), "Whoever takes a **prutah** from Iyov is blessed." A prutah is the smallest of sums, yet because it came from the fund of a man who was "perfect and upright," it brought immense success. Since the fund currently under my hand is also what remains from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and I am his Chossid, I am certain that even a prutah from this fund brings blessing to the endeavor in which it is invested. Nevertheless, since I estimated that your honor was in a state of being "submissive" to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and a dear friend more than a Chossid, I sent a check for a sum that is close to the maximum that can be sent at this time, in accordance with the state of the fund.

The conclusion from the above is: a) My hope is that you will not hold it against me; b) It is a pity that you did not use the check. I reiterate that it surely would have brought success and blessing, and my offer still stands. Perhaps I weighed the matter poorly, as I transgressed the saying stated in the name of the Alter Rebbe, as I wrote in my previous letter.

It is somewhat surprising that you do not mention anything regarding the state of your wife’s health or your own. I will conclude with heartfelt wishes for you and your wife, may they live, that your needs be filled with everything you require soon—and not only "the sufficiency for his need which he lacks," but even more than that, as explained in the words of Torah regarding the distinction between the obligation of "the sufficiency for his need" and the fact that "you are not obligated to make him rich," and [the concept of] wealth.

With blessings,

P.S. Enclosed is the *Maamar* "Ner Hashem" from Chanukah, where this matter of "whoever takes a prutah" is also discussed.

## 1,024

1,024

B"H, 16 Shevat, 5712

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-scholar, etc., Moreinu HaRav A.Y. [may he live and be well],

Greetings and blessings!

I received in due time the two copies of your sefer, *Birkas Avraham* on the *Hilchos Treifos*, and I thank you for them.

You have presented to those who study this subject a collection of halachos from the *Rishonim* and *Acharonim* in a well-organized and beautiful format. Surely, the sefer will bring benefit to many, and the merit of the many will depend upon it.

However, I was very surprised that in many places the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, the *Tzemach Tzedek*—the rabbi of the entire diaspora—were not cited, even though it seems you have seen his sefarim, as his words are transcribed in some places. I have noted in the margins **some** of the omissions.

With blessings to engage in Torah and the work of Heaven with tranquility and proper health, as you requested, I have mentioned you and your wife [may she live and be well] at the holy gravesite.

Enclosed are two scrip notes, each for five shekels.

**Omissions:**

1) **A bone in the skull:** This is entirely missing from your sefer, as are other matters regarding the skull (such as a perforation in it, etc.; see the *Acharonim* on *Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah* 30). Although you transcribed the law regarding a bone in the heart or lung, see *Responsa Tzemach Tzedek, Yoreh Deah* 18-19, and the references there to *Responsa Binyan Avraham* and *Responsa Mishkenos Yaakov*.

2) **A blister on the lung of a non-kosher animal:** In *Likutei Yehuda* (36b), it is noted that the *Shem Chadash* (37, sub-section 1) permits it. See there in the *Shem Chadash* that, on the contrary, where there is no established custom, one should be stringent; however, in *Piskei Dinim* of the *Tzemach Tzedek* (beginning of section 36), he permits it in salted or bitter [lungs], even if there is no custom.

3) **Redness on the lung in a *mevushal* (cooked) state:** See *Piskei Dinim* at the end of section 38, where he permits it in a case of significant financial loss (the opinions on this are in *Likutei Yehuda* 249b, but the *Piskei Dinim* of the *Tzemach Tzedek* was not cited).

4) **Two gall bladders:** See the opinion of the *Tzemach Tzedek* in detail in *Responsa Shaar HaMiluim*, sections 22-23.

5) **A perforation in the spleen of a large ox:** In *Likutei Yehuda* (150a), he brings a *p'sak din* from Rav Kook on this. However, the *Tzemach Tzedek* preceded him in *Responsa Yoreh Deah*, sections 42-43.

#### ***1,024***

**Moreinu HaRav A.Y.:** Moreinu HaRav Avraham Yehuda Duchovni.

## 1025

B.H., 18 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn

To the G-d-fearing, illustrious, and distinguished, who engages in the needs of the community and conducts his business with integrity, etc.,
R' Yaakov, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

Enclosed is my response to the *pidyon nefesh* that I received through you for Mrs. ..., may she live. I am certain that if it is necessary, you will find the appropriate words to explain it to her.

I was pleased to read in your letter that during *Seudah Shlishis* you studied the *maamar* of 13 Shevat. I hope that not only—as the Tzemach Tzedek said to the Chassid, R' Hillel—do the *neshamos* hear, but that you have also found the way for the *neshamah*, in its connection to the body, to ensure that the body also feels it. And if not completely, then bit by bit, just as it says in the *Chumash*, "Little by little I will drive them out from before you."

In your letter, you mentioned the *shalom bayis* of Mr. ... and his wife, may they live. One must explain to the father what I wrote to him when the *shidduch* was still being discussed: that they must establish their home upon proper Torah foundations. This is relevant not only to the happiness of the *neshamah* but also to physical well-being. Whether or not one understands the reason for this does not make a great difference—just as when one follows the instructions of a great professor, one receives the benefit even when one does not know the reason why. This is especially true when it is a directive from the Creator of the world, who is also the "Healer of all flesh."

It goes without saying that when I visit the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention Mr. ... and his wife, may they live, for *shalom bayis*. However, one must not forget the main point: that there must be *shalom bayis* between their own *neshamah* and body. This makes *shalom bayis* in the home incomparably easier.

And since Shabbos Parshas Yisro is the Shabbos on which the giving of the Torah is recounted, you will surely utilize in your *shul* what is recounted in the *Kuntres* of 18 Elul 5713, page 36: that at the giving of the Torah, Hashem led the six hundred thousand Jews—excluding the elders, etc.—into a room and taught them *kamatz aleph: ah*. This is the first letter of *Anochi*. See there at length.

With the blessing of a good Shabbos.

1526

R. Moshe Hakohen Sheyevitch also mentions in his letter your sons, [Name] and [Name]. When I am at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I will also mention them for success in their business, and that they should lead a Jewish life—a happy life, both for the *guf* and for the *neshamah*. This is the true success that one can wish for. I am certain that you, as parents, are also utilizing your influence in a peaceful way to explain to them—your children—that such conduct brings light and warmth into a Jewish life.

I look forward to receiving a letter from you that you are both feeling better, and I thank you in advance for the good news.

With blessings.

## 1,429

B"H, 18 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter of 2/2, and I trust you have conveyed to Dr. Wilder what you wrote to me in your letter regarding the situation with your son, *shye*.

When I was at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zi"a*, I mentioned everyone, and I wish to reiterate what I have said several times already: it is certain that the blessing of the *tzaddik yesod olam* will surely be fulfilled; it is only a question of time.

It is more than self-understood—and it is unnecessary to elaborate—how difficult it is to wait for the coming of that happy hour, especially for a father and mother for whom the son, *shye*, is an only child. However, one must be strong in *bitachon* in the Creator, *yisbarach*, who is the true Master of power, the Healer of all flesh, and the One who performs wonders. Surely, He, *baruch hu*, will send His healing at the proper time, and you and your husband, *shichyu*, will recall with joy the time that he suffered, and you will have much *nachas* from your son, *shye*.

Regarding what you write—that you have stopped giving your son the pills that Dr. Wilder prescribed—you should have discussed this with Dr. Wilder and heard his opinion on the matter.

As for your question of whether you should turn to another doctor: if you only wish to consult, I will not hold you back. However, since my father-in-law, the Rebbe, advised you that your son, *shye*, should be treated by Dr. Wilder, you can rely on him. You only need to keep Dr. Wilder informed so that he is always aware of your son’s, *shye*, condition.

I conclude my letter with a deep wish that the blessing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, be fulfilled speedily, and that you and your husband, *shichyu*, will report on this in good health.

With blessings,

P.S. Since you do not mention yourself in your writing, I hope that your health and the health of your husband, *shichyu*, is satisfactory.

## 1030

1030

B"H, Motzaei Shabbos, 21 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn

Agudas Noshim Tzeirois Lubavitch, may they live long,

Blessings and peace!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter, in which you describe in general terms your work, and also inform me that a Melaveh Malkah is taking place at your location this Motzaei Shabbos, Parshas Yisro.

In response to this letter, I wish to express my hope and blessing that you will fulfill the expectations that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, placed upon your organization. For the words of the righteous endure forever, and the wish and demand of a Tzaddik is not merely a demand; it is also a *natisas koach*—meaning that it grants special strength to those of whom the Rebbe makes the request, so that they may fulfill his demand to the fullest extent. A special trait of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, was that he would present his requests and demands in such a way that the person would fulfill them with grace and joy. All of you who are privileged to be part of this organization, which was founded when the Rebbe was still in this world—and it is certain that even now, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, acts as a shield for the organization in general and for each of its members in particular—will surely exert all your strength to fulfill his demands of you. In doing so, you will provide him with *nachas ruach* in the fullest sense of the word, which in turn serves as a channel and a vessel to draw down blessing and success in your personal affairs as well.

It is also self-evident that your task does not consist only—as you write in your letter—of raising funds for the Lubavitch institutions. For no matter how great that may be, one does not fulfill one’s obligation through that alone. Since you are individuals upon whom a great deal of influence depends within your own homes, as well as an impact upon your specific surroundings, you must also serve as a living example of how a Lubavitcher woman should conduct herself personally, how she should establish her home, and what influence she exerts upon her entire environment. One should be able to say with pride, "Behold the growth that I have nurtured"—this is what a true Chassidishe woman is, and from her, one can learn.

As it is written in the Sidra that we read in the Torah this morning, "Thus shall you say to the House of Yaakov and tell the Children of Yisrael." The Midrash comments on this that the Holy One, Blessed be He, said to Moshe Rabbeinu: first "say to the House of Yaakov"—these are the women—and afterward "tell the Children of Yisrael"—these are the men. In this way, the Torah will have an enduring existence among Jews. So too, specifically regarding the conduct of the ways of Chassidus and the behavior of Chassidim, you must set yourselves up so that one can see the "say to the House of Yaakov" and the proper standing in your homes, and in time, in the homes of your good friends and acquaintances.

With blessings for success in your work.

## 1,031

B"H, 23 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Gaon, renowned for his praise, the G-d-fearing, wise, and understanding,
Who engages in good deeds, etc., etc.,
His Honor, our teacher and Rabbi Eliezer, shlita, Av Beis Din of Cincinnati.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have learned that His Honor, shlita, has reached the age of seventy. On the occasion of his seventieth birthday, I join all those who seek his peace and welfare in wishing him all the best.

May Hashem Yisbarach lengthen his days and years in goodness and pleasantness, that he may flourish in Torah and increase in tzedakah and good deeds for the benefit of the community and the individual.

With the blessings of one who honors and blesses him.

P.S. In the Mishnah at the end of the final chapter of Avos, it states: "At seventy, for old age (seivah)." And it is explained further in Bava Basra (75a) that "seivah" is no less than seventy. This is also the ruling in Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, beginning of section 244. However, in the Siddur of the Arizal (at the beginning, in the laws of the synagogue), he writes that one must stand before a person of sixty years (cited in Birkei Yosef, Yoreh Deah, loc. cit.). This is based on what is written in Tikkunei Zohar (Tikkun 21, p. 56a): "There is no 'seivah' less than sixty... at fifty, for old age (ziknah)."

- The reasoning of the Arizal is proven in his Shaar HaMitzvos and in Sefer HaLikkutim. In Minchas Chinuch, Mitzvah 257, he explains the ruling of the Arizal as being due to a concern for the opinion of the Targum. Perhaps he overlooked what is written in Shaar HaMitzvos and the aforementioned Sefer HaLikkutim. In any case, we find several poskim who hold that one should be stringent according to the opinion of the Zohar even where it disagrees with the Gemara, but there is no such logic regarding a dispute between the Targum and the Gemara. -

It may be said that the Yerushalmi and the Bavli also differ in a dispute parallel to that of the Zohar and the Bavli, for the Yerushalmi holds that from fifty and onward it is not considered *kares*, while the Bavli holds from sixty and onward (Tosafos, s.v. *Asheras*, Yevamos at the beginning. See also Mareh HaPanim, Yerushalmi, beginning of Maseches Bikkurim).

With this, we can also understand the variation in the sugyos, for in the sugya of the Bavli (Moed Katan 28a) it states: "Seventy is for *seivah*," whereas in the Yerushalmi (Bikkurim) it is not mentioned.

Tikkunei Zohar is the "Talmud of the Land of Israel," and consequently, it follows its approach.

See the books cited in Sdei Chemed, Klalim, Maareches Zaken, and in Sefer Kehillas Yaakov (by the author of Malai HaRo'im), Maareches Seivah.

#### ***1,031***

**Rabbi Eliezer:** Silver. Another letter to him — above, Vol. 2, 427.

## 1,533

B"H, 25 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

It is unnecessary for me to express my gratitude to you for this, for our Sages of blessed memory have said, "The reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself"—meaning that the mitzvah itself is the greatest possible reward.

...I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, who said in the name of the Baal Shem Tov (founder of the teachings of Chassidus) that as great as a father’s love is for his only son, the love of Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted, for His firstborn son, Yisrael—for each and every Jew—is infinitely greater. Since you are engaged in this holy work through the institutions of **Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak Lubavitch** to bring many sons and daughters of Yisrael closer to their Father in Heaven, you can imagine how great the *nachas ruach* is that you cause Above, which is infinitely greater than the *nachas ruach* a father derives from his only son. May the merit of this work be great enough to draw down blessings from the Source of all blessings...

Awaiting good news, with blessing and success.

## 1,334

B"H, 25 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., R' Avraham Chaim 

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter has now been received, in which you inform me—among other things—of the marriage of your son, Rabbi Moshe Tzvi, may he live.

I hereby wish to express my blessings of Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov. May it be in a good and auspicious hour, and may they build a home in Israel upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, as explained in the teachings of Chassidus. May you see from them much nachas—Yiddishe nachas, Chassidishe nachas.

The telegram was surely received.

With the blessing of Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov.

P.S. It is worth noting, very briefly, regarding what is written here concerning the marriage of one : In general, there are two ways to understand the role of witnesses. 1) The testimony is merely a matter of clarification, such as witnesses testifying that a certain person’s verdict was finalized in Beis Din in a specific manner. 2) The testimony is a condition that constitutes the reality of the matter itself. This is the nature of witnesses for kiddushin, which must specifically take place in the presence of witnesses. Similarly, regarding what Hashem said, "You are My witnesses", here too there are two ways to understand this: 1) That they are merely testifying about this matter, or 2) That they are also a part of the reality itself. This is especially true regarding the matters of which it is said that one becomes a **partner** to the Holy One, Blessed be He, in the work of Creation. In avodah, this is achieved through avodah that transcends ta'am v'da'as—meaning that he himself is not a "reality"—for only in such a manner can one become a partner in the work of Creation, since He is above creation and its reality. And there is no room here to elaborate.

Regarding what you wrote about what the phrase "all of them shall be permitted" refers to according to our custom—it can be said that it refers to that which is below it: "There is nothing here, no...".

***

 See Ohr HaTorah by the Tzemach Tzedek, Shemos, p. 39 and onwards.

## 1335

1335

B"H, 25 Shevat, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote in your letter, that you feel you are falling, Heaven forbid, compared to your previous state, etc.: It is a well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory (in the name of his father, our master and teacher), that "one action is better than a thousand sighs." Without entering into the essence of the matter—whether this is true or merely an imagination on your part, a tactic of the *yetzer hara* to weaken you in your *avodah*—I see no benefit in your sighs. Instead, you should increase your strength in your *avodah* in the field of proper *chinuch*; this concerns your influence on others. Secondly, you should increase your strength in the study of Chassidus—that is, simply *lerenen opter chassidus mit a varimkeit un a lebedikeit* (to study Chassidus often with warmth and vitality). If you find it difficult to generate this vitality on your own while studying in isolation, you can surely find a *chavrusa* for this in your camp, for "if one says, 'I have labored and found,' believe him." This is especially true given that each of us has the assistance of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, who sacrificed his life for the dissemination of the study of Chassidus in all countries, in all places, and among all types of people.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter, that you must conduct yourself like the elders of *anash* even though you know your own standing and situation and that you do not belong to that category—yet you feel compelled to do so because it is what your position and the people around you demand: It is known from our Sages, "If your friend calls you a donkey, put a saddle on your back" (*Bava Kamma* 92b). How much more so is this true if people speak of you in terms of spiritual elevation; you must exert all your strength to become consistent with what they say about you. For this, too, is the promise: "If one says, 'I have labored and found,' believe him."

Regarding what you wrote concerning the thoughts that confuse you: The advice given by our *Nesi'im* is to have the letters of Torah fixed in your mind so that you can recite them by heart. Whether in *nigleh* or Chassidus—and surely you also know some chapters of Mishnayos and Tanya by heart—*vet dos arois-shtufen di* (this will push out) those thoughts that should not be there.

I was pleased to read in your letter that on the day of the *hilula*, 10 Shevat, you spoke before the students about the themes of the day. I am certain that in your speaking with the students, you intend to bring them to matters of action in practical *mitzvos*. May Hashem grant you success in all your endeavors, and especially in the matter of *nachas chassidish* from your children, may they live.

With blessings for success.

***1335***

**In the name of his father, our master and teacher:** See *Igros Kodesh* of the Rebbe Rayatz, Vol. 2, Letter 482; Vol. 7, Letter 2862.

## 1336

1336

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you inquire on behalf of Mr. ... regarding the offer for him to purchase a business in a field in which he is an expert, whereas until now he has worked as an employee for others. It is understood that if he purchases the business being offered to him, he will be his own boss and bear all the responsibility, but it is to be hoped that he will then be able to involve his sons, may they live, in the business as well. You ask for my opinion on this:

In my opinion, this is the right thing to do, provided two conditions are met: a) that the business will be closed on Shabbos and Yom Tov; b) that he will not have to sell his house for this purpose and live in someone else’s home, as you mention in your letter. If he fulfills these two conditions, it is to be hoped that with the help of Hashem, it will be a success in gashmius, and may Hashem help him transform the gashmius into ruchnius, as per the well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of the Alter Rebbe...

c) Please convey my regards to the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing, and faithful communal worker, Rabbi Moshe Dovid Halevi, shliach. I am sure you are assisting him with all your ability, and it goes without saying that I refer not only to the matter of collecting funds, but also—and primarily—to the sowing of ruchnius. May Hashem grant His blessing and success to each person in what they require. See [the Kuntres] *Limud HaChassidus*, end of chapter 12, and in *Bava Metzia* (2b), "Here, one can say that there is not..."

d) I am sure that, consistent with what we discussed when you were here, you are strengthening yourself in your shiurim in Nigleh and Da"Ch, and I trust that you are also utilizing your influence on your cousin, shluchim, in this direction.

e) You surely received the letter from the secretariat regarding **ETA** in due time.

With blessings for success in communal matters and in your personal affairs, and for a suitable shidduch for you, in a revealed and good manner, very soon, and with regards as mentioned above.

**M. Schneerson**

## 1337

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter from the 2nd of Parshas Yisro in due time. My response was delayed due to the yahrtzeit of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the preparations for the yahrtzeit, and the matters connected to the yahrtzeit that followed. May Hashem help each of us to fulfill the shlichus that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, pointed out and the path he laid out for us to follow—in the path of Torah and mitzvos themselves. For even in the path of Torah and mitzvos itself, the yetzer hara finds ways to weaken and hinder one’s progress.

It pleased me to read in your letter that you are strong in your bitachon in Hashem, and I hope that soon you will also be able to see the realization of your bitachon regarding your business affairs in actual reality.

However, I am surprised: since you have bitachon in Hashem regarding gashmius and parnassah, then surely, *kal v’chomer*, one must be strong in bitachon in Hashem regarding one’s children and their conduct. This is, after all, what touches a Yid more deeply than gashmius matters. Yet, when you come to this subject, you write in your letter that you console yourself with the fact that they are better than others, etc.

Surely you have heard the interpretation—brought in many seforim—of the expression, **"In the heavens above and on the earth below"** (*Devarim 4:39*): When it comes to matters of Heaven, which are connected to Hashem and kedushah, one must look **"above,"** looking up to those on a higher level and striving to reach them. **"And on the earth below,"** regarding gashmius matters, one must look down, at what is happening with those who are on a lower level than oneself. Such an attitude leads one to be *sameiach b’chelko* (happy with one’s lot), which is when one is truly wealthy—"Who is wealthy? He who is happy with his lot."

It is unnecessary to emphasize that Lubavitch in general, and I in particular, are not moralizers without a purpose. My intention in writing the above lines is twofold: a) to contribute what I can to [your] strength of bitachon so that Hashem should grant you parnassah and good health; b) to repeat once again what I spoke to you about when you were here: do not grow weary of speaking with your children regarding their conduct in matters of Torah and mitzvos, for "the words of the wise—especially when they are—spoken gently, are heard."

With blessings that you should share good news.

## 1,338

1,338

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you write in your note, that you wish to continue supporting the elderly and the unfortunate whom you always help: this is certainly among the great and precious mitzvos. However, just as a human body—a *guf*—has many limbs, and one must ensure that all the limbs are healthy, so too must one ensure that all the "limbs" of the *neshamah* are whole. Therefore, one cannot be satisfied with giving *tzedakah* alone. You must ensure that you have *shiurim* in Torah appropriate to your standing and situation. You should also recite a *shiur* of *Tehillim* every day after *davening* in the morning (according to the division of *Tehillim* for the days of the month), and also study every day at least a few *pesukim* of *Chumash* with the commentary of *Rashi* from the *sedra* of the week. I hope that in this, too, you will be able to share good news with me.

With blessings for a speedy recovery.

## 1541

1541

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I have just received your letters of the 22nd and 29th of Teves, and the 4th and 7th of Shevat. Judging by what you write regarding the matter of the mikveh, the proof based on halachic reasoning, pilpul, and debate does not reach the other side. I fear that this falls into the category of "winning an argument" (netzachon), for in any case, it is utterly incomprehensible to challenge the method of constructing mikvaos used by the gedolei Yisrael of various circles in previous generations—who were surely also well-versed in the study of Shas, Rishonim, Acharonim, and the gedolei Yisrael, and based their rulings upon this. It is a pity that among anash there is no such firmness at all, even after instructions have been given regarding the firmness a Yid must possess when drawing close to a person he deems righteous, and certainly when drawing close to his Rebbe and Nasi, zt”l. One sees with one’s own eyes that people do not refrain from anything in order to fulfill the will of a person in whom they perceive human virtues. Yet, this does not motivate them to do everything possible to act according to the words of a person who was clearly—as clear as the sun—a man of G-d (ish Eloki), meaning he possessed G-dly wisdom and was accepted by tens of thousands of Yidden as a guide in Torah and mitzvos in all details. The analogy to our current matter is understood.

Regarding your question as to whether to show my reasoning, etc.: it is well known that with strong bitachon, one achieves the goal. In this matter as well, I am certain that if, upon receiving the telegram, you had proceeded with breadth (b’harchavah) without becoming involved in the imagined fear of people, the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (Maharashab), would have broken through all obstacles and it would have been accomplished. But since others advised the opposite, and consequently you also fell into doubt and felt the need for assistance, questioning, and clarification, I am highly doubtful whether you will be able to proceed with this breadth (mit breitkeit). Consequently, it is liable to cause harm, as is well known: one who wavers between two opinions ruins things even more than one who leans entirely to the other side.

It is not my desire, chas v’shalom, to preach musar, but my heart is pained that after each of us has seen many miraculous matters with our own eyes from our Nesi’im, and relied upon them even in matters concerning our very lives—both physically and spiritually—yet sometimes (and to my regret, this happens all too often), when faced with a test from the opposition, one loses one’s composure (parlirt men zich), begins to search for ways, advice, and tactics, and becomes a diplomat, etc., etc. This itself is further proof that we are still lacking much in the matter of "spreading the wellsprings" (hafatzas hamaayanos). As is explained at length in Chassidus, in order to be "outside" (chutza) even a little, one must be "inside" (bifnim) in abundance. May Hashem help each of us fulfill our shlichus in this world with breadth, and may He, blessed be He, lead us from the narrow straits into the true expanse...

With blessings.

#### ***1541***

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 12, p. 183; completed according to the secretariat’s copy.

## 1442

1442

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5712

I wish to emphasize once again that every Jew, whether a woman or a man, must be strong in bitachon in the Ribono shel Olam. Just as every Jew believes with complete faith that the Hakadosh Baruch Hu is the Master of the world, so too is He, Baruch Hu, the Master of the life of every individual Jew, whether a man or a woman. Since it is certain that Hashem Yisbarach is good, He will surely lead [everything] toward the good. When one finds oneself under the care—Hashgacha Pratis—of Hashem Yisbarach, there is nothing to be afraid of. As Dovid Hamelech says in Tehillim, "I will fear no evil, for You are with me" (Tehillim 23:4), and this "You are with me" applies to every Jew.

I hope that Hashem Yisbarach will show you a clear improvement in your situation as well, and that you will be able to report good news.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

The Secretary

## 1443

1443

By the Grace of Hashem, 1 Adar, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter from the conclusion of Shabbos Parshas Yisro, along with the *pidyon nefesh*. I will, *bli neder*, read it at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukl’l’h n’b’g’m z’y’a*. He will surely intercede on behalf of you and your household for all the things that each of you requires.

Regarding what you write about your distress at not receiving a response as quickly as you would like: this frustration has no basis. It goes without saying that I would also like to answer all letters as soon as possible, but what can I do? It does not depend on me alone. The pressure of many matters takes up a great deal of time, and only a limited amount of time remains for answering letters. Within that time, there is also an order of priority, yet regarding a *pidyon nefesh* and a request for a blessing, I do this as quickly as possible. It is only the notification that I have fulfilled the request that is delayed; therefore, there is no reason for distress, *chas v’shalom*.

It troubles me to read your letter, as well as reports from other *anash* *shichyu*, regarding the material situation of *anash*, which is not currently one of expansion. I hope, however, that this is only temporary, and that soon Hashem will expand their borders in material livelihood, and they will expand their borders in spiritual livelihood. As our Sages of blessed memory said, "Everything is in the hands of Heaven except for the fear of Heaven," which one must do oneself. I also hope that for you in particular, the material situation will improve, especially—as you write in your letter—since you have a vessel for this in the form of a business partnership.

I was pleased to read in your letter about the *farbrengens* of 19 Kislev, the fifth night of Chanukah, and 10 Shevat. Regarding your writing that you do not see any immediate effect from these *farbrengens* in your *avodah*, this is not something that can be known right away. It may be that after some time, it will resonate. Furthermore, any *mitzvah* that one performs, even for a short while, is—as our holy Rebbe writes in *Tanya*, Chapter 25—"a unification that is eternal, forever and ever." And when there is a *farbrengen* of *Chassidim*, a congregation of Jews, then surely "wherever ten are gathered, the *Shechinah* rests" (and the *Mishnah* says that even with three or two, it is **the same**). This remains above, which is the essential, eternal aspect—meaning that one is connected with *Atzmus* forever and ever. This is especially true through the matter of *ahavas Yisrael*, for through the fact that "we are all as one," there is also the "bless us, our Father." May Hashem help us all so that the month of Adar—a month regarding which our Sages of blessed memory ruled that "we increase in joy," without specifying any limitations on how long that joy should last—should also be eternal, forever and ever, as the Alter Rebbe writes, and may it draw down joy in both material and spiritual matters.

Regards to the entire group, and with blessings for livelihood in expansion, very soon.

#### ***1447***

## 1548

1548

B"H, 2 Adar, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Your program of work surely includes the task of engaging in *taamulah* (outreach/propaganda), both among the youth and among the parents, so that every single son and daughter of Yisrael, without exception, will be educated on the knees of Torah in absolute purity. And my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, already said: It is a certainty that *taamulah* does not return empty-handed.

And because of this, may Hashem send you blessing and success in your personal affairs, in the study of Torah with yiras shamayim and in teaching it, to observe and to perform, and to illuminate your surroundings with the light of Torah and the *maor* (luminary) within the Torah.

With blessings for success.

## 1,449

B"H, 2 Adar, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 18 Shevat, in which you inform me that you are beginning to teach Gemara to a class of beginners, and that years ago you studied at the Yeshivas Achei Temimim in Tel Aviv, and you request a blessing.

Surely you are aware of the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that the language used for "blessing" (*bracha*) is related to the "rain" (*geshem*) that brings blessing. The precision in this is that for rain to produce the desired benefit, the field must be plowed and sown. So too with a blessing: for the recipient to experience great and extraordinary success, there must be a corresponding effort on their part. Regarding yeshiva students, the "plowing" is the strict adherence to the yeshiva’s study schedule—even if this sometimes necessitates less sleep, eating, or drinking, and certainly requires resisting the inclination toward laziness, lack of persistence, and lack of diligence. The "sowing" is the study itself, conducted with appropriate diligence and persistence. When this preparation is in place, the blessing draws down success, insight, understanding, and comprehension.

Regarding yourself, your role is twofold: in addition to the plowing and sowing that you must do in your own field, you must also teach all of this to your students in an appropriate manner. When you strive in this with the necessary energy and seriousness, you will surely be successful, may Hashem...

#### ***1,449***

For the content, see letter 1,373 above.

## 1550

B"H, 5 Adar, 5712

I am certain that while you are on site, you will take an interest in ensuring that it is organized properly and becomes a permanent institution. Thank you for informing me of these good tidings.

It is known that "the steps of man are established by Hashem," and since Divine Providence has brought you to Madrid, even if only for a time, the inner intent of this is to merit others in matters of Torah and mitzvos.

We have heard something even greater in the name of the Baal Shem Tov: that there are times when a soul descends to this world for seventy or eighty years for the sole purpose of doing a favor for one of our fellow Jews, whether in material or spiritual matters.

Elaborating on this is surely unnecessary for someone like you, and I have great confidence that you are striving with all your might to disseminate the light of Torah and the "light within it" in your surroundings through actual deeds—for these are the very channels for drawing down and receiving blessings from the Source of Blessings in all your personal affairs, both material and spiritual.

With blessings.

## 1551

B"H, 6 Adar, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have received your letter, in which you write that for some weeks you have not been feeling well, and that the doctor’s opinion is that you will require surgery...

In this month of Adar, regarding which our Sages say in the Midrash that its *mazal* is fish—which is a concept for Jews, and especially for Chassidim, of whom it is said, "and they shall multiply like fish within the land"—it means that even in worldly and physical matters, they conduct themselves like fish: they do not separate from their source of life (*Berachos 61b*), and likewise, they do not separate from the path of Torah and *mitzvos*. May this *mazal* also bring you a swift recovery and true health.

Awaiting good news.

## 1552

1552

B"H, 6 Adar, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the honorable Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., Moreinu Harav Yaakov Yisrael,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Terumah, which you requested be answered as soon as possible, in which you describe the state of shechitah in your location—formerly in Stockholm, Sweden—where the government permits shechitah only by means of electrical stunning beforehand. You prohibited this, but subsequently, you were presented with a heter from rabbis in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. They also wrote to you that there were cases where they examined the animals slaughtered after stunning, checking all the internal organs, and found no defect (*rei'uta*). Furthermore, they claim that if the animal is not slaughtered after the stunning, it stands on its feet after some time, eats, etc.

In response to this: Regarding what you wrote—that a professor and veterinarian examined the animal after the stunning and shechitah and found no visible defect in the internal organs—I am greatly astonished by this. It is a matter known even to beginners in these studies that the electric shock that causes death **does not** necessarily leave a visible mark on the internal organs, because the death is caused by a shock to the nerves. Even if a change is found in the internal organs, it is one of two things: either it existed before the shock and they were simply unaware of it, or there was a weakness in the organ beforehand, and the shock acted as an incidental cause that exacerbated the weakness until it led to these changes. In any case, **this** is not the essence of the shock. A conclusive proof of this is the entire matter of stunning itself, the purpose of which is also to shock the nerves to the point of removing sensation. When one increases the "quantity"—or in other words, the strength of the current—one removes not only the sensation but also the power of movement, etc., meaning the animal dies. It is understood that a shock to the nerves cannot be detected in a post-mortem examination.

2) It is self-understood that even if the aforementioned stunning is performed with an extremely weak current, the reliability regarding the strength or weakness of the current is usually left to a non-Jew, who is the one performing the stunning.

Even if it were entrusted to a Jew, the matter is still not clear. As is known to every physician of human beings, not all people are the same regarding the effect of an electric current. Even in the same person, not all times are the same, whether due to their nerves or due to the nature of their clothing, their standing position, and the like. However, with human beings, one approaches the use of electricity with caution, and it is done using instruments where the strength of the current is visible and recognizable, etc. All of these matters cannot be implemented in the stunning process in a slaughterhouse. Furthermore, they certainly will not change the strength of the current from a large animal to a small one, from a thick-skinned animal to a thin-skinned one, whether the hide is wet or dry, etc.—all of which affects the action of the current.

3) I have seen a copy of the letter of hechsher from the honorable Rabbi, the scholar, etc., Harav Shlomo David Kahana, may he live. I do not know if the matter of the stunning was presented to him as it truly is, but nevertheless, I am extremely surprised and astonished that he does not mention his heter regarding the **convulsions** (*pirchus*) after shechitah! There is much more to elaborate on this, but this is not the place.

However, the conclusion from all this is that since you have already written your opinion prohibiting it, in my view, you should reiterate your position on this, especially in light of everything written above.

With blessings and respect.

***

**Moreinu Harav Yaakov Yisrael:** Zuber. Further letters to him—see above, Vol. 3, 554, and the references in the notes there.

**You prohibited:** See Igros Kodesh of the Rebbe Rayatz, Vol. 4, letter 898.

## 1553

1553

B"H, 7 Adar, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Eleventh Annual Assembly of the
Committee for the Protection and Expansion of Kosher Chinuch
Under the administration of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch
May they live.

Greetings and Blessings!

For your eleventh annual assembly, which will take place on Sunday, the eve of the 13th of Adar, the eve of the upcoming Purim, I send my heartfelt blessing to all the participants in the assembly—the guides, the educators, the members, and the friends of the Committee.

Since the Committee was founded by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and began its educational work, I have been pleased to see that your work—like any living thing, whose sign of life is its growth—continues to grow from year to year, both in the number of guides and the number of Jewish boys and girls influenced by them, and in the quality of the fruits of your good work. It is my hope that you will go from strength to strength, rising in holiness from level to level, as was the desire and will of the great founder, and in accordance with the demands of the hour.

Your assembly is taking place close to the festival of Purim. Everything is by Divine Providence, and there is a great lesson to be seen in this.

Our Sages relate that when the decree was issued to destroy, G-d forbid, Mordechai went out into the city streets and gathered 22,000 schoolchildren to teach them Torah, and together with them, to pour out their hearts before their Father in Heaven in prayer and supplication. He instilled such great mesiras nefesh in their hearts that they cried out with one voice: "Whether in death or in life, we are Yours." Through this, the decree was torn up and transformed from death to life and from sorrow to joy—in the life of the body and the life of the soul alike.

Each and every one must contemplate that Mordechai the Tzaddik was one of the heads of the Sanhedrin, the leader of all the Tzaddikim, like Moshe in his generation, and yet he went out in person to teach Torah, yiras shamayim, and mesiras nefesh to small children, the schoolchildren.

Each and every one of us must always remember: Let no person imagine that their status and position exempt them from attending to the chinuch of the young, or that they should neglect their own lofty deeds and business affairs for it.

One must recognize that it is most important to set aside, at the very least, a portion of one's time, and to dedicate, at the very least, a portion of one's strength to the conquest of the chinuch of the younger generation, in order to plant in their hearts yiras shamayim and mesiras nefesh for all that is holy—holy to us since we became a kingdom of priests and a holy nation at the standing at Har Sinai.

And only then will we be certain that the younger generation will be faithful to Hashem and His Torah, and consequently, the existence of our people will also be secure. Great is the power of this holy and dedicated work to nullify all accusations and decrees, and the people of Israel will dwell in safety, alone.

With a blessing for success in your work, to increase the number of guides and educators many times over, and primarily—to increase the number of Jewish boys and girls influenced by you many times more. And may it be the will that the good attributes of the Holy One, Blessed be He, be fulfilled in you: in abundance, in fruitfulness, in multiplication, in redemption with abundance, in blessing with abundance, in praise with abundance.

**M. Schneerson**

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 6, p. 370, and completed according to a photocopy of the letter.

## 1553*

B"H, 7 Adar, 5712
Brooklyn

To all those participating in the work of kosher chinuch in general, and to those involved in the chinuch of the young sons and daughters of Yisrael in particular,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Shalom u’vracha!

In connection with the approaching days of Purim, I hereby wish to draw your attention to one of the events of Purim, from which a lesson can be learned for your avodah and our avodah.

Chazal relate that when the decree was issued to destroy, etc., G-d forbid, Mordechai went out into the city streets and gathered 22,000 tinokos shel beis rabban to teach them Torah, and together with them, to pour out their hearts before their Father in Heaven in tefillah and supplication. He instilled in their hearts such great mesiras nefesh that they cried out with one voice: "Whether in death or in life, we are Your people." Through this, the decree was torn up, and it was turned around—from death to life and from mourning to joy—in both the life of the body and the life of the neshamah alike.

Each and every one must contemplate that Mordechai the Tzaddik, who was the head of the Sanhedrin, the leader of all the tzaddikim, like Moshe in his generation—nonetheless, he went out in person to teach Torah, yiras shamayim, and mesiras nefesh to young children, the tinokos shel beis rabban.

Each and every one of us must always remember: Let no person imagine that their status or position exempts them from involving themselves in the chinuch of the young, or that they are too busy with their many activities and affairs. One must recognize that it is more important than anything to set aside, at the very least, a portion of their time, and to dedicate, at the very least, a portion of their strength to the conquest of the chinuch of the younger generation, in order to plant in their hearts yiras shamayim and mesiras nefesh for everything holy—that which has been holy to us since we became a kingdom of kohanim and a holy nation at the standing at Har Sinai.

And then, only then, will we be certain that the younger generation will be faithful to Hashem and His Torah, and by extension, the existence of our people will also be secure. The power of this holy and dedicated avodah is great enough to nullify all accusations and decrees, and the people of Yisrael will dwell in safety, alone.

I hope that you will go from strength to strength, ascending in holiness, level after level, in accordance with the demands of the hour.

With a blessing for success in your avodah, and primarily—to increase the number of sons and daughters of Yisrael influenced by you many times over. May it be the will that the good attributes of the Ribono shel Olam be fulfilled in you, in abundance and multiplication, in redemption with abundance, in blessing with abundance, and in praise with abundance.

**M. Schneerson**

## 1554

[7 Adar, 5712]

...Regarding the days of Purim.

It is known that the joy of Purim is far greater than the joy of Yom Tov (where we are obligated by Torah law to be joyful, yet certainly one should not become intoxicated to the point of excess, as the Rambam writes regarding the joy of Yom Tov: "One should not be drawn into wine," etc.). Even though miracles were performed for our ancestors on Yom Tov, the joy of Purim is nonetheless immense and exceeds the joy of Yom Tov.

The reason for this is that on Yom Tov, although we draw down additional light and revelation from above through the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, this drawing down occurs within the order of *Seder Hishtalshelus*, in a measured and defined way. This is not the case on Purim, where, through the *mesiras nefesh* that they possessed at that time—which is a level that transcends *taam v’daas*—they reached a level far above the boundaries of *Seder Hishtalshelus*. Therefore, the joy resulting from this revelation is also above *daas*, to the point of *ad d’lo yada*.

Along with this, the days of Purim are days of feasting and joy, specifically the revelation of lights within vessels, to dwell within the vessel even in a way that the vessel would not be able to contain the light according to the *Seder Hishtalshelus*.

Furthermore, they are permitted to perform work.

This means that even during the time of performing work, and during the time of feasting and joy, one is in a state of *mesiras nefesh* that is completely above *taam v’daas*, with an absence of any desire or will other than for Hashem alone, as it is written: "Whom have I in heaven? And with You, I desire nothing on earth."

This is as the expression was heard from the Alter Rebbe in his *dveikus*, where he would say in these words: "I do not want anything; I do not want Your Gan Eden, I do not want Your Olam Haba, etc. I want nothing but You alone."

## 1554

B"H, 9 Adar, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

I received your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Terumah, and I was distressed to read that your wife, may she live and be well, is feeling weak. Not only that, but you added the word **very** in your letter; surely this addition stems from your own melancholy, in addition to the illness and nerves of your wife, may she live and be well.

If you both were to strengthen your bitachon in Hashem—Who is the One Who brings the world and all that fills it into being, and consequently, brings your world and your children into being at every moment and every second—and [if you realized] that He watches over you with hashgacha pratis so that you lack nothing that you and your children, may they live, require, then you would not need to interfere in the "eye" of Hashem and worry about how Hashem will provide for you everything you need in the future. Everything is revealed and known before Him, and He has already decreed your sustenance in abundance, as the Sages of blessed memory ruled regarding the ten days between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur. Furthermore, it is in your power to add to this whatever you spend on the chinuch of your children in the direction of Torah education—for this direction begins at the very moment the nefesh elokis enters (see Shulchan Aruch of our Rebbe HaZaken, the later edition, end of siman 4, in the brackets; and it is known from our Sages of blessed memory that "a woman is like a vessel filled with [the soul of the child]"). If you were to do this, you would see this tangibly as well.

Enclosed is the Kuntres for the upcoming Purim, and surely you will publicize it in an appropriate manner.

I am distressed by the lack of reports regarding the activities of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in connection with the yom hilula of 10 Shevat that has passed, and in connection with these days of Purim. It seems that "division of hearts" has caused this... and how long will this continue to dance among us! Especially since our holy Rebbes have warned about this specific matter for many generations. Is it truly impossible for the mind to rule over the heart, at least regarding matters that are *b'po'al mamash*?

It is self-understood that these words of mine are not directed at any one individual, but at the youth in general. Surely the one to whom this matter is relevant will take it upon himself to rectify this as **soon** as possible. Especially during the days of Purim, which is a matter of *at-hafpacha*—"and it was turned around"—as is also explained in Chassidus in Torah Or and in many places, that this is the matter of **at-hafpacha** of darkness into light. Therefore, let them use the enthusiasm that previously existed regarding the division, and let it be directed toward the matters of rectification and toward matters of action... Let them contemplate how great the pity is upon me and upon them—what they are exhausting me with, and what they "should" be investing their physical and spiritual strengths into.

With blessings for a proper Purim joy, and for its continuation throughout the entire year.

## 1

B"H, 12 Adar, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

Through the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, who occupies himself with communal needs, Rabbi Shlomo Zalman Hecht, your contribution for our educational work in North Africa has arrived. Your participation is surely a *davar b'ito* (a word spoken in its proper time).

The work in North Africa, which began through the initiative of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, shortly before his passing, has, B"H, developed and expanded. One can see the Divine success that accompanies it on its difficult path. In the latest report I received from there, a list was provided of 52 *mosdos* (institutions) that have already, B"H, been established in various cities and towns, and even in the most remote villages in Morocco.

This broad network of educational institutions—which bears the name *Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak Lubavitch*, after its great founder—includes a *beis medrash* for teachers, *yeshivos*, *yeshivos ketanos*, *talmud-torahs*, *Beis Rivkah* schools for girls, evening courses for adults, and so on. Beyond the *chinuch* (education) *al taharas hakodesh* (in holiness) that the children receive for free, many of them also receive material assistance, such as free meals, clothing, and so on.

Although the results are, B"H, very satisfying, we cannot stop here. For we must not forget that there are still thousands upon thousands of neglected Jewish children who are walking about without Torah and without *chinuch*, and who find themselves in great spiritual danger.

It is therefore to be hoped that our friends will, for their part, also increase their participation in this holy *avodah* of *hatzalas nefashos* (saving souls). This participation opens wide channels to draw down and receive Divine blessings for themselves and all their household, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings to hear good news from you and all yours.

## 1557

[13 Adar, 5712]

...Regarding *machshavos zaros* (alien thoughts), one must increase the *osiyos* (letters) of Torah and the *osiyos* of *tefillah*. It is also appropriate to have certain chapters of *Tanya* and chapters of *Mishnayos* engraved in one’s memory, as this provides protection even at times when one is not reviewing them, and even in thought alone. This is explained in *Likutei Torah* at the end of *Parshas Kedoshim*; consequently, it is proper to also learn the aforementioned *maamar*, *Ve’hadarta Penei Zakein*, by heart.

Since these thoughts frequently cause distraction specifically during *tefillah* and during learning, it is good that during *tefillah* and learning, the *Siddur* or the *sefer* one is studying from should be open before him at the place where he is holding. When he feels his thoughts wandering, he should immediately look into the *Siddur* or the *sefer*—for the written letters hold one’s attention...

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 14, p. 233.

## 1559

B"H, Friday, Erev Shabbos Parshas Ki Sisa, 5712. Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to hear of the improvement in your health, yet I was pained by the subsequent decline, as it indicates a lack of the strength of spirit that should characterize every member of Bnei Yisrael—especially those who have merited the light of Torah, which is the Torah of Chassidus, and who have knowledge of one of its foundations: the concept of Hashgacha Pratis, as explained at length by the Baal Shem Tov and in the Chassidic writings of our Rebbes, the Nesi’im, of blessed memory.

My hope is strong that the aforementioned deficiency is merely a passing state, a momentary lapse, and that immediately and without delay you will awaken the *eisan* (the strength) within your soul, and draw upon its hidden powers. As is known, the interpretation of *eisan* is "strong, hard, and old," for its root is in the *Shem* of 72, *Atik*—it is not something newly created, Heaven forbid, as explained in *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus* in the *maamar* of our Alter Rebbe on the verse, "Maskil l'Eisan HaEzrachi."

During these days of Adar, the month in which we increase in joy—and our Sages did not set any limit to this—even if one is already in a state of joy, there is still room for further increase. May it be His will that the following be fulfilled in you, as the Midrash Rabbah on Megillas Esther concludes: the good attributes of the Holy One, Blessed be He, in abundance and increase—goodness in abundance, kindness in abundance, mercy in abundance, charity in abundance, faith in abundance, redemption in abundance, blessing in abundance, praise in abundance, and peace in abundance—and it concludes, "Hashem will give strength to His people; Hashem will bless His people with peace."

With blessings for a speedy recovery and a *Shabbos tova*,

**M. Schneerson**

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 16, p. 605; completed based on a photocopy of the original letter.

## 1060

1060

B"H, 20 Adar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt,
Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt,
To those upon whom they shall live,

Peace and blessing!

...My proposal is that the name of the organizations should be one, namely:

**Agudas Chassidei Chabad in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt**

— and on the line below this —

Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt.

2) The internal management of Agudas Chabad remains as it has been until now. However, as I have written previously, it is appropriate to add another representative from the Tzeirei — and until now, nothing has been done regarding this. Therefore, the Tzeirei must choose as soon as possible two representatives of their own, in addition to the representative they currently have on the Agudas Chabad board.

Membership in the aforementioned organization will be one for everyone. That is, if a membership card or similar item is printed, both of the aforementioned names should be inscribed on the card. However, among the other details, a clause should be added explaining one’s affiliation with Tzeirei Agudas Chabad.

3) As is customary throughout the world, it is worthwhile to institute a membership fee in Agudas Chabad and Tzeirei Agudas Chabad. During the initial period—that is, approximately three months—the income should be divided equally between Agudas Chabad and Tzeirei Agudas Chabad. After this time, it will be within their authority to change the distribution, by agreement of both sides, in accordance with the expenses that Agudas Chabad and Tzeirei Agudas Chabad will have incurred during these three months.

**Note**: It is to be expected that the income from membership fees alone will not suffice for all the necessary expenses, especially since this fee should be kept as low as possible to allow all those who belong to our organization to join. Therefore, a levy should be imposed on the Lubavitch institutions in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt, such that every *chesed* organization and institution will contribute either a specific sum or, better yet, a certain percentage to the joint fund of Agudas Chabad and Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, since the aforementioned work assists and helps all these institutions.

4) Regarding all matters pertaining to negotiations with outside parties—such as with representatives of the Jewish Agency, various ministers, etc.—this is the specific responsibility of Agudas Chabad. However, in appropriate matters, one of the Tzeirei representatives who serves on the board of Agudas Chabad and Tzeirei Agudas Chabad should also be included.

5) The organization of *hafatzas* *da"ch* in various synagogues and yeshivos, and in general among different circles of people in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt—this is work that requires traveling from place to place, special effort, energy, etc., and this falls under the role of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad. However, in the management of the aforementioned, there should be a representative from the board of Agudas Chabad on the organizing committee.

6) Regarding the printing of *da"ch*, in places where the name of the publisher is required, it should also be written as mentioned above: Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt; Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt.

It is my hope that you will deliberate on the aforementioned **proposals** as soon as possible and inform me of the decisions.

May it be the will of Hashem that the *hiskashrus* of each and every one of us to our holy *Nasi* will effect the mastery of the mind over the heart...

And may we all merit to fulfill our mission in this world with peace of mind and joy of heart.

With a blessing for success in the work—the holy work entrusted to them and to us by our *Nasi*.

Awaiting good tidings.

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***1060***

For the content, see above, letters 1191, 1347.

## 1561

1561

B"H, 20 Adar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the Management Committee of Kfar Chabad, may they live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter, in which you describe the situation where the Jewish Agency is proposing and pressuring you to relocate your settlement to a new site a few kilometers from your current location. The Agency would build a new village there for you, including residential homes and necessary public buildings such as a shul and beis medrash, a school, a mikveh, etc. In this new location, each residence would be adjacent to the field belonging to that home. However, the new site currently lacks an access road, although the construction of such a road is included in the government’s plan as a very urgent matter. It is understood that all residents of the new village would be required to engage in agriculture and the associated work, such as chicken coops, livestock, etc. You are asking for my opinion on how to respond to this proposal, as there are differences of opinion among Anash in the village. Several of them have work outside the village, and at the new site, transportation to areas outside the village is more difficult than at your current location. Furthermore, agricultural work is extremely strenuous, to the point that it is almost impossible for one person to handle all the necessary tasks without the help of family members, and not all families of Anash have this possibility for various reasons.

My opinion on this (as a suggestion) is as follows:

1) You must strive with all means to ensure that even if the Agency insists that your settlement be an agricultural one, they should arrange for this to be done at your **current** location (by transferring to your possession the fields in the vicinity of the village as it is now, or something similar). In my opinion, this is a **very** important matter, and the settlement should be maintained where it is now. For every time one relocates from place to place, *something is broken and lost*, and a word to the wise is sufficient. You have a strong argument: since the Agency itself settled you in this location, and you have already become accustomed to the place and made several improvements, and have also arranged your lives and connections with Tel Aviv and the surrounding area accordingly, the Agency bears the responsibility to stand by its word and provide you with everything necessary for a settlement to function as an agricultural village at your current location specifically. They should not force you to be uprooted yet again from place to place, after you have already endured several exiles, etc., nor should they deny you the rights they promised you as an agricultural settlement if you are unable to relocate to the new village proposed for you.

I suspect that there are some who, for various reasons (which in my opinion are not correct), will exert only weak efforts even if they do attempt the above. Therefore, I emphasize once again that in my opinion, it is of the utmost importance to do everything possible so that everyone remains in one group and in your current location, naturally with all the rights belonging to an agricultural settlement. I have strong confidence that Mr. Shazar, Mr. Gelman, and also Mr. Shragai, upon his arrival from here, will assist you in the aforementioned efforts, although I hope that if you stand firmly on this demand—using the argument that this is how the Agency settled you in your current location—you will succeed even without that.

2) If, despite my assumptions and despite all efforts exerted with the appropriate vigor, you do not succeed in your just demand, then you should strive to establish the Kfar Chabad settlement in both locations simultaneously—that is, at your current location and also at the site of the new village. If there is not a sufficient number of Anash families to constitute an overwhelming majority in both settlements, it is worthwhile to strive in appropriate ways to annex to yourselves some of the new immigrants, as well as suitable veteran residents, so that they too will settle in one of the two villages—either in the current Kfar Chabad or in the new village—in such a way that both locations will conduct themselves in accordance with the spirit of Chabad.

It is self-understood that if it becomes necessary for some to settle in the current village and others in the new settlement, priority should be given to those who, due to their circumstances, must maintain constant contact with Tel Aviv, etc., to remain in the current location. The village management committee should discuss every detail and make a decision on this.

**Note:** The effort to annex additional suitable people, both from among the general public and from among the veterans, is necessary **in any case**, and it is worthwhile to invest strength and energy into this. However, it is understood that if you are forced to settle in two locations, the necessity to increase the number of Anash in the villages is even greater.

3) If even what I mentioned in the previous section cannot be achieved in any way (though in that case, it is clear to me that this would only be due to a lack of effort in the aforementioned), and you will be forced to relocate to the new village, you should continue to delay the matter as much as possible (naturally, without causing harm to your support, etc.). The salvation of Hashem comes in the blink of an eye, and perhaps, in the end, you will succeed in arranging matters in the manner described in the first section, or at the very least, in the manner of the second section.

I will repeat once more before concluding: the effort must be made, with the demand that they promised you all the rights belonging to an agricultural settlement at the time they settled you in your current location. Therefore, the Agency must find the ways and means to rectify and maintain both matters without forcing you into a new uprooting.

With the blessing that Hashem will continue peace in your camp, and that all of you together will succeed in both material and spiritual matters, in accordance with the will of our Nasi, the Rebbe, may his merit protect us.

Awaiting confirmation of receipt of this letter as soon as possible, and looking forward to good news regarding all of the above.

Regarding the results, see below, letter 1584.

## 1562

[20 Adar, 5712]

...And although in every place strife is most despised, in Eretz Yisrael—where this matter has even greater standing, and as our Sages of blessed memory said, it is because of this sin that we were exiled from our land—it is all the more so that one must exert extra effort to avoid strife and its derivatives. For the intensity of this *kelipah* in a specific place also indicates the necessity of breaking it in a particularly focused manner in that specific place...

1563

May it be the will of Hashem that you know no further sorrow or anguish, and that only goodness and kindness may dwell in your tent always, along with peace of heart and peace of mind, and success in your avodah, in Torah and in communal needs, etc.

Several times he quoted in his speech the passage from the holy Zohar (Vol. III, 5a), "A king without a queen, etc.," and similar thoughts. This continued until one of his sons said to him: "I have heard from you personally the teaching of our Sages (Kiddushin 30b), 'And see life with the woman whom you love'—this refers to Torah." The Tzemach Tzedek replied: "You have comforted me, my son, you have comforted me."

It might be worthwhile for you to add a few words of explanation of your own, to strengthen their hiskashrus to the yeshiva. It may also be fitting that the delivery of the letters, etc., take place in the presence of the parents, or that they be made aware of it at the very least; I rely on your discretion.

3) It would be appropriate for you to explain to Mr. ... that Eretz Yisrael and the Jewish people are not like other lands and nations. Consequently, their laws are also different. We must rely upon the Torah of Moshe and not emulate or "dance to the tune of" the laws of the nations. On the contrary, "nations shall walk by your light." This applies even regarding the lives of Jews in the Diaspora, and certainly when establishing a way of life in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established). First and foremost, one must arrange matters so that they are in accordance with the spirit of the Torah and rooted in its foundations, etc., etc.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

## 1765

1765

B"H, 26 Adar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To those engaged in communal affairs, and specifically in Chabad education:
Rabbi Chaim Shaul Brook
R' Yosef Shmotkin
R' Yaakov Yosef Raskin, Shochet u'Bodek
R' M. Brook
And R' Uri Ben Shachar

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters of the 13th and 28th of Shevat, in which you inform me that you have already purchased the building and have set it up, and you request my opinion regarding what name to give this educational institution.

In my opinion, this touches somewhat upon the curriculum. If students will be accepted there from circles that are not so close to Chabad, and consequently it will be impossible to insist that the curriculum be in accordance with Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, then it would be worthwhile for it to join the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch. If, however, you are able to arrange the curriculum so that it is the same as it is in Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, then it should be named Achiezer or Tomchei Temimim—this depends on whether there will also be higher grades there. Seemingly, the first suggestion—that it join the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok—is more appropriate, since then one can accept as students even those who would not initially agree to a full Chabad curriculum. In such a manner, you will draw them toward the spirit of Lubavitch gradually. In any event, the studies must be arranged in such a way that upon completing their studies at the institution in Rishon LeZion, they will be able to enter any of our yeshivos in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, whether in Lod or in Yerushalayim, may it be rebuilt and established.

May it be the will of Hashem that the Shechinah rest upon the work of your hands, and may your avodah be successful in producing students who are G-d-fearing, Chassidim, and scholars.

With blessings for success in your holy work and for a happy Purim.

## 1566

Brooklyn.

## 1,767

1,767

B"H, 26 Adar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...It was pleasing to hear that you are currently being presented with two shidduchim. Hopefully, you will look into them and be able to choose the one that is most suitable for you.

It is certainly unnecessary to emphasize that while, on one hand, one must think things through carefully before deciding on a shidduch, at the same time one must also know that it is impossible to be one hundred percent certain in advance. One must rely on Hashem Yisbarach, who leads the great world, as well as the small world of every individual, and that He, blessed be He, will certainly lead things for the best. One only needs to strengthen one’s connection with Hashem Yisbarach by conducting oneself in the path of Torah and mitzvos. Furthermore, the Ribbono shel Olam asks that for every matter, one should create a vessel in nature—that is, in the natural way. Therefore, in all matters, and likewise in matters of shidduchim, one must take an interest oneself, but without holding onto two extremes: that is, neither grabbing the first thing that comes to hand, nor being overly selective.

I hope that your health is already better, and that soon I will receive good news from you that you have found your bashert zivug and are building a home among Yidden—a happy home in all respects.

With blessings, awaiting good tidings.
