## 1772

B”H, 28 Adar, 5712
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be built and established,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your inquiry regarding the matter I spoke of some time ago—and which I also conveyed through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Moshe Gurary, may he live—concerning the necessity of expanding the Chabad educational institutions through the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok, and likewise to include the religious educational institutions of the Pe’ilim, in such a way that none of the above would bear a partisan label: You raised a concern that this would provide the government with an opening to strengthen their argument that there is no need for political parties at all, and that the government’s Ministry of Education would then deal directly with the individual educational institution, which would, of course, be detrimental.

In my opinion, it is necessary in any event that each institution not remain an independent entity, as this would greatly weaken its strength, both internally and especially externally; there is no need to elaborate on this. Therefore, my intention from the outset was that all the educational institutions gathered into this network should unite as a non-partisan stream, and there should be a general administration through which all negotiations and discussions would be conducted, both with the Ministry of Education and with any other relevant ministry. And since it is my hope that the educational institutions of the Pe’ilim—and in time, those of the Yishuv HaYashan as well—will join this, we should, for the time being, establish an administration that will include one representative from Agudas Chabad, one from Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, and one from the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok, and propose to the Pe’ilim that they also choose one of their own to be on the administration. Of course, these details are merely a suggestion that can be changed, and in particular, the administration can be expanded as more institutions join this non-partisan stream. But it is understood and simple that in order for matters to be conducted without deviating from the goal, it must be certain that those standing at the head of the administration will safeguard the core point. Once the educational institutions are organized in the aforementioned manner, the concern is nullified, and there is no room for the argument that the government’s Ministry of Education will deal directly with the individual educational institution (which is not desirable at all), since this organization will also communicate with the Ministry of Education through a general administration.

2) I have already said many times that for several reasons, there is hope that various circles will assist in bringing the organization of non-partisan educational institutions from potential into reality—and to the wise, a word is sufficient—provided that they, for their part, exert the appropriate energy in this...

With a blessing for success in their holy work,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1573

1573

B"H, 28 Adar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Naftali Hakohen, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I was informed of your question (or bewilderment) regarding what you heard from Mr. Rabinowitz, may he live. When he visited me and mentioned that he was giving a certain sum, I told him that I would deposit the funds into a specific tzedakah fund (Hachnosas Kallah), and you wondered why I felt the need to tell him what I would do with the money.

This is understood based on the statement of our Sages (Chullin 94a) that certain things were prohibited because they might lead to a misunderstanding [d'met'avei], a matter also noted in the poskim as marked in the Ein Mishpat Ner Mitzvah. Since I saw that Mr. Rabinowitz might think these funds would be used for a different purpose, I was obligated by law to inform him that they would be deposited into a specific tzedakah fund.

I am interested to know if you are involved in communal affairs in your city, particularly in matters of education.

Enclosed is a *d'var malchus* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which has just been published.

Please convey my regards to the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Chaim Yaakov Gass, and [I wish] a kosher and happy Pesach to you all.

## 1575

B"H, 28 Adar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...I am interested to know if you are taking part in the observant life of your city, especially regarding education, which is also a matter of the day during these days between Purim and Pesach. The decree of Purim was nullified because Mordechai, the greatest of his generation—both in Torah and in yiras shamayim and wisdom—taught schoolchildren himself, as related by our Sages. This point is also central to the festival of Pesach, which begins with the Seder. We employ various methods to engage the hearts of the children, specifically to ensure they do not sleep (sleep in the physical sense, and certainly in the sense of spiritual sleep), and the Seder begins with the questions of the children. So too, during the days of Pesach, there are matters of *kri'as yam suf* and the stories related in *Shemos Rabbah* regarding the children who were born and raised in Mitzrayim and were the first to recognize Him (Hashem). The lesson to be drawn from this is that the redemption of Yisrael, both physically and spiritually, depends on the education of the younger generation. Every single person in Yisrael—even one as great as Mordechai, of whom our Sages said in *Midrash Esther Rabbah* that "Mordechai in his generation is like Moshe in his generation"—is obligated to personally take part in this education.

May the Ribono shel Olam enable each and every one of us to illuminate our portion of the world, through which we hasten and bring about the complete and true Geulah for all of Klal Yisrael, as explained in *Tanya*, Chapter 37.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach, and for the proper tidings.

## 1576

1576

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In connection with the approaching days of the festival of Pesach, I hereby express my heartfelt wishes that you celebrate the festival of Pesach with kashrus and with the joy of our true time of freedom—freedom in the physical sense and freedom in the spiritual sense, for one is impossible without the other. Therefore, in this generation of ours, the *ikvesa d'Meshicha*, when—as the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nivga"m, zya"e*, goes—he is already standing behind our wall, it is most necessary to pay close attention and exert great effort in the education of the younger generation. This must be in accordance with the Torah—the Torah of truth, the Torah of life—which is what grants freedom to a person, as our Sages of blessed memory said (*Avos*, Chapter 6): "There is no free man except for one who occupies himself with the study of Torah."

The great value of education is emphasized especially during the festival of Pesach, which begins with the *Seder* ritual, starting with the questions of the children and the performance of various actions so that they will change their routine (both physically, and certainly spiritually). This is also true at the conclusion of Pesach, which is the matter of the splitting of the sea, as our Sages of blessed memory said (*Shemos Rabbah*) that the infants and sucklings who were born in Mitzrayim were the first to recognize Him (Hashem).

Concluding as I began, with blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

1577

1577

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our brethren, the Children of Israel, wherever they may be, may Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

The days of the festival of Pesach are approaching.

Every matter in the world teaches a person who contemplates it wisdom and instruction, whether in matters between man and Hashem, in matters between man and his fellow, or in both of these categories.

It is most easy, through appropriate study, to find such instructions in the matters of Torah—Torah, from the word *hora'ah* (instruction), instruction in life, as its name "Torah of Life" implies—and *mitzvos*. This is especially true regarding the general concepts contained within them.

One of the most unique of these matters is the remembrance of the Exodus from Egypt, which is a great foundation and a strong pillar in our Torah and our faith. It is distinguished from all other miracles in that we are cautioned to mention it (as well as the splitting of the Red Sea) every single day. Furthermore, we are commanded to do so with even greater emphasis at the beginning of the festival of Pesach—on the night the festival is sanctified.

There are many things to be learned both from the essence of this matter and from the ways and details of its observance. I have come here to emphasize just one point—a point shared by the beginning and the conclusion of the festival, and which contains an instruction for action in our lives, not only during the days of the festival, but throughout the entire year.

For this is the intention: that all the influences and lights revealed during the festivals and appointed times should be drawn down into all the days of the year, especially those of the festival of Pesach.

The beginning of the laws and customs of the festival, as soon as night falls, is the "Seder." And immediately upon the beginning of the Seder, one of its primary elements is: **"And you shall tell your son."** We change several things and innovate several things in order to arouse the children. Moreover, this obligation is not only regarding the wise son, but rather—one who is wise, one who is wicked, one who is simple, and one who does not know how to ask. All of them must be gathered to the Pesach Seder, and according to the mind and capacity of understanding **of the son**, the father teaches him.

And the conclusion of the festival of Pesach is the miracle of the day, when the Ribono shel Olam split the sea for us, and every one of the Jewish people points with his finger and says: "This is my G-d and I will glorify Him." The sons and daughters who were born and raised during the difficulties of the galus, these children recognized the Ribono shel Olam **first**.

The end of the festival is embedded in its beginning.

We must strive with all our might and energy to seek ways, advice, and strategies (even if it requires changing one's nature and habits, provided that—) to honor the younger generation, and to bring all the sons and daughters of Israel—the wise, the wicked, the simple, and the one who does not know how to ask—closer to Torah and *mitzvos*. Then we are assured that with our youth and our elders we will go toward the Geulah, with our sons and our daughters.

And our generation—a generation born and raised during the time of the difficulty of the galus, the decrees and persecutions, Heaven forbid, and against whom, even regarding the *She'eris HaPleita*, and especially the children whom Hashem has given and left as signs and wonders (so that Torah will be maintained in Israel through them), there are those who rise up to destroy them, G-d forbid, through an education that calls evil good and good evil, that puts darkness for light and light for darkness, [bitter for sweet and sweet for bitter], because it has despised the Torah of Hashem Tzevaos—

May the Ribono shel Olam save them and save us from their hand, and may this generation merit, speedily in our days through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, to also be the generation of the Geulah, [the true Geulah, as prophesied by our holy prophets], not by might and not by power, but by the spirit of Hashem Tzevaos. And every one of them will recognize Him, point with their finger, and say:

"Behold, this is our G-d; we have waited for Him, and He will save us. This is Hashem; we have waited for Him, let us rejoice and be glad in His salvation."

With the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1778

1778

B"H, 2 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to learn from the administration of Yeshivas Toras Emes regarding the manner of their studies in Nigleh and Chassidus. May it be the will of Hashem that this be successful, and that they may ascend higher and higher in their study of Torah with Yiras Shamayim, in accordance with the will of our Nasi, our holy Rebbes, may their merits protect us.

However, along with this, one must always keep before their eyes what is explained in many places in Chassidus: that regarding others, it is the duty of every Jewish person to judge them favorably (see also the letter printed at the end of *Kuntres 2 Nissan 5712* and the references there to *Kuntres Hechalotzu*). This is in contrast to oneself, where one must stand with the strength of a demand—a justified demand—when one contemplates that "days were fashioned, and not one of them [is to be wasted]." The meaning of this is that all the days granted to each person should not see a single moment go to waste. That is to say, when a moment passes without filling it with the content of Torah and Mitzvos, it is: 1) A loss that cannot be recovered; and 2) This is what is most concerning—that the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, gave him a most precious gift, this moment of time, and he did not use it in accordance with the will of Hashem. It is as if, Heaven forbid, the gift holds no significance for him, etc., etc. Further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

Regarding the matter at hand: even if the administration of the Yeshiva is, for the time being, satisfied with their conduct and studies, this does not affect their own personal obligation to demand more of themselves. They must look at the aforementioned, in accordance with the words of our Sages, "We increase in matters of holiness."

With blessings for success in the study of Nigleh and Chassidus, and a Kosher and Happy Pesach.

#### ***1778***

**In the printed letter:** *Sefer HaMaamarim Kuntresim*, Vol. 3, p. 45.

## 1579

B"H, 2 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from the beginning of Adar in due time. It was a pleasure to read that you are well and that you strive at every opportunity to influence your surroundings as well, to bring peace within their borders. It is understood that peace in the physical realm is dependent upon peace in the spiritual realm. As is also known from the new discoveries in medical science, the state of the nerves and peace of mind are of great consequence to the health of the physical body. Since the two souls within a Jewish person are in conflict—as one is concerned with spirituality and the other with physicality—peace between them is only possible in one way: through the victory of the nefesh elokis. If, Heaven forbid, the opposite were to occur, it would not be true peace, for even at the moment of sin, the nefesh elokis remains in a state of faith in Him, may He be blessed, as is written in Tanya, end of Chapter 24. Furthermore, even the yetzer hara is only given permission to confuse a person, but its own desire is also for the person to defeat it, for through this, its "remembrance"—that is, the reward of the yetzer hara—is increased. See Tanya, end of Chapter 29, and Zohar, Parshas Terumah 163a.

Enclosed is a copy of my general letter for the upcoming Pesach, which I hope will interest you, and perhaps also those people with whom you come in contact.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 1,580

1,580

B"H, 2 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 28 Adar, in which you write that you are teaching at the Talmud Torah in classes where the children are between the ages of 8 and 10, but that due to the local situation, the boys and girls are learning together, and you ask for my opinion as to whether you should continue teaching in this class.

In my opinion, since you conclude in your letter that in the older class the boys and girls are taught separately—which is how it should be—it is worthwhile for you to remain in your position. However, you should immediately arrange that they do not sit in a mixed fashion; rather, have one group sit on the right side and the other on the left. In time, you will surely be able to improve the situation even further.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 1581

B"H, 3 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...I have written long ago that it is not my nature to engage in words of rebuke, especially toward people who are in the Holy Land, upon which the eyes of Hashem are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year, such that—**whether they want it or not**—the King, Hashem Himself, is their guardian. Nevertheless, necessity is not to be condemned, and therefore I will speak briefly. The matter is as follows:

Whether we wish it or not, we are filling the place of the Chassidei Chabad of the generations before us, and before them, back to the generation of knowledge of the Chassidim of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, founder of the Chabad philosophy. Generation after generation paved the way for us, and nothing remains for us but to complete the "small vessels." On the other hand, the obligation is placed upon us and our generation to finish the *birurim* of the *ikvesa d'meshicha* and to draw down the revelation of Moshiach to below ten *tefachim* in this physical world. Even with a slight contemplation of these matters, one should be seized with trembling and fear, knowing that all the awesome matters spoken of by our Sages regarding Moshiach and the revelation of that time—especially as explained in *Chassidus*—all depend upon our *avodah*. And yet, after all this, one feels... everyone thinks about their own personal affairs...

The inner nature of such claims is self-evident. To avoid any room for error in this, one should imagine: if a colleague were to present such claims to him, how would he receive them? Consequently, according to the Torah's ruling, "As water reflects the face to the face," there is room to assume that their own responses are received by their colleagues in that very same way. One could elaborate on this at great length. Who can say? If the Dubner Maggid were brought before them, he would surely have invented a fitting parable, and perhaps it would have been accepted. But it is a pity to waste their time and my own on arguments and debates of this nature. The main point is that every moment in our time is extremely precious. Every moment spent on pilpulim and negotiations between them and their colleagues—who did not fulfill their obligation to whom, and who is greater in Torah, *avodah*, and *gemilus chasadim*—I do not know who gains from all this back-and-forth.

Regarding the practical application: let them approach the *avodah* with *mesiras nefesh*. If there is no other choice, let them decide for themselves that they are one hundred percent in the right. But since they were educated in the light of *Chassidus*, Hashem has graced them with a sense of *mesiras nefesh* in practice, each for the benefit of his fellow. Consequently, they should overlook their own feelings and do everything for the benefit of their peers...

I ask forgiveness if I have perhaps offended anyone’s honor, but the truth remains the truth, whether or not someone’s honor is offended by it.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and may Hashem grant you the merit that you should feel—not only with the *nefesh elokis* but also with the human intellect—that Hashem has privileged you to be among those who assist and participate in the work of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in building the Chabad sanctuary in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily.

Awaiting good tidings and celebrations.

## 1,782

B"H, 3 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding your military service and that you have now been appointed as a religious officer for an entire brigade, which includes several units:

Surely you are utilizing the full force of your influence to improve the state of spiritual life in all areas. It has already been explained here at a farbrengen at length: if each person were required to act using only **his own** strengths, then one would have to take stock of those strengths and, consequently, the authority he possesses. However, when one is required to fulfill a role connected to Torah and mitzvos, he acts as a shaliach of the Ribono shel Olam. Consequently, he does not proceed with his own strength, but with the strength of the One who spoke and the world came into being, and who renews the work of creation every single day. From this, two conclusions follow: a) that he has sufficient strength, and b) that ultimately he will succeed in the matter, for who can say to Him, "What are You doing?" when he comes on the mission of the Makom.

You conclude your letter by mentioning that you have received a proposal of marriage and have already met with the young lady, may she live, and that the proposal found favor in your eyes, and you have decided to arrange the engagement. May it be the will of the Hashem that it be in a good and auspicious hour, for good fortune in both material and spiritual matters.

Since the bride is a Kohenes, she should increase her study of Torah. Until the day of the wedding, you should acquire proficiency in one tractate of Gemara, and if possible, also in the necessary laws found in the Kitzur Shulchan Aruch.

With blessings for a mazal tov,

P.S. Regarding what you wrote in your letter—that you apparently intend to set the date of the wedding for a year from now, since that is when your military service will be completed and also when the bride’s time of study at Bais Yaakov will conclude—this delay does not seem right to me. If there are no special obstacles, it would be worthwhile to consider setting the date of the wedding in the month of Kislev, the upcoming month of Geulah.

## 1,583

1,583

B"H, 3 Nissan, 5712

Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification that you have decided to enter into an engagement with the avreich Mr. ..., I hereby express my blessing that it should be in a good and auspicious hour, for good fortune in both material and spiritual matters.

You are surely well aware of the responsibility that rests upon the one who is the "foundation of the home." The words of our Sages are well known, that blessing is drawn into the home on account of the woman (Yevamos 62b, and explained in Likutei Torah, end of Parshas Bracha). It is understood that these words refer to both material and spiritual blessing. Since the Ribono shel Olam does not deal unjustly with His creations, a special understanding (*binah*) has been granted to the woman to organize the home through appropriate preparation beforehand, to build her home in Yisrael filled with the "candle of a mitzvah and the light of Torah"—this is the inner dimension of Torah, the teachings of Chassidus.

With blessings for mazal tov.

Awaiting good tidings and celebrations.

## 1785

1785

B”H, 4 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote, that you have distanced yourself from anash and are distressed by this: It is known from our Sages that everything is in the hands of Heaven except for the fear of Heaven. Consequently, it depends entirely on you to draw closer, for "you have labored and found—believe it." However, this must be done as explained in Tanya, Chapter 42, in the same way a person searches for a treasure or a cache hidden in the depths of the earth, digging for it with tremendous exertion.

I have already said several times that the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, is well known: that now is the time immediately preceding the coming of Moshiach, and every single moment is precious. One should not waste time on "clouds" of thought or searching for reasons and justifications as to why one’s situation is as it is and not better. Rather, one must utilize every single moment for avodah, both within oneself and with others. Then, one naturally sees that there is no foundation for melancholy, for when one seeks the truth, one succeeds both regarding oneself and regarding others. This is especially true given that we are assured by the well-known promise of the Alter Rebbe (cited in a letter of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, at the end of *Sefer Kitzurim L’Tanya*, end of page 122) that because of his mesiras nefesh, it was decreed in the Heavenly Court that in every matter of Torah, fear of Heaven, and good character traits, the hand of those who are connected to him and follow in his footsteps will be uppermost...

## 1586

B"H, 4 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the distinguished Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Moshe, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 18 Adar, in which you inform me that a daughter was born to your daughter, Mrs. Chana, may she live, and she has been named in Israel Rivkah, may she live.

I hereby express my blessing of Mazal Tov. May you raise her, together with her husband, may he live, to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, with peace of mind and physical well-being.

It is known from my father-in-law, the Rebbe (the Rashab), that our custom is to say "to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds" even upon the birth of a daughter, in accordance with the words of our Sages (Berachos 17a) regarding how women merit [the reward of Torah]—by having their sons study, by waiting for their husbands, etc., and by guarding [their children], etc.

I read with pleasure in your letter regarding the setting of times for Torah study in your beis medrash in general, and among them, the portion of the shiurim in Chassidus. It is somewhat surprising that you do not mention anything regarding any shiurim in Chassidus, or at the very least Tanya, during the weekdays. As it is known from our Sages that one should not go three days without Torah, there should be such a practice at least for the study of Chassidus as well. Perhaps this is merely a slip of the pen, and you do study Chassidus during the weekdays as well.

Although you do not mention anything regarding this, surely you hold farbrengens from time to time in the beis medrash, and it is obvious that you do so every Shabbos Mevarchim, in accordance with the takanah of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

You are surely correct in your request regarding the sending of the sichos of Shabbos Mevarchim and the like, but what can I do? I am burdened with work, even more so due to the preoccupations that consume my time, etc., etc. Nevertheless, I endeavor to do so as much as possible. Enclosed is the maamar for 10 Shevat, as well as the sicha for 5 Chanukah, for which I recently edited the transcript in Lashon HaKodesh.

Enclosed is a copy of a general letter regarding the upcoming holiday of Pesach. It is worthwhile to publicize it in an appropriate manner, as it is a general matter that concerns not only Chassidim or anash, but everyone.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach, and success in your holy work.

**R' Moshe:** Axelrod. Another letter to him—above, Vol. 3, 744.

## 1787

B"H, 4 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the G-d-fearing, honorable, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs with faith, etc.,
R' Moshe HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

...Through our friend who engages in communal needs and heavenly work, R' Yosef Player, I received a letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, addressed to him, dated 13 Teves 5710. In it, he writes—and these are his holy words: "And he shall continue his presidency at the Shaarei Tefillah synagogue of Bnei Reuven, and Hashem shall grant him success, etc." R' Yosef Player writes that he is uncertain as to the interpretation of this: what is the nature of this "continuation"? He wishes to interpret it as applying only for a specific, limited time and no longer. However, I see no basis for this interpretation, as the matter is written without qualification. Therefore, in my opinion, he should not involve himself in this, but rather leave the matter in the hands of Heaven. That is to say, if they put forward his candidacy for the coming period as well, he should not interfere at all and should consent to his nomination. Surely, everything will be successful for the best, for him and for the synagogue. It goes without saying that when they elect him—in a good and auspicious hour—as president of the synagogue, it may be worthwhile to endeavor to live in the vicinity of the synagogue, so as to minimize unnecessary exertion, and in exchange, invest those energies into matters that are beneficial for the many and for the individual.

As we approach the upcoming festival of Pesach, for which there is great preparation in every Jewish home—the essence of which consists of two things: removing that which is forbidden on Pesach, and introducing that which is required for Pesach—may Hashem grant each and every one of us that this should also be done in a spiritual sense: to remove from our domain those things that are forbidden to every Jewish son and daughter, until "it shall not be seen and it shall not be found"—meaning, that it should not exist even in secret—and to introduce into our domain all things necessary to serve Hashem from a state of true freedom, as our Sages of blessed memory said: "There is no free man except one who engages in Torah."

With blessings for a kosher and joyous Pesach.

P.S. As per his request, enclosed is a copy of the letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

## 1,889

B"H, 5 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from 4 Vayikra, in which you inform me of the situation between your sister and brother-in-law, may they live, and the conflict between them:

For a long time now, I have not viewed it as proper at all for others to intervene between a husband and his wife. Even the closest relatives—such as a brother and sister, or a father and mother—should not do such a thing. It is well known how much Chazal have elaborated on the importance of peace between a woman and her husband, to the extent that the Ribono shel Olam said, "My name may be erased in the water in order to bring peace between a man and his wife." When a third party intervenes—who surely possesses two souls, both a nefesh elokis and a nefesh habehamis—it generally does not help to strengthen that peace.

I do not wish to dwell on this at length, as I do not know if my words will be of any avail; and if they are, the lines above are sufficient.

Regarding your question about the aforementioned conflict, there is a din in Yisrael, and they must clarify the din with the Rabbonim of anash. May the Ribono shel Olam bless His people with peace.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 1,190

B"H, 5 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and diligent in his communal work, etc.,
Moreinu HaRav Yochanan, may he live, Shochet u'Bodek.

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received the first contributions from the Ma'os Chittim fund, the collection of which was entrusted to you by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. It is well known that a Tzaddik—and especially a Nasi in Israel—when he entrusts a Shliach with a mission, he simultaneously grants him the necessary strengths to fulfill that mission in the best possible manner, both for the sake of the mission and for the sake of the Shliach. It is understood from this that, as a result, the Shliach is granted an increase in spiritual health, and likewise in physical health.

And as one good deed leads to another, I hereby add my own blessing that together with all your family members, may they live, you should celebrate the upcoming Pesach holiday in good health, with kashrus, with joy, and with long life and good years. May you and your wife, may she live, receive much Yiddishe nachas and Chassidishe nachas from all your offspring, may they live. And may you stand at your holy post for many years to come, both as a Shochet u'Bodek and as a Gabbai in those matters to which my father-in-law, the Rebbe, appointed you.

With blessings for all the best and for a kosher and joyous celebration of the days of Pesach.

## 1. Tetzaveh

B"H, 5 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding your question concerning your study schedule, where you study eighteen chapters of Mishnayos every day, and consequently the study is somewhat superficial, and there is also little time left for other studies, and you ask my opinion on this:

In my opinion, you should maintain your good custom of reviewing eighteen chapters every day, especially since, according to your letter, this also has the nature of a vow. You should study only a few Mishnayos each day in depth, and in this way, you will have both—the breadth and the depth—and there will also be sufficient time for studies in other areas of Torah...

## 1,992

B"H, 5 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter received after Shabbos, in which you inform me that you have an offer for the position of Rav and Shochet in the city of..., and you ask for my opinion:

1) Regarding whether to accept the position:
If, according to the information you have received, this is an Orthodox community, it is worth looking into and accepting.

2) Regarding whether to negotiate conditions concerning the women’s section:
As you describe in your letter, this is not a practical question, since they already have a women’s section. Consequently, you will surely be able to arrange this over time without magnifying the matter or presenting it as a question that could be resolved in two ways; rather, it is a matter that is entirely simple: that women pray in the women’s section and men in the men’s section.

3) Since you wear a long coat every Shabbos and are in doubt as to whether you should do so on the Shabbos you visit them:
As far as I know, even in communities that are not Chareidi, there are Rabbis who wear a long coat on Shabbos and Yom Tov, at weddings, and the like. Therefore, I do not see any concern that wearing the kapote will weaken your standing there. And since this is also connected to the question of the permissibility of a vow, etc., in my opinion, there is no need for such a thing at all. On the contrary, one should consider that they will be impressed when they see a Rabbi with a beard and wearing a long coat on Shabbos and Yom Tov, and during a speech before Yizkor.

May Hashem help you in finding a suitable position quickly, and may you celebrate the Festival of Matzos with kashrus and joy.

With blessings.

## 1,593

B"H, 5 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...On this occasion, and as the days of the festival of Pesach are drawing near, I will take the liberty of writing the following lines.

It is easily understood by anyone who observes the events of recent years that they cannot be explained by the laws of history, for the course of events was entirely different from what could have been predicted by those laws. This is especially evident in the events that have occurred in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, during this time.

One of the conclusions from this observation is that, very often, the spirit and the form govern and prevail over the physical and the material, to such an extent that we have seen recently that victory, even in physical matters, went specifically to the side that was weaker in physical terms, but whose strength lay in its spiritual state. Since this is true in the life of the collective, one can also learn from this regarding the individual. This is especially true regarding the individuals of the Jewish people; after the terrible destructions of recent years, the responsibility of each and every one of us—the *she'eris hapeleitah*—toward the collective is greater than it was until now. This is particularly so if one is in a position where the conduct of this individual serves as an example from which those in his surroundings will learn, in which case his responsibility is immense, as many others will be drawn after him.

It is understood that I am not writing this for the sake of preaching. My intention in this letter is that, insofar as I know about you—and especially knowing that you studied for some time at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch—it is certain that this cannot be lost, *chas v'shalom*. If this is true of physical matter, where it is a law of nature that it is not lost, but merely changes its form or is transformed from matter into energy—yet in any case, not even a small part of it is lost at all—then how much more so is this true in spiritual matters, which are not subject to the accidents of matter. Since Hashem has granted you the merit of living in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established—which, in the words of the verse, is "a land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are at all times, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year"—and since your situation is such that you hold a position in the community that serves as an example for a certain circle of people, surely even a brief reflection will make you feel the great responsibility resting upon your shoulders. This includes the responsibility toward the tens of generations of your ancestors and forefathers, each of whom surely gave and contributed from their lives to the golden chain of Jewish history as they ascended the path leading to Beis-El; the responsibility toward the founders and directors of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, who invested the best of their land, their attention, and their souls in each and every student of the yeshivah; and the responsibility toward yourself and all your household—that is to say, toward the *nefesh elokis* that exists in every single Jew, which yearns and thirsts to utilize its powers in daily life and in practical matters. As is known, this is the nature of the Jewish person and the Jewish power, whose motto is "Action is supreme."

Through reflecting on this responsibility, my hope is strong—in the spirit of the Sages' saying, "Throw a stick into the air, and it will land on its root"—that you and your household will, in the end and in the near future, *im yirtzeh Hashem*, serve as a symbol and example of a Chassidish Jewish home, not only in ideas but also in actual deeds. And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for proper health and a kosher and happy Pesach for you and all your household, may they live.

## 1,494

B"H, 7 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Agudas Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established,

Peace and blessing!

1) My letter of 28 Adar has surely been received, and I await a response to it.

2) In several of my previous letters, I wrote regarding the Coordinating Committee here, and the fact that the Jewish Agency promised to provide, for the time being, a sum of one hundred thousand for housing for youth immigrating from Yemen, Morocco, and the like. After much delay from day to day and month to month, at a meeting held yesterday between representatives of the aforementioned committee and Mr. Nahum Goldmann and his assistants, they officially announced that they have already begun to distribute the aforementioned sum, that the decision regarding this rests with Mr. Koll of the Jewish Agency, and that they have already given 10,000 to Sejera—which I believe is a settlement affiliated with Mizrachi. Together with this, I also received the telegram from Mr. Gelman regarding the building in Lod, and I have once again strongly demanded here that from the aforementioned sum of one hundred thousand, they should grant funds to Chabad, specifically for the building in Lod, which should be allocated for students from the aforementioned countries. However, it is understood that since the decision rests with Mr. Koll, and there will be many claimants and applicants for the total sum, you must exert yourselves in every possible way to ensure they grant you the maximum possible for the building in Lod, as well as for the building in Kfar Chabad-Safria, where improvements have begun but for which you lack all the necessary means. It is likely that they will make it a condition that the building be used specifically for the aforementioned youth, and you will surely be able to arrange matters in an appropriate manner. It is to be hoped that in time there will be further sums beyond the aforementioned one hundred thousand, but one cannot set a date for this, and consequently one cannot rely upon it; therefore, speed and energy in this matter are most necessary. I may send a telegram regarding this today, but I am providing a more detailed description of the situation in this letter as well.

3) According to the promise of Mr. Goldmann and others, the building materials—for which a large portion of the aforementioned sums has been earmarked—should be obtained at the lowest possible price, in accordance with the regulations and the currency exchange rate now established in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established.

4) It is a pity that you do not provide detailed information in a timely manner regarding everything pertaining to these matters, without my having to receive the news from outside sources, and perhaps even with a delay, since information is not always received from faithful friends and supporters of Lubavitch; sometimes they only inform me because they have no other choice, and to the wise it is sufficient...

With the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach and success in your holy work,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1,295

B”H, 7 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished R’ Pinchas, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

... 3) Regarding what you raise concerning the printing of the Tanya: I have already written many times, regarding several matters, that the things I write are by way of suggestion and an explanation of my opinion. Consequently, the choice is in your hands whether to accept or decline. However, my opinion is that the Tanya should not be reprinted except by photo-offset from the edition that was proofread by my father-in-law, the Rebbe [Rashab], of blessed memory—the Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch edition of 5660.

4) Regarding what you wrote in your letter, that you heard a story that the Alter Rebbe was so precise in his Tanya that he even scrutinized a superfluous "vav," and you do not know which "vav" is being referred to: As is implied by the letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of 28 Tammuz 5692, this relates to the words "ve'ikara veshorsha" (and its essence and its root) at the beginning of Chapter 41. He could have written "reishis ha'avodah ikara" (the beginning of the avodah is its essence), yet he wrote "ve'ikara" (and its essence).

5) Regarding what you note in your letter that even in the Tanya printed in 5660 there is room for correction, and you point to Iggeres HaKodesh, Chapter 31: Indeed, in several places the aforementioned edition requires correction. There is a list of several corrections from the letter of the esteemed Rav, the G-d-fearing man, one of the elders of Anash, R’ Asher the Shochet of Nikolayev. G-d willing, in the new edition of the Tanya, a list of corrections will also be printed at the end of the book, for I did not have the heart to correct it in the body of the text, so as not to deviate from the aforementioned edition.

With the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 1,496

1,496

B"H, 7 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...It is certainly unnecessary to emphasize that you must write to your son, Mr. [Name]—may he live and be well—that while it is the duty of every Jew at all times to put on tefillin, it is even more vital for someone serving in the army. Putting on tefillin protects them and ultimately brings them home safe and sound at the appointed time.

We heard this from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, during the last world war, and we also saw it with our own eyes—it is a firmly established fact—that all those Jews who were careful to put on tefillin while in the army returned home safe and sound.

It happens that during maneuvers or exercises, when it is impossible to manage to put on tefillin in the morning, one must know that it can be done—putting on tefillin—throughout the entire day until sunset. At the very least, one should put on the tefillin and recite Krias Shema while wearing them, and then take them off—if it is not possible to spend a longer time to recite the other prayers as well. These few minutes can be found at any time while in the army, even during maneuvers, exercises, and the like. I am certain that you will find the appropriate words to explain the above to your son—may he live and be well—and Hashem Yisbarach will bring him back home safe and sound at the appointed time.

I conclude with a wish for a kosher and happy Pesach for you and your household, and regards to your brother, Mr. [Name]—may he live and be well—who was here a while ago, at which time we had a lengthy conversation.

P.S.
Enclosed is a message for Pesach, which I hope you will find interesting.

I am doing it bit by bit, as time permits, and that is why the preparation for printing is delayed. 1599

By the Grace of G-d
9 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn

To the Honorable Rabbi, the Honorable Chossid, scion of holy ancestors, leader of his community, walking in the straight path, son of Torah scholars and son of ancestors of a chain of lineage, etc., etc.,
Rabbi Yisrael, may he live and be well,

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your esteemed letter from some time ago, as well as this second letter from the end of Adar. It seems you did not receive the response to your first letter, and I am sorry for this. I will therefore take this opportunity to offer my humble opinion regarding your question—for the question of a wise man is half the answer, and a wise man and leader in Israel is even more than that. The essence of your question is that since your desire is to sit and occupy yourself with Torah and avodah, you have therefore moved your tent to Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established), and there is a thought that perhaps you should travel to the United States.

Now, in my opinion—and this is by way of introduction to what our Sages said regarding the verse, "You shall surely set a king over you," from which we derive the laws regarding other positions of authority in Israel, and especially for one who leads many holy communities—beyond the fact that generally "the Sages are the kings," he also possesses the power to act in general, and in particular within the communities of our Sephardic brethren, who have the authority and permission to judge even monetary cases, etc., etc. It is known what the Holy One, blessed be He, said to Yehoshua bin Nun, who was the successor to Moshe Rabbeinu, who was a king in Yeshurun: "My children go out to war, and you..." From this it is understood that the completeness of the matter of a king is that he must be together with his people, especially in times of war.

Since the Holy One, blessed be He, has merited you to be a person of general influence and a leader in Israel, to whose voice thousands and tens of thousands listen, it is certain that you have also been given the powers to bring this into reality in the daily lives of all those who are influenced by you and listen to your voice in their daily conduct. And since every detail, and certainly a general matter, is by Divine Providence and with a supreme intent—the Cause of all causes and the Reason for all reasons—this is also the path through which a person of general influence ascends to the level of perfection to which his soul aspires, which is hewn from beneath the Throne of Glory and whose root is above and beyond, without end. For the souls of Israel "arose in thought"—and the precision in this word **arose** (*alu*) is that even in the "thought" itself, they are at the highest level of elevation possible within the thought, the thought of the Holy One, blessed be He, and even higher in holiness, for the souls of Israel are rooted in the Essence and Being of the Ein Sof, blessed be He.

It is understood from all of the above that since you are in close proximity to the places where our Sephardic brethren (may they live and be well) are found—who are thirsty for the word of G-d and yearn to receive guidance in the avodah of the Holy One, blessed be He, and the acceptance of the yoke of Heaven and the yoke of Torah and mitzvos—it is your role, your duty, and your privilege to do this day after day. Through this, there will be drawn down from above the dimension of time, "day after day," with success that is above nature within nature.

It should be noted that the Sefirah of Malchus, from which all appointments of authority in Israel stem, is described in the Zohar: even though it has nothing of its own, and the "lower light" constantly calls to the "upper light," and the *chirik* vowel point is below all the letters—yet the *zarka segolta*, which was the "cornerstone," is the *cholam* point, which is above and beyond, without end. As is explained at length in the books of Kabbalah, even though the Sefirah of Malchus receives from all the Sefiros, Arich Anpin contains nine points, for Malchus is rooted in *Radla* (the Unknowable Head), where the hidden strength of the Essence resides. The "depth of the bottom is embedded in the depth of the top," and the soul, which is rooted in the Essence and Being of the Ein Sof, blessed be He, descended from a high mountain to a deep valley to be clothed in a body and an animal soul. This descent is for the sake of an ascent—an ascent to a level even greater than what it was before the descent, namely, to be absorbed into the "Body of the King," the King of the world. The preparation for this is the fulfillment of one’s role in this world to carry out the supreme will and the desire of the Holy One, blessed be He.

It is a common expression in the teachings of Chassidus that from the perspective of *bitul* to the **Owner** of the will, there is no difference what the Owner of the will commands—whether it is putting on Tefillin, which is the drawing down of supreme intellects and the intellects of *gadlus*, or chopping wood and drawing water, which are the lowest levels in the complete structure of the Jewish people, which begins with "your heads, your tribes" and ends with "your woodchopper and your water-drawer." For from the perspective of the acceptance of the yoke of Heaven and from the perspective of one's surrender and dedication to the Owner of the will—as our Sages said, "their only desire is for their Father in Heaven"—there is no difference to him in what manner the "Supreme Name" is glorified.

The conclusion from all the above is that according to the situation, since you are in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established), where there are now tens of thousands of our Sephardic brethren (may they live and be well), and who, due to the multitude of trials, concealments, and hiddenness, are in need of frequent guidance on their difficult path in both material and spiritual matters—a tremendous and great privilege has fallen to your lot to use the talents and virtues with which the Holy One, blessed be He, has graced you, and the "treasures of kings" that were passed down to you from your holy ancestors, generation after generation, to go out to war against the *yetzer*, the *kelipos*, and the *sitra achra* at the head of the armies of the members of the holy communities who are influenced by and listen to your will. To fight the war of G-d and to publicize His Divinity, may He be blessed, in all their surroundings, that there is nothing else besides Him **literally**, that everything is Divinity.

Especially, and in particular, as it is the duty of the hour to conquer with a strong hand the entire younger generation—all the sons and daughters, "one wise, one wicked, one simple, and one who does not know how to ask"—and in the order of *Seder Hishtalshelus*—*Atzilus, Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah*—that the Holy One, blessed be He, revealed Himself from the world of Atzilus to the worlds of Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah, all together equally, to recount the exodus from Egypt. This is the story as per the Zohar: "The heavens declare," sparkling and shining to emerge from the exile of Egypt, which is the opposite of this, and to emerge also even from the "Egypt of holiness," the "narrowness of the throat" (*meitzar hagarohn*), where there is a possibility for the sustenance of Pharaoh and the three ministers of Pharaoh, as is explained at length in *Likutei Torah* from the Arizal, and to bring them to a "good and spacious land," as the matter is explained there.

Especially since you are in a good and spacious land, but it is necessary to reveal in practice that this land of ours is the Holy Land, the land upon which the eyes of the L-rd your G-d are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year, even during the time of exile. The matter depends only on us to illuminate the darkness of the exile, a double and redoubled darkness (double—two, and redoubled—two more, corresponding to the three *kelipos* and *kelipas nogah*, the Jordan that takes from this side of holiness and gives to that side of the *sitra achra*), and to illuminate it with the light of the Essence and Being of the Ein Sof, blessed be He, and the fulfillment of the prophecy that "**the night** shall shine like the day." This corresponds to the exodus from Egypt, when "He illuminated **the night**," that the night itself shone, and "as in the days of your exodus from Egypt, I will show you wonders."

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach, that you may celebrate it with joy together with all your household (may they live and be well) and all those you influence. I await the revelation of the light of Torah and the "dew of Torah" in fear of Heaven, to draw them down into this physical and material world to make it a dwelling place for Him, may He be blessed, speedily in our days, with kindness and mercy.

With respect, appreciation, and admiration.

**Rabbi Eliezer:** Krasik. Additional letters to him — see above 1358, and the references in the notes there.

## 1,001

B"H, 9 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

As we approach the upcoming holiday of Pesach, I hereby wish you a kosher and joyous holiday. Since the primary mitzvah from the Torah that applies even in our time is the eating of matzah (for the essence of Pesach depends on the offering of the Korban Pesach, while the eating of maror, according to most halachic authorities, is a rabbinic obligation in our time), which is called the "food of faith," it is explained at length in Chassidus that by eating matzah in its literal sense—at a time when this eating is a mitzvah, namely during the days of Pesach and especially on the first night of the holiday—one strengthens the power of faith. Faith means, of course, that one believes, and the strengthening of faith lies in the fact that this faith does not remain merely in the mind as intellectual knowledge, but rather penetrates—it permeates—the person regarding their daily life in thought, speech, and action. Furthermore, faith becomes a realization, like seeing with physical eyes, even though in actual practice this will only be fully realized in the future to come with the fulfillment of the prophecy, **"And all flesh shall see together** that the mouth of Hashem has spoken." However, the preparation for this, and a semblance of this, exists even in our time, and the holiday of Pesach is particularly auspicious for this. In simple terms, this means that in all matters of thought, speech, and action, one should first and foremost **conduct oneself** according to Torah and mitzvos as they are explained in the light of Torah—which is the teachings of Chassidus—without waiting until Hashem grants one the merit to **understand** the matter in its entirety.

1512

If they have any doubt about the matter, they may write to me on your behalf. Generally, the established order has always been that in such matters, there must be appropriate discipline; therefore, first and foremost, you must turn to your mashpia to hear his opinion.

As for the Chitas shiurim—if necessary, you may complete the previous day’s shiur at night; this is what my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, instructed.

## 1,503

B"H, 9 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings,

I received your letter in due time, in which you inform me of your work in the field of kosher education as a teacher in a charedi school founded by the Chever HaPe'ilim. You also express your request and desire to be blessed by the Ribono shel Olam with children who are alive and enduring, and you add that a specialist doctor has suggested that you stop your work, as it is damaging your health.

In my opinion, since your work consists of bringing the hearts of Yisrael closer to their Father in Heaven and awakening within them the feeling that they are children to Hashem Elokeinu, it is not advisable to stop this entirely in order to be blessed with children who are alive and enduring, as these two things are contradictory. On the contrary, by bringing His sons and daughters closer so that they belong to the Ribono shel Olam, this itself is a segulah for the birth of children as well. Therefore, my advice is that you continue your involvement in the field of education, but in a manner that does not strain your health as much as possible. Surely, with appropriate effort, you will be able to find work of the aforementioned type in close proximity to your place of residence, and also to improve the nature of the work, even if this results in a lower salary, provided that you continue in the work of kosher education. May the Ribono shel Olam help you and your husband, may he live, to share good news soon, that the desires of your heart have been fulfilled for the good and that you have been blessed with children who are alive and enduring.

It is understood that there must be an anchor for all of the above within the ways of nature, and consequently, you and your husband, may he live, must follow the instructions of specialist doctors regarding this matter.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach and for good news soon.

## 1504

B"H, 9 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter of 22 Shevat in due time. Due to an abundance of preoccupations, my response has been delayed until now. There is another reason for this: it is difficult to preach morality in general, and especially to those from whom one hopes for great things in many areas, yet who are instead invested in complaints and demands, failing to realize that this stems from the *Yetzer Hara’s* counsel to distract a person from their *avodah* to Hashem.

You write at length regarding the reasons that compel you not to participate in the field of Chabad education, as well as regarding the matter of... Without entering into the substance of these arguments—whether they are justified or not—in general, when there are two sides, after the sin of the Tree of Knowledge where good and evil became intermingled, it is rare for one side to be one hundred percent right and the other side one hundred percent at fault. Certainly, both sides are partially at fault and partially in the right.

In general, regarding this matter, there are two approaches: Either the approach should be that the matter is essential—meaning, your involvement in the field of Chabad education is necessary, and since there are difficulties, one must seek strategies and counsel on how to remove them. Or, on the other hand, that since there are difficulties and unpleasantness, etc., this is not for you, and the matter is either left to be done by others or, as the Mishnah at the end of Sotah states regarding the era of *Ikvesa D’Meshicha*, "We have no one to rely upon but our Father in Heaven." To my regret, you have grasped the second path rather than the first. The practical difference between these two is understood, and there is no need to elaborate.

It is my hope that after this, you will endeavor to accustom yourself to the first path, and may Hashem grant you success in producing fruit through your *avodah* in this.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 1,107

1,107

B"H, 11th of the Month of Redemption, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of the Yeshivos, may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

With the permission of the esteemed Rabbis, the directors of the Yeshivos, I turn to you, my friends, the students of the Yeshivos, in this letter, in addition to my general letter from Rosh Chodesh Nissan.

The beginning of the upcoming festival of Pesach, which approaches for us and for all of Yisrael for the good, is the conducting of the "Seder." Every person must be "trembling with awe to fulfill the statement of the Sages who instituted the mitzvah of the Seder and the Haggadah... for there is **nothing** empty within them."

Regarding the "telling to your son," the Torah speaks of four sons: one wise, one wicked, one simple, and one who does not know how to ask. The author of the Haggadah places the wicked son immediately after the wise son, with the additional letter *vav*—"and one wicked" (*ve'echad rasha*)—the *vav* of addition.

This means: 
a) Even the wicked son has hope, for Hashem provides him with a wise son who can influence him and help him improve his ways—provided that he who was wicked until now attaches himself to the wise one and becomes secondary to him. 
b) The wise son must not say, "What have I to do with the wicked one? Let him perish in his wickedness," for all of Yisrael are responsible for (and intertwined with) one another. It is incumbent upon everyone to strive to bring the other back to the good path, provided he always remembers that the wicked one is attached and secondary to him, to be influenced and to receive from the wise one, and not the other way around. 
c) The wise son must always remember that "sin crouches at the door," and "whoever is greater than his fellow, his inclination is greater than his," and the wicked one (within himself) watches the righteous one and seeks to kill him. Therefore, he must be extremely careful with himself and pray for mercy that the Ribono shel Olam help him, for only through this will he be able to overcome the wicked one within himself.

And if regarding the wicked one one must strive to help him (with the appropriate caution, as mentioned above), then all the more so regarding the simple one (the fool) and regarding the one who does not know how to ask.

When the wise son adds, joins, refines, and elevates the wicked one, the simple one, and the one who does not know how to ask—each of whom begins with the *vav* of addition, the *vav* that is the "letter of truth," the drawing down of the light of truth—then we fulfill our request: "Bless us, our Father, **all of us as one**."

Just as it was at the time the Torah was given to His people Yisrael, "And Yisrael camped there" (*vayichan*)—in the singular form.

This is the ultimate purpose of the Exodus from Egypt, as it is written: "When you bring the people out of Egypt, you shall serve Elokus upon this mountain."

However, the sin occurred afterward, and they and the world became coarsened. Through our *avodah* now, we return to clarify and refine, until in the days of Moshiach the clarification will be completed, the physicality of the body and the world will be refined, and the glory of Hashem will be revealed.

With the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach,

**Menachem Schneerson**

P.S. This letter was written for the upcoming Pesach, but its content is **timely for all times**.

## 1508

In the sicha of Acharon Shel Pesach, printed at the end of this kuntras, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, emphasizes the necessity of purifying the air through the letters of Torah, for the health of a person depends upon the air. In an atmosphere of Torah and mitzvos, life is healthy; in an atmosphere of heresy—Heaven forefend—there is a danger of contagious illness of various kinds. End quote.

If this is true for a healthy person, it is all the more so for one who is weak. The danger is even greater for someone who is ill, even if only with a minor ailment, and certainly for one with a life-threatening illness.

Our Sages have said that "illness" refers to the yetzer hara, which Hashem will slaughter only in the time to come. This is the source of life-threatening illness—the cravings for forbidden things—and of non-life-threatening illness—the cravings for permitted things.

The Rebbe specifically mentions and awakens us regarding this—the concept of the Exodus from Egypt, the eating of matzah, and the prohibition of chametz on Pesach, when the people left in **haste** (b'chipazon). This was because the evil within the souls of the Jewish people was still in its full strength within the left chamber (for their impurity had not ceased until the Giving of the Torah, and it returned with the sin of the Golden Calf). The Jewish people were then like the only son of a king who is ill, of whom it is said that he must eat healing foods, and no other food or nourishment is to be found in the house.

Consequently, the necessity of purifying the air is also mentioned, and we are urged to do so with vigor, specifically through thought and speech in the letters of the Chumash, Tehillim, Mishnayos, and Tanya—as explained at length in the sicha.

Through all of this, we also hasten the end of the Geulah, when chametz will no longer be able to rule over or harm the Jewish people. More than that, the yetzer hara, which is called chametz, will be burned away by the power of the illumination of Malchus. Then the prophecy will be fulfilled: "For you shall not go out in haste, nor shall you go in flight, for Hashem goes before you"—speedily in our days, truly.

**Menachem Schneerson**

11 Nissan, 5712, Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 109

109

B”H, 12 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, scion of holy ancestors, etc.,
Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Greetings and blessings!

I received with pleasure your letter of blessing for the eleventh of the month of redemption. The promise of Hashem is well known, especially regarding the Kohanim, His holy people: "And I will bless them," for the one who blesses is blessed by the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam and His addition, with an addition that is greater than the essence.

It can be said that this is similar to the interpretation brought in many places in Chassidus regarding the Sages’ statement, "The power of the son is greater than the power of the father"—that even so, it is from the power of the father. It is the same here: although the addition is greater than the essence, it nevertheless comes from the essence. This is similar to how, although the *is'arusa d'leila* (arousal from above) is greater than the *is'arusa d'letata* (arousal from below), it is nonetheless drawn down through the *is'arusa d'letata*. Consequently, there is a similarity and correlation between them, and there is a virtue in the *is'arusa d'letata* in that it is the cause, the factor, and the "compelling force," as it were. It could be said that this is why one is called the "addition" and the other the "essence." And this is our strength: even though "what are we and what is our life," etc., where we only open an opening "like the eye of a needle," nevertheless, the opening of the *ulam* (the great hall) depends on our "eye of a needle."

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach, with all its interpretations.

P.S. I have already requested that you be informed by telephone in response to your questions:

a) That I am not present during the baking of the *matzah shemurah* on Erev Pesach.

b) If you decide to be present during the baking of the *matzah shemurah*, you may take part, whether in the task of pouring the water or another matter during the baking.

c) The completion time for the baking of our *matzah shemurah* is approximately midday.

#### 109

The content of this letter (excluding the P.S.) was sent to several people.

**Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer, may he live:** Yalles. Additional letters to him—see above, 117, and the references in the notes there.

## 1510

1510

B”H, 13 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R’ Yitzchak, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

1) Regarding your opinion that since he is the *baal korei* (Torah reader), it naturally follows that he should begin *Baruch She’amar* after *chatzos* (halachic midnight):

In my opinion, this is incorrect. While one could, with difficulty, justify this according to *din*—since he recites the *Krias Shema* of the *katan* (minor) service, etc.—one must certainly take into account the matter of "what will people say." As is understood, this is not comparable to those who begin in due time and are davening the entire time, but happen to reach *Baruch She’amar* around *chatzos*; in that case, they have been occupied with the matter of *tefillah* and its preparation beforehand. This is not the case in the situation you describe, where he is the one reading from the Torah, which has no connection to *tefillah* and its preparation.

2) Regarding the students’ question of which *Chassidus* to study—*Likutei Torah* or the *Kesuvim* (writings):

Generally, not all students are the same in this regard. To a certain extent, this also depends on the amount of time they have set aside for the study of *Chassidus*. I have already stated in the past that one should strive for both: not only to study certain topics in depth (*iyun*), but also, to a certain extent, to have at least a superficial knowledge of many topics. This is achieved through studying *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah* and *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* in *Tanya*, several of the *mitzvos* in the *Tzemach Tzedek’s* *Derech Mitzvosecha*, and various letters. As for directing them to specific *Kesuvim*, as mentioned above, this depends on the type of student and their method of study, and the *mashpia* must decide this on the spot.

3) Regarding his question concerning what is brought in many places in *Chassidus*: that growth from a seed is only possible after it first rots and returns to the earth, and as is known, there is no *yesh mi’yesh* (being from being) except through an *ayin* (nothingness) in between. He finds it difficult: how does something grow whose seed does not perish?

To me, this is not difficult. In that case, the growth is from *katan* (smallness) to *gadlus* (greatness), not a *yesh mi’yesh* of something **else**. This is unlike chicks growing from an egg, or a stalk of grain growing from a seed, and the like. A thing whose seed does not perish is analogous to a tree growing from *katan* to *gadlus*. Consequently, it is understood that in the *nimshal* (the concept being explained)—which is the *Seder Hishtalshelus*—that is a *yesh* from the true *Yesh* to the created *yesh*, and it is not a matter of *katan* to *gadlus*, *chas v’shalom*. It is appropriate that it is only through an *ayin* in between.

4) Regarding his question as to whether, when counting *Sefiras HaOmer* after *Aleinu*, one should say *Kaddish* after the *Sefirah*:

If I had the power, I would establish a practice not to increase the number of *Kaddishim* unnecessarily; they should say *Kaddish* only after *Sefiras HaOmer*, and not between *Aleinu* and the *Sefirah*. If, however, they do not agree to this and wish to say *Kaddish Yasom* after *Aleinu*, then it is possible to say *Kaddish* after the *Sefirah* as well, if that is the local custom.

5) I, too, am saddened by the fact that I am unable to edit the *maamarim* and *sichos* from the days of the *farbrengens*. But what can I do? My time is not my own, etc. I am striving to do so to the extent that is possible. The same applies to answering the letters I receive, which are delayed for the aforementioned reason.

With the blessing of a kosher and happy *Chag HaPesach*.

## 1,511

B”H, 13 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter informing me about Mr. [Name] and his wife, may they live, noting that he is suffering from various ailments and that his wife is also not in good health, and you request a blessing for them.

It must be explained to them that the Ribono shel Olam is the sole Master of the world and all it contains, and He Himself, may He be blessed, is goodness, kindness, and mercy. We have nothing to do but prepare the appropriate vessels to draw down and receive blessings from Above, and the vessels for a Jewish man and woman are the matters of Torah and mitzvos.

Just as in physical life, when one is hungry and eats bread, or thirsty and drinks water, it is irrelevant whether one understands intellectually how the bread satisfies the hunger or how the water quenches the thirst—so too is it in spiritual life. When the neshamah is hungry and finds the bread and water of Torah and mitzvos, the main thing is to act, to satisfy its hunger and thirst with Torah and mitzvos. Once it becomes healthier and stronger through this, it naturally gains the ability to understand the matters of Torah and mitzvos more easily and in a shorter amount of time, even with its limited human intellect. But one must not reverse the order by declaring that we will first hear (and understand, and only then) do.

All these things apply to Mr. [Name], may he live, to whom Hashem will surely send a refuah. However, he, for his part, must not set conditions—that he will first be healed, and then, in his spare time, he will endeavor to understand the necessity of Torah and mitzvos, and only then will he increase his strength in Torah study and the fulfillment of mitzvos. This is like a sick person who says he will not accept any medicine for his illness until he finishes studying the science of medicine and understands intellectually how the medicinal ingredients work to cure his illness and restore his health. On the contrary, by taking the medicine, the power of his intellect is strengthened, enabling him to understand more easily and more quickly once he begins to study the science.

When Mr. [Name], may he live, begins the fulfillment of mitzvos—specifically the putting on of tefillin and eating kosher—and his wife is careful regarding the conduct of the home in accordance with kashrus and the lighting of candles on Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov, and before lighting the candles she gives to the tzedakah of Rabbi Meir Baal HaNes (Rambahan), may Hashem grant them the merit to bring good news soon regarding the improvement of their health.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach for you and all those with you, may they live.
