Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 11, p. 294.

## 1512

1512

B”H, 13 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter from the 2nd of Tzav, and I was happy to read that you have already settled in and have the opportunity to maintain your Torah shiurim and also your Tehillim.

You also ask for my opinion, as while you were in... you took upon yourself, for various reasons, to recite shiurim of Tehillim, and you wish to know if you should continue them now that you are in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, especially since you will not have as much time for Gemara study as you would like.

My opinion is that, since this custom of reciting Tehillim to such an extent takes up a significant amount of time, even though it seems to you that the reason [for taking it on] no longer exists, you should nevertheless continue the recitation of Tehillim just as you have until now. One cannot know what is more precious in the eyes of the Ribono shel Olam, especially since this good custom has been yours for quite some time.

Surely you have read stories regarding the virtue of reciting Tehillim in the holy seforim, and especially in the seforim of Chassidus.

As we approach the festival of Pesach, which is coming upon us and upon all of Yisrael for good, I hereby wish you and your family, may they live, a blessed holiday—a kosher and happy Pesach.

And as the promise we hope for, "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders," may the Ribono shel Olam merit us, in our immediate time, with the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With holiday blessings.

## 1,513

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn

To the congregants of the Nusach Ari Shul in Albany Park, Chicago, may they live,

Peace and blessing!

With pleasure, I received through the esteemed and G-d-fearing individual, who engages in communal needs, R' Avraham Hanzburg, the check for the Maos Chittim fund under my direction. I send my blessing to all the donors, that Hashem should repay them many times over. Because they are participating so that "all who are hungry may come and eat, and all who are in need may come and celebrate Pesach," may Hashem help them and their households to have a kosher and joyous holiday.

Pesach is mentioned throughout the entire year, as we recite in various prayers, "a remembrance of the exodus from Egypt." Therefore, even though this charity is associated specifically with Pesach—like Maos Chittim—we must remember it throughout the entire year. This applies both literally, in that one must give charity not only for the Pesach holiday but throughout the entire year (though it is certainly unnecessary to remind you of this), and even more importantly, in that one must give charity not only with money, but by doing kindness for a fellow Jew—man or woman—by giving of one’s time and effort, and by influencing others to do the same.

There is an additional detail regarding charity: just as one must surely have compassion for a Jew's body, one must have compassion for his soul. When you see that his soul is naked of mitzvos and hungry for Torah, you must help him in this regard, as our Sages say in Tanna D'bei Eliyahu Rabbah, Chapter 27: "‘When you see the naked, you shall cover him’—how? If you see a person who possesses no words of Torah, teach him and encourage him in mitzvos."

With blessings for a kosher and joyous Pesach to all the congregants of the shul.

## 1514

B”H, 13 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

As we, together with all of Klal Yisrael, prepare to celebrate the Yom Tov of Pesach, I would like to wish all the members of the Ladies Auxiliary and their families a kosher and happy Pesach.

It is surely known to all what the Midrash relates: that the Exodus from Egypt came about in the merit of the righteous women of that generation. Their merit consisted in the fact that they raised a Jewish generation—boys and girls.

So too, regarding the awaited Geulah, which we all hope will come through Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days, this also depends to a great extent on the conduct of Jewish women in every place where Jews are found. This is primarily through their involvement in the chinuch of children—of their own children—and by helping others to raise the new, young generation in the path of Torah and mitzvos.

Your Ladies Auxiliary, which was founded exclusively to support the mosdos established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, follows this path of Torah and mitzvos. I hope that the Ladies Auxiliary will grow, that your work will be successful in gashmius, and that it will bring forth good fruits in ruchnius. May Hashem Yisbarach bless all the members, the activists, and the officers with blessing and success in their private matters.

With the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 1115

1115

B"H, Erev Pesach, 5712
Brooklyn.

Blessings and peace!

As we approach the Yom Tov of Pesach that we, together with all of Klal Yisrael, are about to celebrate, I wish you a kosher and a happy—a truly happy—Yom Tov of Pesach.

You surely know what is related in the Midrash: that the merit through which the Yidden were redeemed from Mitzrayim was the merit of the righteous women of that generation.

One of the righteous acts of these women consisted of the fact that, regardless of all the difficulties and the darkness of that galus—and especially in those final decades—they always maintained a strong bitachon in Hashem Yisbarach that He, Baruch Hu, would fulfill His promise regarding the Geulah. Even though they did not know when the Geulah would come, and from time to time Pharaoh’s decrees became ever stronger and more difficult—especially the decree against the Jewish children, even to the point of the severe decree, "Every son that is born, you shall cast into the river"—their hope did not diminish. They still sought to raise a new generation, not taking the decrees into account. Even though they did not see a way before them as to how the children who were born would be saved, and how they would avoid Pharaoh’s decree of "Every son that is born, you shall cast into the river,"

It was this bitachon and strength—not to take into account any human logic, because the Ribono shel Olam is the Master of the entire world and no one can stand against Him—that enabled them to raise an entire generation of tens and hundreds of thousands of children. And these children were the ones who were the first to recognize Hashem Yisbarach at the Krias Yam Suf, and they were the ones who subsequently received the Torah at Har Sinai and upheld the Jewish people.

From everything in the Torah, we must derive a lesson for every Yid. So too, regarding us and regarding you: one must be strong in bitachon in Hashem Yisbarach, that He, Baruch Hu, alone is the absolute Master of the world, and against Him no one can do anything. Even when one does not see this within the natural order, Hashem Yisbarach will fulfill His will, so that all those who are connected to Him—Baruch Hu—through bitachon in Him, and especially regarding children, *zera chaya v'kayama* for long days and years—just as in Mitzrayim, even though they did not see a way in nature beforehand as to how the Geulah would come, it did not weaken their bitachon to have and raise children, and [their belief] that the children would have long lives. We must hope that in our time as well, through strong bitachon in Hashem Yisbarach, we will all merit the Geulah Amitis V'Hashleima through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach, and much nachas and health for long days and years.

## 1,516

B"H, Erev Chag HaPesach, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed individual of noble character, scion of noble ancestors, one of Anash who engages in the needs of the community with faithfulness, etc., Mr. Shneur Zalman [Shazar] sheyichyeh,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I receive news from time to time from Anash in general, and from the village in particular, regarding your kind interest in their standing and situation. I hope that in the future as well, you will be of help and assistance to them whenever the need arises.

Although our Sages have said that the benefactor does more for the poor person than the poor person does for the benefactor, nevertheless, they have extolled the act of tzedakah in helping the needy in their time of distress, especially when it involves the merit of the many. I deeply value your interest in the details of the matter, for I see in it a continuation of the golden chain from the rock from which you were hewn—loyal bonds that connect you to your fathers and forefathers. Just as anything of eternity is never lost and demands expression in action, so too, your interest in the situation of Anash sheyichyeh and the assistance you provide them are the channels flowing from the fountain of Torah in general, and Chassidus in particular.

For this reason, I am confident that in the future you will increase your strength in your interest and assistance to Anash sheyichyeh in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, just as any living thing, full of the vigor of youth, whose growth is a sign of its vitality. It is unnecessary for me to express my feelings of gratitude, as it is self-understood; the matter itself speaks its thanks in the fruits that are visible and those that are yet to come.

It was also a source of satisfaction for me to hear from my relative by marriage, the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, the energetic activist and thinker, etc., Moreinu HaRav Avraham Chen sheyichyeh, about the assistance he received from you in his work at the Ministry of Education and Culture, and I am sure that in the future as well, you will endeavor to assist in this as much as possible.

Approaching the festival of Pesach, on the eve of the holiday, I wish you and yours a kosher and happy Pesach. You are surely aware of the statement of our Rabbeinu HaZaken that the exodus from Mitzrayim must take place every day—meaning, an exodus and liberation from constraints and boundaries. This is also the purpose of the human species: to emerge from limitations, ascending from level to level, such that today is higher than the limitations of yesterday, and tomorrow will be higher than the constraints of today, through the preparations made for this today.

With holiday blessings and proper health.

## 1,517

26 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 5 Nissan, in which you share the news of the birth of your daughter, may she live and be well. Although it depends to a certain extent on the type of children, their age, and their home background, a general guideline can be given that applies in all cases. Namely, in the current time, the main emphasis must be placed on planting in Jewish children matters of yiras-shamayim, as well as the concept that Yiddishkeit must be practiced in daily life. It is not enough to merely learn about it, or even to practice it only on Shabbos and Yom Tov in shul.

Proceeding from this standpoint, one must utilize every opportunity so that children can know how to make brachos, observe Shabbos, kashrus, and so on. Even if there are children whom such instruction might intimidate, one must give it to them bit by bit; in any event, this must be the primary goal and objective.

Since the check was sent out and arrived in the days before Pesach, I have distributed it: half to the fund for maos-chitim, and half to our educational institutions for girls in Morocco in the name of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory — Oholei Yosef Yitzchak Lubavitch — in honor of your newborn daughter, may she live and be well, for long, good days and years.

Enclosed is a general letter for Pesach, the content of which is valid for the entire year.

With blessings.

## 1118

27 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned man, engaged in communal work, etc.,
R' Chaim Zusia, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letters from Adar and 14 Nissan:

... 2) Regarding your question concerning the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok: I have already written to Agudas Chabad in Tel Aviv regarding the necessity of arranging the matter of "non-partisan" flow (in response to their letter after their visit to Rabbi Kahana). They have surely already begun to take action, and I hope that if they exert the appropriate, great energy, they will succeed in this. You have surely already been informed of my aforementioned letter as well. In any case, it is proper to make the necessary preparations for the aforementioned matter, etc., which, according to your letter, should take place in the coming month of Sivan.

3) Regarding what you write—that some of your assistants seem to be working only out of *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke), and consequently lack the necessary energy: We have heard this addressed several times in instructions regarding communal work: "If you want someone to work, you must give them room to grow and develop." This means that all those assisting in the matter must be given the opportunity to express their opinions regarding the workflow and to demonstrate their own initiative, so that they are not merely fulfilling the orders of others, etc. It is understood that one should not jump from one extreme to the other, which would cause anarchy in the work, but there is surely a middle path to be found: that everyone should consult together regarding the work. Since each person expresses their opinion, even if there are details decided by a majority vote against their suggestion, they will still have the satisfaction of having been heard, and at the very least, they will know the reasoning for why it was rejected. *V'dai l'chacham* (a word to the wise is sufficient), as it is difficult to elaborate on such matters, which depend on the character of the people who must work together on a single project. I hope to hear good news from you that this matter has also been resolved.

4) Regarding your question of where to establish the center of the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok: The appropriate place for this, at least for now, is Tel Aviv. You are surely familiar with the saying of the Baal Shem Tov: "Though your beginning was small, your end will flourish greatly."

5) Regarding the inclusion of more young people in the work: I do not wish to name anyone from here, because such matters must be done with good will—both on the part of those already in the work, including yourself, and those whom you wish to add to the work. This is different than if it were done by way of an order from above. As mentioned, if you speak with the young people and inform me who they are, I will then express my opinion as to how suitable they are for this.

6) You write that the fundraising campaign for the benefit of Oholei Yosef Yitzchok has not yet begun, but you do not state the reason for this.

7) Enclosed is a script that may be used as a supplement, and thereby provide some small measure of assistance with the financial shortage felt in the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok.

## 1,519

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It has been a long time since I have heard from you, and surely this is a good sign, as is the custom among Chassidim that when everything is good, peaceful, and smooth, one does not write. May it be the will of Hashem that this remains the case, both regarding physical matters and spiritual ones. Nevertheless, a *talmid chacham* should inform me of this in writing as well.

I am also interested to know what is happening with your son, *sheyichyeh*, who visited me a few months ago—whether he is continuing his work as a journalist, and where he has settled, whether in Eretz Yisrael, *tizkeh l'mitzvos*, or elsewhere. In any case, surely you are using your influence on your son, *sheyichyeh*, to add to his involvement in matters concerning *yiras shamayim* in general, and the ways of Chassidus in particular. There are some parents who are either embarrassed to speak about such matters with their children, or who tell themselves that it surely will not help, and that just as there is a *mitzvah* to say something that will be heeded, there is a *mitzvah* not to say something that will not be heeded. However, based on what we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzuklalleh-h, nbg"m, zya*, many times, this is not the case. There is a presumption that *ta'amulah* (outreach/propaganda) does not return empty-handed. This is true even when it comes from an ordinary Jew, and all the more so when one hears words of inspiration from someone close—and who can say this more than a father? According to what is explained in Chassidus, the father is one essence with the son, so the possibility and speed with which words of inspiration will be accepted are all the greater. This is especially true in such a case, where the words will surely be those that come from the heart, as we say in our prayers, "as a father has compassion upon his children."

With blessings for *nachas chassidish* from your children and from yourself as well.

## 1520

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Yehuda Zev Halevi, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter informing me of the Bar Mitzvah of your son, Pesach, may he live, I enclose my letter to him. May it be the will of Hashem that you derive from him much Yiddishe nachas and Chassidishe nachas, with tranquility of soul and body. Great is the merit of your engagement in drawing the hearts of the Children of Israel to their Father in Heaven, and the attribute of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is "measure for measure"—may you see much nachas from your children and students, may they live.

I was pleased to read in your letter about the arrangements in the yeshiva during the past period, and my hope is strong that for the coming time as well, their borders will expand with students, both in quantity and quality. May you succeed in your influence upon them, to draw their hearts near and to illuminate their nefesh, ruach, and neshamah with the inwardness of "the mitzvah is a candle and the Torah is light." This also awakens the inwardness of the soul, as it is written, "You have said, 'Seek My face'; my heart said to You, 'Your face, Hashem, I will seek'"—and the paved path for this is through the study of the inwardness of the Torah. May Hashem grant that there be success, both from the side of the teachers and mashpiim, and from the side of the students and recipients.

With blessings for much nachas from your son, the Bar Mitzvah mentioned above, and success in communal and personal matters.

P.S. Regarding what you wrote in your letter concerning the conduct of the students, may they live—that you are not entirely comfortable with their lengthiness in davening, etc., since it does not match their conduct in other matters and you fear it may lead to arrogance, etc.—perhaps you are correct in your arguments. However, it is known from what is tangible and visible to anyone who examines the nature of the youth in our generation, that for them in particular, this is a period of crisis. Therefore, one must be extremely careful regarding any matter that could weaken their power of resistance against the winds blowing in the world. Even if there are such matters that, given their current state, the time has not yet come for them to engage in such things, since this is, in any event, a detail that adds to their ability to stand firmly against the winds blowing in the world, it is a responsibility not to remove, nullify, or weaken the matter. If, in your opinion, there is a contradiction between the lengthiness in davening and their conduct in other matters, you should endeavor—gently but firmly—that they improve their ways in those other matters, but not to nullify the matter of lengthiness in davening, etc. For ultimately, this adds yiras shamayim and a detachment from worldly pleasures, even if it is only in a way of makif (encompassing). It is understood that a judge has only what his eyes see on the spot, but as you describe it in your letter, my opinion is as stated above. Our hope—your hope and my hope—is that the interpretation of our Sages of blessed memory on the verse, "There is no breach and no outcry in our streets," will be fulfilled: "Happy is the people that is in such a case; happy is the people whose G-d is Hashem" (see Zohar Vol. III, 291b).

The Above

## 1521

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the avreich, Mr. Pesach, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your notification that on the upcoming 5th of Iyar you will reach the age of mitzvos,

I hereby express my blessing that you should be a G-d-fearing person, a Chassid, and a scholar, and that you should be diligent in your study of Torah with fear of Heaven.

With blessing.

P.S. It is known that there are two opinions regarding the source of the law that a thirteen-year-old is obligated in mitzvos: 1) The opinion of Rashi (Nazir 29b, s.v. *v'Rabbi Yossi*), that we find a thirteen-year-old referred to by Scripture as an "ish" (man), as it is written, "And the two sons of Yaakov, Shimon and Levi, took each man his sword" (Bereishis 34:25). This is also found in Machzor Vitry (Avos, end of chapter 5). The intention here is that the term "ish" denotes maturity, as it is written, "Who made you an ish" (see Rashi and Rabbeinu Bachya there; this is unlike what is written in Shemos Rabbah there), and "Be strong and show yourself an ish," and so on. 2) The opinion of the Rosh (Responsa, beginning of Klal 16), that this is among the *shiurin* (measurements) which are a Halacha L'Moshe MiSinai.

One could suggest a practical difference between these two opinions regarding the law of a Ben Noach: according to the first opinion, a Ben Noach is also obligated in his mitzvos at thirteen, whereas according to the second opinion, he is not (see Rambam, Hilchos Melachim 9:10, 10:2; Responsa Chasam Sofer, Yoreh Deah 317).

This is because according to the second opinion, this is a Torah decree, whereas according to the first opinion, it is a matter of nature—in the majority of cases—that a thirteen-year-old becomes mature in intellect and understanding.

One may hint at a moral lesson: that the proof for the obligation in mitzvos from the verse "And they took... each man (*ish*)"—which is based on reason and intellect—is appropriate.

Yet, it is written, "Return to your side" (i.e., look at the context): one should not say that conduct based on reason and intellect is sufficient for the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos. Therefore, they point out to him:

See and contemplate what the sons of Yaakov did: "They took each man his sword"—immediately upon their obligation in mitzvos, they began with the avodah of mesiras nefesh specifically.

And the deeds of the fathers are a sign for the children—for every bar mitzvah in every generation—that this is the only way to fulfill mitzvos: not through conduct measured by intellect, but rather, first and foremost, one must accept upon himself the **yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven**, and only afterwards accept upon himself the **yoke** of the mitzvos.

## 1522

1522

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, may it be the will [of Hashem] that your wife’s pregnancy proceeds as it should, and that the birth takes place at its proper time and with ease. If there is no impediment, it is appropriate that you endeavor to open the Aron Kodesh on the days when the Torah is read. May the Ribono shel Olam grant you the merit to share good news regarding this. Please convey to your wife that she should be strong in her bitachon in the Ribono shel Olam that everything will occur at its proper time and with ease. She should increase the amount she gives to tzedakah before lighting Shabbos candles for the tzedakah of the Rambah"n, up to 18 pennies each time.

Regarding your writing that you received word from your brother... that he must travel by ship to the East: surely, as I spoke with him, he has taken his tefillin with him. It is also worthwhile to encourage him to have a Siddur and Tehillim with him. So that he can carry them with him, you will surely be able to find these in a small format to send to him. May it be the will [of Hashem] that the Ribono shel Olam protect him wherever he may be and bring him home healthy and whole in every respect.

As you requested, when I visit the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention your father for parnassah, and your wife, may she live, to raise all their children to Torah, chuppah, and maasim tovim, in comfort and abundance.

With blessings.

## 1523

1523

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter of 11 Nissan. May you who bless be blessed with the abundant increase of the Ribono shel Olam, both you and your wife and all your descendants, may they live.

I trust that in the meantime you have received the kuntres and the copies of my general letters, and that you have publicized them in an appropriate manner.

Thank you for the stories of Chassidim that you transcribe in all your letters. I am certain you will continue to do so in the future, and I thank you in advance. It is well known how much our Nesi'im, the Rebbeim, cherished the stories of Tzaddikim and Chassidim. The sicha of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, on this matter is well known: that the Book of Bereishis precedes the books that follow it, even though its essence and the majority of its content are stories of Tzaddikim, while the subsequent books contain the mitzvos of the Torah, and so on.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter, your opinion that you wish to come for a visit to the U.S., and your reason and rationale as stated in your letter:

I must reveal my opinion that this does not seem right to me. The reason is: the Ribono shel Olam has merited you to establish your residence in the land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year, and within it, in Yerushalayim, the Holy City, which is holier than all of Eretz Yisrael. Regarding the matter of traveling from Eretz Yisrael, there are many doubts and misgivings involved. Therefore, it is not understood at all why you should enter into such doubts, and to exert yourself and weary your feet to cross seas, rivers, and deserts, to expend so much money and waste so much time on the journey from there to here and from here to there—at a time when, in every moment, hour, and day that you are in Eretz Yisrael and in the Holy City, you can draw down the light of Hashem into this physical world and strive to disseminate the wellsprings of the Baal Shem Tov, his students, and his students' students, and especially those of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, and those who followed him, in Eretz Yisrael. This matter is most necessary there, and from day to day the necessity for this only increases, as the darkness, G-d forbid, is also growing. At such a time, you wish to leave your place to "seek fortune." May the Ribono shel Olam bless you with long, good years and health, and may you stand strong at your post, utilizing every opportunity and every matter to strengthen faith, to raise the horn of the elder Israel, and to disseminate the light of Chassidus—its Torah, customs, and instructions—in every place and among every type of person that you can reach.

## 1,524

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, involved in communal needs,
Rabbi Zalman Tuvia Hakohen, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from Erev Pesach. Regarding your question concerning the Oholei Torah network, I have already written to Agudas Chassidei Chabad to urge them regarding the organization of the non-partisan school system, and surely you are already aware of the developments in this matter.

2) Regarding your question as to whether girls should also be taught at Oholei Torah, and whether it should also involve a kindergarten: in principle, this is correct. However, for the sake of the order of the work, it is not advisable at this time. Once the first stage is strengthened, then the second stage—that is, the kindergarten and the girls—should be initiated. If, however, the matter is already in such a state that the second stage will not interfere with the first, then one should begin with this as well...

With blessings.

## 1,525

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter with pleasure... You inform me that a letter has arrived from the consul regarding your visa, and you request a blessing that the obstacles and delays be removed.

For some time now, I have not understood why you write that you are facing obstacles and delays. Who among us knows what is truly best for him—whether to remain for a few more weeks in the place where you are now, to illuminate it with the candle of mitzvah, Torah, and the light of Torah, which is the Torah of Chassidus—or whether it is specifically necessary to relocate from there as soon as possible to pursue new matters? In a situation of such uncertainty, it is better to rely on the Ribono shel Olam, who is the essence of good. One has a duty to create a vessel through natural means, and you have already done this with the greatest energy. Surely, the Ribono shel Olam will grant you success in both general and personal matters—for you and your entire family, may they live.

I trust you have received a copy of my general letter for the upcoming holiday and have publicized it in an appropriate manner.

With blessings.

## 1526

1526

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5712

Brooklyn.

Mrs. Rachel, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

With joy I received your letter from after Pesach, in which you inform me that your students have already begun to daven, and you ask for a blessing for them.

Surely you know what is brought in many seforim: that every Jew, and Jewish children in particular, are precious to the Ribono shel Olam even more than an only child is to his parents. Consequently, there is no doubt that the Ribono shel Olam wishes to grant each of them blessing and success in all their affairs.

However, there lies a holy obligation—and it is a zechus for those who educate and teach the children—that they should do everything within their power so that the children may be pure vessels and good vessels to receive the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach. Specifically in this case, you must endeavor to implant within them matters connected to yiras shamayim: that they should wear yarmulkes, a tallis katan, and be careful to say Modeh Ani, berachos, berachos hanehenin, Shema Yisrael, and the like. If this is done, you will surely be successful with the children, and this will draw down blessing and success to those who assist in this holy work.

With a blessing for success in your personal matters as well.

#### ***1526***

**Mrs. Rachel, may she live:** Teleshevsky.

## 1527

1527

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your regards via... and it is a pleasure for me to see the closeness of hearts between you, as is evident from your letter. If at all times and in every era the value of Ahavas Yisrael is of the greatest importance, how much more so at the end of this galus of ours, which, according to our Sages in Yoma (9b), is due to the sin of baseless hatred. And our generation, the *ikvesa d'meshicha*, is at the point where "behold, he is standing behind our wall." As the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, indicate, this is literally true—Moshiach is standing behind the wall, waiting for the completion of the *birurim* and *zikuchim* of each and every one of us, even in small matters. Thus, the matter of Ahavas Yisrael is all the more significant, for it is the rectification for the primary sin that caused this galus of ours. It is well known that the Alter Rebbe stated that "Love your fellow as yourself" is the vessel for "Love Hashem your G-d."

From time to time, I receive regards from you via the esteemed Rabbi, the chossid, the G-d-fearing man, who engages in communal needs with faith, etc., Rabbi Shlomo Zalman Hecht, regarding your participation in the administration of the work of Agudas Beis Knesses Lubavitch and the Anash synagogues in Chicago and the surrounding area. It is unnecessary for me to express thanks on my part for this, for "the reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself"—meaning that in performing a good deed, the essence of the reward is the deed itself. The same applies to expressing thanks, for the good deeds and their fruits—which I firmly hope will be seen with physical eyes in the near future—will themselves be the tangible expression of gratitude. I write only to offer a note and an insight regarding the preference in this matter, as our Sages say, "We elevate in matters of holiness," and there are several opinions that this is a Torah obligation (see Pri Megadim, Mishbetzos Zahav, Orach Chaim, end of siman 42; Chasan Sofer, Sefer HaTotafos, siman 20; Sdei Chemed, Klalim 40, subsection 194; Minchas Chinuch, part 1, siman 27). I do not come to deliver a sermon, but rather to address the practical application, in accordance with the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of his grandfather, the Rebbe Maharash: "If 'good' is good, is 'better' not better?"—asked rhetorically. Surely, in the days to come, you will increase your participation and utilize your influence and talents to expand the scope of the activities of Agudas Beis Knesses Lubavitch, etc., and elevate them to the height appropriate to their name, Agudas Beis Knesses Lubavitch and the Anash synagogues in Chicago and the surrounding area. Surely, when you open [a path] as small as the eye of a needle, Hashem will open for you—as He promised—a path as wide as the entrance to the Ulam, and may it be with success, both materially and spiritually.

## 1528

1528

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Blessings and peace!

I have just received your airmail letter from the 3rd of Chol Hamoed Pesach, in which you write regarding your son, may he live, that he is not developing as he should, and you ask for my opinion and request a blessing.

I am pleased to read in your letter that you remember your lineage, and in particular your grandfather, who was renowned in the Chassidic world, as well as your father, may they rest in peace. I hope that it is not only that you remember them, but also that this influences you to conduct your home in a spirit that would satisfy not only your father but also your grandfather, may they rest in peace. Through **this** remembrance, one draws down, receives, and maintains the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach regarding yourself, your husband, and your children, may they live.

Regarding your question concerning your son in particular, you surely know that for every matter, it is easier to find advice when the cause is known. Therefore, I trust you will not take offense at my question, and will answer me as the reality was: was your son, may he live, born in purity—that is to say, at that time, did you observe the Jewish customs of mikveh and taharah as they ought to be observed? After receiving your sincere answer, I will provide you with my opinion on the matter. In the meantime—until I receive your answer—when I am, G-d willing, at the end of the month at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may his merit protect us, I will mention your son, may he live, for good health. When you write to me the name and mother’s name of your husband, as well as the name of your daughter, may she live, I will also mention them at the holy gravesite.

In the meantime, you should have the mezuzos of your home checked to see if they are kosher, and also ensure that your son, may he live, sleeps with a yarmulke and wears a tallis katan, and, it goes without saying, eats **only** kosher food.

With blessings to her and to all her household, may they live.
